<leme no="577">

<page sig="a1r">
<section type="Title page">
A
Physical Dictionary;
In which, all the
TERMS
Relating either to
ANATOMY, CHIRURGERY,
PHARMACY, or CHYMISTRY,
are very accurately explain'd.

By STEPHEN BLANCARD,
M.D. and Physick-Professor at 
<f type="i">Middleburgh</f> in <f type="i">Zeeland</f>.

<f type="i">LONDON</f>;
Printed by <f type="i">J.D.</f> and are to be sold by
<f type="i">John Gellibrand</f> at the Golden-Ball in
St. <f type="i">Paul</f>'s Church-yard, M.DC.LXXXIV.
</section>
</page>

<page sig="a1v">
</page>

<page sig="a2r">
<section type="Dedication">
TO
My honoured Friend,
Mr. <f type="i">William Moulins</f>.
<f type="i">SIR</f>,
BEing very unwil&shy;
ling to be singu&shy;
lar, as to send this 
Book into the World
without either Epi&shy;
stle or Preface, would
certainly be, I resol&shy;
ved from the time of
my setting it to Press,
</page>

<page sig="a2v">
to send it out with
both; and had no 
sooner made that Re&shy;
solution, but present&shy;
ly pitcht on a Patron
under whom to shelter
it. I now humbly de&shy;
dicate it to yourself;
and beg of you to be&shy;
live that I am in all
sincerity,
<f type="i">Sir</f>,
Your very humble
Servant,
<f type="i">J.G.</f>
</section>
</page>

<page sig="a3r">
<section To the Reader>
Courteous Reader;
T<f type="i">He ensuing Dictiona&shy;
ry was compil'd in La&shy;
tin, by the eminently
Learned and Famous Phy&shy;
sician, Dr.</f> Stephen Blan&shy;
card, <f type="i">now Physick-Professor
at</f> Middleburgh <f type="i">in</f> Zee&shy;
land; <f type="i">in which he hath taken
that pains, and done it with
such Accurateness, that the
like has never yet been ex&shy;
tant. The Authors he has
consulted (and out of which
he has made the following
Dictionary) you have a Ca&shy;
</page>

<page sig="a3v">
talogue of, ensuing this Pre&shy;
face. But chiefly, and most
of all, he has extracted the
most useful of all the Terms in
Anatomy, Pharmacy, Chi&shy;
rurgery, and Chymistry, out of
ancient Authors, as</f> Eroti&shy;
an, Galen, <f type="i">and others; and
from the more modern, as</f>
Gorr&aelig;us, F&oelig;sius, Castellus,
<f type="i">and others; out of whole Wri&shy;
tings he has not omitted any
one useful term in the whole
art of Physick. I am certain,
that things of this nature are
extremely wanting, that so
the terms (in which all, or the
most part of Mankind has
daily occasion to use) may not</i>
</page>

<page sig="a4r">
<f type="i">be talkt by rote; but may give
a rational account of their
discourse, than which, no&shy;
thing is more rational or de&shy;
monstrative than this of Phy&shy;
sick.

That the Publick-Good
has all along been drove at in
this Affair, both by the Au&shy;
thor and Bookseller, is very
apparent, in that it might
have made a Book of three
times the price, and the mat&shy;
ter spun out to a far great&shy;
er bulk; but in things of this
nature, the Buyer's Interest
ought to be, and has been
consulted.</f>

Vale.
</section>
</page>

<page no="1">
<section type="Dictionary A-H">
<heading>
THE
Physical Dictionary
OF
STEPHEN BLANCARD
</heading>

<wordgroup1 type="a" object="A">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">ABaptista</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Modiolus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Abdomen</form>, <xpln lang="en">which <term lang="la">Juvenal</term>
calls <term lang="la">sumen & equaliculus</term>, is
the lowermost Belly, con&shy;
taining the Liver, Spleen,
Reins, Stomach, Intestines,
Bladder, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. The innermost
part of it is begirt with a 
Membrane called the <term lang="la">Perito&shy;
n&aelig;um</term>, the foremost part is divided into the <term lang="la">Epi&shy;
gastrum</term>, the right and left <term lang="la">Hypochondres</term> and the
Navel, and the lowermost Region or part is cal&shy;
led <term lang="la">Hypogastrium</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ablactatio</form> <xpln lang="en">is when a Child of one or two years
of Age is weaned.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Abortus</form> <xpln lang="en">is the bearing of a <term lang="la">F&oelig;tus</term> before
the Female have gone out its full time, which hap&shy;
pens either through the abundance of nutritious
juice, or defect or depravation of it; as likewise
</page>

<page no="2">
it may come by a fall, a blow, a sudden fright,
diuritics, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Abscessus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Apostema</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Abstemius</form> <xpln lang="en">is he who abstains from whatsoever
meats and drinks his Physician has forbid him
the use of.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Abstergentia</form> <xpln lang="en">are those things which consisting of
rugged, hard, and sharp particles, do as it were
shave and scour off all filth from the <term lang="la">superficies</term>,
and the pores and passages of bodies, where
they are frequently put into various fermentati&shy;
ons from the spirits, and other elements lodged in
those parts.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Acamatos</form> <xpln lang="en">signifies the best constitution and fi&shy;
guration of humane body, as also one that takes
no pains, and a person that is not tired with it.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Acantabolus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Chyrurgeons Tool called <term lang="la">Vulsel&shy;
la</term>, which is to take out Thorns, or any such
prickly substance that shall chance to stick in 
the <term lang="la">&oelig;sophagus</term> or Gullet.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Acautha</form> <xpln lang="en">is the most backward protuberance of
the <term lang="la">Vertebres</term>, called <term lang="la">spina dorsi</term>, as also the Thorn
of Trees or Plants.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Accessio</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Paroxismus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Accidens</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Symptoma</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Acetabulum</form> <xpln lang="en">is that cavity in the Huckle-bone
which is appointed to receive the head of the
thigh-bone within it: Also certain glandules in
the Chorion are called <term lang="la">Acetabula</term>, concerning
which see <term lang="la">Cotyledones</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Achylus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a certain dark distemper of the eye;
it is reckoned amongst the species of <term lang="la">Amblyopia</term>, or
dimness of sight.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="3">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Achor</form> <xpln lang="en">is a sort of crusted Scab which makes
an itching and stink on the surface of the head,
and is occasioned by a serous, salt and sharp mat&shy;
ter; the difference betwixt an <term lang="la">Achor</term> and <term lang="la">Favus</term>
consists in this, that in <term lang="la">Achors</term> the holes or Cavi&shy;
ties are small, and sometimes not visible; but in a 
<term lang="la">Favus</term> they are more large and conspicuous.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Achroi</form> <xpln lang="en">are men that have lost their colour, such 
as are melancholly persons, men of an ill habit of
body, and they who are troubled with the Jaun&shy;
dies.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Acia Celsi</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Fibula Chyrurgcrum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Acida dyspepsia</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">dyspepsia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Acidul&aelig;</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Balan&aelig;um</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Acinefia</form> <xpln lang="en">is the immobility of the body, or of a&shy;
ny part thereof, as in a Palsie, Apoplexy, swound&shy;
ing, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Acini</form> <xpln lang="en">are small grains; whether they grow by
themselves, as Elder-Berries; or shut up in a husk,
as Grape-stones; nay, sometimes they are taken
for the Grapes themselves.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Acmastica</form> <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Synochus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Acme</form> <xpln lang="en">is the height of a disease : Many distem&shy;
pers have four Periods, the first is called <term lang="gk">&#x1F70;&#x03C1;&#x03C7;&#x1F74;</term> or
the <f type="i">beginning</f>, when the matter is but yet raw,
as it were, and unripe; the second is <term lang="gk">&#x1F70;&#x03BD;&#x03AC;&#x03B2;&#x03B1;&#x03C3;&#x03B9;&#x03C2;</term> the
growth or increase, when the morbifick matter
becomes a little digested and ripened; the third
is <term lang="gk">&#x1F70;&#x03BD;&#x03BC;&#x03AE;</term>, when 'tis fully and compleatly so; the
fourth is <term lang="gk">&#x03C0;&#x03B1;&#x03C1;&#x03B1;&#x03BD;&#x03BC;&#x1F74;</term>, or the <term lang="la">declension</term> of a distemper
when its rage is abated, and the Patient is judged
beyond danger, for none die in the declension of a
disease : This diversity of periods arises from the
bloods imbibing of crude juices, which have their
</page>

<page no="4">
times of crudity, maturation, or ripening, de&shy;
section, and volatility; and thus the case may be
said to stand in Fevers and other distempers.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Acopum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a medicine which applied by fomen&shy;
tation, allays the sence of weariness, contracted by
a too violent motion of the body, compounded
of warming and mollifying ingredients.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Acosinia</form> <xpln lang="en">is an ill state of health, joined with the
loss of colour in the face.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Acoustica</form> <xpln lang="en">are medicines which help the hearing.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Acrasia</form> <xpln lang="en">is the excess or predominancy of
one quality above another in mixture.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Acrisia</form> <xpln lang="en">is when a distemper is in so uncertain
and fluctuating a condition, that the Physitian
can hardly pass a right Iudgment upon it.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Acrochodum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a species of warts.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Acromium</form> <xpln lang="en">is the upper process, or increase of
the shoulder-blade, or the top of the shoulder
where the neck-bones are joined with the shoul&shy;
der-blades.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Acromphalum</form> <xpln lang="en">is the middle of the Navel.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Acros</form> <xpln lang="en">is the height and vigor of diseases, as also
it signifies the prominency of bones, the tops of 
fingers, and of plants.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Acrotes</form> <xpln lang="en">is the vigor, top, and extremity of any
thing, as sulphureous and saline particles exalted
<term lang="la">ad</term> <term lang="gk">&#x1F70; &#x03B7;&#x03C1;&#x03CC;&#x03B6;&#x03BD;&#x03C4;&#x03B1;&#x03C2;</term> that is, brought to the most exalted
vigour their nature is capable of.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Actio</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Operation or Function, which men
perform either by the body alone, or by both body
and mind; and it is either <f type="i">animal</f>, which de&shy;
pends upon the brain; or <f type="i">natural</f>, which is owing
to the <term lang="la">Cerebellum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="5">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Acutus morbus</form>, <xpln lang="en">an acute disease, is that which
is over in a little time, but not without imminent
danger; and it is either very <f type="i">acute</f>,  or most <f type="i">acute</f>;
the later is meant when the distemper is over in
three or four days; but the former is that which
continues till the seventh day; or else a disease is
called simply <f type="i">acute</f>, when it lasts fourteen, or it
may be twenty days; or lastly <term lang="la">acute ex decidentia</term>,
which lasts forty days at most.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Aden</form> <xpln lang="en">is a glandule, which is either <f type="i">conglobated</f>
as the glandules of the Mesentery of the Groin,
and the Pinealis, whose office is to dispense the
separated humour to the veins, or <f type="i">conglomerated</f>,
like a Cluster, as the salival glandules, the Pan&shy;
creas, or Sweet-bread, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. which convey their
juice by their own proper channels into some  no&shy;
table cavities of the body; they are made up seve&shy;
ral little bladders, and fibres, or little hollow con&shy;
duits disposed in a confused manner: <term lang="la">Aden</term> some&shy;
times also signifies the same with <term lang="la">bubo</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Adephagia.</form> <xpln lang="en">is the greediness of children, who e&shy;
ver now and then fall to fresh feeding before their
former victuals are digested.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Adeps</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Pinguedo</term>, fat is a similar part, made of
earthy and sulphereous blood, white, soft, insensible,
apt to preserve natural heat, and  nourish the bo&shy;
dy in time of need: The eye-lids, the lips, the 
yard, the <term lang="la">Scrotum</term>, or outward skin of the cods,
the membranes of the testicles, the brain, the
tendons, the nerves, the bones, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. are destitute
of fat by nature. <term lang="la">Adeps</term> and <term lang="la">Pinguedo</term> differ in this,
that <term lang="la">Adeps</term> is a thicker, harder, and more earthly
substance than <term lang="la">Pinguedo</term>, the fat which is particu&shy;
larly meant by <term lang="la">Adeps</term>, flows from the blood through
</page>

<page no="6">
peculiar vessels into little bags or bladders appro&shy;
priate thereunto, as is plain from the observation
of <term lang="la">Malphighius</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Adiapneustia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a different perspiration through
the insensible pores of the body.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Adnata tunica</form> <xpln lang="en">is the common membrane of
the eye, called <term lang="la">Conjunctive</term>; it springs from the
skull, grows to the exterior part of the <term lang="la">tunica cor&shy;
nea</term>; and that the visible species may pass there,
leaves a round cavitie forward, to which is annex&shy;
ed another <term lang="la">tunic</term>, without any particular name
made up of the tendons of those muscles which
move the eye; by reason of its whiteness 'tis cal&shy;
led <term lang="la">Albuginia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Aegilops, Angilops, <term lang="en">and</term> Anchylops</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a little swel&shy;
ling about the glandule of the eye called <term lang="la">Carancu&shy;
la major</term>, for the most part accompanied with an
inflamation; <term lang="la">Anchylops</term>, and <term lang="la">Aegilops</term> are often used
indifferently; yet some for distinction's sake say,
that <term lang="la">Anchylops</term> is a swelling betwixt the greater cor&shy;
ner of the eye, and the nose, not yet open; but
that <term lang="la">aegylops</term> is a swelling betwixt the nose and an&shy;
gle of the eye, which if it be not seasonably o&shy;
pened, the bone underneath grows putrified; <term lang="la">Ae&shy;
gilops</term> is often taken for the <term lang="la">Fistula lachrymalis</term>; it
signifies likewise a sort of grass that is destructive
of Barley.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Aeipathia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a passion of long continuance.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Aeromeli</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="manna(n)">is Manna, or aerial honey; for in <term lang="la">Cala&shy;
bria</term> and other places the air is impregnated with
several delicious particles which in the night time
cleave to trees, leaves, or any other thing they meet
with; and in the day time, are farther concocted 
and condensated by the heat of the Sun.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="7">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Aetas</form> <xpln lang="en">is part of the duration of life, wherein
from the continual action and fermentation of the
blood and spirits, the temperature of humane bo&shy;
dies undergo a considerable and sensible change;
and it is sixfold, <term lang="la">Pueritia</term>, childhood, which is
reckoned to the fifth year of our age, is distin&shy;
guished into the time before, at, and after breed&shy;
ing of teeth. 2. <term lang="la">Adolescentia</term>, Youth, reckoned to the
eighteenth, and youth properly so called to the
twenty fifth year. 3. <term lang="la">Fuventus</term>, reckoned from
the twenty fifth to the thirty fifth. 4. <term lang="la">Virilis Aitas</term>,
manhood, from the thirty fifth to the fiftieth.
5. <term lang="la">Senectus</term>, old age, from fifty to sixty. 6. <term lang="la">De&shy;
crepita Aitas</term>, decrepit age follows, which at last is
all swallowed up in death.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Aetiologia</form> <xpln lang="en">is the cause or reason which is given
of natural and preternatural contingencies in hu&shy;
mane bodies; whence <term lang="la">Aetilogica</term> is part of Physick,
which explains the causes of diseases and health.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Aetiologica</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Aetiologia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Affectio Hypochondriaca</form>; <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Hypochondriacus af&shy;
fectus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Affectus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Pathema</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Agerazia</form> <xpln lang="en">is growing old.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Agonia</form> <xpln lang="en">is fear and sadness of mind.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Agonia</form> <xpln lang="en">is barrenness, or impotence of the
Womb, whereby the mans feed corrupts.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Agrippa</form> <xpln lang="en">is one who is born with his feet fore&shy;
most.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Agrypnia</form> <xpln lang="en">signifies watching, or a dreaming
slumber which proceeds from a too great agitati&shy;
on, or attension of the animal spirits in the pores
of the brain, whence it happens that the pores are
not permitted to close and wet.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="8">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Agripnocoma</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Coma Vigil</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Agyrta</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="mountebank(n)">is a Mountebank, one who vends his
Empyrical Receits to the Rabble that surrounds
him.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Aisthesis</form>, <xpln lang="en">or Sence, is either <f type="i">external</f>, as seeing,
hearing, smelling, tast, and touch; or <f type="i">internal</f>, as
the common sensory, (as 'tis usually called) the
Fancy, the estimative faculty, and the memory; but
two of them will serve the turn, the fancy and
the memory; <term lang="la">Aisthesis</term> or sence, is a reception
whereby motion from external objects being im&shy;
pressed upon the slender strings or fibres of the
nerves, is communicated to the common sensory,
or to the beginning of the <term lang="la">medulla oblongata</term> in the
brain, by the mediation or continued motion of 
the animal spirits in the same nerves.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Aisteterium</form> <xpln lang="en">is the common sensory: which <term lang="la">Car&shy;
tesius</term> and others his Abettors make the <term lang="la">glandula
pinealis</term>; but the common sensory ought rather to
be placed where the Nerves of the external senses
are terminated, which is not in the <term lang="la">glandula pine&shy;
alis</term>, but (as the most ingenious <f type="i">Willis</f> has demon&shy;
strated) about the beginning of the <term lang="la">medulla ob&shy;
longata</term> (or top of the spinal marrow) in the 
<term lang="la">Corpus striatum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Al&aelig;</form>, <xpln lang="en">signifies the sides of the Nose; the little
fins, as it were, of the <term lang="la">nymph&aelig;</term>, or the lips of a
Womans private parts; the upper part of the
ear, the Arm-pits, and the process of the bone,
<term lang="la">Sphenoides</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Alantoides</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Allantoides</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Albaras nigra</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">lepra Gr&aelig;corum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Albaras al&shy;
ba</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Leuce</term>.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="9">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Albuginea oculi</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a white tunic of the Eye,
which proceeds from the <term lang="la">pericranium</term>, grows
to the <term lang="la">tunica cornea</term>, and leaves a hole forward
for the opening of the Apple of the Eye; see <term lang="la">tu&shy;
nica adnata</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Albuginea testis</form>, <xpln lang="en">is the membrane which im&shy;
mediately involves the testicles.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Albugo oculi</form>, <xpln lang="en">is the same with <term lang="la">album oculi</term>, the
white of the Eye; it signifies also a white speck in 
the <term lang="la">tunica cornea</term>, which proceeds either from hu&shy;
mours, or a scar, or ulceration.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Album oculi</form>, <xpln lang="en">is that part of the Eye, where
the <term lang="la">tunica adnata</term>, and the <term lang="la">albuginea</term> grows to the
<term lang="la">tunica sclerotes</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Albumen oculi</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">albugo</term>, the same with <term lang="la">album oculi</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Alcali</form>, <xpln lang="en">is all such Salt as is extracted from the
ashes of any substance by a boiled <term lang="la">lixivium</term>, or
Lie, proper for any thing liquid as well as solid.
'Tis said to borrow its name from the herb <term lang="la">Kali</term>,
with whose Salt the <f type="i">Egyptians</f>, as well as we, make
glass.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Alchymia</form>, <xpln lang="en">is the same with <term lang="la">Chymia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en">Alcohol</form>, <xpln lang="en">is the purer substance of any thing sepa&shy;
rated from the impurer; it signifies also most sub&shy;
til and refined dust; and sometimes a most high&shy;
ly rectified Spirit, in so much that if it be set on
fire, it shall burn all away without any dregs or
phlegm at the bottom.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Alcol</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Alcohol</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Alcool</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Alcohol</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Alembicus</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Alembicum</term>, is a Chymical In&shy;
strument used in Stilling. It has the shape of an
helmet, concave within, and convex without;
and towards the bottom is placed a beek or nose,
</page>

<page no="10">
about a cubit long, by which the vapours de&shy;
scend; if they be made without a nose, they are
rather used in circulatory vessels; they are made of
Brass, Pewter, or Glass.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Alexipharmacum</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a medicine which expels poy&shy;
son, so that it shall not be hurtful to the Body; they
are most commonly such things as attenuate the
Blood, that it cannot be coagulated with Poyson
in the Air, as <f type="i">Acids</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Alexiterium</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a remedy which preserves the 
Body, that it not take Poyson.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Algema</form>, <xpln lang="en">pain, is a sad troublesome Sensation,
impress'd upon the Brain from a smart Vexatious
irritation of the Nerves; it arises from either a 
sensible or insensible solution of the <term lang="la">Continuum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Algematodes</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Algema</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Alhasef</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Hydroa</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Alkahest</form>, <xpln lang="en">signifies an universal Menstruum or
liquor, which resolves Bodies into their first matter,
still preserving the virtues or their seeds and es&shy;
sential form: a thing of great fame, if of equal
virtue, which every one estimates according to
his success in the Operation. Some take it for
prepared <f type="i">Mercury</f>, others for <f type="i">Tartar</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Aliformes processus</form>, <xpln lang="en">are the prominencies of the
<term lang="la">Os Cuneiforme</term>, from the sore part.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Alimentum</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Body so convenient for, and
adapt to the nature of an animal, that it may be
digested by its heat and fermentation, and assimi&shy;
lated into its own nature; and it is either Meat
or Drink. Upon the account of its different
degrees, it is taken three ways by <term lang="la">Hippocrates</term>;
one is for <f type="i">future</f> nourishment, which passes from
the Mouth into the Ventricle or stomach: another 
</page>

<page no="11">
is for that <f type="i">which is as it were</f> nourishment, and
that is the arterious Blood and animal Spirits.
The third is <f type="i">true</f> or proper nourishment, that
which fastens to the parts, and at last is assimi&shy;
lated into their nature,</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Alindesis</form>, <xpln lang="en">is an exercitation of the Body,
wherein people first anointed with Oil, were
wont afterwards to rowl themselves in the dust.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Alipasma</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a small dust, which mixt with
Oil is used to be soaked into the Body to hinder
sweating.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Alitura</form>, <xpln lang="en">is the action of a live Body, where&shy;
by the perpetual waste of Blood, Spirits, and
substance, is as continually repaired by the acces&shy;
sion of new nutritious juice, rightly prepared and
fermentated, and then stuck upon the parts that
are to be nourished.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Allantoides</form>, <xpln lang="en">is the urinary tunic, placed betwixt
the <term lang="la">Amnion</term> and the <term lang="la">Chorion</term>, which by the Na&shy;
vel and <term lang="la">Urachus</term>, (or passage by which the
Urine is conveyed from the Infant in the Womb),
receives the urine that comes out of the Bladder.
'Tis called likewise <term lang="la">Farciminalis</term>, because that
in many brutes 'tis of the shape of a gut-pud&shy;
ding; but in man and some other few animals, it 
is round, and like the thin soft skin which wrappeth
the Child in the Womb.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Allioticum</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Medicine which by Fermen&shy;
tation and cleansing alters and purifies the Blood;
boiled up for the most part of the root of Sow&shy;
thistle, Cichory, Fennel, Endive, Lettice, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Allogotrophia</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a disproportionate nutrition,
when one part of the Body is nourished dispropor&shy;
tionately to another.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="12">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Alopecia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a shedding of the Hair, occasioned
by the Pox, or otherwise. So called from a Fox,
<term lang="gk">&#x1F00;&#x03BB;&#x03CE;&#x03C0;&#x03BD;&#x03BE;</term>, whose Urine is said to make places bald
and barren for a year, as the Scholiast of <term lang="la">Calli&shy;
machus</term> observes; or from a disease peculiar to a
Fox. It is called likewise, <term lang="gk">&#x1F40;&#x03C1;&#x03B9;&#x03B1;&#x03C3;&#x03B9;&#x03C2;</term> from the figure,
because that the parts smooth and destitute of
Hair, look winding like a Serpent, in Greek <term lang="gk">&#x1F42;&#x03C1;&#x03B9;&#x03C2;</term>.
Its common to both these Distempers that the
hair falls, or <term lang="la">Areatem</term>, by shedding, whence in
general this Disease is called <term lang="la">Area</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Alphus</form> <xpln lang="en">is described by <term lang="la">Celcus</term>, to be a Distem&shy;
per wherein the white colour of the skin is some&shy;
what rough, but not continued, like so many se&shy;
veral drops: Sometimes it disperses it self wider,
and with some intermissions. <term lang="la">Alphus</term> is likewise cal&shy;
led <term lang="la">morph&aelig;a</term>; it differs from <term lang="la">Leuce</term>, in that it
penetrates not so deep.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Alterantia</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Alliotica</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Alteratio</form> <xpln lang="en">is a depuration, or a preparation
and expurgation of the Blood by breathing a
Vein, or purging.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Alvearium</form> <xpln lang="en">is the cavity of the inward Ear,
near the passage which conveys the sound where
that yellow and bitter excrementitious stuff is
bred.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Alvi fluxus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Diarrh&aelig;a</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Amalgamatio</form> <xpln lang="en">is the corrosion of metal by
<f type="i">Mercury</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Amaurosis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a dimness of sight, whether the
object be placed near or at a distance; but so, that
no external fault appear in the Eye, if you in&shy;
spect it never so narrowly; the defect consists in
the obstruction of the optick nerve; it is called also
<term lang="la">gutta serena</term>.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="13">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ambe</form> <xpln lang="en">is a superficial jutting out of the Bones:
also a Chyrurgeons Instrument with which dis&shy;
jointed Bones are set again.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Amblotica</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines which make abortive,
as are all diureticks.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Amblyopia</form> <xpln lang="en">is dulness of sight, which is fourfold;
<term lang="la">Myopia</term>, <term lang="la">Presbytia</term>, <term lang="la">Nyctalopia</term>, and <term lang="la">Amaurosis</term>, of
which in their proper place.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ambon&aelig;</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">ambe</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ambrosia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a solid Medicine, but prepared as
grateful and pleasant as can be; it seems to take
its name from the meat of the gods, because the 
gods eat <term lang="la">Ambrosia</term>, and drink <f type="i">Nectar</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ambustio</form> <xpln lang="en">is a solution of the <term lang="la">Continuum</term>, caused
by some external burning matter, which offends
the inward thin skin always, oftentimes the out&shy;
ward thick skin, and sometimes also the muscles,
veins, arteries, nerves and tendons.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Amethodicum</form> <xpln lang="en">is that which is done without
any methodical rational prescription, as your Em&shy;
puricks, or Quacks do.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Amma</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Bracherium</term>, is a sort of a girdle, useful
to those who are troubled with a Rupture in the
Belly, wherewith the privy parts are closely con&shy;
nected with the Abdomen, the Ribs, and the
Loins, lest the intestines should fall out. It seems to 
have took its name of <term lang="la">Bracherium</term>, from the girdles
which are made for the Reins and Loins, which
<term lang="la">Isidorus</term> calls the Amber Monkish Bracelet; it is
called <term lang="la">Brachile</term> or <term lang="la">Brachiale</term>, tho it be not any gir&shy;
dle belonging to the Arms, but the Reins. <term lang="la">Cas&shy;
sianus</term> calls it <term lang="la">rebrachiatorum</term>, whence without
doubt the <term lang="la">Bracherium</term> of the Chyrugeons had
its rise; that girdle or swathe which they
</page>

<page no="14">
use in Ruptures of the Belly.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Amnion</form> <xpln lang="en">is the membrane with which the
<term lang="la">f&oelig;tus</term> in the Womb is most immediately clad,
which with the rest of the <term lang="la">secundin&aelig;</term>, the <term lang="la">chori&shy;
on</term> and <term lang="la">alantois</term>, is ejected after the birth; it
is whiter and thinner than the <term lang="la">chorion</term>. It con&shy;
tains not only the <term lang="la">f&oelig;tus</term>, but the nutritious hu&shy;
mour, whence the <term lang="la">f&oelig;tus</term> by the Mouth and
Throat sucks its nourishment. It is outwardly
clothed with the urinary membrane, and the <term lang="la">cho&shy;
rion</term>, which sometimes stick to close to one another,
that they can scarce be separated.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Amolyntum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Medicine which will not de&shy;
file the hands that touch it.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Amphemerinus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Quotidian distemper.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Amphiblestroides</form>, <xpln lang="en">or the <term lang="la">tunica retina</term> of the
Eye, is a soft, white, and slimy substance, which
is so named, because that being thrown in the
water, it resembles a net. It shoots from the ve&shy;
ry center of the optick nerve; and expanding it
self over the vitreous humour, is extended as
far as the ligament of the Eye-lids; this tunic, in
that it is whitish and of a marrowy substance,
seems to proceed from the very marrowy and fi&shy;
brous substance of the optick nerve; so that it is
as it were an expansion of nervous fibres, which
are there gathered into one bundle, into a con&shy;
texture made like a net; and indeed if the whole 
eye were taken for a flower which grows to the
brain by the stalk, as I may call it, of the optick&shy;
nerve, the <term lang="la">tunica retina</term> would be the very flower
it self, and the two former be only in the nature
of a stem; They receive the sensible species
</page>

<page no="15">
within the bed of the eye much after the same
manner as a whited wall in a darkned chamber
receives and represents the visible species which
are intromitted through a little hole.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Amphibranchia</form> <xpln lang="en">are places about those glandules
in the jaws which moisten the <term lang="la">Aspera Arteria</term>, Sto&shy;
mach, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Amphid&aelig;um</form> <xpln lang="en">is the top of the mouth of the
Womb, like the lips of a cupping-glass.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Amphismela</form> <xpln lang="en">is an anatomical instrument, use&shy;
ful in the dissection of bodies.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Amulatum</form> <xpln lang="en">is the same with <term lang="la">Periamma</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Amygdal&aelig;</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Antias</term> and <term lang="la">Paristh&shy;
mia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Amigdalatum</form> <xpln lang="en">is an artificial milk, or an emul&shy;
sion made of almonds, and other things.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ana</form> <xpln lang="en">is an equal portion of different ingredients
in the same receit.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anabasis</form> <xpln lang="en">is the increase of diseases.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anabatica</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Synochus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anabrochismus</form> <xpln lang="en">is when any thing superfluous
and corrupted is taken up by the letting down of
a band fit for <emend err="thar">that</emend> purpose; it is likewise a way of 
drawing out the inverted prickling hairs of the
eye-lids, by the help of a thread of fine silk in the
eye of a needle; which when you have doubled,
you put the hair through, and draw it out.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anabrosis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a consuming or wast of any part of
the body by sharp humours.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anacatharsis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a medicine that discharges na&shy;
ture by some of the upper parts; as any thing
that provokes to vomit, to sneezing, to salivation,
<term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="16">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anacollema</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a sort of ointment, or dry me&shy;
dicine, either applied to the forehead and nostrils
to stop bleeding; it signifies likewise a medicine
that will breed flesh, and conglutinate the parts.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anadiplosis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a frequent reduplication of Fe&shy;
vers.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anadosis</form> <xpln lang="en">is whatsoever tends upward in the bo&shy;
dy, as the distribution of Chyle, or a Vomit.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anaisthesia</form> <xpln lang="en">in defect of sensation, as in paraly&shy;
tick and blasted persons.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Analeptica</form> <xpln lang="en">are medicines which cherish and re&shy;
new the strength; it signifies also a part of <term lang="la">Hygiei&shy;
na</term>, or art of preserving health, whereby weak per&shy;
sons are recovered.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Analgesia</form> <xpln lang="en">signifies indolency, or absence of pain 
and grief.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Analogia</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Analogismus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Analogismus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a comparison and perception of
causes that help by likeness.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Analysis</form> <xpln lang="en">is the reduction of a body into its first
principles; also it is an Anatomical demonstrati&shy;
on of the parts of mans body, which is perfor&shy;
med by insisting upon the parts severally.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anamnestica</form> <xpln lang="en">are medicines which restore the
memory, as all spirituous things do.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anaplerosis</form> <xpln lang="en">is part of Chyrurgery, whereby
that which either Nature has denied, or has by
chance decayed, is restored by art.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anarrhopus</form> <xpln lang="en">is the same with <term lang="la">Anodosis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anasarcha</form> <xpln lang="en">is a white, soft, yielding tumor of
the whole outward body, or of some of its parts,
which dints in by compressing the flesh; it is
caused by the blood upon a double account; first,
when it does not rightly sanguifie, or assimilate
</page>

<page no="17">
the Chyle; and again, when it is not rightly ac&shy;
cended in the Lungs. The blood thus perverted,
pours forth the <term lang="la">Serum</term> at the extremities of the
Arteries in greater quantity than it can receive
and reduce by the Veins and Lympheducts, or 
expel by the Veins and Pores, and other passages
that send it forth. If the humours be too viscous,
it is called <term lang="la">Leucophlegmatia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anastoichiasis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Chymical resolution of bo&shy;
dies.</xpln></wordentry> 

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anastomasis</form> <xpln lang="en">is an effluxion of the Blood, the
Lympha or Chyle, at the meeting of Vessels that
close not narrowly. It is also taken for the mu&shy;
tual opening of Veins and Arteries into one ano&shy;
ther, as some long ago dream't, though they were
awake; for this were to offer violence to the Laws
of Circulation: yet it is not impossible neither,
since Veins open into Veins, and Arteries into Ar&shy;
teries; as is plain in the Spermatick Vessels; the
<term lang="la">Plexus Choroides</term>, <term lang="la">rete mirabile</term>, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anastomotica</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines which open the
Pores and Passages, as Purgatives, Sudoriferous
things, and Diuretics.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anatasis</form> <xpln lang="en">is the extention of the Body towards
the upper parts.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anatica portio</form>, <xpln lang="en">See <term lang="la">ana</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anatomia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a neat Dissection of an Animal, es&shy;
pecially Man, whereby the Parts are severally
discovered and explained, for the use of Physick
and Natural Philosophy.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anatomicus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Physitian that is skilful in Dis&shy;
sections.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anatripsis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a bruising or Comminution of the
Stone, or a Bone.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="18">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anchoralis processus</form>, <xpln lang="en">See <term lang="la">Ancyroides</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anchyle</form> <xpln lang="en">is a contraction of a Ioynt, or the back
part of the Knee. </xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anchylops</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Aegilops</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ancon</form>, <xpln lang="en">or the top of the Elbow, is strictly ta&shy;
ken for the backward and greater shooting forth
of that Bone of the Cubit which is called <term lang="la">Ulna</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ancon&aelig;us</form>, <xpln lang="en">See in <term lang="la">Ancon</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ancyle</form> <xpln lang="en">is the contraction of the Ham. See
<term lang="la">Anchyle</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ancyloblepharum</form> <xpln lang="en">is the growing of the Eye-lid
to the <term lang="la">tunica cornea</term>, or to the <term lang="la">Albuginea</term>, or when
as it sometimes happens, both the Eye lids grow 
together: this concretion sometimes happens be&shy;
fore the delivery of a Child, and then 'tis the
fault of the Birth.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ancyloglossum</form> <xpln lang="en">is when the little string under the
Tongue is too straitly tied, which causes difficulty
of utterance.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ancyroides</form> <xpln lang="en">is the shooting forth of the Shoulder&shy;
bone like a beek, which is called <term lang="la">Coracoides, An&shy;
choralis</term>, and <term lang="la">Cornicularis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Androgynus</form>, <xpln lang="en">or an <f type="i">Hermaphrodite</f>, is one who
hath both Man and Womans Members: also one
who has had his Members cut out; also Effemi&shy;
nate.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Aneurisma</form> <xpln lang="en">is a dilatation or bursting of the Ar&shy;
teries, always beating, and swelling sometimes to
the bigness of an Egg, which yields, if you com&shy;
press it, but recoils presently.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Angina</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Inflamation of the Jaws or Throat,
attended with a continual Fever, and a difficulty
of respiration and swallowing: and it is two-fold;
either <term lang="la">Spuria</term> or <term lang="la">Exquisita</term>, a bastard or a true
</page>

<page no="19">
<term lang="la">Squincie</term>: the later is again four-fold, <term lang="la">Synanche</term>, 
<term lang="la">Parasynanche</term>, <term lang="la">Cynanche</term>, and <term lang="la">Parachynanche</term>: of all
which in their proper place.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anhelatio</form>, <xpln lang="en">See <term lang="la">Asthma</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ani procidentia</form>, <xpln lang="en">See <term lang="la">Procidentia ani</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Animalis facultas</form>, <xpln lang="en">the Animal Faculty, is an
Action whereby a man exercises Sense, Motion,
and the principle functions of the Mind, which 
are three, Imagination, Ratiocination, and Memo&shy;
ry.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la"><term lang="gk">&#x0391;&#x03BD;&#x03C9;</term> purgare</form>, <xpln lang="en">to discharge upwards, as in a Vo&shy;
mit, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. opposite whereunto is <term lang="gk">&#x039A;&#x03B1;&#x03B6;&#x03C9;</term> <term lang="la">purgare</term>, to
do it downwards.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anodynum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Medicine that allays Pain.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">An&oelig;a</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="madness(n)">is Madness, or an extinction of the Ima&shy;
gination and Judgment.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anomeomeres</form> <xpln lang="en">is the same with <term lang="la">Heterogeneus</term>; or
that which consists of several and different Par&shy;
ticles.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anorexia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a loathing of Meat, arising from
an ill disposition of the Stomach.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Antagonista</form> <xpln lang="en">is the opposite Situation of <f type="i">Mus&shy;
cles</f>, as may be seen betwixt the Adductor and
Abductor, that which contracts and expands the
Arm.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Antarthriticam</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Medicine against the <f type="i">Gout</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Antasthmatica</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines proper for <term lang="la">Asth&shy;
matic</term> people.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Antecedens causa</form>, <xpln lang="en">See <term lang="la">Proegumena</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Antecedentia signa</form>, <xpln lang="en">Antecedent Signs are such
as are observed before a Disease, as an ill disposi&shy;
tion of the Pancreatic Juice, or the Bile, is an
Antecedent cause to infinite Diseases.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Antemetica</form> <xpln lang="en">are such things as hinder Vomiting 
too much.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="20">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Antendaxis</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="counter indication(n)">is a <f type="i">Countre</f>-indication, or a con&shy;
tradictory  indication, which forbids that to be
used which the former indication suggested as
proper: as for instance abundance of ill juice in 
blood requires Evacuation; but then again the
weakness of the Patient may forbid it.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Antepileptica</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines against the <f type="i">Falling&shy;
sickness</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anthelix</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Protuberance of the Ear, or
the inward brink of the outward Ear.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Antherum</form> <xpln lang="en">is any thing that's florid in our Bo&shy;
dies. <term lang="la">Anthera</term> are also the tops in the middle of
Flowers, which lean upon little hairy threads.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anthracosis oculi</form> <xpln lang="en">is a scalie corrosive <f type="i">Ulcer</f> of
the Eye, attended with a Defluxion and fear of
the whole Body, especially about the Eyes. The
Cause is now and then an Inflamation of the Eye
from a Malignant <f type="i">Fever</f>.
</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anthrax</form>, <xpln lang="en"><term lang="la">Carbo</term>, <term lang="la">Pruna</term>, or <term lang="la">Carbunculus</term>, is defined
to be a <term lang="la">Tumor</term> that arises in several places, sur&shy;
rounded with hot fiery and most sharp Pimples,
accompanied with acute Pain, but without ever
being suppurated; and when it spreads it self
farther, it burns the Flesh, throws off lobes of
it when it is rotten, and leaves an <f type="i">Ulcer</f> behind
it, as if it had been burnt in with an Iron.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anthypnotica</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines which hinder Sleep.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anthysterica</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines good against the
Fits of the <f type="i">Mother</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Antias</form>, <xpln lang="en">in the <f type="i">Plural</f> <term lang="la">Antiades</term>, <term lang="la">Tonsill&aelig;</term>, <f type="i">Glan&shy;
dules</f> of the Neck, which <term lang="la">Chyrurgeons</term> commonly
call <f type="i">Almonds</f>, which they do not too much re&shy;
semble neither. They are two <f type="i">Glandules</f>, which 
in reality make but up one Body, placed at the
</page>

<page no="21">
sides of the <term lang="la">Epiglottis</term>, or cover of the Wind&shy;
pipe; its substance is similar, and made like sepa&shy;
rate Grains, just like Honey or Oyl, hardned with
cold; but that they stick closer together, as if they
were joyned by a <f type="i">Membrane</f>; 'tis of somewhat a
yellowish Colour, and soft; it has on each side
one common large oval hollow passage which
opens into the Mouth within the skirt, whereof
it contains two somewhat big, and several less
Cavities. Its use is to collect the snotty viscous
Matter, and to moisten the adjacent parts there&shy;
with. It signifies also, the Inflamations of these
parts. See <term lang="la">Paristhmia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Antiballomena</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines of a like strength,
which are now and then used in the defect of one
another: <f type="i">Apothecaries</f> call them <term lang="la">quid pro quo</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anticardium</form> <xpln lang="en">is a cavity in the Breast above the
region or place of the Heart.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anticnemium</form> <xpln lang="en">is the former part of the Leg.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Antidotum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Medicine against deadly Poy&shy;
son.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Antinephritica</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines which Cure the
Distempers of the <f type="i">Reins</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Antipathia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Contrariety and Repugnancy
in the Body, or in Medicines: also a loathing and
abhorrence of any thing without a manifest
cause.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Antiperistasis</form> <xpln lang="en">is the surrounding of the Air, as 
in the Hay that is cocked and made up into Ricks too
moist. <term lang="la">Hippocrates</term> the first great Author of <term lang="la">Phy&shy;
sick</term>, says in his <term lang="la">Aphorisms</term>, That <f type="i">Bodies are hotter
in Winter, and colder in Summer</f>. I interpret it
thus, That this does not come onely from the
<term lang="la">Antiperistasis</term> of the Air, but from the Nitre with  
</page>

<page no="22">
which the Air in <f type="i">Winter</f>-time is impregnated;
especially, when the <f type="i">North</f>-Wind blows; so that
when we come to breathe, the Sulphureous Blood
is more fermentated and inflamed in the Lungs.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Antipharmacum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Remedy against Poyson;
or a Remedy against any other Disease.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Antipleuriticum</form> <xpln lang="en">signifies any Remedy against a
<term lang="la">Pleurisie</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Antipyreuticum</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">antipureticum</term>, is a Medicine
that temperates and allays too much heat in
<f type="i">Fevers</f>, as any <f type="i">acides</f> do.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Antiqui morbi</form>, <xpln lang="en">old Diseases, are such as from the
fourth day continue often many Years, and there&shy;
fore they are called also inveterate.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Antipasis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a revulsion of a Disease; that is,
when Humours which flow into some one part,
are turned into another by the opening of a
Vein in a remote part.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Antispasmodicum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Medicine that hinders
contractions.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Antispasticum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Medicine that diverts Distem&shy;
pers to other parts.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Antitasis</form> <xpln lang="en">is an opposite placing of parts in the
Body, as the <f type="i">Liver</f>, and the <f type="i">Spleen</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Antrum buccinosum</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Cochlea</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en">Anus</form> <xpln lang="en">is the extremity of the <term lang="la">intestinum rectum</term>;
it consists of Three <f type="i">Muscles</f>, two called <term lang="la">levatores</term>,
which distend and open it in time of necessity;
and one called <f type="i">Sphincter</f>, which shuts it, and keeps
it so. It is also a cavity in the Brain, which ari&shy;
ses from the contact of four Truncs of the <f type="i">Spi&shy;
nal Marrow</f>; also the Skin which goes over the
Navel, which when wrinkled, are a sign of old
Age.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="23">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Aorta</form>, <xpln lang="en">or the great Arterie, is a Vessel which
proceeds from the left Ventricle of the Heart,
consisting of four Tunics, a <term lang="la">Nerveous</term>, <term lang="la">Glandulous</term>,
<f type="i">Muscular</f>, and <f type="i">Membraneous</f>, or <f type="i">Internal</f> one; it
beats continually, and distributes Blood into the
whole Body for nourishment. The branches 
which creep from the Heart to the Brain, are cal&shy;
led <term lang="la">Carotites</term>: those which run laterally towards
the Arms, are called <term lang="la">Humeraris</term>: as the Trunc of 
it discends, the Branches extend themselves to&shy;
wards the Bowels: and going further on to the
Thighs and Feet, it ends.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Apagma</form> <xpln lang="en">is the thrusting of a Bone or other
part out of its proper place.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Apanthismus</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Obliteration of a part in the
Body, so that it can be no more found; as it of&shy;
ten happens to a little Arterious Pipe about the
Heart.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Apathia</form> <xpln lang="en">is an utter want of Passions.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Apepsia</form> <xpln lang="en">is when the Stomach has no Concocti&shy;
on.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="gk">&#x0391;&#x03C0;&#x03B5;&#x03C0;&#x03B6;&#x1F70; &#x03C6;&#x1F7A;&#x03BC;&#x03B1;&#x03B1;&#x03B6;</form> <xpln lang="en">are Crude Wheals or Knobs
in the Body, not yet ripe.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Aperientia</form>, <xpln lang="en">opening things, are those which con&shy;
sisting of sharp, small Particles, penetrate the Bo&shy;
dy profoundly, and by attenuating and expelling
the more crass and gross, open the Pores and
Passages of the Body and its Vessels.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Aperistatos</form> <xpln lang="en">is a holow <f type="i">Ulcer</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Aph&oelig;resis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a part of <f type="i">Chyrurgery</f> so called;
which teaches to take away superfluities.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Aphonia</form> <xpln lang="en">is want of Voice.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Aphorismus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a short determinative sentence.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Aphrodisius morbus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Lues Venerea</term>.</xpln></wordentry>
