<page no="24">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Aphth&aelig;</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="wheal(n)" lexeme="pimple(n)" lexeme="ulcer(n)">are Wheals or Pimples about the In&shy;
ternal parts of the Mouth; as also about the
Ventricle and Guts, which when they come to 
be ripe, fall off by piece-meal, and are often ac&shy;
companied with a <f type="i">Fever</f> in those of riper Years.
In new-born Children, I believe it arises from some
Impurities which the Mass of Blood contracts
in the Mothers Womb; for the Blood for want
of Eventilation there, being more impure, pre&shy;
sently after the birth of the <term lang="la">F&oelig;tus</term> begins to flou&shy;
rish and refine. <term lang="la">Celsus</term>'s <term lang="la">Aphth&aelig;</term> are otherwise
described; but, says He, <f type="i">There are extream dan&shy;
gerous Ulcers in Children, which the</f> Greeks <f type="i">call
<term lang="gk">&#x0391;&#x03C6;&#x03B8;&#x03B1;&#x03C2;</term>, for they often kill them</f>. There is not the
same danger in Men and Women. These <f type="i">Ulcers</f>
begin in the Gums, then by little and little spread
over the Palate and the whole Mouth; and then 
at last descend to the <term lang="la">Epiglottis</term>, or cover of the
Wind pipe, and the upper part of the Throat,
which being once Infected, the Child hardly re&shy;
covers.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Apn&aelig;a</form> <xpln lang="en">is a suppression of Respiration, either
wholly, or at least to Sense.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Apochylisma</form>, <xpln lang="en">called <term lang="la">Succago</term>, <term lang="la">Robub</term>, and <term lang="la">Rob</term>, is
the boiling and thickning of any juice with Su&shy;
gar and Honey, into a kind of hard consistence.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Apocope</form> <xpln lang="en">is the cutting off of a part.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Apocrusticum</form> <xpln lang="en">is any thing that helps by vertue
of binding and repelling.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Apodacryticum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Medicine that provokes
Tears.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Apolepsis</form> <xpln lang="en">is the interception of Blood and Ani&shy;
mal Spirits.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Apomeli</form>, <xpln lang="en">is <term lang="la">Oxymel</term>, or a Decoction of Honey
and Vinegar.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="25">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Aponeurosis</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="tendon(n)">is the end, tail, or string of Muscles;
it is called also a Tendon. <f type="i">Chyrurgeons</f> take it
falsly for a Nerve.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Apoflegmatica</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Apophlegmatismus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Apoflegmatismus</form>, <xpln lang="en"><term lang="la">Commansum</term>, some <f type="i">Physicians</f>
call it in Barbarous Language <term lang="la">Masticatorium</term>; it
is a Medicine which being kept in the Mouth, and
often also chewed, draws forth Pituitous Humors,
which are excited at the Mouth, made of the Root
of bastard <f type="i">Pellitory</f>, <f type="i">Salt</f>, <f type="i">Holly</f>, <f type="i">Mastich</f>, <f type="i">Wax</f>, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.
when it is used in this solid Form, it is called
<term lang="la">Masticatorium</term>: it is used also in a Liquid Form,
and is of the Nature of a Gargarism, made up
of <term lang="la">Cephalics</term>, and attenuating Ingredients, boiled
and prepared.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Apophthora</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="abortion(n)">is an Abortion, or the Birth of a
<term lang="la">F&oelig;tus</term> before its due time.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Apophysis</form>, <xpln lang="en"><term lang="la">Probole</term>, <term lang="la">Echphysis</term>, <term lang="la">Processus</term>, <term lang="la">Productio</term>,
<term lang="la">Projectura</term>, <term lang="la">& Protuberantia</term>, is a part of a Bone
that is not contiguous, as an <term lang="la">Epiphysis</term> is, but
continuous with the Bone, and stretching it self
beyond a plain surface.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Apoplecta</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="jugular vein(n)">is the Jugular Vein, which the An&shy;
cients falsly called, the <term lang="la">Soporalis</term>, or Sleepy Vein.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Apoplexia</form>, <xpln lang="en"><term lang="la">Attonitus stupor</term>, <term lang="la">Sideratio</term>, and <term lang="la">Mor&shy;
bus attonitus</term>, is a profound Sleep, wherein the
Patient being vehemently shaken, tossed, and prick&shy;
ed, yet perceives nothing, nor affords any sign of
Action; accompanied with a difficulty of Respi&shy;
ration for the most part, and sometimes with 
none at all: it arises frequently from <term lang="la">viscous</term> Blood,
which obstructs the least Pores of the Brain: or
from Blood Extravasated about the Basis of the
Brain, which oppresses and straitens the <term lang="la">Carotidal
Arteries</term>, or the Brain.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="26">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Aporrho&aelig;</form> <xpln lang="en">are Vapours, and Sulphureous <term lang="la">Efflu&shy;
viums</term> which exhale through the pores of the bo&shy;
dy, and other breathing holes.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Apositia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a loathing of Meat.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Apospasma</form> <xpln lang="en">is when the unity of Organical com&shy;
pounded parts is dissolved, and those things which
were of different natures, yet naturally compacted
together, are disjoyned by the Rupture of those
Ligaments, and little Fibrous Threads or Fil&shy;
ments which held them together: as when the
Skin is separated from a Membrane, a Membrane
from a Muscle, one Muscle from another; and in
short, any one part from another, which natu&shy;
rally adhered to it.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Apostasis</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Apostema</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Apostema</form>, <xpln lang="en">which <f type="i">Pliny</f> calls <term lang="la">Apostasis</term>, <f type="i">Hippocra&shy;
tes</f> <term lang="la">Metastasis</term>, and <term lang="la">Celsus</term>, <term lang="la">Abscessus</term>; is an Exul&shy;
ceration left after a <f type="i">Crisis</f>: but <term lang="la">Apostasis</term>, and
<term lang="la">Metastasis</term> sometimes differ in this, That the for&shy;
mer is meant of an Acurate <f type="i">Crisis</f>, the later of
the translation of a Disease from one part to ano&shy;
ther.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Aposurma</form> <xpln lang="en">is a shaving away of the Skin, or
Bone.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Apotherapia</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="cure(n)" lexeme="remedy(n)">is a Cure, or Remedy: also an Ex&shy;
ercitation, which both Purges the Excrements,
and secures from Weariness.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Apothermus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Apochilysma</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Apozema</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="decoction(n)">the <f type="i">Apothecaries</f> call it a <f type="i">Decoction</f>,
is a Decoction of Roots, Woods, Barks, Herbs,
Flowers, Fruits, Seeds, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. which is boiled down
commonly to Twelve, Fifteen, or Twenty Oun&shy;
ces. It is either Purging, Loosning, Altering, or
Drying, <f type="i">Cephalic</f> (for the Head) <f type="i">Stomachic</f>, <f type="i">Diu</f>&shy;
</page>

<page no="27">
<f type="i">retic</f>, <f type="i">Splenetic</f>, or <f type="i">Hepatic</f>, (good for the Liver.)</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Appetitus alimentarius</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="hunger(n)">or Hunger, is a certain
Constitution of the Phansie, arising from the Mo&shy;
<f type="i">Inter&shy;
costal</f>, which for want of Nourishment, is moved
inordinately in the Stomach; whereby we are
impell'd for Animal Spirits, to those Motions of our
Members which are most conducive to the pro&shy;
curing of Nourishment. It is occasioned in as
much as the Animal Spirits being any way exci&shy;
ted about the middle of the Brain, shoot thencey
towards the body of the Nerves: or it may be
thus defin'd, <term lang="la">appetitus alimentarius</term> is an incitement
to seek Nourishment, proceeding from an <f type="i">acid
Humor</f> which arises from a <f type="i">ferment</f> in the Sto&shy;
mach, with which the Nerves being <f type="i">vellicated</f>, they
communicate the sense of want of Nourishment
to the Brain; which want, the Brain naturally
judges ought to be supplied.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Apsychia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a <term lang="la">Deliquium</term> of the Mind.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Aptystus</form> <xpln lang="en">is want of Spittle, so that a Man can&shy;
not spit.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Apyrexia</form> <xpln lang="en">is an intermission, or cooling of <f type="i">Fe&shy;
vers</f>: the cause of it is, that all the <f type="i">Morbific</f> Mat&shy;
ter is spent in one Fit, and it intermits till new
come, and begin to swell and <f type="i">ferment</f> as the other.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Aqua distillata</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="distilled water(n)">distilled Water, is such as is
drawn out by Distilling, consisting of Watery and
Spirituous Parts, but more of Watery.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Aqua inter cutim</form>, <xpln lang="en">Water betwixt the Skin; the
same with <term lang="la">Anasarca</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Aqualiculus</form>, <xpln lang="en">or the lowest part of the Belly;
the same with <term lang="la">Hypogastrium</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Aqu&aelig;us humor</form>, <xpln lang="en">the Watery Humor, see <term lang="la">Hu&shy;
mores Oculi</term>.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="28">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Arachnoides</form> <xpln lang="en">is the <f type="i">Cristalyne tunic</f> of the Eye;
so called from its likeness to a Spiders Web.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ar&aelig;otica</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Rarefacientia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Aranea tunica</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Cristalyna</term>, is that which sur&shy;
rounds the <f type="i">Cristalyne humour</f>, by reason of its
light thin <f type="i">contexture</f>, like the workmanship of a 
Spider, it has the name of <term lang="la">Aranea</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Arcanum Theophrasto</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Quintessence of a 
thing most highly exalted, or, as He says, it is the
vertue of a thing Refined by a thousand Exaltations.
He boasts of four <term lang="la">Arcana</term> especially; 1. The <term lang="la">Ar&shy;
canum</term> of the First Matter. 2. Of the <f type="i">Philosophers
Stone</f>. 3. Of the <f type="i">Mercury</f> of Life. 4. Of <f type="i">Tincture</f>.
Others call it an <f type="i">Extract</f> specially so called.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Arche</form> <xpln lang="en">is the beginning of a Disease.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Archeus</form> <xpln lang="en">is the highest, and exalted, and invisible
Spirit, which is separated from Bodies, is Exalted
and Ascends, an hidden Vertue of Nature com&shy;
mon to all things; an Artist, a Physitian. Also
<term lang="la">Archiatios</term>, or the Chief <f type="i">Physitian</f> of Nature, which
distributes to every thing, and to every Mem&shy;
ber its peculiar <term lang="la">Archeus</term> occultly by the Air. Al&shy;
so <term lang="la">Archeus</term> the first in Nature, is a most occult
quality, which produces all things from <term lang="la">Iliastes</term>,
being onely immediately sustained by the Divine
Vertue it self.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Arcuatus Morbus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Icterus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ardentes febres</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="burning fever(n)">burning <f type="i">Fevers</f>, are those which
are accompanied with a great Heat and Thirst,
by reason of a too high Exaltation of the <f type="i">Sulphur</f>;
as in that called <term lang="la">causus</term>, and <term lang="la">lipiria</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ardor</form> <xpln lang="en">is a very <f type="i">intense acute</f> Heat raised in our Bo&shy;
dies by a too high Exaltation of <f type="i">Sulphur</f> or <f type="i">Spirits</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ardor ventriculi</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="heart-burning(n)">that which we call Heart&shy;
</page>

<page no="29">
burning, is a particular sort of Pain in the Sto&shy;
mach which at the same time molests the whole
Gullet; some call it a Fervent Heat of the Sto&shy;
mach; some an <f type="i">Ebullition</f>, and a boiling bubling
heat of the Stomach; when a certain fiery Pain
is felt in the Ventricle, and the Throat, as if it
burnt; it happens often to people that are in good
Health enough, and that either Feeding or Fasting;
especially when they belch, as if there were a fie&shy;
ry sort of Blast closely pent up, and which could
not break out. Yet it happens sometimes in <f type="i">Fe&shy;
vers</f> too. It is caused by a certain <f type="i">effervescence</f> of
little, very sharp <f type="i">bileous particles</f>, with <f type="i">Sulphureous</f>,
whence is perceived that <f type="i">Ebullition</f>, or bubling
heat of the Stomach.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Area</form>; <xpln lang="en"><f type="i">Celsus</f> reckons two sorts of <term lang="la">Areas</term>. This
is common to both of them, that the uppermost
little Skin being decayed, the hairs are first lessen'd,
and then fall off: and if the place be beat, it sends
forth a liquid matter of an ill savor; both of them
spread in some swiftly, in others slowly; that is
the worst that makes the Skin thick, fattish, and
perfectly bald: That which is called <term lang="gk">&#x1F00;&#x03BB;&#x03BF;&#x03C0;&#x03B5;&#x03BD;&#x03AF;&#x03B1;</term>
dilates it self in any shape, it happens both in the 
Head, and in the Beard; the former is called,
<term lang="gk">&#x1F40;&#x03C1;&#x03AF;&#x03B1;&#x03C3;&#x03B9;&#x03C2;</term> from its resembling a Serpent, it begins at
the hinder part of the Head, exceeds not the
breadth of two fingers, spreads it self towards the
Ears in two branches, in some to the Fore-head,
till they both joyn in the fore-part of the Head:
the one Distemper is incident to any Age; the
other common to Infants. The former is scarce
ever cured, the later often ends of his own accord.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Arena</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="gravel(n)">Gravel, is a thing bred in the body of
</page>

<page no="30">
a great deal of Salt and Earth, which often grows
up into a Stone.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Argemon</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="ulcer(n)">is a little <f type="i">Ulcer</f> of the Eye in that circle
of it which is called <f type="i">Iris</f>, comprehending part of
the white and black.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Arilli</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">acini</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en">Aroma</form> <xpln lang="en">is any Odoriferous Spice, as Cloves,
Cinnamon, Galangal, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Arquatus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Icterus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Arteria trachea</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="wind-pipe(n)">or <term lang="la">Aspera</term>, the Wind-pipe, is a 
<f type="i">Cartilaginous</f> Vessel implanted in the Lungs, and
consisting of various rings and parts: the fore&shy;
part of it is full of <f type="i">ligaments</f>, and depressed for
the better passing of the Gullet; its upper part
is called <f type="i">Larynx</f>, and the lower <term lang="la">Bronchius</term>: its
use is for the Voice and taking in breath.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Arteria aorta</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="great artery(n)">or <term lang="la">magna</term>, the great Arterie, is
a Vessel that beats continually, fastned to the left
Ventricle of the Heart: it consists of four <f type="i">tunics</f>,
and receives the Blood in the Lungs, which is
sent from the Heart, and Elaborated by the <term lang="la">Nitre</term>
in the Air, and diffuses it through the whole Body
for its Nourishment.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Arteria c&aelig;liaca</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">c&aelig;liaca arteria</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Arteriaca</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Arteria</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Arteriotomia</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Artificial opening of an <f type="i">Ar&shy;
terie</f>, for the Letting of Blood in an inveterate
Head-ach, Madness, Falling-sickness, Pain and
Inflamation in the Eyes and Ears. The Section
is made in the Fore-head, Temples, or behind
the Ears: the manner of it is thus, After the <f type="i">li&shy;
gatures</f> made in the Arms or Neck, the Arterie is
cut just as a Vein is, and when the blood is Emit&shy;
ted, you apply a very <f type="i">Astringent</f> Plaister, with
</page>

<page no="31">
a Leaden Plate, to the Orifice, and then swathe
it well; the Cure is performed in Seven or Nine
days time.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Arthritica</form>, <xpln lang="en">see in <f type="i">Arthritis</f>,</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en">Arthritis</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="gout(n)">or <term lang="la">Morbus articularis</term>, the <f type="i">Gout</f>,
exercises its Tyranny about two or three, or more
Joynts; and it is defined to be a pain about the
Joynts, proceeding from an <f type="i">effervescence</f> of the
Nervous <f type="i">Acid</f> Juice, with the fixed <f type="i">Saline Particles</f>
of the Blood, whence the <f type="i">Nerves</f>, <f type="i">Tendons</f>, <f type="i">Liga&shy;
ments</f>, the thin <f type="i">Membrances</f> about the Bones, are
contracted, and miserably Tormented; whence
proceeds Swellings, Redness, hard sandy <f type="i">concreti&shy;
ons</f> in several parts of the Body, and other symp&shy;
toms that accompany it. It is fourfold, <term lang="la">Chira&shy;
gia</term>, the <f type="i">Gout</f> in the Hands; <term lang="la">Ischias</term>, in or about
that Bone which is connected to the <term lang="la">Os Ilium</term>:
<term lang="la">Gonagra</term>, in the Knees; and <term lang="la">Podagra</term>, in the Feet,
almost an incurable Distemper.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Arthritis vaga</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="wandering gout(n)">a Wandering <f type="i">Gout</f>, is a Disease
in the Joynts that creates pain sometimes in one
Limb, sometimes in another. It proceeds from a
double cause. We may suppose in this Disease a 
great many heaps, as it were, of fixed Salt thrust
out from the Mass of the Blood, to be placed like
so many Nests here and there about the Limbs
and Joynts, which being treasured up in several di&shy;
stinct Cells, or Repositories, like the Spawn of Fish,
or the Seed of Women; the lower <f type="i">recrements</f> of
the Nervous Juice comes afterwards, like the Man's 
Seed, and Impregnates them; and hence from the
mutual <f type="i">Effervescence</f> of these two, the <f type="i">Membranes</f>
and <f type="i">Nervous Fibers</f> being <f type="i">vellicated</f> and contracted
cause an extraordinary quick and acute Pain. It
</page>

<page no="32">
is called <term lang="la">vaga</term>, wandring, because 'tis not con&shy;
stant to one and the same place, as the true <f type="i">Gout</f>
is.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Arthrodia</form> <xpln lang="en">is the joyning of Bones, when the
cavity that receives the Bone is in the Surface, and
the little head or top of the Bone that is received,
is depressed: as in the lower Jaw-bone, with the
Bone of the Temples.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Arthon</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="joint(n)">is a Joynt, or Connexion of Bones, pro&shy;
per for the performing of Motion. <term lang="la">Articuli</term> are
sometimes the Knuckles of the Fingers.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Anthropologia</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="anatomy(n)" lexeme="psychology(n)">is the Doctrine of Man: which
<f type="i">Batholine</f> distinguishes into two parts: <f type="i">Anato&shy;
mie</f>, which Treats of the Bodie and its Parts; and
<f type="i">Psucologie</f>, which Treats of the Soul.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Arthrosis</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Articulatio</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Articularis morbus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <f type="i">Arthritis</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Articulatio</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="closer(n)">is a Conjunction of Limbs for the
performing of Motion: and it is twofold, <term lang="la">Diar&shy;
throsis</term>, or a more loose <f type="i">Articulation</f>: and <term lang="la">Synar&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Articulus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Arthron</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Artomeli</form> <xpln lang="en">is Broth made of honey and bread.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Artus</form> <xpln lang="en">are Members growing to Cavities in 
the body, and distinguished by Joynts.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Aryt&aelig;noides</form> <xpln lang="en">are two <f type="i">Cartilages</f>, which with others
make up the top of the <f type="i">Larynx</f>; it is taken also
for certain <f type="i">Muscles</f> of the <f type="i">Larynx</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Arythmus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Pulse lost to sense.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ass</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Assis</term>, is the least piece of Money that's
Currant, and in Weight a Pound.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Asaphia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a lowness of Voice, which proceeds
from a loose or ill constitution or contemporation
of the Organs.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="33">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ascaris</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Ascarides</term>, are little worms which
breed in the <term lang="la">Intestinum rectum</term>, and then tickle
and trouble it. They are bred of some Excre&shy;
ments which stay longer than they ought, and there
putrifie.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ascites</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="dropsy(n)">is a Dropsie or swelling of the <f type="i">Abdomen</f>,
and consequently of the <term lang="la">Scrotum</term>, Thighs, and
Feet, proceeding from a Serous, and sometimes
Lymphatic or Chylous Matter, like the wash&shy;
ing of flesh, collected in the cavity of those parts.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Asef</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Hydroa</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Asema</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="crisis(n)">is a <f type="i">Crisis</f> beyond hope, happening with&shy;
out any previous indication by signs.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Asitia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a loathing of Meat.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Asodes</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Assodes</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Aspera Arteria</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Trachea</term>, is an Oblong Pipe,
consisting of various Cartilages and Membranes,
which begin at the Throat, or lower part of the
Jaws, lies upon the Gullet, descends into the
Lungs, and is dispersed by manifold Ramifications
or Branches through their whole substance: the
upper part is called <term lang="la">Larynx</term>, and the lower <term lang="la">Bron&shy;
chus</term>, to which <term lang="la">Malpighius</term> adds a third, or lowest,
called by him <term lang="la">Vesicular</term>: It is subservient to Speech
and Respiration.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Asphyxia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a pulse that is sensibly decayed.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Assodes</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="continual fever(n)">signifies a continual <f type="i">Fever</f>, wherein
the outward parts are moderately warm, but
with a great heat within, an insatiable drought,
perpetual tossing, watching, and raving.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en">Asthma</form> <xpln lang="en">is a frequent respiration, joyned with
a hissing, a sound, and a cough, especially in
the Night-time. The causes thereof are a sharp
and scorbutic blood, which too much vellicates
</page>

<page no="34">
the Organs of respiration, and puts them into a 
meer convulsive motion, whereby the Lungs are
puft up, and the Circulation of the Blood is
hindred; whence suffocations, swounds, and coughs
easily proceed.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Astragalus</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="pastern(n)">is the first and most principal Bone,
which together with other little bones in the Foot,
make up that little part of the Foot which im&shy;
mediately succeedeth the Leg in Beasts, called the
Pastern.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Astringentia</form>, <xpln lang="en">binding things, are those which with
the thickness and figure of their Particles, force
and bind together the parts of the body.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Astrologia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a reasoning about the Vertues of
the Stars; not so necessary to <f type="i">Physicians</f>, as the
Ancients imagined.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Astronomia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a naming of the Stars, or a know&shy;
ledge of the laws and rules of Stars and Constel&shy;
lations; or a knowledge concerning, or about the
Stars.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ataxia</f></form> <xpln lang="en">is a confounding of Critical Days.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Atecnia</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Agonia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Atheroma</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="tumor(n)">is a tumor contained within its own
coat, arising from a pappy humour, without pain,
not easily yielding to the Fingers, nor leaving
any dint after 'tis compressed.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Athymia</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="defection of the mind(n)" lexeme="anxiety of the mind(n)">is a Defection or Anxiety of the Mind.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Atlas</form> <xpln lang="en">is the first <f type="i">Vertebre</f> under the Head;
so called, because it seems to hold up the Head;
it wants Marrow.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Atomus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Body so small, that it is not capa&shy;
ble of being divided into lesser parts, as are the
Elementary Particles of Spirit, Salt, Sulphur, Wa&shy;
ter, and Earth.</xpln></wordentry> 
</page>

<page no="35">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Atonia</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="faintness(n)" lexeme="infirmity(n)">is a faintness, infirmity, defect of strength.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Atra Bilis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a sulphureous, and saline, earthy,
adust and black blood, which is bred in the bo&shy;
dy, and gathered in the Spleen; for there it is
volatilized, and exalted into a ferment fit to mix
with the blood.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Atretus</form> <xpln lang="en">is one whose Fundament or privy
parts are not perforated.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Atrophia</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Tabes</term>, is when the whole body, or
any one part of it is not nourished but gradually
withers and decays away. <term lang="la">Tabes</term> is often taken
only for an Ulcer in the Lungs, whereby the whole
body by little and little perishes and decays.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Atta</form>, <xpln lang="en">says <f type="i">Festus</f>, is one who by reason of the
tenderness of, or other defects in his Feet, touches
the ground, rather than treads it.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Attenuantia</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">incidentia</term>, are those things which
opening the Pores with their acute Particles, cut
the thick and viscous humours in the body.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Attonitus morbus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="apoplexy(n)" lexeme="blasting(n)">the same with an <f type="i">apoplexy</f>;
<f type="i">Celsus</f> takes it for Blasting.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Attrahentia</form>, <xpln lang="en">drawing things, are those which
opening the Pores with their little Particles, and
dilating the humours, and expelling them, where
their resistance is weaker, not onely swell the
parts, and make them red; but by driving more
vapours and humours out of the Skin and Flesh
than can make their way through a thick inner
Skin, gather them under it, and swell it into lit&shy;
tle bladders.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Auctio</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="nutrition(n)">is Nutrition, whereby more is restored
than was lost.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Auditus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="hearing(n)">Hearing, is a Sense wherein sounds
from the various trembling Motion of the <term lang="la"><f type="i">circum&shy;
</page>

<page no="36">
ambient</f></term> Air, beating the Drum of the Ear, are
communicated to the common sensory by the au&shy;
ditory Nerve, and are there felt and perceived.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Augmentum Fabricum</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">incrementum</term>, is a com&shy;
putation from what time the heat of a continual
<f type="i">Fever</f> has seised upon the whole Mass of Blood,
till it hath arrived at the height.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Aureus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a sort of Weight amongst the <f type="i">Ara&shy;
bians</f>, of a Dram, and a Seventh part; the same
with <term lang="la">Denarius</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Auricula infima</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Lobus auris</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Auricula cordis</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="ear of the heart(n)">Ear of the Heart; there are
two of them, the right and the left; the right
receives the blood from the <term lang="la">vena cava</term>, or great
Vein, which is carried into the right Ventricle,
and then enters the Lungs: the left is that which
receives the blood rightly prepared and fermen&shy;
ted by the Nitrous Air from the Lungs, that it 
may be discharged by the left Ventricle into the
great Arterie, and thence be distributed into every
part of the body.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Aurigo</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Icterus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Auris</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="ear(n)">the Ear, is the Organ of hearing,
which is either <f type="i">External</f>, whose upper part is called <term lang="la">Pin&shy;
na</term>, or <term lang="la">Ala</term>; and the under <term lang="la">Lobus</term>, the <f type="i">Lobe</f>, or <term lang="la">Au&shy;
ricula infima</term>, the lowest part of the Ear: its Ex&shy;
ternal circumference is called <term lang="la">Helix</term>; the Internal,
<term lang="la">Anthelix</term>, or <f type="i">internal</f>; in which you may consider
the Drum, the four little Bones, with the little
Muscles, the Concha, or Hollowness, the <term lang="la">Fora&shy;
men Ovale</term>, the Oval hole, the <f type="i">Labyrinth</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Automatos</form> <xpln lang="en">is that which moves of its own ac&shy;
cord, as the Motion of the Heart, the digestions
and fermentations of the bowels.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="37">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Autopyros</form> <xpln lang="en">is bread made of whole Grains, with&shy;
out any bran taken from it, or added to it. This
sort of bread is preferr'd before any other, because
the Bran is cleansing.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Auxilium</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">remedium</term>, is whatsoever is good
against a Disease by a contrary vertue; and it is
three-fold, Diet, Medicine, and Chyrurgery.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Axilla</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="arm-pit(n)">is the Arm-pit, hairy in adult people.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Axioma</form> <xpln lang="en">is a proposition built upon the Autho&shy;
rity of <f type="i">Hippocrates</f>, or <f type="i">Galen</f>; but of little validity,
now that Physick is built upon Reason and Ex&shy;
perience.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Axis</form> <xpln lang="en">is the third Vertebre from the Scull.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Axungia</form> <xpln lang="en">is the fat or tallow of an Hog.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Azoth</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="mercury(n)">sometimes signifies the Mercury of any
Metallic body, sometimes an Universal Remedy,
as 'tis thought, made of Mercury, and prepared
with Gold and Silver; a few years ago, it was
famous amongst the Vulgar, and Persons of Qua&shy;
lity too; of different colour, according to the di&shy;
versity of the preparation, which was often too 
troublesome, whence it begun to decrease both in
price and repute.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Azygos</form> <xpln lang="en">is a famous Vein about the Heart, called
<term lang="la">sine pari</term>, or <term lang="la">jugo</term>, which reaches to the Vertebres,
and proceeds from the <term lang="la">Vena Cava</term>, the great hal&shy;
low Vein.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Azymus</form> <xpln lang="en">is unleavened, unwholesome Bread.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordgroup1 type="a" object="B">B.

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">BAcilli</form>, <xpln lang="en">are called those Medicines which are of 
a long, round Figure, like a stick or Pillar.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Balan&aelig;um</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Balneum</term>, is properly a washing
</page>

<page no="38">
of the whole Body; yet it is sometimes taken for
a washing of the lower parts only, which they
commonly call <term lang="la">Nisessus</term>, and <term lang="la">semicupia</term>; and it is ei&shy;
ther <f type="i">dry</f>, or <f type="i">moist</f>; the dry are prepared of Ashes,
common Salt, Sand, filed Steel, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. the <f type="i">moist</f> are
either <f type="i">vaporous</f> or <f type="i">watery</f>. The former are made
of the boiling of Roots, Herbs, Flowers, Seeds, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.
the Vapour whereof is all that's taken. The <f type="i">wa&shy;
tery</f>, are either <f type="i">artificial</f>, which are made of Phy&shy;
sical Decoctions; or Natural, which are called 
<term lang="la">Therm&aelig;</term> Bathes, whose Waters are either Alumi&shy;
nous, Ironish, Copperish, Nitrous, Sulphureous,
Bituminous, Vitriolie, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. all which Waters are
called <term lang="la">Acidul&aelig;</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Balanus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="nut of the yard(n)" lexeme="earth-chestnut(n)">or <f type="i">glans</f>, is the Nut of the Yard, co&shy;
vered with the Fore-skin; also the Clitoris of a 
Woman. Also all Fruits and Roots that have
round Heads, as a Walnut; also an Acorn, an 
earth-Chesnut: also a Suppository.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Balneum</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Balaneum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Balsamus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="balsam(n)">or <term lang="la">balsamum</term>; the Word <f type="i">Balsame</f> is
used very differently in the Shops. 1. It signifies 
a certain sort of Perfume, of somewhat a thick
Consistence, like an Ointment; and this is its most
usual signification; as for instance, Balsame of
Roses, Apoplectic, and the like. 2. There are a
sort of Liquors distilled from Gum, and resinous
Substances, with spirit of Wine, which are anointed
outwardly, and these are called Balsams too; as
Nervous Balsame, Sciatic, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. 3. It signifies a
Liquor that is anointed into the Body, thicker than
Oyl, and more Liquid than an Ointment. 4. Salt
things funded and melted, are called Balsame, as
the Balsame of Salt of Jewels. 5. There are a 
</page>

<page no="39">
sort of particular preparations called Balsams,
as the balsam of Sulphur, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. 6. and Lastly, some
Gums of Trees are called Balsams.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Bamma</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="tincture(n)" lexeme="liquor(n)">is a Tincture, or a Liquor, wherein any
thing is tinged or moistned, as bread sopt in 
broth.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Barycoja</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="heaviness of hearing(n)">is heaviness of hearing.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Basilareos</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">basis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Basilica</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="liver vein(n)">is the inner Vein of the Arm, called

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Basilicum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a rich precious Medicine, that ex&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Basioglossum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a pair of Muscles that depress

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Basis</form> <xpln lang="en">is the upper part of the Heart, which is

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Bathmis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Cavity in the bone of the Arm

the whole hand is stretched forth and bended,
the process of the undermost and lesser of the

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Batrachus</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="tumor(n)">is a Tumor under the Tongue, which

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Bechica</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines good against a Cough.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Belenoides</form> <xpln lang="en">is the process or shooting forth of a

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Benignus morbus</form>, <xpln lang="en">a favourable disease, is that

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Bicongius</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="pint and a half(n)">is a measure which contains Twelve
</page>

<page no="40">
<term lang="la">Sextaries</term>, one of which is just our Pint and an

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Bilis</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="gall(n)">the <f type="i">gall</f>, is a Sulphureous Saline Excre&shy;
ment of the blood, separated in the Liver by means
of little Glandules, and is sent either into the lit&shy;
tle bag that contains the Gall, or into the Gut
called <term lang="la">Duodenum</term>, by the <term lang="la">Ductus Hepaticus</term>, that it
may farther promote the fermentation of the victu&shy;
als, and carry off the Dregs that are left behind
when the Chyle is separated from the whole Mass.
The Gall consists of Sulphur, Adust Salt, and a
little Serum; it is naturally yellow: preterna&shy;
turally it is of the Colour of the yolk of an
Egg, green like a Leek, rustie, and sky-coloured;
all which variety of colours proceed onely from
different degrees of Heat and Fermentation. <f type="i">Syl&shy;
vius</f> maintained, That the Bile ascended to the 
Heart by the <term lang="la">ductus hepaticus</term>; but this Opinion, as
it is neither consonant to Experience, nor Reason,
so nor to Truth neither; this excrement is not
called Bile, but when it is separated from the Blood;
and therefore the Opinion of the Ancients con&shy;
cerning this Bilious Humour, is quite out of
doors, since that Circulation of the Blood was
found out. See <term lang="la">Humores Sanguinei</term></xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Billychnion</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="natural heat(n)">is Natural Heat, which is commu&shy;
nicated to the <term lang="la">F&oelig;tus</term> from the Parents; but when
it is brought forth, the heat gradually decays, after
that the Blood and Spirits of the Child are alter&shy;
ed, fermented, and accended by nourishment and
nitrous Air. They do but babble who tell us, that
this Heat lasts for many years; for if it be Heat,
it is in continual Motion, and is therefore dispel&shy;
led as other Fires and Heats are.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="41">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Bl&aelig;sitas</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="stammering(n)">is a stammering in speech which pro&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Bl&aelig;sus</form> <xpln lang="en">is one that has an Impediment in his

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Blenna</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="snot(n)">is a thick Snot which distills through the

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Bocium</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Bronchocele</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Bolus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Medicine taken inwardly, of a con&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Bovina fames</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Bulimus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Bothor</form> <xpln lang="en">signifies Pimples in the Face, which don't

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Bronchocele</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Tumor in the top, or the mid&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Bronchotomia</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Section of the Wind-pipe, in a

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Bronchus</form> <xpln lang="en">is the middle Fistulous part of the

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Bubo</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="groin(n)">is the Groin, or place from the bending of

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Bubonocele</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="rupture(n)" lexeme="swelling(n)">is a Rupture; when the Intestines

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Bucca</form> <xpln lang="en">is the inferior lax part of the Face,

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Buccinator</form> <xpln lang="en">is the round Muscle of the Cheeks,

with various Fibers, and inseparably girt about 
with the Tunic of the Mouth. <f type="i">Casserius</f> has ob&shy;

</page>

<page no="43">
it self about the Cheek-bone, is terminated in a lit&shy;
tle slender Muscle directly opposite to that part
of the Face called <term lang="la">Bucca</term>: it arises from the up&shy;
per Jaw-bone, and is fastned in the lower, at the
Roots of the Gums. Its use is to move the Cheeks
with the Lips; and serves as a hand to the Teeth,
whilest it tosses the Meat to and fro, and throws
it upon the Teeth, that it may be more exactly 
chawed.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Buccula</form> <xpln lang="en">is the fleshy part under the Chin.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Bulimia</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Bulimus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Bulimus</form> <xpln lang="en">signifies an extraordinary Appetite, of&shy;

of the Stomach, whence the Membranous Tu&shy;
nics and Nerves being irritated, the Animal seeks

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">CAcatoria febris</form> <xpln lang="en">is an intermittent Fever, (so
called by the famous <f type="i">Sylvius de le Boe</f>) ac&shy;
companied with a violent Purging, which is some&shy;
times griping, and very painful, extreamly afflict&shy;
ing, and weakning the Patient when it comes.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chachecticus</form> <xpln lang="en">is one that has an ill Habit of Bo&shy;
dy.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cachexia</form> <xpln lang="en">is an ill Habit of Body, proceeding
from an ill disposition of the Humours of the Bo&shy;
dy; whence lingring Fevers, Consumptions, and
Dropsies are contracted: in this Disease the Face
is often pale, and discoloured, and the Body big,
and swoln: <term lang="la">Cachexia</term> taken in a large sense is op&shy;
</page>

<page no="44">
posed to <term lang="gk">&#x1F40;&#x03BD;&#x1F10;&#x03BE;&#x1F77;&#x03B1;</term>, and as a good Habit of Body is
common to all sound parts, so an ill one is pro&shy;
pagated by all the ill parts. Strictly <term lang="la">Cachexia</term>
is onely taken from an ill disposition of the Ha&shy;
bit of the Body; and <term lang="la">Euexia</term> on the contrary for
a good disposition of the Humors, or Blood, and
Body.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cacochymia</form> <xpln lang="en">is the abundance of ill Humors in
the Blood: and it is either Ulcerous, Bilious, Pi&shy;
tuitous, Melancholic, Acid, Salt, or Sharp.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cacoethes</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="malignant ulcer(n)"><term lang="la">Chironium ulcus</term>, or <term lang="la">Telephium</term>, is a Dis&shy;
ease or Ulcer beyond Cure, which is called Ma&shy;
lignant Ulcer; this happens when an Ulcer is 
callous, or sinuous, under which there sometimes
lie little putrified bones that have fallen down.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cacophonia</form> <xpln lang="en">is an ill voice, proceeding from an
ill constitution of Organs.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cacotrophia</form> <xpln lang="en">is an ill Nutriment, proceeding from 
a fault in the blood; as in a Leprosie, Ring&shy;
worms, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Caducus morbus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Epilepsia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Casarea sectio</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Hystertomotocia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Calamus Scriptorius</form> <xpln lang="en">is a certain Dilatation, about
the fourth Ventricle of the brain, which is after&shy;
wards pointed, from which shape it has its Name.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Calcaneus</form> <xpln lang="en">is the same with <term lang="la">Calx</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Calchoidea</form> <xpln lang="en">are three little bones in the Foot,

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Calcinatio</form> <xpln lang="en">is the solution of a mix'd body into

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Caldarium</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Laconicum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<page no="45">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Calculus</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="stone(n)">the Stone, is an hard pr&aelig;ternatural
concretion in a Mans body, which is often bred
in the Reins, Testicles, and other parts, from Sa&shy;
line and Earthy Particles concreted together.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Calidum innatum</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Emphitum thermum</term>, or
<term lang="la">Biolychnium</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Callicreas</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Pancreas</term>, is a conglomerated Glan&shy;
dule, placed under the hinder part of the Ventri&shy;
cle, about the length of three or four fingers in
a Man; it is clotted with a thin Membrane from
the Periton&aelig;um: it is terminated in Man near the
common Ductus, or Passage of the <f type="i">Bile</f> into the
Gut <term lang="la">duodenum</term>, and distils a volatile inspipid sort of
a juice: but <f type="i">Sylvius de le Boe</f>, and <f type="i">de Graaf</f> affirm,
That they have found an Acid and a somewhat 
Acid juice there; nay, sometimes an austere and
a sweet one; thence also they bring the Original
of all Diseases: but we must know, that this possi&shy;
bly was observed, when scarce one in twenty which
they dissected was found exactly sound. Con&shy;
cerning this question, see my <f type="i">Anat</f>. of things, <f type="i">l</f>. I.
<f type="i">c</f>. 21. Its use is, to temperate the Chyle, which 
is something Acid, and the bitterness of the Gall
with its Volatile Juice, that it may at last enter the 
Lacteals with a sweet taste.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en">Callus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a kind of swelling without pain, like 
Skin contracted by too much labour.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Calor nativus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Biolychnium</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Calva</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="skull(n)">is the Scull, also the upper hairy part
of the Head, which either by Disease, or old Age,
grows Bald first.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Calvaria</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Calva</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Calvitium</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="baldness(n)">is that Baldness which is naturally
incident to old Age.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="46">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Calx</form> <xpln lang="en">is the second Bone in that part of the Foot
which succeeds the Ancle, bigger and stronger
than the rest; oblong, and grows backward, that
a man may stand more strongly upon it, and not
fall so easily backward. <term lang="la">Calx</term> also is that which
by Calcining, is either turn'd into Alcool, as
<term lang="la">Calx Saturni</term>, or at least is made friable, as <f type="i">Harts&shy;
horn</f> burnt.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Camarium</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Fornix</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Camarosis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a blow upon the Scull, whereby
some part of the Bone is left suspended, like an
Arch.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cambium</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="nameless humour(n)" lexeme="glew(n)">is a secundary humour according to
<f type="i">Avicen</f>, which yet is reckoned amongst the Hu&shy;
mours, and its use was said to be to nourish the
parts: the first was called the <f type="i">nameless humour</f>:
the second <f type="i">Glew</f>; and the fourth, which was very
near converted into Nourishment, was called 
<term lang="la">Cambium</term>: but these figments are quite Exploded
since we found out the Circulation of the Blood,
by the Fibres.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cameratio</form> <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Camerosis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Capulum</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Contortion of the Eye-lids, or
its Hairs.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Canales</form> <xpln lang="en">are passages by which the Juices of the
Body flow: as those which serve for the Spittle,
the Bile; that in the Liver, Pancreas, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Canaliculus Arteriosus</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Vessel betwixt that
Arterious Veins of the Lungs, and the great Ar&shy;
tery in <term lang="la">F&oelig;tus's</term>; for 'tis obliterated in Adult per&shy;
sons: its use in <term lang="la">F&oelig;tus's</term>, is, that the Blood may be
discharged by this Ductus out of the Arterious
Vein, into the great Artery, because that the Blood
is not accended in their Lungs, for want of Respi&shy;
ration in the Womb.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="47>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en">Cancer</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Carcinoma</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Canina appetentia</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Cynodes orexis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Canina rabies</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Hydrophobia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Canini dentes</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Cynodontes</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Canities</form> <xpln lang="en">is a hoariness of the Head before the
usual time: it is twofold, the one is according
to the ordinary course of Nature: the other is
ill, and as <f type="i">Aristotle</f> calls it, Diseased.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Canna major</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">tibia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Canna minor</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Fibul&aelig; os</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Canthus</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">hircus</term>, is the angle or corner of the
Eye; which is either the greater or the Internal;
or the less or External.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Capreolus auris</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Helix</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Capsul&aelig; artrabilari&aelig;</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Renes succenturiati</term>, are
Glandulous Bodies placed above the Reins; their
use is to receive the Watery Substance called 
<term lang="la">Lympha</term>, into their Cavities, wherewith the Blood in
its return from the Reins being thicker, and much
destitute of Serum, may be diluted, and circulate
more fluidly.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Capsula cordis</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Pericardium</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Capsula communis</form>, <xpln lang="en">which <f type="i">Glisson</f> has observed in
the Liver, is nothing but a Membrane which pro&shy;
ceeds from the <term lang="la">Periton&aelig;um</term>, which includes both
the <term lang="la">Porus bilarius</term>, and the <term lang="la">Vena porta</term>, or great
Vein in the <f type="i">Liver</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Capsul&aelig; seminales</form> <xpln lang="en">are the Extreme Cavities of
the Vessels which convey the Seed, dilated like
little Coffers, which by two small holes emit the
Seed received from the Testicles into the little
seminary Bladders, that it may be either preserved
there against the time of Coition, or be reduced
into the Blood by the Lymphatic Vessels.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="48">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Caput mortuum</form> <xpln lang="en">is that thick dry matter which
remains after the Distillation of Minerals especi&shy;
ally: but most commonly it denotes that which
remains of Vitriol.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Caput purgium</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Errhinum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Carbo</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Anthrax</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Carbunculus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Anthrax</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Carcinodes</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="tumor(n)">is a Tumor like a <f type="i">Cancer</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Carcinoma</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="cancer(n)"><term lang="la">Carcinus</term> or <f type="i">Cancer</f>, is a Tumor that
arises from a Salino sulphureous and sharp Blood;
it is round, hard, livid, painful, at the beginning
as big as a Pea, but afterwards 'tis surrounded
with great swelling Veins, which resemble the Feet
of a Crab, though not always.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Carcinus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see in <term lang="la">Carcinoma</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cardia</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="heart(n)">is the Heart, or Principle Muscle ordain&shy;
ed for the Circulating of the Blood.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cardiaca</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="suffocation of the heart(n)" lexeme="coagulated blood(n)">is a  Suffocation of the Heart from a
Polypus, or Coagulated Blood.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cardiacum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Medicine which (as they for&shy;
merly thought) corroborates the Heart: but it 
rather onely puts the Blood into a fine gentle Fer&shy;
mentation, whereby the Spirits formerly decayed,
are repaired and invigorated, whereupon the
Blood by consequence Circulates more easily
and briskly.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cardialgia</form> <xpln lang="en">and <term lang="la">Cardiogmos</term>, is a gnawing or
contraction of the Nerve called <term lang="la">par vagum</term>, and
the Intercostal implanted in the Stomach, pro&shy;
ceeding from a pungent vellicating Matter in the
Ventricle; so that the heart being straitned and
contracted by consent with the Stomach, occasions
a swooning away.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cardiogmos</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Cardialgia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="49">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Caries</form> <xpln lang="en">is the corruption of a bone, from the
continual Afflux of vicious humors, or from their
Acrimony and Malignity; or from an occult
quality: or from a bruise that some way affects
the bone, or from sharp Medicines.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Caro</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="flesh(n)">flesh, is a similar Fibrous part, bloody,
soft, thick, together with the bones, the prop of
the body, and what covers the Spermatic parts;
and it is five-fold, <term lang="la">Musculous</term>, <term lang="la">Fistulous</term> or <term lang="la">Fibrous</term>,
as in the Muscles, and the Heart; <term lang="la">Parenchymous</term>,
as the Lungs, Liver, Spleen; <term lang="la">Viscerous</term>, as the Guts;
<f type="i">Glandulous</f>, as the <term lang="la">Pancreas</term>, the Glandules of the
Breasts, those for Spitting, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. <term lang="la">Spurious</term>, as the
Gums, Lips, the Nut of the Yard, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Caro</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="pulp(n)" lexeme="flesh(n)">also signifies that soft pappy substance of
succulent Fruits which we call the <f type="i">Pulp</f>: as the
<f type="i">Pulp</f> or Flesh of a <f type="i">Quince</f>, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Carotidis arteria</form>, <xpln lang="en">is either External or Internal,
the External which arises near the Heart, divides
it self into two branches, the outermost whereof
is variously distributed to the Jaws, the Face, the
top of the Head, and behind the Ears; but the
other, with a sort of Mechanical Preparation for 
its Reception, passes through the <term lang="la">Os cuneiforme</term>; for
Nature has dug a peculiar Channel in both sides
of it, wherein this Artery for its greater security 
is clothed with a new Adventitious and thicker
Tunic, and there representing the Figure of an
S. it goes double out of its Channel of bone, puts
off its borrowed Coat, and tends toward the 
Brain, with its charge of Blood; ascending there&shy;
fore about the Ocular Nerve, it spreads it self
towards the sides, than to the foremost part of
the Brain betwixt the passage of the Olfactory
</page>

<page no="50">
Nerves: Lastly, it tends backward, and taking
leave of the Brain near the <term lang="la">Medulla Oblongata</term>, and
the Spinal Marrow, waters it with its blood, as
far down as the <term lang="la">Os Sacrum</term>. They formerly cal&shy;
led this the <f type="i">Vertebral</f> or <f type="i">Internal Arterie</f>, because
they thought it ascended and joyned with the 
<f type="i">Carotidal</f> in the Brain; which yet is otherwise
found by Experience, according to the acurate
Dr. <f type="i">Willis</f>; they are called <term lang="la">Soporales</term>, or <term lang="la">Carotides</term>;
in as much as if they be tied, they immediately in&shy;
cline the person to sleep: but the Ancients mistook 
when they ascribed Natural Sleep to them.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Carpia</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="tent(n)">is a Tent that is put into a Wound or
Ulcer, to cleanse it.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Carus</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="sleep(n)">is a Sleep, wherein the person affected
being pulled, pinched, and called, scarce shews
any sign of either hearing or feeling; it is with&shy;
out a Feaver, greater than a Lethargy, and less
than an Apoplexy. It proceeds from an obstructi&shy;
on, or compression of the Pores and Passages
which go towards the middle of the Brain, and
are placed at least in the utmost Extremity of
the <term lang="la">Corpus Callosum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Carpus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="wrist(n)">commonly <term lang="la">Brachiale</term>, the first part of
the Palm of the Hand. <f type="i">Hesichius</f> calls it that
part of the Arm which is betwixt the lowermost
part of the Cubit, and the Hand, the Wrist:
it consists of Eight small bones, with which the 
Cubit is joyned to the hand.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cartilago</form> <xpln lang="en">is a white part, dryer and harder
than a Ligament, and softer than a Bone; it is
said to be Similar and Spermatic, but falsly; for
'tis no more made of Seed, than any other parts;
it renders Articulation more easie, and defends
</page>

<page no="51">
several parts from injuries from abroad.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Caruncul&aelig; Myrtiformes</form>, <xpln lang="en">are the wrinklings of
the Orifice of a Woman's Vagina, or Membra&shy;
nous inequalities, not to be reckoned in any cer&shy;
tain number, which in Women with Child and
after Child birth are so obliterated, that they are
altogether imperceptible, there are for the most
part four of them.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Caruncul&aelig; oculi</form>, <xpln lang="en">are Glandules placed at each
greater corner of the Eye, which separate Moisture
for moistning the Eyes, the same with Tears, which
afterwards by the <term lang="la">Puncta Lachrymalia</term>, placed in
the bone of the Nose, are discharged into the No&shy;
strils.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Caruncul&aelig; papillares</form> <xpln lang="en">are Ten little Bodies that
are in the Reins: they are properly little bundles
which arise from the centring together of a great
many small Channels, which the Reins are in a
great measure made up of; and these receive the
Serum from the little <term lang="la">ductuses</term>, and convey it into
the <term lang="la">Pelvis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Casus Uvul&aelig;</form>, <xpln lang="en">see in <term lang="la">Cion</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cataclida</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="first rib(n)">is the first Rib, called the <term lang="la">Subclavian</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Catagma</form> <xpln lang="en">is the breaking of bones, or a separati&shy;
on of the <term lang="la">Continuum</term> in the hard parts of the bo&shy;
dy; which is effected with some hard Instrument
forcibly impressed upon the part; whose differen&shy;
ces are taken from the Form, the Part, and seve&shy;
ral accidents.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Catalepsis</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Catochus</term> is an abolition of all the
Animal Functions, wherein the Respiration re&shy;
mains entire, and the Patient preserves the same
habit of body that he had before he fell sick: the
cause of it seems to consist in the Obstruction or
</page>

<page no="52">
Angustation of the <term lang="la">Corpus striatum</term> in those Pores
by which Objects are Represented in the brain,
so that there's no perception of any Object; but the
Pores, by which the Animal Spirits are Conveyed
from the Brain to the Organs of Sense, are left free
and open.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Catalotica</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Cicatrizantia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Catamenia</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="woman's courses(n)">are Womens Courses, which gather&shy;
ing every Month by the Fermentation of the blood,
and being come to a Turgency by the Accession
of a Ferment that is in the Womb, discharge them&shy;
selves at their set-time; others say, they proceed
from Seed bred in the Testicles, and communi&shy;
cated to the blood. Some ascribe the Courses to
the motions of the Moon; but if this were true,
then all Women would have them at the same
time. They begin at Twelve, Thirteen, or Four&shy;
teen Years of age, and stop about Fifty; but this
cannot be exactly determined: they are supprest
in breeding-Women, and Nurses; yet this is not a
rule neither.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Catapasma</form> <xpln lang="en">is Fragrant Powder, which by rea&shy;
son of its Scent is strewed amongst clothes: also a
fragrant Powder, which after anointing is appli&shy;
ed to the Stomach or Heart.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cataphora</form> <xpln lang="en">is the same with <term lang="la">Coma</term>; they only
differ in this, that <term lang="la">Cataphora</term> is taken as the ge&shy;
nus to all sorts of Stupors that are not attended
with a Fever.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cataplasma</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Topical Medicine of the con&shy;
sistence of a Pultise; it is usually prescribed two
ways, either boiled, or without it; the former is
more frequent, the latter of more efficacy. In
the former, they are to take such Vegetables as are
</page>

<page no="53">
proper, as Roots, Herbs, Seeds, Flowers, Fruits,
<term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. adding proper Meals, or omitting them;
all which are boiled up in a convenient quantity
of Liquor, <term lang="la">v.g.</term> Water, Beer, Milk, Honey, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.
to the consistence of a Pultise: the latter is prepa&shy;
red commonly of Vegetables shred small with the
Infusion of so much Liquor onely as may make
it of the former consistence. You may add
here Meal, crumbs of Bread, Oyles, Oyntments,
as in the former sort of Cataplasms too.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Catapotium</form>, <xpln lang="en">commonly <term lang="la">Pillula</term>, is a Medicine
given inwardly, Purging Pills.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cataptosis</form> <xpln lang="en">is one Symptome of an Epilepsie;
when Men fall suddenly to the Ground.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cataracta</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="suffusion(n)" lexeme="cataract(n)">is Two-fold, either <f type="i">beginning</f>, or a
<f type="i">suffusion</f> onely, or <f type="i">confirmed</f>, or a Cataract proper&shy;
ly so called; the <f type="i">incipient</f> is but a suffusion of
the Eye, when little Clouds, Motes, and Flies seem
to flie before the Eyes; but the confirmed <f type="i">Cata&shy;
ract</f>, is when the Pupil of the Eye is either wholly or
in part covered and shut up with a little thin Skin;
so that the Sun-beams have not due admittance
to the Eye. Confirmed <f type="i">Cataracts</f> are cured with
thrusting a Needle through the <term lang="la">Albugineous</term> and
the hornie <f type="i">Membrane</f> as far as the <f type="i">Cataract</f>, which
is to be depressed with the Needle, and if it start
back to be broken, then the Eye is to be tied up
with Water of Roses, the white of an Egg, and
Alumn, all shaken together.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Catarrhopus</form> <xpln lang="en">is when Humours, Vapours, or
Wind, go downward.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Catasarca</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Anasarcha</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cataschesis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a good state of Body, opposite to
an Hectic.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="54">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Catastasis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a disposition of Humane Body, or
of time.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Catatasis</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Extension of the Body towards
the lower parts.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Catheretica</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines that take away su&shy;
perfluities.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Catharma</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Catharcticum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Catharrhus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Defluction of Humours from the
Head towards the parts under it, as the Nostrils,
the Mouth, Lungs, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Catharsis</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Catharcticum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Catharticum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a purging Medicine, which clean&shy;
ses the Stomach, the Guts, and whatsoever is vi&shy;
tious and <f type="i">heterogeneous</f> in the Blood, and throws
it into the Common-shore of the Guts. See <term lang="la">Pur&shy;
gatio & Vomitorium</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cathemerina</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Quotidiana Febris</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en">Catheter</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Fistulous Instrument which is thrust
up the Yard into the Bladder, to provoke Urine
when it is suppressed by the Stone; or into whose
cavity an Instrument called <term lang="la">Itinerarium</term> is thrust
to find out the Stone in the Bladder, that then the
<term lang="la">Sphincter</term> of the Bladder may be shown, and an
Incision be made in the <term lang="la">Perin&aelig;um</term>, <term lang="la">i.e.</term> betwixt the
Fundament and the Privities.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cathetetrismus</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Administration or Opera&shy;
tion of Injecting any thing into the Bladder by a 
<term lang="la">Catheter</term>, or a <term lang="la">Siringe</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Catholicum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a common Medicine that expels
all ill Humours; which is kept in the shops.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="gk">&#x039A;&#x03AC;&#x03C4;&#x03B1; <term lang="la">purgare</term></form>, <xpln lang="en">to Purge downwards.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Catoche</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Catalepsis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Catochus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Catalepsis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Catopsis</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Myopia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="55">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Catoretica</form> <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Purgantia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cavitates</form> <xpln lang="en">are the greatest Cavities in the Body,
wherein some Principal part is contained, as the
Brain in the Head; in the Chest, the Lungs,
Heart, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. in the <f type="i">Abdomen</f>, the Liver, Spleen,
Reins, Stomach, Intestines, Bladder, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. and they
are three, the Head, the Chest, the Belly.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cavitates minores</form> <xpln lang="en">are the Ventricles of the Heart
and Brain, of which in their proper place.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cauledon</form> <xpln lang="en">is the breaking of the bones a cross,
when the parts of the bones are so separated
that they will not lay direct.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Causodes</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Causus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Caustica</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Escharotica</term> are those things which
burn the Skin and Flesh into an hard crust, as
burnt Brass, unquenched Lime, sublimated Mer&shy;
cury, and hot Iron, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Causus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="burning fever(n)">or a burning Fever, is that which is at&shy;
tended with a greater heat than other continued
Fevers, an intolerable thirst, and other Symptoms
which argue an extraordinary accension of the
blood: and that which formerly discriminates it
from other putrid Fevers, is, that the temper of 
the blood is hotter, <term lang="la">i.e.</term> abounds more with com&shy;
bustible Sulphur; and therefore when it begins
to boyl, is accended in a greater measure, and
in its deflagration diffuses Particles of most Intense 
Heat through the whole body; its Motion is
acute, it comes presently to its height, is accom&shy;
panied with dreadful Symptoms, has a very diffi&shy;
cult Crisis, and a dangerous Event?</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cauterium</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Chyrurgeons Instrument, made
of Iron, Silver, or Gold, which after 'tis healed,
has an actual power of burning into any thing;
</page>

<page no="56">
they differ in Bulk, and in Form; it is sometimes
taken for a <f type="i">potential cauterie</f>, prepared of <term lang="la">Lixi&shy;
viums</term>, or Lime and Sope.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cedmata</form> <xpln lang="en">are defluxions upon the Joynts, espe&shy;
cially the Hip.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cele</form> <xpln lang="en">is a tumor in any part.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cellul&aelig; intestini coli</form>, <xpln lang="en">the little Cavities of the
Gut <term lang="la">Colon</term>, are where the Excrements lodge some
while, that they may refresh some adjacent parts
with their Heat, and digest and ferment any oc&shy;
curring crudities.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cementium</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Powder by whose means <f type="i">Cemen&shy;
tatory Calcination</f> is performed: or as others say,
it is an acute piercing Mineral Matter, where&shy;
with Metals being strewed are Reverberated to
cement, and it is either simple or mixt; and ei&shy;
ther in form of a Powder, or a <f type="i">Confection</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cenchrias</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="wildfire(n)">is a sort of spreading Inflamation which
we call Wild-fire, called <term lang="la">Herpes Miliaris</term> from the
resemblance it bears to the Seed of the small Grain
called <f type="i">Millet</f> or <f type="i">Hyrse</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ceneangia</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Evacuation of the Vessels, by
opening a Vein. 1. It is expedient in a <term lang="la">Plethora</term>,
to free Nature from too great a load. 2. 'Tis 
expedient to draw back the blood when it rushes
too plentifully towards any one part. 3. To di&shy;
vert the blood from one part to another, though 
it be no way lodg'd there, nor be Extravasated.
4. To Ventilate and Cool the Blood in Burning
and in Putrid Fevers.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Centrum</form> <xpln lang="en">is the middle of a Body not taken
Mathematically, but Physically, and that they say
is the Heart; from which, as from a Center, the
blood continually Circulates round the most di&shy;
stant parts of the body.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="57">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cephal&aelig;a</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="headache(n)">is an obstinate Head-ach.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cephalalgia</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="headache(n)">is an Head ach that proceeds from
Intemperance, or ill Confirmation of the Parts.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cephalartica</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines which purge the
Head.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cephalica</form> <xpln lang="en">are Spirituous and Volatile Medicines
used in the Distempers of the Head. Also the
outermost Vein in the Arm is called <term lang="la">Cephalica</term>,
because it uses to be opened in Diseases of the
