Head.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cephalopharyng&aelig;i</form> <xpln lang="en">signifies the first pair of <f type="i">Muscles</f>
of the upper part of the Gullet, which proceed
from beside the Head and Neck, and are spread
more largely upon the <f type="i">Tunic</f> of the Gullet.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cephalophonia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a pain or heaviness in the
Head.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cer&aelig;a</form> <xpln lang="en">are the Horns of the Womb in Bruits,
wherein Generation is performed.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ceratium</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Siliqua</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ceratoglossum</form> <xpln lang="en">is the proper pair of <f type="i">Muscles</f> be&shy;
longing to the Tongue, proceeding from the
horns of the Bone called <term lang="la">Hyoides</term>, and joyned
to the sides of the Tongue; their use is to move
the Tongue straight downwards towards the in&shy;
ward parts, when they act joyntly: but if either
the one or the other be contracted singly, they 
move it to the right or left side.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ceratodes</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Cornea Tunica</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ceratomalagma</form> <xpln lang="en">is a softening Composition, pre&shy;
pared of Wax, and other ingredients.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ceratum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Medicine applyed outwardly,
made of Wax, Oils, and sometimes Dust mixed
thicker than an Ointment, and softer than a Plai&shy;
ster.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="58">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cerchnos</form> <xpln lang="en">is a certain <f type="i">Asperity</f> of the <term lang="la">Larynx</term>, which
is felt as it were like so many <f type="i">Juniper-berries</f>,
whence proceeds a little dry Cough.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cercis</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Second Bone of the Cubit, called
<term lang="la">Radius</term>, because it is like the spoke of a Wheel.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cerea</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Achor</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cerebellum</form> <xpln lang="en">is the hinder part of the Brain, con&shy;
sisting, like the Brain it self, of an Ashie or Barkie
Substance, and a white Marrowie Substance,
wherein the Animal Spirits which perform Invo&shy;
luntary and meer Natural Actions, are Generated.
In Man, but not so in Beasts, it seems to consist
of a great many thin Plates that lay upon one
another.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cerebrum</form>, <xpln lang="en">the Brain, is strictly taken for the
foremost part of the Substance which is within the
Skull; and it is a Substance of a peculiar sort to
it self; outwardly it is covered with the Skin cal&shy;
led <term lang="la">Pia Mater</term>; it is wrought with many turnings
and windings, its Exterior Substance is Ashie,
wherein the Animal Spirits are Generated: the 
Interiour is white, which receives the Animal
Spirits from the former, and discharges them by
the <term lang="la">Corpus Callosum</term>, and the <term lang="la">Medulla Oblongata</term>
into the Nerves; upon which voluntary actions
do chiefly depend. Likewise the Brain is the sub&shy;
ject of Imagination, Judgment, Memory, and Re&shy;
miniscence; for the <f type="i">Id&aelig;a's</f> or Species of things
being received from the Organs of the External
Senses, are carried to the common <f type="i">Sensory</f>, or the
beginning of the <f type="i">Oblong</f>-marrow, and then by the
<term lang="la">Corpora striata</term>, and the <term lang="la">Corpus callosum</term>, there the
judgement and imagination are formed; but the
Seat of the Memory is said to be in the Ashie
</page>

<page no="59">
Barkie Substance; and if the <f type="i">Idea's</f> after some time
chance to be called for out of the place of the
Memory, then it is properly said to be <f type="i">Reminiscence</f>,
or Remembring; Sleep is likewise transacted in the
Brain; concerning which, see in its proper place.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cerel&aelig;um</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Ointment made of Wax and
Oyl.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cerevisia medicata</form>, <xpln lang="en">Physick-Drink, is wherein
Medicines, proper for any Diseases, have been
infused.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ceria</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Favus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cerio</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Favus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cerotum</form> <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Ceratum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cerumina</form> <xpln lang="en">are the filth of the Ear, which seems
to be sweat out from the <f type="i">Cartilages</f>: others think
it comes from the <f type="i">Glandules</f> which border upon
the Ears; it consists of abundance of salt and
adult Sulphur, which gives it its bitterness: it is
good to hinder Dust, Motes, or little Animals from
getting into the Ear.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chalastica</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines of a moistning Quali&shy;
ty, which Relax the parts that are too hard bound
up.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chalazia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a little swelling in the Eye-lids,
like a Hail-stone.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chalaz&aelig;</form>, <xpln lang="en">every Egg has two of them, one in
the Obtuse, and the other in the Acute end:
there's more of them in the White; yea they 
stick closer to the Yolk, and are fastned to its
Membrane. They are something long bodies,
more Concrete than the White, and whiter; knot&shy;
ty, have some sort of Light, as Hail, whence
they have their name: for each <term lang="la">Chalaza</term> consists
as it were of so many Hail-stones separated from
</page>

<page no="60">
each other by that White: one of them is bigger
than the other, and farther from the Yolk; is ex&shy;
tended towards the Obtuse-end of the Egg: the
other is less, and extends it self from the Yolk
towards the Acute-end of the Egg. The greater
is made up of two or three Knots like so many
Hail-stones, which are moderately distant from
each other, the less, in order succeeds the grea&shy;
ter. It is also a Disease incident to Swine.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chalinos</form>, <xpln lang="en"><f type="i">Aurelian</f> says it is the Ultimate An&shy;
gle, and joyning of the Mouth, or that part of
the Cheeks which adjoyns upon the Lips.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="character(n)">Character</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Mystical Sign or Figure, which
signifies or denotes something amongst Chymists.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Charta Virginia</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Amnios</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cheimetlon</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Pernio</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cheironium</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Cacoethes</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chemia</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Chimia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chemosis</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Tumor of the <f type="i">Albuginious Tunic</f>,
that makes the black of the Eye appear Concave.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chimetlon</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Pernio</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chiragra</form> <xpln lang="en">is a sort of <f type="i">Gout</f> in the Hands, arising
from the Effervescence of <f type="i">Acid Particles</f>, and fixt
Salt.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chiromantia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Divination from inspecting the
hand, when men Predict futurities from the Linea&shy;
ments thereof, not at all necessary to a Physitian,
since it is rather a Diaboloical and deceitful art.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chirones</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Sirones</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chyronia</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="ulcer(n)">is a great Ulcer, and of difficult Cure.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chyrurgia</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="surgery(n)">Chirurgery, is an Art, wherein by
the help of our Hands or Instruments we endea&shy;
vour to Cure Diseases. Or, it is a part of the Art
<f type="i">Theraputic</f>, wherein Diseases are Cured by Inci&shy;
</page>

<page no="61">
sion, Burning, and Setting Joynts. Or, it is a <f type="i">Sci&shy;
ence</f> which teaches the manner and way of Ope&shy;
ration upon Living Human Bodies; and it is five&shy;
fold; tho others chuse rather to divide it into
Four Parts. 1. <f type="i">Synthesis</f>, a setting together of
things separate. 2. <term lang="la">Di&aelig;resis</term>, a separating of things
that were continued before. 3. <term lang="la">Diorthosis</term>, a cor&shy;
recting of things squeezed together and contor&shy;
ted. 4. <term lang="la">Exeresis</term>, a taking away of Superfluities.
5. <term lang="la">Anaplerosis</term>, a Restoring of that which was De&shy;
ficient.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chirurgus</form>, <xpln lang="en">one skilful in this art of Chirur&shy;
gery.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chlorosis</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Morbus virgineus</term> commonly <term lang="la">Icterus
albus</term>, seems to be a kind of Phlegmatick Pitui&shy;
tous Dropsie, arising from an obstruction of the
Courses, want of Fermentation in the Blood, and
a Detention or Depravation of the Ferment in the 
Womb; whereupon the Muscular <f type="i">Fibres</f> being
obstructed, they become lazie, and unfit for Acti&shy;
on.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Choana</form> <xpln lang="en">is a sort of Cavity or Tunnel in the
<f type="i">Basis</f> of the Brain, by which the serous Excre&shy;
ments are brought down from the Ventricles of
the Brain to the <f type="i">Pituitary Glandul&aelig;</f>: also the <term lang="la">Pel&shy;
vis</term> of the Reins, of which in its proper Place.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Choenicis</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">modiolus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Choenix</form> <xpln lang="en">is a sort of Measure containing two
<term lang="la">Sextaries</term>, which is Three Pints of our Measure.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Choeras</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Scrophula</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cholagoga</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines which purge Sulphu&shy;
reous and Bilious Humors; as <f type="i">Rhubarb</f>, <f type="i">Senna</f>, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Choledochus</form> <xpln lang="en">is the <term lang="la">Ductus bilarius</term>, or passage of
the <f type="i">Bile</f>, called <f type="i">Common</f>, wherein the <f type="i">Bile</f> from
</page>

<page no="62">
the Bladder that contains it, and the <term lang="la">Ductus</term> in the
Liver, is carried on to the Gut called <term lang="la">Duodenum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cholera</form> <xpln lang="en">is a depraved motion of the Ventricle
and the Guts, whereby the <f type="i">Bilious</f> Excrements
are discharged in great plenty upwards and down&shy;
wards: the cause of it consists sometimes in the
very <f type="i">Acrimonie</f> of the Gall, which meets and fer&shy;
ments highly with the juice of the <term lang="la">Pancreas</term>, as
sharp and <f type="i">Acid</f> as it self.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chondros</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Cartilago</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chondrosyndesmus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a <f type="i">Cartilaginous Ligament</f>,
or the joyning of Bones by the <f type="i">intervention</f> of a 
<f type="i">Cartilage</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chorda</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="tendon(n)" lexeme="nerve(n)" lexeme="gut(n)">the same that a Tendon, Nerve, or Gut,
of which in their proper place.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chordapsus</form>, <xpln lang="en">so <f type="i">Celsus</f> calls it, barbarously call'd
<term lang="la">Miserere mei</term>, by others <term lang="la">Illiaca passio</term>; by others,
<term lang="la">Volvulus</term>, commonly <term lang="la">Ileus</term>, and it is an Ejection
of the Excrements at the Mouth only, procee&shy;
ding from an Obstruction of Excrements, from 
Wind, Inflammation, or Contortion, or Convulsi&shy;
on of the Guts; when the upper part of the <f type="i">In&shy;
testines</f> are twisted with the lower; or on the con&shy;
trary, whereupon the <f type="i">Peristaltic</f> or <f type="i">Vermicular</f> Mo&shy;
tion of the Guts, whereby the Excrements are
Excluded, becomes Inverted.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chorea sancti Viti</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="madness(n)">is a sort of  Madness, which
formerly was very common amongst some Peo&shy;
ple, wherein the persons affected lay'd not down, 
but ran hither and thither dancing to the last gasp
if they were not forcibly hindred. <f type="i">Horstius</f> says,
<f type="i">That he hath spoke with some Women, who paying
an yearly visit to the Chappel of Saint</f> Vitus, <f type="i">which
is near the City</f> Ulme <f type="i">in</f> Sweedland, <f type="i">have been ta&shy;</f>
</page>

<page no="63">
<f type="i">ken with such a violent fit of Dancing Night and
Day, together with a sort of Frantickness in the Mind,
that they fall together like so many people in Extasies:
and are sensible of little or nothing for a Year toge&shy;
ther, till next</f> May <f type="i">about which time they perceive
themselves so tormented with a restlessness in their
Limbs, that they are forced to repair to the same
place again about the Feast of Saint</f> Vitus, <f type="i">to Dance.</f></xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chorion</form> <xpln lang="en">is the outward <f type="i">Membrane</f>, which with
the rest of the <f type="i">Membranes</f> and Humours, con&shy;
tain the <term lang="la">F&oelig;tus</term> in the Womb. It is of an Orbicu&shy;
lar Figure in Women, and its upper part is an&shy;
nexed to the <term lang="la">Placenta</term>, where it adheres to the
Womb.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Choroides</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="apple of the eye(n)">is the folding of the <f type="i">Carotidal Arterie</f>
in the Brain, wherein is the <term lang="la">Glandula Pincalis</term>. It
is also the <term lang="la">Uvea Tunica</term>, which  makes the Apple of
the Eye.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chromatismus</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Natural Colour and Tin&shy;
cture; for Example, of Urines, Spittle, Blood, or
Excrements.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chronicus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a daily inveterate Distemper, that
has continued above forty days, and a Quartane
Fever, a Consumption, an Asthma, Dropsie, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chronius</form> <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Chronicus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chrysoceraunius pulvis</form>, <xpln lang="en">is <term lang="la">Aurum fulminans</term>, which
is prepared of Gold, dissolved in a <term lang="la">Menstruum</term>, im&shy;
pregnated with Armoniac Salt, infused in Oyl of
<f type="i">Tartar</f>; the <term lang="la">Calx</term> is precipitated to the bottom,
which is sweetned and dryed for use.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a measure that contains four <f type="i">Sextaries</f>,
or two <term lang="la">Ch&oelig;nices</term>, in our Measure six Pints.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chylificatio</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Natural Action which makes
<f type="i">Chyle</f>.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="64">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chylosis</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Chylificatio</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chylus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="chyle(n)">Chyle, is a white Juice in the <f type="i">Ventricle</f>
and <f type="i">Intestines</f>, proceeding from a light Dissolution
and Fermentation of Victuals, especially of their
Sulphur and Salt, with which Edible things abound,
and which by the Intervention of the <f type="i">Acid</f> Hu&shy;
mour in the <f type="i">Ventricle</f>, becomes white: for if you
pour an <f type="i">Acid</f> upon any Liquor that is impreg&shy;
nated with Sulphur and Volatile Salt, it presently
turns Milkie; as is obvious in preparing Milk
of Sulphur, or the resinous Extracts of Vegeta&shy;
bles. Nay, <f type="i">Spirit</f> of <f type="i">Harts-horn</f>, and of <f type="i">Soot</f>, aboun&shy;
ding with Volatile Salt, if it be Mixt with an
<f type="i">Acid</f> or but with plain Water, grows to be of a
Milkie Colour; at last the <f type="i">Chyle</f> after a Com&shy;
mixion and Fermentation with the <f type="i">Gall</f>, and the
<f type="i">Pancreatic Juice</f>, either <f type="i">Volatile</f>, or <f type="i">Acid</f>, passing
the <f type="i">Lacteal</f> Veins, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. is mixed with the Blood.
It is called in <f type="i">Latin</f> also <term lang="la">Chymus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chymerlon</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Pernio</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chymia</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Chemia</term> is a Resolution of <f type="i">Subluna&shy;
ry Bodies</f> into their Elements; and again, a <f type="i">Co&shy;
agulation</f> of the same Elements into the Bodies
which they constituted before, in order to the
preparation of Medicines more grateful, more 
healthful, and more safe; there are two parts of it;
<f type="i">Solution</f> and <f type="i">Coagulation</f>: by the addition of the <f type="i">Ar&shy;
abic</f> Article 'tis call'd <term lang="la">Alchymia</term>, or <term lang="la">Alkymia</term>; it is cal&shy;
led also <term lang="la">Spagiria</term>, <term lang="la">Hermetica ars</term>, <term lang="la">ars perfecti Magiste&shy;
rii</term>, <term lang="la">ars Segregatoria</term>, <term lang="la">Seperatoria</term>, and <term lang="la">Destillatoria</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chymica</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Chymicalia</term>, are Medicines which the
<f type="i">Chymists</f> prepare, that they may be taken in a less
or more grateful quantity.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chymicus</form> <xpln lang="en">is one skilful in the Art of Dissolv&shy;
</page>

<page no="65">
ng and Coagulating one skilful in Chymistry.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chymosis</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Chemosis</term>, is a Distortion of the Eye&shy;
lids, by an  Inflamation: also an inflamation
of the <term lang="la">Tunica Cornea</term> in the Eye.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Chymus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Chylus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cicatrisantia</form> <xpln lang="en">are such things as by drying, bind&shy;
ing, and contracting, fill up <f type="i">Ulcers</f> with Flesh,
and cover them with a skin.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cicatrix</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="scar(n)"><term lang="la">Cicatrices</term>, Scars, are Marks which are
left after great Wounds or Ulcers: some are sim&shy;
ple, others accompanied with a Cavitie, Diminu&shy;
tion, or Excrescence in the part Affected.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cilia</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="eyebrows(n)">and <term lang="la">Supercilia</term>, are the Eye-brows, hard
Cartilaginous Bodies; but <term lang="la">Supercilia</term> properly the
hair upon the Eye-brows, at the Extremity of the
Forehead; they are like two hairy Bulwarks or
Ramparts to the Eyes, to defend them from the
sudden Incurse of any thing from the Head or
otherwise.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cion, Columella, Gargareon, Gurgulio, uva, uvula,
uvigena, uvigera, epiglottis, sublinguium</form>, <xpln lang="en">is the co&shy;
ver of the Wind-pipe; it hangs betwixt the two
<f type="i">Glandules</f>, called <term lang="la">Amygdal&aelig;</term>, above the Chink of the
<term lang="la">Larynx</term>, and is a Process from a Substance, as one
would think, Glandulous, Sponge, and Red;
which <f type="i">Columbus</f> is of opinion, arises from the <f type="i">Tu&shy;
nic</f> of the Mouth redoubled in that place. But
<f type="i">Riolan</f> says, it proceeds from some <f type="i">Muscles</f> which
are terminated there; it is of a Figure roundly
Oblong, in the upper part thicker, and ending
Obtusely in an Acute. Its use is to attemperate
the coldness of the Air, and to hinder the Drink
from falling upon the Nostrils: sometimes this
<term lang="la">Uvula</term> sticks out too far from the Humours that 
</page>

<page no="66">
fall upon it, which cannot return by the <f type="i">Lympha&shy;
tic</f> Vessels, whence proceeds the falling of the
<term lang="la">Uvula</term>, which we call Roof of the Mouth.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cionis</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Cion</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Circuitus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Periodus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Circulatio sanguinis</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">periodus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Circulatio Chymica</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Exaltation of pure
Liquor, by a Circular Distillation in an Instrument
called a <f type="i">Pelicane</f>, or a blind <f type="i">Alymbic</f>, by the virtue
of Heat.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Circulatorium</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Glass Vessel, wherein the Li&shy;
quor infused by its Ascending and Descending,
rowls about as it were in a Circle: there are se&shy;
veral sorts of these Vessels, but two especially of
moment and use, that called <term lang="la">Pelicanus</term>, and the
other <term lang="la">Diota</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Circulus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a round Instrument, made of Iron,
for the cutting of Glass; which is performed thus:
The Instrument being heated, is applyed to the
Glass, and is there continued till it grow hot, then
with a drop of cold water, or a cold blast upon
it, it flies into pieces.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cirsocele</form> <xpln lang="en">is a swelling of the preparing Vessels
about the Testicles, so that they sometimes look
like a Third Testicle.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cirsos</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Varix</term>, is a Dilatation and swelling of
the Veins, crooked or winding, and arising in
one or more parts of the Body, insomuch that the
Veins threaten a Rupture.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Citta</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Pica</term>, is a depraved Appetite, when peo&shy;
ple long for those things which are not fit to be,
nor are ever eat, as Lime, Coles, Shells, Cloth,
Hides, Sand, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. that cause lies in the Deprava&shy;
tion of the ferment of the <f type="i">Ventricle</f>.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="67">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Claretum</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="hypocras wine(n)">is an Aromatic Wine, impregnated
with an Infusion, and sweetned with Sugar, it is 
otherwise called, <term lang="la">Vinum Hypocraticum</term>, Hypocras
Wine: also a medicated Wine. It is so called,
because it is percolated and purified by a Wine&shy;
sack through which it is drained from its dregs, 
called <term lang="la">Manica Hippocratis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Clarificatio</form> <xpln lang="en">is when Juices or thick Decoctions
become clearer and finer: which is done three 
ways, by subsiding Fermentation, or the additi&shy;
on of Vinegar, white of an Egg, or Milk.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Clavicu&aelig;</form> <xpln lang="en">are two little Bones which close the
Chest of a Man, fastening the Shoulder-bone like a 
Key, with the Breast bone, that pat where the
Ribs joyn together: they are otherwise called,
<term lang="la">Ligul&aelig;</term>, or <term lang="la">Furcale</term>, <term lang="la">Furcala Superior</term>, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. they are
placed transverse under the very bottom of the
Neck, in the top of the Breast, on each side one.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Clavus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Helos</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Clavus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="wimble(n)">according to <term lang="la">Tornamira</term>, is a pain in a small
part of the Head, commonly above the Eye in the
Eye-brow, and seems as if that part of the Head
were bored through with a little Auger, or Wimble.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cleidion</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Clavicula</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Clitoris</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="prepuce(n)">is a part in a Woman, resembling the
Yard of a Woman, whose use is Titillation; it
consists, like a Mans Yard, of two Nervous Bodies,
which arise from the lower part of the bones of
the Privities, and at the end is covered with a Nut,
and a Prepuce, or fore-skin; its substance is spun&shy;
gie, so that it is capable of Increase and Relaxati&shy;
on, but is not perforated as in Men.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Clydon</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Fluctuation in the Ventricle.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Clysma</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <f type="i">Clyster</f>.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="68">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en">Clyster, and <term lang="la">Clysterium</term>, or <term lang="la">Enema</term>,</form> <xpln lang="en">is a fluid Me&shy;
dicine given inwardly, injected into the Bowels by
the Fundament; some <f type="i">Clysters</f> are softening and
loosning, others scouring, others astringent, others
which ease pain, and others for other uses. <f type="i">Cly&shy;
ster</f> is sometimes taken in a larger sence, for <term lang="la">Me&shy;
henchyta</term>, <term lang="la">Otenchyta</term>, <term lang="la">Ritenchyta</term>, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. which see in
their proper places.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cnismus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Pruritus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Coccyx</form>, <xpln lang="en">the last Portion of the Back, is made
up of three little Bones, sometimes four, which
are under the <term lang="la">Os Sacrum</term>, and serve for easier sit&shy;
ting.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cochlea</form> <xpln lang="en">is the cavity of the inner part of the
Ear, so called from its windings and turnings, for
it has three or four Rings which mutually succeed
one another; it is girt about with a very soft and
thin <f type="i">Membrane</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Coctio</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="concoction(n)" lexeme="digestion(n)" lexeme="coction(n)" lexeme="boiling(n)">Concoction or Digestion, is the fermen&shy;
tation of the smallest <f type="i">Particles</f> which our Nourish&shy;
ment consists of, that they may be made fit and
proper for the nourishment and increase of a
Living Body. The <f type="i">first</f> Concoction is made in
the Stomach by a Ferment which partly remains
there, from the reliques of the former Meat, and
partly flows thither from the <f type="i">C&aelig;liac Arteries</f>. The
<f type="i">second</f> is made in the Guts by the Gall and <f type="i">Pan&shy;
creatick</f> juice. The <f type="i">third</f> is in the <f type="i">Glandules</f> of the
<f type="i">Mesenterie</f>, from a <term lang="la">Lympha</term> or Water which mixes
it self with the <f type="i">Chyle</f>. The <f type="i">fourth</f> is in the Lungs,
from the Inspiration of <f type="i">Nitrous</f> Air. The <f type="i">fifth</f> is
in the Vessels and Bowels, as in the Spleen, Liver,
Testicles, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. It is ill called coction, or boiling, be&shy;
cause 'tis the property of Fire to boyl: for if Heat
</page>

<page no="69">
were the cause of Fermentation, what should be
then of Fish and other things, wherein there's no
sensible heat at all.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Codia</form> <xpln lang="en">are the tops of Poppies, of which they
make Syrup.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cecum intestinum</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Fourth, in order from
the Stomach, and first of the thick Guts; in Chil&shy;
dren new born, 'tis found full of Excrements; but
in <f type="i">Adult</f> persons its Cavitie often disappears, and 
onely hangs like a Worm.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">C&aelig;lia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a great Cavity, as the uppermost, mid&shy;
dle, and the lowest Region or Cavity.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">C&aelig;liaca Arteria</form> <xpln lang="en">is that which arises from the
<f type="i">Trunc</f> of the great <f type="i">Arterie</f>, and spreads it self to&shy;
wards the <f type="i">Ventricle</f> and <f type="i">Liver</f> with its Branches.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Coeliaca passio</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Affectio</term>, is a Purging, where&shy;
in the Meat either wholly changed, or in part is 
ejected, without any Chilification; and it is two&shy;
fold: the <f type="i">first</f>, in which the Meat is onely Digest&shy;
ed in the Stomach; the <f type="i">other</f>, when Concoction
or Fermentation is performed in the Stomach and
Intestines both at once; but by reason that the
<f type="i">Lacteal</f> Vessels, or little Teats of the Guts, are Ob&shy;
literated through long Fasting, a <f type="i">Purulent Dissen&shy;
terie</f> or the like, the <f type="i">Chyle</f> is not distributed.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Coeloma</form> <xpln lang="en">is a hollow and round Ulcer in the
<f type="i">Horny Tunic</f> of the Eye.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Coelum</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Cavitie of the Eye towards the
Corners. The <f type="i">Palate</f> is also called <term lang="la">C&oelig;lum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cohobatio</form> <xpln lang="en">is when a distilled Liquor is poured
upon its <term lang="la">Menstruum</term> again, and afterwards is Di&shy;
stilled.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Coindicantia</form> <xpln lang="en">are signs which do not indicate by
themselves, but by another.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="70">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Colatura</form> <xpln lang="en">is that which after Boyling, or Infu&shy;
sion, is <f type="i">percolated</f> through a Sive or Cloth.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Colcothar</form> <xpln lang="en">is the dry Substance which remains
after Distillation, commonly called <term lang="la">Caput mortuum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Coles</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Penis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Colica passio</form>, <xpln lang="en">the <f type="i">Colic</f> is a vehement pain in the
<f type="i">Abdomen</f>, from an ill disposition of the Animal Spi&shy;
rits, begun in the Nervous foldings of the <f type="i">Mesen&shy;
terie</f>, and is sometimes falsly imputed to the Gut
<term lang="la">Colon</term>. Others make this Disease to proceed from
an <f type="i">Acid Pancreatic</f> Juice; others, other ways, but
falsly.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Colla</form> <xpln lang="en">is Glue.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Colletica</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines that <f type="i">Conglutinate</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Collici&aelig;</form> <xpln lang="en">are the joyning of the <term lang="la">puncta Lachry&shy;
malia</term> into one passage on both sides, which de&shy;
rive the humour of the Eye-lids into the Cavitie of
the Nostrils; the holes that are made in the very
tops of the Eye-brows descend in little Channels,
easily to be shown, unless the bones of the No&shy;
trils be so cautiously broken, that the <f type="i">Tunics</f> re&shy;
main entire; for after they have penetrated the
Bones (whither they are separated with a thin 
Membrane) they spread themselves into a larger
Channel, and are continued to the <f type="i">Tunic</f> of the
Nostrils. The same holes or openings in Sheep,
Hares, Calves, Rabbits, are not found in the very
Eye-brows, but a little more inward; and most of
all in Birds, where they are larger than in any
other Creatures; the <f type="i">Membrane</f> which separates
the holes here, is very short.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Collutio</form> <xpln lang="en">is a washing of the Mouth, when we 
scour loose Teeth, the Gums, or Ulcers.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Collyrium</form> <xpln lang="en">was once an Oblong Medicine which
</page>

<page no="71">
was taken in Distempers of the Eyes; it is prepa&shy;
red in an Oblong, sometimes an Orbicular Form,
and is dissolved in a convenient <f type="i">Vehicle</f> for curing
the Eyes.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Coloboma</form> <xpln lang="en">is a fault in the Lips, Eye-lids, Ears,
Nostrils, and the like, when one part either from 
the Nativity, or by some accident grows to ano&shy;
ther, which were either before actually loosned, or
at least ought to have been so.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en">Colon</form>, <xpln lang="en">is the second of the great Guts; it is thus
situate; it arises from the <term lang="la">C&aelig;cum Intestinum</term>, in the
right Flank, and adheres to the right Kidney; then
it tends upwards under the Liver, where some&shy;
times it is annexed to the Bladder of the Gall,
which dyes it a Clayish Colour: it goes on further
transverse under the bottom of the <f type="i">Ventricle</f>, and
on the left hand is joyned to the Spleen; then
again it is fastned to the left Kidneys, where it
winds and turns very obliquely; and after that, 
descends in a right Line; it is commonly about
Eight or Nine hand-breadths in length; but the
widest and largest Gut of all, it has a great many
little Cells, or Cavities in it; a certain Ligament
is twisted with it the breadth of the middle Finger
about its middle upwards; and then by reason
of its largeness it is guarded with two strong Liga&shy;
ments, the one upwards, the other downwards,
that it may be fastned to both the upper and un&shy;
der <emend err="parrs">parts</emend>: about the beginning it has a Valve 
that looks upwards, lest any thing should re&shy;
turn from the great Guts into the small.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Colpus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Sinus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Columella</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Cion</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Columma nasi</form> <xpln lang="en">is the fleshie part of the Nose pro&shy;
</page>

<page no="72">
minent in the middle, near the upper Lip.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Columma oris</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Cion</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Coma somnolentum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a deep sleep, less than a 
Lethargie, without a Fever, wherein the Patient
being awakned, answers to any Questions pro&shy;
pounded to him, but falls into a profound Sleep
again, with his Mouth open, and his under-Jaw
fallen, liker to one dead than alive. It proceeds
from an Obstruction of the Brain, when the <term lang="la">Se&shy;
rum</term> has invaded the <f type="i">Tegument</f> of the windings
and foldings of the Brain, and the little streaks
of the Marrow that is included therein. It is the
same that <term lang="la">Cataphora</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Coma vigil</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Disease wherein the Patients
are continually inclined to Sleep, but scarce can
sleep, being affected with a great drowziness in
the Head, a stupidity in all the Senses and Fa&shy;
culties, and many times with a <f type="i">delirium</f> too. If
the reason of these things be demanded, we may 
solve them thus, That the Pores and Passages of
the Brains, wherein the Spirits move, are very much 
stuffed up with a thick <f type="i">Soporiferous</f> Matter from
the Blood, whereby the Spirits being hindred from
their usual <f type="i">Explosion</f> and Commerce with one ano&shy;
ther, seem to induce a profound and almost
irresistable Drowziness upon the Person Affected;
but in as much as there are some sharp nimble 
<f type="i">Particles</f>, like so many Stings, intermixed with the
Spirits, and which keep them in perpetual Motion,
therefore some of them still force their way, and
directly or obliquely, as they can find a passage,
meet and exert; and this Motion, such as it is, con&shy;
fused and wandring, tho it do not perfect the com&shy;
pleat Exercise of the Animal Function, yet easily
</page>

<page no="73">
interrupts its Rest; so that persons thus Affected,
enjoy neither perfect day, nor perfect night, but
live in a continual Twilight betwixt sleep and
waking.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Comitialis morbus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Epilepsia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Composita</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines made up of many sim&shy;
ple Medicines; as certain Waters, Syrups, Electu&shy;
aries, <f type="i">Opiates</f>, <f type="i">Trochies</f>, Ointments, Plaisters, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Conarium</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Glandula pinealis</term>, hangs in the fold&shy;
ing of the <term lang="la">Choroides</term> in the Brain, so called from
the shape of a <f type="i">Cone</f>. It is seated betwixt the two
beds of the Optique Nerves, and the Prominences
of the <term lang="la">Nates</term>. We can scarce believe, that this
<term lang="la">Glandul&aelig;</term> is the seat of the Soul; or that the Prin&shy;
cipal Faculties in a Man arise hence; because that
several Animals which are in a manner wholly
destitute of the Prime Faculties of the Soul, Ima&shy;
gination, Memory, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. yet have this <term lang="la">Glandul&aelig;</term>
very fair and ample: it ought therefore to be
look'd upon rather as a <f type="i">Sensorie</f>, whence the
<f type="i">Nerves</f> arise; to wit, about the beginning of the
Oblongated Marrow. Its <f type="i">use</f> is, to receive and
contain the <f type="i">Serous Humours</f> which are Excerned
from the <f type="i">Alterious Blood</f>, till either the Veins be&shy;
ing emptied, suck them again; or else the <f type="i">Lym&shy;
pheducts</f> (if there be any at hand) convey them
away. Yet the Learned <f type="i">F. Boyle</f> doubts of its
use, when he says, <f type="i">That it is not so easie to deter&shy;
mine what its use is.</f> Since I have observed this
<term lang="la">Glandul&aelig;</term> to be always impregnated with an ap&shy;
parent and pretty sharp saltness in several Brains of
Men, Oxen, and Sheep; I cannot but imagine, that
it separates some <f type="i">Volatile Humour</f> from the Blood,
<f type="i">Analogous</f> to a <f type="i">Volatile Armoniac Salt</f>, which be&shy;
</page>

<page no="74">
ing diffused upon the Trunc of the <f type="i">Spinal Marrow</f>,
communicates some new Vigor to the Animal
Spirits, and hinders their Coagulation.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Concha</form> <xpln lang="en">is the winding Cavitie of the inner part
of the Ear.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Condensantia</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Incrassantia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Conditum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a composition of Conserves, Pow&shy;
ders, Spices, made up into the Form of an <f type="i">Electu&shy;
arie</f>, with a convenient quantity of Syrup: it is
taken also for a Simple Medicine, sweetned with
Honey or Sugar; as candid Ginger, or Helicam&shy;
pane.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Condyloma</form> <xpln lang="en">is the knitting or joyning of Joynts.
Also a certain Tumor in the little skin of the
Fundament; an hard and <f type="i">Callous</f> Swelling, grow&shy;
ing from black Humors that flow thither and
rather troublesome than painful: sometimes also
it is accompanied with an Inflamation.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Condylie</form> <xpln lang="en">are the joynts and knuckles of the Fin&shy;
gers, thicker thereabout the Joynts, than in other
places.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Confecta</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="confiture(n)"><f type="i">Confitures</f>, are things (as Seeds, Al&shy;
monds, Cinnamon, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.) crusted over with dry
Sugar.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Confectio</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="lozenge(n)" lexeme="opiate(n)" lexeme="preserve(n)" lexeme="conserve(n)">is a Composition of Powders, Gums,
Sugar, Honey, Syrups, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. made up into one
Substance, and it is Twofold; either dry, as
<f type="i">Lozenges</f>, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. or moist, as Opiates, Preserves, Con&shy;
serves, and all sorts of Antidotes.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Conformatio</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Essential part of Health, or
Sickness; and therefore is either good or bad;
it consists in these Six following Particulars, <f type="i">Num&shy;
ber, Magnitude, Figure, Cavitie, Surface</f>, and <f type="i">Sci&shy;
tuation.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="75">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Congius, <term lang="en">or</term> Choa</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Measure that contains Six
<f type="i">Sectaries</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Conjunctiva tunica</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Adnata</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Conoides</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Conarium</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Consensus</form>, <xpln lang="en">a Disease by Consent, is when one
Disease is caused by another, as Respiration is hin&shy;
dred by a Pleurisie; it is likewise the <f type="i">correspon&shy;
dence</f> of different parts, by the mutual and com&shy;
mon <f type="i">Ligaments</f> of both; to wit, <f type="i">Nerves</f> and <f type="i">Ten&shy;
dons</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Conserva</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="conserve(n)">a <f type="i">Conserve</f>, is a Composition of Flow&shy;
ers or Herbs beat together, to every pound where&shy;
of, if they be dry, are added three pounds of Su&shy;
gar; if moister, two pounds, so that they may be
kept several years.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Consolidantia</form> <xpln lang="en">are those things which cleansing
with a moderate heat and force, by taking Cor&shy;
ruption out of Wounds, and preserving the temp&shy;
perature of the parts, cause the Nourishment to
be fitly applyed to the part Affected.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Contagium</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="poison(n)">is a Poison, which from one Sub&shy;
ject is propagated to another; which happens
two manner of ways, either at a distance by the
Air, or by simple Contact.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Contemplabiles dies</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Critici dies</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Continens causa</form>, <xpln lang="en">is the Internal Cause of a Dis&shy;
ease, with the matter of it, which ariseth elsewhere,
which is so near a kin to the Disease, that if it be,
the Disease is too; and if it be taken away, the
Disease follows. As the Stone, which proceeds
from ill Humors arising from ill qualities in Meats
and Drinks, Obstructs the <f type="i">Ureters</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Continens febris</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Fever that continues with&shy;
out any Intermission: and it is Twofold, either
</page>

<page no="76">
<f type="i">Primarie</f>, or <f type="i">Secundarie</f>; the former proceeds from
a too great Exaltation of <f type="i">Sulphur</f>, as in a burning
Fever, a Pleurisie, Quinzie, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. the latter, which
is also called <term lang="la">Symtomatica</term>, is caused by Wounds,
Ulcers, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. as in a Consumption, Wounds in the 
Head, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Continua Febris</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="fever(n)" lexeme="ague(n)">is a Fever (or Ague) which
is continually troublesome, but with some inter&shy;
mission: and it is either <f type="i">Quotidian</f>, <f type="i">Tertian</f>, <f type="i">Quar&shy;
tane</f>, or <f type="i">Erratic</f>. The cause of its continuance
proceeds from a too high Exaltation of <f type="i">Sulphur</f>;
as in the former sort of Fevers: but the <f type="i">Paroxismes</f>,
or Fits, proceed from that equal portion of <f type="i">Chyle</f>
which is continually added to the Blood.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Contraindicatio</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Indication which hinders
that to be done which the first Indication suggested;
and it is either <term lang="la">Contra indicians</term>, which hinders of it
self; or <term lang="la">Correpugnance</term>, which is <f type="i">Secundarily</f> Repug&shy;
nant, and in Conjunction with other <f type="i">Indications</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Contusio offis</form>, <xpln lang="en">a bruising of a Bone is when a
Bone is so hurt with some hard blunt Instrument,
that outwardly it appears whole, when as inward&shy;
ly it is otherwise.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Convulsio</form>, <xpln lang="en"><f type="i">Convulsion</f>, is a Motion whereby the
<f type="i">Nerves</f> or <f type="i">Membranes</f> are contracted and remitted
without the Will, as in the Falling-sickness, Cramp,
<term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. of which in their proper place.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cophosis</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="deafness(n)">is a Deafness.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Copos</form> <xpln lang="en">is a weariness of the Body when the
<f type="i">Muscles</f>, or their <f type="i">Fibers</f> rather, are loaden and ob&shy;
structed with such Viscous Humors, that they are
rendred unfit for Motion.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Coprocritica</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines which Purge away
the Excrements in the Guts.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="77">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cor</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="heart(n)"  lexeme="basis(n)" lexeme="auricle(n)" lexeme="ear(n)" lexeme="ventricle(n)" lexeme="great vein(n)" lexeme="pulmonary vein(n)">the Heart, is a Fleshy <f type="i">Fibrous</f> Substance,
made up of several <f type="i">Muscles</f> and <f type="i">Tendons</f>; it has
two <f type="i">Auricles</f> or <f type="i">Ears</f>, and as many <f type="i">Ventricles</f>;
the <term lang="la">Vena Cava</term>, or Great Vein, is fastned to the 
right <f type="i">Auricle</f>, and the <f type="i">Pulmonarie Vein</f> to the left;
the <f type="i">Pulmonarie Arterie</f> is joyned to the Right <f type="i">Ven&shy;
tricle</f>, and the great <f type="i">Arterie</f> to the left. It is clothed
with a little <f type="i">Membraneous</f> Bag, called the <term lang="la">Pericar&shy;
dium</term>, wherewith it is joyned to the <term lang="la">Mediastinum</term>,
and the <term lang="la">Diaphragme</term>; its <f type="i">Basis</f> is upwards, and 
Point downwards, and is placed in the middle of
the Chest, amongst the Lobes of the Lungs. Its
use is onely to receive and disperse the Blood to all
parts in the Body; though others place I know
not what Flame, others a <f type="i">Ferment</f> in its <f type="i">Ventricles</f>,
which are all Fables, and no way consonant to
Reason, as we have sufficiently Evinced in our
Tract, concerning <f type="i">The Circulation of the Blood</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Coracohyoides</form>, <xpln lang="en">are <f type="i">Muscles</f> which proceed from
the Process of the Shoulder-bone, called <term lang="la">Coracoi&shy;
des</term>, and go on as far as the Bone <term lang="la">Hiordes</term>: their
use is to move obliquely downwards.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Coracoides</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Process of the Shoulder-blade
in form of a Beek.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cordialia</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines which are commonly
thought to strengthen the Heart: but they onely
put the Blood into a fine gentle Fermentation,
which Corroborates and Facilitates the Motion of
the Heart.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cornea oculi tunica</form>, <xpln lang="en">which is also called <term lang="la">Sclero&shy;
tes</term>, and <term lang="la">Dura</term>, the hard <f type="i">Tunic</f>, proceeds from a 
skin in the Brain called <term lang="la">Dura Menix</term>; it is <f type="i">pellu&shy;
cide</f> forwardly, that it may transmit the visible
<f type="i">Species</f>; its sides are covered with the <f type="i">Albugine</f>&shy;
</page>

<page no="78">
<f type="i">ous tunic</f>; inwardly it contains the <f type="i">Aqu&aelig;ous Hu&shy;
mour</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cornicularis processus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Ancyroides</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cornua uteri</form>, <xpln lang="en">are two lateral parts of the Womb
in some Bruits, as Cows, Harts, Sheep, Goats, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.
yet some Authors have attributed the same parts
to a Womans Womb, from something which imi&shy;
tates them there; for at the sides of the bottom
of the Womb, there is a sort of <f type="i">Protuberance</f> on
both sides, where the <term lang="la">Vasa deferentia</term> are inserted:
a Womans Womb is rarely <f type="i">bipartite</f>, as it is in 
Bruits.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Coronalis sutura</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="suture(n)">is a Cleft in the Head, made
like a Comb, and joynes as if the Teeth of two
Saws were closely compacted into one another;
it is placed in the upper part of the Skull, from
one Temple to another, and is circumscribed
with the bones of the Forehead, and that parti&shy;
cularly called <term lang="la">Bregma</term>, in the middle whereof the
<f type="i">Suture</f>, stiled <term lang="la">Sagitalis</term>, is terminated.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Coronaria vasa</form> <xpln lang="en">are the Veins and Arteries which
surround the Heart, to Nourish it.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Corone</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Acute Process of the lower Jaw&shy;
bone, from its likeness to the Beek of a <f type="i">Raven</f>,
called <term lang="la">Rostriformis</term>, in form of a Beek.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Corpus Callosum</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Marrowie part of the
Brain, whose Complication makes the foremost
<f type="i">Ventricle</f> of the Brain; and it is wholly Marrowie,
without any <f type="i">Membrane</f>, and is fastened on both
sides to the little Tuffs of the Oblongated Marrow;
from which, as from its rise, this <f type="i">Medullarie Sub&shy;
stance</f> which overspreads the Arches of the Brain
is expanded towards the hinder parts, and gradu&shy;
ally diminishes; at length the Exteriour Edge of
</page>

<page no="79">
this <f type="i">Expanded Substance</f> is more narrowly con&shy;
tracted, and lower down is joyned to the <f type="i">Trunc</f>
of the <f type="i">Oblongated Marrow</f>, by the connexion of
<f type="i">Membranes</f> and <f type="i">Vessels</f>: and farther, that the Con&shy;
nexion may be firmer, there arises a <f type="i">Medullary
Process</f> from its former part, near its little Tufts,
which subtending the opening of the Brain, goes
to the very Extremities of it; with which, as with
two Arms folded, it is united on both sides: which
Arms embrace the <f type="i">Trunc</f> of the <f type="i">Oblongated Mar&shy;
row</f>, and so unite that <term lang="la">Limbus</term> of the Brain too
more firmly to themselves.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Corpus glandolosum</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Prostata</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Corpus varicosum</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Varicosum corpus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Corpus Pampineforme</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Varicosum corpus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Corrosio Chymica</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Calcination of mixed Bo&shy;
dies by <f type="i">Corrosives</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Corrosivum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Medicine that has a power of
<f type="i">Corroding</f>, as Lime, Aquafortis, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Corrodentia</form>, <xpln lang="en">Corroding things, are those which
eat up and consume Excrescent Flesh, with their
sharp <f type="i">Particles</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Corticalis substantia cerebri</form>, <xpln lang="en">is the outward Sub&shy;
stance of the Brain, full of <f type="i">Labyrinths</f>, and <f type="i">Mean&shy;
ders</f> in the outside; it is covered with a thin skin,
it is of an Ash-grislie Colour, and full of little
Vessels: inwardly the <f type="i">Medullary Substance</f> is next
to it. Its use is to generate Animal Spirits from
the Blood, and hence they are conveyed by the
<f type="i">Medullarie Substance</f> to the <f type="i">Nerves</f>, and distribu&shy;
ted through the whole Body. <f type="i">Secondly</f>, The Seat
of the Memory, and Sleep is placed there.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Coryphe</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="crown of the head(n)">is the Crown of the Head; also the
</page>

<page no="80">
interior Extremity of the Fingers, near the
Nails.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Coryza, <term lang="en">or</term> gravedo</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a defluction of a sharp,
salt, and thickned Humour, into the Mouth, Lungs,
and Nostrils, from the <f type="i">Ventricles</f> of the Brain, by
the <f type="i">Nerves</f> of smelling; for when it grows thick,
it can neither be <f type="i">Percolated</f> by the Reins, nor pass
from the <f type="i">Pitutarie Glandule</f>, thorough the <term lang="la">Infindi&shy;
bulum</term> into the <f type="i">Veins</f>, and therefore it Distills into
the Nostrils by the aforesaid <f type="i">Nerves</f>, which if it
meet with an Accension of <f type="i">Sulphureous Particles</f>,
it produces a Fever, and consequently thirst.
Hence comes that <term lang="la">Coryza</term>, either with or without
a Fever.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cosmetica</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines which whiten and soften
the Skin, as Oyl of <f type="i">Tartar</f>, a dissolution of Subli&shy;
mated <f type="i">Mercury</f>, <f type="i">Sulphur</f>, <f type="i">Camphor</f>, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en">Cost&aelig;</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="rib(n)"> the Ribs, are those Bones which with
other parts make the <f type="i">Chest</f> or <term lang="la">Thorax</term>: backward
they are connexed with the <f type="i">Vertebres</f> of the Back,
forward with the <f type="i">Cartilages</f> of the Breast-bone;
they are Twelve in Number on both sides; the
seven upper are called <f type="i">true</f>, the five lower <f type="i">spurious</f>,
the broader part of the Ribs is called <term lang="la">Palmula</term>, the
straiter towards the <f type="i">Vertebres</f>, <term lang="la">Remulus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cotyla attica</form>, <xpln lang="en">is Nine Ounces, as an <f type="i">Italian He&shy;
mina</f>; but <term lang="la">Cotyla Italica</term> contains Twelve.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cotyle</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Acetabulum</term>, is the Cavitie of
the Huckle-bone, which is appointed to receive the
head of the Thigh-bone.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cotyledon</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Cotyle</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cotyledones</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Acetabula uterina</term>, are <f type="i">Glandules</f>
dispersed up and down the uttermost <f type="i">Membrane</f>
of the <term lang="la">F&oelig;tus</term>, called <term lang="la">Chorion</term>; which separate <f type="i">Nu&shy;</f>
</page>

<page no="81">
<f type="i">tritious</f> juice from the Womb to nourish the <term lang="la">F&oelig;&shy;
tus</term>; but this is found onely in some Animals: the
<term lang="la">Placenta</term> in the Womb supplies their place in Wo&shy;
men. Also the gaping meetings of the Veins in
the Womb, are called <term lang="la">Cotylidones</term>, and <term lang="la">Acetabula</term>,
these Glandules are so called, from the resem&shy;
blance they bear to the Leaves of the Herb Pen&shy;
nywort, in Latin <term lang="la">Cotyledon</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cox&aelig; os</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="hip-bone(n)">the Hyp-bone, called otherwise <term lang="la">In&shy;
nominatum</term>, and <term lang="la">illium coxendix</term>, because it contains
the Gut called <term lang="la">ileum</term>; it is annexed to the sides of
the <term lang="la">Os Sacrum</term>; in Infants it consists of Three Bones,
<term lang="la">Ilium</term>, <term lang="la">Ischium</term>, and <term lang="la">Os pubis</term>, which are joyned to&shy;
gether by <f type="i">Cartilages</f> till Seven Years of Age, then
it is distinguished by a Triple Line; it grows in&shy;
to one continued Bone in <f type="i">Adult</f> persons.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Coxendix</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Coxa</term> and <term lang="la">Ischium</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Crama</form>, <xpln lang="en"><term lang="la">Croma</term>, and <term lang="la">Chrama</term>, is a mixture of any
thing, whether Medicines or Elements.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cranium</form> <xpln lang="en">is the compages of the Bones of the
Head, to which belong the Bones of the Fore-head,
of the sides of the Head, of the hinder-part of the
Head, of the Temples, the Bone called <term lang="la">Sphenoi&shy;
des</term>, and another called <term lang="la">Cribriforme</term> like a Sieve:
it is like a <term lang="gk">&#x039A;&#x03C1;&#x03AC;&#x03BD;&#x03BF;&#x03C2;</term> an Helmet to the Head; which
defends it from External Injuries; its upper part
is double: some call it <term lang="la">Calva</term> and <term lang="la">Calvaria</term>. See
<term lang="la">Calva</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Crapula</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="headache(n)">is an Head-ach proceeding from too
much Wine.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Crasis</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="temperament(n)">or <term lang="la">temperamentum</term>, is a convenient mix&shy;
tion of qualities; temperament is either <f type="i">Simple</f>, or
<f type="i">Compound</f>; <f type="i">Simple</f>, is when onely one quality ex&shy;
ceeds the rest, as hot, cold, moist, dry, salt, sharp,
</page>

<page no="82">
&amp;c. <f type="i">Compound</f>, is when more qualities exceed, as
hot and dry, hot and bitter, salt and sharp, acid
and frigid, acid and acrimonious, and also one is
<f type="i">inherent</f>, which is fixed in the parts; another <f type="i">in&shy;
fluent</f>, which is derived upon the parts, from the
Blood and Spirits; and it is either <f type="i">moderate</f>, or <f type="i">im&shy;
moderate</f>; <f type="i">total</f>, or <f type="i">partial</f>; <f type="i">natural</f> or <f type="i">acquired</f>; <f type="i">per&shy;
manent</f> or <f type="i">transitorie</f>, to an <f type="i">equality in weight</f>, or <f type="i">a
just proportion</f>; and so they make a great many
distinctions, which signifie little or nothing.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Craticula</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Chymical Instrument made of
square pieces of Iron, as thick as ones Finger,
placed so near one another in Acute Angles, that
there's half a Fingers space betwixt them; it is used
in making of Fires, to keep up the Coles.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cremasteres</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="hanger(n)">are two Muscles of the Testicles,
called <term lang="la">suspensores</term>, <f type="i">hangers</f>; they grow outwardly
to the Membrane of the <term lang="la">vagina</term>, and proceed in
men from the Ligament which is the <term lang="la">os pubis</term>;
and are fast connexed to the lower part of the
Testicles.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cribrosum os</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Ethmoides</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cribrum benedictum antiquorum</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="strainer(n)" lexeme="blessed sieve(n)">the Ancients
fancied Two Cavities placed long-ways in the
Reins; one uppermost, whereinto the Serous Blood
was poured from the Emulgent Arteries; another
lowermost, which they fancied was distinguished
with a certain Transverse Membrane full of little
holes like a Sieve; whence they called it <term lang="la">Colatorium</term>,
a Strainer, and <term lang="la">Benedictum Cribrum</term>, a blessed Sieve,
through which they would have the <term lang="la">Serum</term> Per&shy;
colated into the <f type="i">Ureters</f>, and the good Blood stay
behind for the nourishment of the Reins.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cricoaryt&aelig;noides</form> <xpln lang="en">are Muscles which proceed
</page>

<page no="83">
from the Cartilage, called <term lang="la">Cricoides</term> and are in&shy;
serted into the <term lang="la">Aryt&aelig;noides</term>, which whilst they draw
back-ward and outwardly, the opening of the <term lang="la">La&shy;
rynx</term> is Dilated.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cricoides</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="windpipe(n)">is the Cartilage of the <term lang="la">Larynx</term> or Wind&shy;
pipe, which is in fashion of a Ring.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cricothyroides</form> <xpln lang="en">signifies a pair of Muscles, which
proceed from the Cartilage like a Ring, and are
terminated in that which is called <term lang="la">Scutiformis</term>, or
like a Shield; they Dilate the opening of the
<term lang="la">Larynx</term> by moving a little obliquely.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Crimnoides</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Crimnodes</term>, is Urine with thick
Sediments at the bottom, like Bran.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Crisima</form> <xpln lang="en">are Signs by which one may discern
and judge.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Crisis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a sudden Change in a Disease, either
towards a Recovery, or Death. It sometimes sig&shy;
nifies a <f type="i">Secretion</f> of Humors; but is more frequent&shy;
ly taken for a Judgment passed upon a Disease.
One <f type="i">Crisis</f> is called <f type="i">perfect</f>, another <f type="i">imperfect</f>; the
<f type="i">perfect</f> is that which frees the Patient perfectly
and entirely from the Distemper; and it is either
<f type="i">Salutary</f>, or deadly. 1. It must be judged by ve&shy;
ry good Signs. 2. Be manifest. 3. Happen
upon a Critical Day. 4. Be faithful. 5. Secure
6. Suitable to the Disease, and the Distemper of
the Patient. An <f type="i">imperfect Crisis</f>, is that which does
not clearly determine the Tendency of the Dis&shy;
ease, but leaves room for another <f type="i">Crisis</f>: and this
is Two-fold, either <f type="i">for the better</f>, or <f type="i">for the worse</f>:
the former is that which does not quite take away
the Disease, but enables the Patient to bear it bet&shy;
ter: the latter, is when the Disease becomes more
violent and dangerous. That <f type="i">Crisis</f> depend up&shy;
</page>

<page no="84">
on the Motion and Influence of the Moon, and
Stars, and follow their Quadrate and opposite As&shy;
pects, or their Conjunctions, is false and frivo&shy;
lous; for Critical Evacuations are determined only
according to the store and turgescencie of <f type="i">Adust</f>
Matter, which is Expelled the Body sooner or la&shy;
ter, according to the different Temperament of the
Persons Affected: whereupons depends the variety
of <f type="i">Critical</f> days.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Crist&aelig;</form> <xpln lang="en">are Excrescencies of Flesh growing
about the Fundament, from a preposterous use of
<term lang="la">Coition</term>, the Roots whereof are often Chapt, and
Cleft.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Christa Galli</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Third part of the Bone <term lang="la">Eth&shy;
moides</term>, or the inner Process not much unlike the
Comb of a Cock: it arises betwixt the <f type="i">Olfactory
Nerves</f>; and has the Extremity of the Third Ca&shy;
vity of the hard skin of the Brain, called <term lang="la">Dura me&shy;
ninx</term>, implanted in it.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Criterium</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <f type="i">Crisis</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Crithe</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="push(n)">or <term lang="la">Hordeolum</term>, is a little Oblong Push, or
Swelling, which grows to the Eye-brows where
the Hairs are; so called from its resemblance to
a Barly-corn.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Critici dies</form> <xpln lang="en">are those whereon there happens a
sudden change of a Disease, and they are Three&shy;
fold: some are called <f type="i">truly and perfectly Critical</f>;
others <f type="i">Indices</f>; others <f type="i">Intercidentes</f>. The <f type="i">perfectly
Critical</f> Days are called <term lang="la">Principes</term>, or <f type="i">Radicales</f>;
because that the <f type="i">Crisis</f> which happen on these
days have all the marks of a perfect <f type="i">Crisis</f>: and
these are the Seventh, the Fourteenth, and the
Twenty-first Day. <term lang="la">Indices</term> which are called also
<term lang="la">Contemplabiles</term>, and <term lang="la">Internuncii</term>, are those which
</page>

<page no="85">
Indicate, that the <f type="i">Crisis</f> will be on the Seventh day:
and these are Three: the Fourth, the Eleventh,
and Seventeenth Day. <term lang="la">Intercidentes</term>, which are
called also <term lang="la">Intercalares</term>, <term lang="la">irrepentes</term>, or <term lang="la">provocatorii</term>,
are those which fall betwixt the days called <term lang="la">Prin&shy;
cipes &amp; Indices</term>, and they onely aim at an imper&shy;
fect <f type="i">Crisis</f>, and are the Third, the Fifth, the Ninth
the Thirteenth, and the Nineteenth; but all other
Days which are neither <term lang="la">Principes</term>, nor <term lang="la">Indices</term>, nor
<term lang="la">Intercidentes</term>, are called <term lang="la">Vacui</term>, and <term lang="la">Medicinales</term>,
and they are the Sixth, the Eighth, the Tenth, the
Twelfth, the Sixteenth, and the Eighteenth. The
computation of Critical Days, is to be Instituted
from that hour wherein the Patient first felt him&shy;
self ill. We may observe by the by, That the
computation of Critical Days in these Countries
does not exactly correspond with <f type="i">Hypocrates</f> his 
Accounts. All these days depend upon the soo&shy;
ner or later Fermentation and Maturation of the
Morbific Matter.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Critica Signa</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="critical sign(n)">Critical Signs, are such as are
taken from a <f type="i">Crisis</f>, either towards Death, or a
Recovery; and some of them are <f type="i">antecedent</f>, which
either fore-tell the time of a <f type="i">Crisis</f>, or signifie a
kind of <f type="i">Crisis</f>. Others are <f type="i">concomitant</f>, which ap&shy;
pear at the same time with the <f type="i">Crisis</f>. And others,
Lastly, are <f type="i">Subsequent</f>, which shew, whether an
imperfect Recovery be to be expected; or there
be fear of a Relapse.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Crotaphites</form> <xpln lang="en">are the Muscles, Veins, and Arteries
about the Temples. Sometimes <term lang="la">Crotaphium</term> is
taken for a pain in the Head.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Crotaphium</form>, <xpln lang="en">See in <term lang="la">Crotaphites</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Crucibulum</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="crucible(n)">a Crucible, is a Vessel for melting
</page>

<page no="86">
Minerals and Metals made of Earth, extraordi&shy;
narily hardned by Fire, with an Acute Basis, but a
larger top, round, or triangular. There is also
a sort of Crucible made, commonly called <term lang="la">Testa</term>,
which is sufficient to melt Metals.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cruditas morborum</form>, <xpln lang="en">a Crudity in Diseases, is
when the Blood (as in continued Fevers) is not
yet duly fermented, and brought to a right con&shy;
sistence.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cruditas Ventriculi</form>, <xpln lang="en">a Crudity of the Stomach,
is when meat out of a defect of Nourishment, or
some other cause, is not rightly fermented, and 
turned into Chyle: and it is Threefold, <term lang="la">Apepsia</term>,
<term lang="la">Bradypepsia</term>, and <term lang="la">Dispepsia</term>: of which in their pro&shy;
per places.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cruor</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="blood(n)">Blood, see <term lang="la">Sanguis</term>. <f type="i">Helmont</f> makes a 
distinction betwixt <term lang="la">Sanguis</term>, and <term lang="la">Cruor</term>; the for&shy;
mer whereof, he says, <f type="i">Is the Blood in the Arteries;
the latter, that in the Veins</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Crus</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Magnus pes</term>, is all that part of the Body
which reaches from the Buttocks down to the end
of the Toes; it is divided into the Thigh, Leg, 
and Foot.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Crusta lactea</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="scurf(n)" lexeme="scab(n)">is a species of <term lang="la">Achor</term>, a Scurf, or
crustie Scab: onely with this difference, that an 
<term lang="la">Achor</term> Infects onely the Head; but this, not onely
the Face, but almost the whole Body of an Infant
at the time of its first Sucking. <term lang="la">Crusta Lactea</term>
turns white, but <f type="i">Achors</f> have another colour.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Crymodes</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="cold fever(n)">is a cold shivering Fever, but many
times accompanied with an Inflamation of the
inner parts.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Crysorchis</form> <xpln lang="en">is an absconding of the Testicles in
the Belly.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="87">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Crystalinus humor oculi</form>, <xpln lang="en">called also <term lang="la">Glacialis</term>, the
Crystaline humor of the Eye, within the opening 
of the <term lang="la">Tunica Uvea</term>, like a Glass put over a hole,
collects and refringes the Rays which strike upon
it from all parts; its Substance is like Glue, or
the Gum of a Tree, very pellucide, and of a con&shy;
sistence like melting Wax, which though it be
pressed, does not yet easily yield and separate.
In Men it is shaped like a Lintel, whose outward
Surface is pretty plain, but the inner gibbous and
<emend err="risiing">rising</emend>: this Humor, though it be not apt to 
spread abroad, yet is cloathed with a small Mem&shy;
brane of its own, called <term lang="la">Aranea</term>, by reason of its
thinness, like to a Spiders Web.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Crystalloides tunica</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Aranea Tu&shy;
nica</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cubiforme</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Cuboides</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cubitus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the middle part betwixt the Shoulder&shy;
bone and the Wrest; it consists of two Bones,
one called <term lang="la">Ulna</term>, and the other <term lang="la">Radius</term>: the ends
whereof meet indeed, but the middle parts are
separate, though they be tied together a little by
a Membranous Ligament.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cuboides</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Fourth bone in that part of the
Foot which immediately succeeds the Leg, and
that in both Feet. It is called also <term lang="la">Grandinosum</term>,
and <term lang="la">Cubiforme</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cucupha</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Cover for the Head, made of Odo&shy;
riferous and Cephalic Spices beat to Powder, and 
stitched betwixt two pieces of Silk; or else, sow&shy;
led within a Cap, and worn upon the Head against
<term lang="la">Catarrhs</term>, and other Diseases of the Head.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cucurbita</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Chymical pointed Vessel made
of Earth or Glass, used in Distillations by an <f type="i">Alem&shy;</f>
</page>

<page no="88">
<f type="i">bic</f>: sometimes it is taken for <term lang="la">Cucurbitula</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cucurbitini lumbrici</form> <xpln lang="en">are broad Worms, like
the seed of a Gourd.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cucurbitula</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="cupping-glass(n)">or <term lang="la">Cucurbita</term>, a Cupping-glass, is
a wide, hollow Vessel, made of Glass or Tin,
which is applyed to the Body with Scarrification,
or without it, to divert, to derive the Blood into
another part, or to let it out; if it be applyed
without Scarrification, it is called <term lang="la">Cucurbita c&aelig;ca
&amp; ventosa</term>. Cupping-glasses are applied to the
most fleshy parts, where the large Vessels and
Nerves cannot be hurt. The drawing which is 
performed by these Glasses, is done thus: after the
Skin is scarrified, the Air in the Cupping-glasses is
rarified, and dilated by the flame of the Towe
that is fired within it, which after it is cooled and
condensed, takes up less room than before; so
that the External Air pressing upon the Flesh
without, forces the Blood into the Glass. There
are two sorts of Cupping-glasses, says <f type="i">Celsus</f>, one
of <f type="i">Brass</f>, and the other of <f type="i">Horn</f>; the former is
open on one part, and shut on the other; the lat&shy;
ter is equally open on one part, on the other has
a little hole: burning Towe is thrown into the
Brazen one, and so its mouth is applyed, and
forced upon the Body till it stick. That of Horn,
is applyed singly by it self, and by a violent suck&shy;
ing at the little hole, which must presently be
stopt up close with Wax, it sticks as fast as the
other: but if other things fail, then a little Cup
or Goblet with a strait mouth may be very fitly
applyed to the same Effect; after it has stuck, if
