the Skin be scarrified before with a Pen-knife, it
draws out the Blood; if it be whole and entire, it
</page>

<page no="89">
draws out the Flatulent Matter; therefore where
the matter within is hurtful and offensive, it must
be applyed the former way; where there's an
Inflamation, the latter. The <f type="i">&AElig;gyptians</f> at this
day use those of Horn; as appear from <f type="i">Prosper
Alpinus</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cuneiforme os</form> <xpln lang="en">is so called from the resemblance
they say it has to a Wedge; in Latin <term lang="la">Cuneus</term>;
the Ancients called it <f type="i">Multiforme</f>, of many Shapes,
by reason of the various Processes inside and out&shy;
side, which render it rough and unequal: it is situ&shy;
ate in the midst of the Basis of the Brain, and is
placed under it like a Basis, so that it touches up&shy;
on most of the Bones of the Head, and the upper
Jaw.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cuneiformia ossa</form>, <xpln lang="en">are those bones which make the
Fifth, Sixth, and Seventh bone of that part of the
Foot which immediately succeeds the Leg: which
<f type="i">Fallopius</f> calls <term lang="la">Sphenoidea</term>, <term lang="la">Innominata</term>, and <term lang="la">Calco&shy;
idea</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cunnus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Womans Privie Parts, consisting of
a <term lang="la">Clytoris</term>, <term lang="la">Nymph&aelig;</term>, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Curatio</form> <xpln lang="en">is a right way or method of finding
out by Symptoms and Indications, proper Reme&shy;
dies for any Disease, in order to the Recovery of 
Health.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Curativa indicatio</form>, <xpln lang="en">is an Indication which respects
the Disease to be cured.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Curculio</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Cion</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cuticula</form> <xpln lang="en">the little thin skin, is a cover of the
skin without sense, extended outwardly over the
whole skin like a Membrane, full of Innumerable
small Pores, accommodated to the avoiding of
injuries from abroad, to the shutting up of the
</page>

<page no="90">
Cutaneus Vessels, and to the more Acurate Per&shy;
fecting of Tactile Qualities: It is nourished by
the Blood; for if it be lost or perished, it comes
again, though its Vessels be but little conspicuous. 
It is not condensed by <f type="i">Cold</f>; for I have often shown
it in Abortions; nor is it condensed by Oily Va&shy;
pours, because that condensed Vapours easily slide
off again.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cutis</form> <xpln lang="en">is the skin in a living Man: but <term lang="la">Pellis</term>,
is that which is flead off, and it is the outermost
cover of the whole Body, or a pretty thick Mem&shy;
brane wrought of several Filaments of the Veins
and Arteries, Nerves, and Nervous Fibres, Com&shy;
plicated and Interwoven with one another, full of 
Glandules, and Limpheducts, or Vessels that con&shy;
vey away the Vapours and Swet, abounding with
a great number of Pores here and there, and sen&shy;
sibly Perforated in many places to let in and out,
as occasion requires, as at the Mouth, Nostrils,
Eyes, Ears, Privities, Fundament, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. it is thickest
of all upon the Head; moderately hard in the
Neck and Back; finer in the Face, Yard, and outer
skin of the Cod; thin on the sides; thinnest of all 
on the Lips; in some places, as the Elbow, Fore&shy;
head, soles of the Feet, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. it sticks very close
together.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cyathus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="beaker(n)">we English it properly a <f type="i">Beeker</f>, is a
Measure of Dry things as well as Liquids; not
as some think, a common sort of Cup, but the
Eighth part of a <f type="i">Sextarie</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cyclisci</form>, <xpln lang="en">are Surgeons Tools wherewith they
scrape away Corrupt Flesh, or the like; made
in the form of an Half Moon.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cyema</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Embrion</term>.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="91">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cylindrus</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="plaster(n)">is a Plaister made oblong; which
Physicians call <term lang="la">Magdaleo</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cyllosis</form>, <xpln lang="en">see in <term lang="la">Cyllum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cyllum</form> <xpln lang="en">signifies a Leg put out of joynt out&shy;
wardly. Also one Lame and Crooked.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cymbiforme os</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">os Naviculare</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cynanche <term lang="en">and</term> Lycanche</form>, <xpln lang="en">so called, because it
is frequently incident to Dogs and Wolves, is an 
Inflamation of the inner Muscles of the <term lang="la">Larynx</term>,
accompanied with a difficulty of breathing, and
a continual Fever.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cynantropia</form> <xpln lang="en">is Madness given by a Dog, where&shy;
in the Patient flies light, and any thing that is bright
and splendid; fears Water, and trembles at the
sight and remembrance of it; it proceeds usually
from a poysonous bite, or the like, of some mad
Creature, as a Dog, a Wolf, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cynodes orexis</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Canine Appetite, or an Ex&shy;
treme hunger joyned with Vomiting, or a Loose&shy;
ness: it arises from too much, or a too Acid
Ferment in the Stomach.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cynodesmus</form> <xpln lang="en">is the band which ties the little skin
of the Yard to the Nut.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cynodontes</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="eye-teeth(n)">are those Teeth betwixt the Axel
Teeth and the Grinders, called <term lang="la">Canini</term>, <term lang="la">Columel&shy;
lares</term>, and <term lang="la">Oculares</term>, Eye-Teeth, as we say.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cyphosis</form> <xpln lang="en">is the bending of the Vertibres of the
Back towards the Back parts.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cyrtoma</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="bunch(n)" lexeme="tumor(n)">is a bunch on the Back, or a Tumor in
any other part.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cyrtosis</form>, <xpln lang="en">the fame with <term lang="la">Cyrtoma</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cyssaros</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="fundament(n)">is the Gut called <term lang="la">Rectum</term>, the lower&shy;
most of all: Also the Fundament.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cystica</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines used against Distempers
in the Bladder.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="92">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cystis</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="bladder(n)">is the Bladder that holds the Urine, or
the Gall.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Cystis choledochus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Folliculus fal&shy;
lis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordgroup1 type="a" object="D">D.

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">DAcryodes</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="ulcer(n)">are Ulcers which continually send
forth Matter.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Danich</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Lupinus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Darsis</form> <xpln lang="en">is an <f type="i">Excoriation</f> of the Skin.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dartus</form> <xpln lang="en">is the second <f type="i">Tunic</f> of the common Cotes
which mediately cover the Testicles of a Man:
it arises from the Fleshie Membrane; but in Wo&shy;
men the Testicles are immediately covered with
the Cote of the <term lang="la">Periton&aelig;um</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dasymma</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Superficiarie in equalitie of the
inner part of the Eye-lids, accompanied with a
redness.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Debilitas</form> <xpln lang="en">is a weakness proceeding from Swound&shy;
ing, Fainting, Hunger, Disease, or otherways.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Declinatio morbi</form>, <xpln lang="en">the declension of a Disease is
when it recedes from its height, and the Patient
is beyond danger: for none dyes in the declension
of a Disease but accidentally. See <term lang="la">Acme</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Decoctum</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Apozema</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Decussis</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Denarius</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Decussorium</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Chyrurgeons Instrument where&shy;
with the <term lang="la">Dura Mater</term> being highly pressed, is acu&shy;
rately adjoyned to the Scull, that the puss or snot&shy;
tie Matter gathered betwixt the Scull and the Skin
called <term lang="la">Dura Menix</term>, or <term lang="la">Mater</term>, may be Evacuated
by a hole made with a Chyrurgeon's instrument
called <term lang="la">Trepanum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="93">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Defectio animi</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Lypothomia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Deflagratio febrium</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Apyrexia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Defluvium capillorum</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Alopecia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Deflexus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Catarrhus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Deglutio</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="swallowing(n)">swallowing, is an Animal Action where&shy;
by Meat chawed in the Mouth, or any thing more
Liquid, descends into the Stomach by the con&shy;
traction of the Fibers of the Gullet.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Delirium</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Depravation of the imagination
and judgment, arising from a Tumultuary and
disorderly motion of the Animal Spirits; where&shy;
upon the Persons Affected speak several absurd and
incongruous things, the antecedent cause where&shy;
of lies either in the Blood, or in the Animal Spi&shy;
rits; there are several species of it: some who
speak little, some who dote in their talk; and not
onely think, but speak things ridiculous, strange,
magnificent, and malicious; others again really
execute what they think, and that either with
laughter, or in great earnest: but all these orders
of doting people, are reduced to certain destincti&shy;
ons.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dejectio</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Evacuation of the Excrements
by the Peristaltick Motion of the Guts.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Deleterium</form> <xpln lang="en">is any Poysonous Medicine.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Deligatio</form> <xpln lang="en">is a part of Chyrurgery that concerns
the binding up of Wounds, Ulcers, broken Bones,
<term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. and it is either Simple or Compound. The
Simple is is either equal or unequal: the equal is
onely round, which swathes the affected Member
without any Declention to either side: the une&shy;
qual is divided into <term lang="la">Ascia</term> and <term lang="la">Sima</term>, which at least
differ upon the account of one being greater, and 
the other less; <term lang="la">Ascia</term> declines little from a round,
</page>

<page no="94">
but <term lang="la">Sima</term> much. There are a great many distincti&shy;
ons of Swathing, taken from the likeness of the
parts which are swathed, or from certain Animals
and other things.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Deliquium animi</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Eclipsis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Deliquium chymicum</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Distillation by the
force of Fire: or a melting of the <term lang="la">Calx</term> which is
suspended in moist Cells, and a Resolution of it
into a Lixivious Humour.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Deltoides</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Triangular Muscle, like the <f type="i">Greek</f>
<term lang="gk">&#x0394;</term>, it proceeds from the Channel Bone, from
the upper Process of the Shoulder-blade, and
from the process of the same, which is called
<term lang="la">Spiniforme</term>, or like a Thorn; and being fastned 
to the middle strong Tendon of the Shoulder,
lifts up the Shoulder it self.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Denarius</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Seventh part of an Ounce.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dentarpaga</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Forfex</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dentes</form> <xpln lang="en">the Teeth, are little bones of both Jaws
fastned one within another like so many Nails.
Men are said to have Thirty, and Woman Twen&shy;
ty eight; as far as they appear above the Gums
there's no Membrane about them; they grow
continually, otherwise they would be worn out
by daily grinding, they are not onely provided 
with Veins and Arteries, but with Nerves too;
as the great pains which they are subject to, ma&shy;
nifestly evince.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dentiducum</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Forfex</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dentifricium</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Medicine for whitening, scou&shy;
ring, and fastning the Teeth, and for strengthening
the Gums.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dentitio</form> <xpln lang="en">is the time that Children breed Teeth,
which is about the seventh Month, or later; and
</page>

<page no="95">
usually the upper Teeth come first, in some the
under; and amongst these, the fore-teeth first:
many times Fevers, Convulsions, Loosnesses, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.
attend Children in the time of breeding Teeth.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Derivatio</form> <xpln lang="en">is a means whereby blood that flows
towards one part, but is not fixed there, is drawn
away by a neighbouring part.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Derma</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Cutis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Descensum</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">per descensum distillare</term>; See <term lang="la">De&shy;
licquium</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Desiccatio</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Evaporation of superfluous moist&shy;
ness by heat.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Destillatio</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Extraction of the moist or
unctuous parts, which are rarified into Mist, or
Smoak as it were, by the force of Fire. Distilla&shy;
tion is performed by a Bladder, by the Chymi&shy;
cal Instrument called <term lang="la">Cucurbita</term>, (before described)
by a <f type="i">Retort</f>, by <term lang="la">Deliquium</term>, by <f type="i">Filtre</f>, by <f type="i">Descent</f>;
<term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. and that either in <term lang="la">Balneo Mari&aelig;</term>, <f type="i">Sand</f>, <f type="i">Va&shy;
pours</f>, <f type="i">Dung</f>, the <f type="i">Sun</f>, a <f type="i">Reverberatorie</f>, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Detergentia</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Abstergentia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Deuteropathia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Disease that proceeds from
another Disease; for Example, If the Head-ach
from the Distemper of another part, the Morbi&shy;
fic Matter being translated thither from its for&shy;
mer Repositorie.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Diabetes,</form> <xpln lang="en">so <f type="i">Galen</f> calls it, and <term lang="la">Agineta dipsacus</term>,
from the great Thirst that attends it: and as
others will have it, from a certain sort of Serpent
called <term lang="la">Dipsacus</term>, found especially in <f type="i">Lybia</f>, which
Poysons with its bite, and brings an unquencha&shy;
ble Thirst upon the persons Affected. It is a rare
Distemper, which <f type="i">Galen</f> says, he has seen but twice.
The Famous Doctor <f type="i">J. Van Dueren</f>, and I, obser&shy;
</page>

<page no="96">
ved it once in a Reverend Pastor of the Church;
and it is too great a Fusion of the Blood, where&shy;
upon the <term lang="la">Serum</term>, joyned with a violent Thirst,
passes the Reins, and is Excerned in great quan&shy;
tity by the passages of the Urine; it proceeds
ordinarily from a too much exalted, or a too 
Acid Ferment in the Reins.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Diabrosis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a solution of the <term lang="la">Continuum</term>, by eat&shy;
ing out of parts.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Diaclisma</form> <xpln lang="en">is a washing of the Mouth to cleanse
it, or to strengthen the Teeth or Gums; the
Washes are made of several Astringents, as of the
Herbs <term lang="la">Britannica</term>, <f type="i">Tormentil</f>, bark of <f type="i">Pomgranates</f>,
<f type="i">Galls</f>, <f type="i">Allum</f>, <f type="i">Flowres</f>, or <f type="i">Blossoms</f> of wild <f type="i">Pomgra&shy;
nates</f>, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Diacopr&aelig;gia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Medicine made of Goats-dung,
against Tumors in the Spleen, and Glandules be&shy;
hind the Ears, called  <term lang="la">Parotides</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Diacrisis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a distinction and dijudication of Dis&shy;
eases and Symptomes.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Diacritica</form>, <xpln lang="en">see  <term lang="la">Diacrisis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Diadoche</form> <xpln lang="en">is a succeeding by a <f type="i">Crisis</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Diadosis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a distribution of Nourishment through
all the parts.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Di&aelig;resis</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Eating out, or consuming of Ves&shy;
sels, as <f type="i">Senertus</f> says, when from some cutting 
corroding Cause, some ways and passages are
made which naturally ought not to have been; or
when some which really are, yet are dilated more
than ordinary, so that the Humours which ought 
to have been contained in the Vessels, run out.
For first, a <term lang="la">Dia&aelig;resis</term> may be occasioned by sharp
Humors which dissolve the Unity, and cut away;
which likewise sharp Medicines will do, if they
</page>

<page no="97">
consist of thick parts; for those of Minute parts
are nor Corrosive, because they stick not long
enough. Again, plenty of Humours may occasi&shy;
on a <term lang="la">Di&aelig;resis</term>, by distending and bursting the parts.
Thirdly, There are several evident causes of a
<term lang="la">Di&aelig;resis</term>; to wit, all those which by Contusion and
Stretching, do break the Unity of the Vessels; such
as are Vehement Motion Noise, great Weight,
things that Wound, that Bruise, a Fall, a Leap, and
the like; amongst which, you may reckon Wind,
which being long pent up, does sometimes so for&shy;
cibly distend the parts of the Body, that it does
not onely Dilate the natural Cavities which con&shy;
tain it, but make new, when it breaks out, and
dissolves the Unity of the parts also; a Chyrur&shy;
gical Operation, which either by Incision, Burn&shy;
ing, Perforating, Shaving, Filing, Sawing, or 
Eating, solves the Continuity of parts.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Di&aelig;ta</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="diet(n)">Diet, is a method in sound Persons of
living moderately; in Sick, a Remedy consisting
in the right use of things necessary to life; and
upon that account is either of a <f type="i">thick</f>, <f type="i">moderate</f>,
or <f type="i">thin</f> consistence: the first is done by a good
quantity of firm solid Meats, and such as afford
good nourishment; this sort of Diet is called <f type="i">sim&shy;
ply full</f>, and was formerly made of whole Barley&shy;
corns husked and boyled, like Furmety: or it is
<f type="i">more full and thick</f>, which is done by Pullets flesh,
and poched Eggs: or it is <f type="i">most full</f>, which allows
of eating of things Gelt: that of a <f type="i">moderate</f> con&shy;
sistence, is which consists of Meats of a moderate
quantity and substance; this was formerly done
by Bread sopt in Pottage, or with young tender 
Flesh: that of a <f type="i">thin</f> consistence is, which is done
</page>

<page no="98">
by little Nourishment, and that thin and weak;
which for the most part is agreeable in sharp Dis&shy;
eases: and this is Threefold, either <f type="i">simply weak</f>,
which was formerly done by the juice of <f type="i">Ptisane</f>:
or <f type="i">more weak</f>, when the Patient drunk Water and
Honey boiled together: or <f type="i">weakest of all</f>, when
the Patient took no meat; but now-adays Diets
are not so strictly observed as formerly; especi&shy;
ally in these Countries.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Di&aelig;tetica</form> <xpln lang="en">is a part of Physick that prescribes
the use and knowledge of Six things which are
not Natural.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Diagnosis</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Knowledge of present signs
or a knowledge whereby we understand the pre&shy;
sent condition of a Distemper; and it is Three&shy;
fold, either a right instigation of the <f type="i">part Affected</f>,
of the <f type="i">disease</f> it self, or of its Cause.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dialeimma</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Apyrexia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Diapasma</form>, <xpln lang="en">according to <f type="i">Pliny</f>, is a dry Medi&shy;
cine, made up of dry Powders, to be sprinkled
upon something; as either upon Clothes to Per&shy;
fume them, or upon Ulcers, and Wounds, several
ways; or upon Drink, to make it more Delicious.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Diapedesis</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Eruption of the Blood, by rea&shy;
son of the thinness of the Vessels.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Diaphanum</form> <xpln lang="en">is that which is Transparent, as the
Humors of the <f type="i">Eyes</f>, the <term lang="la">Tunica Cornea</term>, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Diaphoresis</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="sweating(n)">Sweating, is a Perspiration of all
manner of <term lang="la">Effluvia</term> through the invisible pores of
the Body.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Diaphragma</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Septum Transversum</term>, and <term lang="la">Dis&shy;
septum</term>, is a Transverse <f type="i">Muscle</f> which separates the
Thorax or Chest from the Abdomen; in the mid&shy;
dle it is Membranous; the Gullet, the great Ar&shy;
</page>

<page no="99">
terie, and the great hollow Vein, all pass through
it: it conduces to respiration with other Muscles,
and pressing upon the Guts, helps forward the
Secretion of the Excrements.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Diaphrattontes</form> <xpln lang="en">are Membranes called <term lang="la">Pleura</term>,
which cover the inside of the Thorax, and leave
a kind of partition in the middle, called <term lang="la">Mediasti&shy;
num</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Diaphthora</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Corruption of any part of the
Body.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Diaplasis</form> <xpln lang="en">is the setting of a Limb out of joynt.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Diaplasina</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="ointment(n)" lexeme="fomentation(n)">is an Ointment or Fomentation.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Diapnoe</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Diaphoresis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Diapyema</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Empyema</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Diapyetica</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines which ripen the Pus,
or Crass snotty Matter.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Diaria febris</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Ephemera</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Diarrh&aelig;a</form> <xpln lang="en">is a looseness in the Belly which Ejects
several Bilious, Pituitous, and other f&aelig;culent Ex&shy;
crements.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Diarthrosis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a good constitution of the Bones, 
whereby they are apt to move easily and strong&shy;
ly; such as is in the Arm, Hands, Thigh, Foot,
<term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Diastole</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="dilatation of the heart(n)">is the Dilatation of the Heart, when
the Blood flows into it, from the place where it
is accended, the Lungs.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Diateretica</form> <xpln lang="en">is part of the art of preserving
Health, which is various according to the Age
and Constitution of Men.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Diathesis</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Natural or Pr&aelig;ternatural Dis&shy;
position of the Body, whereby we are inclined to
perform all Natural Actions, ill or well.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dichophyia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a fault in the Hair, when it parts.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="100">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dicrotus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Pulse that beats twice.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Didymi</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="twins(n)">are twins.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dies Critici</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Critici dies</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Digastricus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a double-bellied Muscle, which
arises from the Process called <term lang="la">mammiformis</term>, or like
a Teat, and ends in the inner middle part of the
Chin, and draws it downwards.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Digerentia</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">pr&aelig;parantia</term>, are those things
which change the qualities of fermenting Heat,
which resist Action.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Digestio Chymica</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="chemical digestion(n)">a Chymical Digestion, is when
things are Digested by an Artificial heat, just as
they are naturally in the Stomach.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Digestiva</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Digerentia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dilatatio</form> <xpln lang="en">is when any Passages or Receptacles
in the Body are too much distended, as in Veins
that swell with Melancholy, corrupt Blood in the 
Temples, Legs, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dilatatorium</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Chyrurgeons Instrument
wherewith the Womb or the Mouth is dilated or
opened. It is called likewise <term lang="la">Speculum</term>, because by 
it one may see into the Mouth, or the Womb.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dilutum</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">infusio</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dinus</form> <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Vertigo</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Diota</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Vessel that surrounds a thing; so cal&shy;
led from its Two Ears, which Environ both Arms,
applyed to its sides: its Inferior part is made
like a Cupping-glass, upon which an Alembic is 
put, wherein there is a Channel at the top which
serves to pour Liquor in; and it has besides two
crooked Noses conveniently placed, which convey
the Condensed Humor from the Head of the In&shy;
strument into the Cucurbite.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dioptra</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Instrument whereby one may see
</page>

<page no="101">
into the Matrix, otherwise called <term lang="la">Dilataterium</term>,
wherewith the Womb is dilated and enlarged in
the extraction of a dead <term lang="la">F&oelig;tus</term> out of it, or in in&shy;
specting any Ulcers that are in it.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Diplasiasmus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Reduplication of Diseases: also
Two Muscles of the Arm, which serve to turn it 
about.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Diploe</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="double vessel(n)">is the lower thin plate or shell of the
Scull: also a double Vessel usual with Chymists.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Diploma, <term lang="en">the same with</term> Diploe</form>: <xpln lang="en" lexeme="complicated cloth(n)" lexeme="folded cloth(n)">sometimes it is
taken for a complicated or folded cloth.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dipsacus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Diabetes</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dislocatio</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Luxatio</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dispensatorium</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="dispensatory(n)">a Dispensatorie, is a Book useful
for <f type="i">Apothecaries</f>, wherein all Medicines, at least
the most usual, are contained, and prescribed;
that they may be prepared in the Shops all the
Year round.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dispositio</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Habit whereby we are well or
ill disposed to perform an Action.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dissimilares partes</form>, <xpln lang="en">Dissimilar parts, are such as
can be divided into various parts different from 
one another; as the hand into Veins, Muscles,
Bones, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dissolutio</form> <xpln lang="en">is when Electuaries and Powders are
mingled and dissolved in water or a decoction.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Distentio</form> <xpln lang="en">is when parts are puffed up, dilated,
or relaxed by any thing, as the Guts by Wind, rai&shy;
sed from Effervencies within them, whence Op&shy;
ressions and Pains frequently proceed.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Distorsio</form> <xpln lang="en">is when parts are ill placed, or ill figu&shy;
red.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Distributio Chyli</form>, <xpln lang="en">the Chyle is distributed when
after a due fermentation in the Ventricle and the
</page>

<page no="102">
Guts, it soaks into the little Teats in the Intestines,
(which Dr. <f type="i">Willis</f> calls the Glandulous Tunic)
and passing through the Lacteal Veins, and its 
proper Channel along the side of the Thorax, at 
last falls into the Subclavian Vein, that it may 
Circulate with the Blood, and receive its Co&shy;
lour.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Districheasis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a double row of Hair on the
Eye-lids.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dieuresis</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Secretion of the Urine by the
Reins; which is done after this manner: there
are little Glandules placed near the Emulgent
Arteries, wherewith the <term lang="la">Serum</term> is separated from
the Blood, and is conveyed by little Channels (of
which the substance of the Reins does principally
consist) to the <term lang="la">Caruncul&aelig; Papillares</term>, little Pappie
pieces of Flesh, thence to the <term lang="la">Pelvis</term>, the Basin,
thence to the Ureters, thence to the Bladder, and
so out of Dores.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Diuretica</form>, <xpln lang="en">are those Medicines which by parting,
dissolving, and funding the Blood, do precipitate
the <term lang="la">Serum</term> by the Reins to the Bladder.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dodecadactylum</form> <xpln lang="en">is the first of the small Guts,
beginning from the Pylorous of the Stomach, and
ending where the Gut <term lang="la">jejunum</term> begins: it is so
called, as if it were the length of Twelve Fingers,
which yet is never observed in any men amongst 
us; perhaps the Ancients mistook from inspect&shy;
ing the Guts of some Brutes.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dogmatica Medicina</form>, <xpln lang="en">or rational: <f type="i">Hippocrates</f>
was its first Author, and after him <f type="i">Galen</f>; who
both added reason to experience.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dolor</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="pain(n)">Pain, the same with  <term lang="la">Algema</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dolor Nephriticus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Nephritis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dosis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a set quantity of Physick, or as much as

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dracunculus</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="ulcer(n)">is an Ulcer which eats through a

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Drastica</form> <xpln lang="en">are the most ready Medicines.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dropacismus</form> <xpln lang="en">is that wherewith all the External
Members being extenuated, loosened, cold and
moist, are anointed; and it is either <f type="i">Simple</f> or <f type="i">Com&shy;
pound</f>: the <f type="i">Simple</f> is made of a little Pitch melted
with Oyl: The <f type="i">Compound</f>, besides that, has Pepper,
wild Pellitory, Brimstone, and Rosemary-seed in
it; and if there be occasion for drying, they add
<f type="i">Natural Brimstone</f>, as it is digged out of the Earth,
<f type="i">Salt</f>, and the <f type="i">Ashes</f> of <f type="i">Vine-branches</f>: but if it be
to <f type="i">Vellicate</f>, then you must add <f type="i">Euphorbium</f>, (a
Tree first found by King <f type="i">Juba</f>) it is made up in
different Forms; sometimes like an <term lang="la">Emplastrum</term>,
other times like a <term lang="la">Cataplasme</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Dropax</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Dropacismus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ductus bilarius</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Porus bilarius</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ductus chyliferus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Vessel, in the lower part 
whereof, all the Lacteal Veins, and many Lym&shy;
pheducts are terminated: it arises about the Glan&shy;
dule of the Kidney on the left side; and ascending
</page>

<page no="104">
along the Thorax near the great Arterie, ends at
the Subclavian Vein on the left side; it is furnish&shy;
ed with several Valves, that the Matter which as&shy;
cends by it, may not fall down again: betwixt
the Fourth and Sixth Vertebre it is variously for&shy;
ked as Nature has been pleased to sport. Its use
is to convey the Chyle and the Lympha from the
lower parts to the Heart.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ductus pancreaticus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="pancreas(n)" lexeme="sweetbread(n)">is a little Channel which ari&shy;
ses from the Pancreas or Sweet-bread, which is
inserted into the Guts near, or not far off the
passage which conveys the Bile; it runs with a
Lymphatic juice, which it discharges into the Gut
<term lang="la">Duodenum</term>, to ferment and volatise the Meat from
the Acid ferment of the Stomach, and the mix&shy;
ture of Gall: The Learned Dr. <f type="i">Graaf</f> knew how
to get a juice out of it, that was something Acid;
though other Physicians doubt of it, and of cer&shy;
tain Diseases which the Excellent <f type="i">Sylvius</f> Attri&shy;
butes to the Effervescence of this Acid Pancrea&shy;
tic juice, with the Gall in the <term lang="la">Duodenum</term>. But we
Affirm, That there is sometimes an Acid juice
found in it, and often a salt and austere; but fre&shy;
quently an insipid volatile Liquor. See my <f type="i"><emend err="An">Ana</emend>&shy;
tomie Reformed. Chap.</f> 11. <f type="i">l</f>. I.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ductus Roriferus</form>, <xpln lang="en">so the Noble <f type="i">Bilsius</f> calls it;
the same with <term lang="la">Ductus Chyliferus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ductus Salivares</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Salivarii</term>, are passages which 
proceeding from the Maxilarie Glandules, goes
as far as the Jaws and sides of the Tongue, where
they emit the juice we call Spittle, which con&shy;
duces to the better chewing and swallowing of
solid Meat, and something to its Fermentation
too.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Effervescentia</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Intestine Motion of Particles

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Electuarium</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Confection of Simple Ingredi&shy;

or Honey, of a Consistence like a Conserve;
and it is either <f type="i">Simple</f>, or <f type="i">Compound</f>; the <f type="i">Simple</f>
consists onely of the Pith of <f type="i">Cassia</f>, <f type="i">Tamarinds</f>, or
<f type="i">Pruines</f>; but the <f type="i">Compound</f>, for the most part of 
several <f type="i">Simple</f> Ingredients, Pulps, condensated
