</page>

<page no="109">
rup. <f type="i">Electuaries</f> are Digestive, Loosning, Purg&shy;
ing, Strengthning, Alexipharmic, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Elementa, <term lang="en">or</term> Principia</form>, <xpln lang="en">are the Simplest Bodies 
that can be, which are neither made of one ano&shy;
ther, nor of any thing else, of which all things
are made, and into which they are ultimately re&shy;
solved. There are Five Elements, Spirit, Salt,
Sulphur, Water, and Earth; the two last whereof
are called <f type="i">Passive</f>, the rest <f type="i">Active</f>. Others reckon
Three only, Salt, Sulphur, and Mercury; but not
so well. The <f type="i">Peripateticks</f> reckon Four, Fire,
Air, Water, and Earth. <f type="i">Cartesius</f> supposes a First
Matter, a Second, and a Third; but all those
Elements are compounded of others; wherefore
to say, that any thing consists thereof, is as if one
should say, That a Three is compounded of a
Root, Trunc, Branches, Leaves, Flowers, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Eleosaccharum</form>, <xpln lang="en">is nothing but Distilled Oyl, mix&shy;
ed with Sugar.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Elephantiasis Arabum</form>, <xpln lang="en">of which the <f type="i">Greeks</f> speak
nothing, but the <f type="i">Arabians</f> do frequently, is a kin
to a <term lang="la">varix</term>, or crooked swelling in the Veins; and 
proceeds from thence, and is only a Tumor in the
Feet. <f type="i">Avicenna</f> Treats of this Distemper, where
he speaks of the <term lang="la">varices</term>: yet <f type="i">Rhases</f> differs from
him, and <f type="i">Haly Abbas</f> follows the <f type="i">Greeks</f>; who says,
That an <term lang="la">Elephas</term> is a Disease, which corrupts all
the Members of the Body, and is as it were an 
Universal <f type="i">Cancre</f>: but neither is he consistent with
himself when he Writes, That <f type="i">Ulcers</f> in the Legs
and Feet are called <term lang="la">Elephas</term>; and that <term lang="la">Elephanti&shy;
cus Morbus</term> is an Aposthume proceeding from Me&shy;
lancholy, in the Legs and Feet: and a sign of it,
is that the shape of the Foot is like the figure of an
</page>

<page no="110">
Elephant. All the rest Treat separately of a <f type="i">Le&shy;
prosy</f>, and an <term lang="la">Elephantia</term>, and make the latter to
be a swelling of the Feet, proceeding from Me&shy;
lancholy and Pituitous Blood, and the crooked
swelling of the Veins, whereby the Feet resemble
the Feet of an Elephant in shape and thickness,
and this sort of Tumor is often seen in Beggars
who wander much.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Elephantiasis Grecorum</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="leprosy(n)">which the <f type="i">Arabians</f> call
a <f type="i">Leprosie</f>: it is called also <term lang="la">Elephas</term>, <term lang="la">Elephantiasis</term>,
and <term lang="la">Elephantia</term> from an Elephant; as some think,
because it makes People big like an Elephant:
which is a foolish notation of the Word; for the
Body is no bigger, though the Disease be. Others
think it so called, because the Distemper lying
in the Legs, makes them stiff and equal, like an
Elephant: or because 'tis a strong vehement Dis&shy;
ease like an Elephant; with such like stuff. <f type="i">Ga&shy;
len</f> in his Fourteenth Chapter of <f type="i">Tumors</f> says, <f type="i">That
this Disease is called</f> <term lang="la">Saturiasmus</term>, <f type="i">when it first be&shy;
gins, because it makes the face like that of a Satyr.
For the Lips are thick, the Nose swells, the Ears de&shy;
cays, the Jaws are red, the Forehead is set with Tu&shy;
mours, like so many horns.</f> Though others think
it is called <term lang="la">Saturiasmus</term>, because the Persons Affected
are much inclined to Leachery at the beginning,
as <f type="i">Satyrs</f> are. <f type="i">Celcus</f> Describes it thus, <f type="i">The whole
Body</f>, says he, <f type="i">is so affected, that the very bones may
be said to be Corrupted: the upper parts of the Body
are full of Spots and Tumours, the Redness whereof 
is gradually turned into Black: the top of the Skin
is unequally Thick, Thin, Hard, Soft, Rough, as if it
had Scales on it; the Body decays, the Bone, Calves of 
the Legs, and Feet swell: when the Disease is old and</f>
</page>

<page no="111">
<f type="i">inveterate, the Toes and Fingers are hid in the swel&shy;
ling, and a small Fever arises which easily consumes
a man loaden with so many Infirmities.</f></xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Elevator,</form> <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Elevatorium</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Elevatorium</form>, <xpln lang="en">so called from lifting up, is a Chy&shy;
rurgions Instrument wherewith Sculls that are de&shy;
pressed are raised up again.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Elixir</form>, <xpln lang="en">so called from the <f type="i">Arabic</f> Word <term lang="ar">Elec&shy;
schir</term>, or <term lang="ar">Elieschir</term>, or <term lang="ar">Eleschus</term>; is the Essence of any
thing Extracted with the Spirit of Wine, or some&shy;
thing of that Nature; it is the same that a Tin&shy;
cture.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Elminthes</form> <xpln lang="en">are little Worms bred in the Guts;
especially that called <term lang="la">Rectum</term>, the lowermost.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Elodes</form> <xpln lang="en">is a continual Fever, wherein the Patients
are almost melted through moisture.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Elythroides, <term lang="en">or</term> Vaginalis</form>, <xpln lang="en">is the second proper
<f type="i">Tunic</f> which mediately involves the Testicles.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Embrocatio</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Embroche</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Embrocha</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Embroche</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Embroche</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="irregulation(n)" lexeme="instillation(n)" lexeme="sanders(n)">an irregulation, or instillation, is a 
sort of Fomentation, when a Liquor is distilled
from on high, like Rain, upon a part, which is ei&shy;
ther done by a Vessel with a Nose that inclines, or
by distillation, or out of an Ewer. First, it is used
in Distempers of the Brain, where the Liquor is
first poured upon the <f type="i">Suturs</f> called <term lang="la">Coronalis</term>, and
is permitted to run by that called <term lang="la">Sagittalis</term>. Se&shy;
condly, it is applyed to the top of the Spinal
Marrow, in Diseases of the Nerves, and is permit&shy;
ted to run down the whole ridge of the Back.
Thirdly, it is used to warm or dry the Ventricle,
and the Liquor is suffered to run through the whole
<term lang="la">Abdomen</term>; and if the Bowels be weak, they ap&shy;
</page>

<page no="112">
ply a Sear-cloth of <term lang="la">Santalum</term> (some <f type="i">English</f> it
<f type="i">Sanders</f>) to the Liver, when they apprehend it
may be over-heated. The matter whereof these
<f type="i">Embroches</f> are made in common Bathe water, a
Decoction, Milk, and Oyl, according as the Di&shy;
stemper of the part, and necessity require.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Embryon</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Rudiment of a Child in the
Womb.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Embryatomia</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Anatomical Dissection of a
<term lang="la">F&oelig;tus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Emetica</form> <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Vomitoria</term>, are Medicines which
with their Pungent Particles contract the <f type="i">Fibres</f>
of the Stomach upwards, and so Eject at the
Mouth whatsoever is offensive to the Stomach;
they are made of Decoctions, Tinctures, and In&shy;
fusions, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. and therefore for the most part are
Liquid.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Emetologia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a description of things that pro&shy;
voke Vomiting.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Emmenagoga</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines which excite the
Courses.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Emmoton</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Liquid Medicine, which is injected
into Ulcers, with a little Instrument which they
use in Wounds, fashioned like a Man's Yard.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Emollientia</form>, <xpln lang="en">softning things, are such as with a 
moderate heat and moisture, dissolve the parts,
which before cohered close, and dissipating others,
make them loose and soft.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Empasma</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with  <term lang="la">Catapasma</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Emphraxis</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="obstruction(n)">is Obstruction in any part.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Emphratica</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Emplattomena</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Emphysema</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="inflammation(n)">is an Inflamation, proceeding from
an Effervencie, or otherwise.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Emphyton Thermon</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="innate heat(n)" lexeme="native spirit(n)">is the innate heat, or heat
</page>

<page no="113">
first sown in the <term lang="la">F&oelig;tus</term> from the Parents Seed,
which afterwards, when Respiration is begun,
and the <term lang="la">F&oelig;tus</term> subsists of it self, decays by degrees.
Both Philosophers and Physitians call this heat
an <f type="i">innate</f> and <f type="i">native Spirit</f>, and say that it con&shy;
sists of Three parts, of a <f type="i">primogenial moisture</f>, an
<f type="i">innate Spirit</f> and <f type="i">Heat</f>. Whence <f type="i">Fernelius</f> defines
<f type="i">innate heat</f>, to be a <f type="i">primogenial moisture every way
qualified with an innate spirit and heat</f>: but these
toys of the Ancients are nothing to us; for 'tis cer&shy;
tain, that <f type="i">Heat</f> belongs onely to new-born creatures.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Empirica Medicina</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="quacking(n)" lexeme="quack(n)" lexeme="mountebank(n)">quacking, is Curing the
Sick by guess, without reason. <term lang="la">Acron Agrigenti&shy;
nus</term> was the first Author of it, who neglecting the
reasons of things, contended himself with bare 
Experience. <f type="i">Quacks</f> first flourished amongst the
<f type="i">&AElig;gyptians</f>; from this Trade came <f type="i">Mountebanks</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Emplastica</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Emplattomena</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Emplastrum</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="plaster(n)">a Plaister, is a Medicine applyed
outwardly to the skin, spread upon Linnen, or
Leather; it is commonly made of Oyls, or of
those things which are of a like consistence with
Oyl; as Swines-grease, Butter, Slimie viscous ex&shy;
tractions from Gums, Roots, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. also of Powders
and Wax, or those things which are of a like con&shy;
sistence with Wax; as Rosin, Pitch, Gum, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.
the Mass whereof being yet hot, is formed 
into a <f type="i">Cylindriacal</f> Figure.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Emplattomena <term lang="en">or</term> Emplastica</form>, <xpln lang="en">are Salves which
so constipate and shut up the pores of the Body, 
that Sulphureous Vapours cannot pass.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Empneumatosis</form> <xpln lang="en">is an alternate dilatation of the
Chest, whereby the <f type="i">Nitrous Air</f> is continually
breathed in, and by the Wind-pipe, and its Bladdery
</page>

<page no="114">
parts is communicated to the Blood to accend it:
but if we inspect the matter narrowly, Inspirati&shy;
on does not seem to depend principally upon the
<term lang="la">Thorax</term>, but upon the contraction of the <f type="i">Membrane</f>
which covers the Wind-pipe, the upper part of
the Gullet, and the Nostrils; for take this away,
and you take away the motion of the Chest, the
Lungs, and the Abdomen.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Emprosthotonos</form> <xpln lang="en">is the continual Contraction of
the Muscles of the Neck towards the fore-parts.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Empyema</form>, <xpln lang="en">properly so called, is a Collection of Pu&shy;
rulent Matter in the Cavity of the <term lang="la">Thorax</term>; but
largely taken, signifies the same in the <term lang="la">Abdomen</term> too.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Empyreumata</form> <xpln lang="en">are little Feverish remains after a
<f type="i">Crisis</f>: also that thick Viscous Matter which sub&shy;
sides to the bottom in Distilled Waters.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Emulgentia vasa</form> <xpln lang="en">are the Arteries and Veins
which pass under the Reins.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Emulsio</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="emulsion(n)">an Emulsion is a Medicine to be Drunk,
made of the Kernal of some Seeds, infused in a
convenient Liquor.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Emuncteria</form> <xpln lang="en">are Cavities into which something is
emptied, as the Pituitous Humour of the Brain into 
the Nostrils; the yellow thickish Humour, which
we call Ear-wax, into the Ears, the Excrements in&shy;
to the Bowels; the Urine into the Bladder, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Enarthresis</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="jointing(n)">is joynting, when the Cavitie that
receives is deep, and the head of the bone that's
inserted is Oblong; as may be seen in the Huccle&shy;
bone, and its Cavitie; in the principal Bone of that
part of the Foot which immediatly succeeds the
Leg, with the Bone call'd <term lang="la">Cymbiforme</term>, or like a Boat.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">En&aelig;mon</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Medicine which stops the Blood, or
which by binding, cooling, or drying, closes the pas&shy;
</page>

<page no="115">
sages of the Vessels which were open, stops or dimi&shy;
nishes the fluidity and violent Motion of the Blood.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">En&aelig;orema</form> <xpln lang="en">is that crass Substance which is sus&shy;
pended in the middle of Urines.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Encanthis</form> <xpln lang="en">is the <term lang="la">Caruncula Lachrymalis</term>, or an Ex&shy;
crescence & Swelling of the inner angles of the eye.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Encathisma</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Insessus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Encephalos</form> <xpln lang="en">is <emend err="whotsoever">whatsoever</emend> is within the compass
of the Scull: as the Brain, the <term lang="la">Cerabellum</term>, the
Oblongated Marrow, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Encharaxis</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Scarificatio</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Encheiresis Anatomica</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a readiness in Dissecti&shy;
ons; when an <f type="i">Anatomist</f> shews the parts of a 
Carcase dexterously.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Enchymoma</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="afflux of blood(n)">is an Afflux of the Blood, whereby
the External parts are rendred black and blew;
as in the Scurvey, Blood shot Eyes, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. also an
Afflux of Blood, by the quickness and suddenness
of its Motion, as in Anger and Joy.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Enchyta</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Instrument wherewith Liquids
are instilled into the Eyes, Nostrils, or Ears.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Enclysma</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <f type="i">Clyster</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Encope</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Incision of any part, as in a <f type="i">Gangrene</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Encranium</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Cerebellum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Endeixis</form> <xpln lang="en">is an indication of Diseases, whereby
is shown what is to be done: as for Example, a
<term lang="la">Plethora</term>, too much fullness of blood, indicates
the opening of a Vein.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Endemius, <term lang="en">or</term> Morbus Vernaculus, <term lang="en">and</term> Communis</form>, <xpln lang="en">
is a Disease which always infects a great many in
the same Country, proceeding from some cause
peculiar to the Countrey where it reigns. Such
is Scurvie to the <f type="i">Hollanders</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Endemus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Endemius</term>.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="116">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Enema</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <f type="i">Clyster</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Energia</form> <xpln lang="en">is an agitation or operation of the Ani&shy;
mal Spirits and Blood.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Engizoma</form> <xpln lang="en">is a blow upon the Skull, wherewith
the bone descends to the inner Membrane of the
Brain, and presses upon it. Also an Instrument
which we use in such like cases.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Engonios</form> <xpln lang="en">is the bending of the Arm or Leg.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ensiformis Cartilago</form> <xpln lang="en">is the lowest part of the
Brest-bone, pointed like a Sword.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Entera</form> <xpln lang="en">are long Membraceous Winding-pipes,
annexed to the Mesenterie, that they be not
confounded with one another; and they are
six (unless you reckon the Gullet, the Stomach, 
and the Bladder amongst the Intestines, which I
should not stand upon, since they have the same
substance, and almost the same action) the Gut
<term lang="la">Duodenum, Jejunum, Ileum, C&aelig;cum, Colon</term>, and the
<term lang="la">Rectum</term>; the Three uppermost are called <f type="i">small</f>
Guts, the lower <f type="i">great</f> Guts, they are clothed with
Four <f type="i">Tunics</f>; the outermost is <f type="i">Membranous</f>,
which arises from the <term lang="la">P&aelig;ritoneum</term>: The Second is
<f type="i">Fibrous</f> or Fleshie, whose Exteriour <f type="i">Fibres</f> are
<f type="i">long</f>, the Interior <f type="i">round</f>, placed upon one another
at Right Angles: The Third is <f type="i">Nervous</f>, and
contains the meetings of both Lacteal and San&shy;
guinarie Vessels, to which there inwardly adheres
a Fourth <f type="i">Tunic</f>, which is <emend err="Glandulons">Glandulous</emend>, or rather
of a pappie Substance, whereby the Chyle is imbi&shy;
bed and communicated to the Milkie Veins. The
Intestines, for the most part are about six times as
long as the Man whose they are. Some take <term lang="la">Lactes</term>
to signifie the small Guts only; others take them
for fat Guts, as particularly <f type="i">Persius</f>.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="117">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Enterenchyta</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="clyster-pipe(n)">is a Clyster-pipe, which is also cal&shy;
led <term lang="la">Siphon</term>, and <term lang="la">Syringa</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Enterocele, <term lang="en">or</term> Hernia Intestinalis</form><xpln lang="en">is the fall of the
Intestines, especially of the <term lang="la">Ileum</term>, through the
Processes of the <term lang="la">Peritoneum</term> Dilated, into the Groins
or outer skin that covers the Cods.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epacmastica</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="fever(n)">is a Fever that continually grows
stronger.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epaph&aelig;resis</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="phlebotomy(n)">is an iterated <f type="i">Phlebotomie</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epar</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Hepar</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Eparmata</form> <xpln lang="en">are Tumors of the Glandules cal&shy;
led <term lang="la">Parotes</term>, behind the Ears.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Eph&aelig;beum</form> <xpln lang="en">is the place from the <term lang="la">Hypogastrium</term>,
or lower part of the <term lang="la">Abdomen</term>, to the Secret Parts.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ephelscis</form> <xpln lang="en">is that Bloody substance which is brought
up in spitting of Blood: also a shell or crust that
is brought over Ulcers.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ephelis</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="freckle(n)">is a dewie Spot, we call it a <f type="i">Freckle</f>,
which proceeds most commonly from Sun-burn;
they grow especially in Spring and Summer, and 
chiefly in those who have very thin Skins; but
about Winter they disappear again: they are
about as big as Flea-bites, and often disfigure
the whole face.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ephemera</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="fever(n)">or <term lang="la">Diaria</term>, is a continued Fever which
lasts but a day, arising from a Commotion and
Accension of the fine parts of the Blood: if it
last above a day, it is called <term lang="la">Synochus Simplex</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ephialtes, <term lang="en">or</term> Incubus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="nightmare(n)">the Night-mare, is a de&shy;
praved Imagination, whereby people asleep fan&shy;
cie that their Wind-pipe is oppressed by some su&shy;
perincumbent body, that their breath is stop'd,
and they are excited to Venerie: this proceeds
from a compression of the <term lang="la">Cerebellum</term>, when the
</page>

<page no="118">
Ventricles are too full of moisture: or, if those
who are thus Affected lye upon their backs, then
the whole bulk of the Brain lies upon the <term lang="la">Cere&shy;
bellum</term>, whereupon all the Pores and Passages
being stopped by so much weight, the Spirits are
hindred from Influencing the Nerves, called <term lang="la">par
vagum</term>, and the <f type="i">Intercostal Nerve</f>, which being thus
destitute of Spirits, the Lungs are oppressed, and
flag, and cannot perform their office.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ephidrosis</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="sweating(n)">is Sweating.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ephippium, <term lang="en">or</term> Sella Equina, <term lang="en">or</term> Tursica</form>, <xpln lang="en">is part of
the Bone <term lang="la">Sphenoides</term>, wherein the <term lang="la">Pituitarie Glan&shy;
dul&aelig;</term> is placed.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epiala</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="fever(n)">is a continued Fever, wherein the Pati&shy;
ent feels both Heat and Cold at once.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epialtes</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Ephialtes</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epicarpium</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Medicine applyed outwardly,
like a Plaister or a <f type="i">Cataplasme</f>, applied to the
Pulse or Wrist of the hand to drive away inter&shy;
mitting Feavers.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epicauma</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="ulcer(n)">is a Crustie Ulcer that sometimes hap&shy;
pens to the black of the Eye.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epicerastica</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines which obtund and
temperate sharp Humours.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epicheiresis</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Encheiresis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epicolic&aelig; regiones <term lang="en">or</term> Laterales, <term lang="en">or</term> Lumbares</form>. <xpln lang="en">
<f type="i">Glisson</f> calls that part <term lang="la">Epicolica</term> which lyes up&shy;
on the parts of the Gut <term lang="la">Colon</term>: whence it has its
Name.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epicrasis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a gradual Evacuation of ill Humors
in the Blood.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epicrisis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a judging of a Disease.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epicrusis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a percussion of the soft parts, with
light <term lang="la">Ferula's</term>, an usual Custome amongst the <f type="i">Ja&shy;
paneses</f>.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="119">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epicyema</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="superfaetation(n)">is a Superf&aelig;tation, which rarely hap&shy;
pens.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epidemius</form> <xpln lang="en">is a common Disease, proceeding from 
a common Cause, spreading it self over divers
Countries, at divers times; such are the Plague,
Malignant Fevers, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. the reason is, that the <f type="i">Ni&shy;
tre</f> of the air, with other particles that are in it,
acquire the Vertue of an <f type="i">Arcenic</f>, or a <f type="i">Sublimate</f>,
as we see in making <f type="i">Sublimates</f>; for the Particles
of which that consists, if they be given severally,
are not so destructive; but taken together, they 
make a deadly Poyson.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epidermis</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Cuticula</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epedesis</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Injection of a Ligament, to stop
the Blood.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epidesmus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a tying of Swathes underneath.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epididymis <term lang="en">or</term> Paristata</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="winding vessel(n)">in Latin <term lang="la">Supergemina&shy;
lis</term>, and it is a winding Vessel, making a Figure
like the winding of crooked Vessels that are swoln
with ill Blood, and is affixed to the back of the
Testicles: its greater Globe is annexed to the
Testicles, consisting of one Vessel or Passage above
five Ells long: the lesser Globe is connected to the
Vessel that carries the Seed.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epigastrium</form> <xpln lang="en">is the fore-part of the lowermost
Belly, whose upper part is called <term lang="la">Hypochondrium</term>;
the middle part <term lang="la">Umbilicalis</term>; and the lowermost
<term lang="la">Hypogastrium</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epigennema</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="symptom(n)">is that which happens to a Disease
like a Symptome: also the order of parts in Ge&shy;
neration, which is done successively.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epiginesis</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Epiginema</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epiglottis</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Fifth Cartilage of the <term lang="la">Larynx</term>,
the cover of the opening of the Wind-pipe: it is 
also called <term lang="la">Sublinguium</term>.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="120">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epigonatis</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="whirlbone of the knee(n)">is the Whirl-bone of the Knee.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epilepsia</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Morbus Caducus</term>, because that the
persons Affected fall down on a sudden: or <term lang="la">Her&shy;
culeus</term>, because it is hard to be cured; also <term lang="la">Lues
Deifica, Sonticus, Comitialis, Sacer</term>, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. and it is 
an Interpolated Convulsion of the whole body,
which hurts all Animal Actions, proceeding from
an Explosion of Animal Spirits in the Brain, where&shy;
by the persons Affected are suddenly cast upon
the ground. This Explosion arises either from an
irritation or pricking in the Spirits: or when some&shy;
thing <f type="i">Heterogeneous</f> is intermixed with the Animal
Spirits.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epilogismus</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Vote of <f type="i">Physitians</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epinyctides</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="pimple(n)">are Pimples that send forth matter,
and are painful, especially in the Night.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epiparoxismus</form> <xpln lang="en">is when a Patient endures more
Fits in a Fever than usual, which happens in inor&shy;
dinate Fevers.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epiph&aelig;nomena</form> <xpln lang="en">are signs which appear afterwards
in Diseases.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epiphisis, Appendix, Adnascentia, Additamentum,</form>
<xpln lang="en">signifie one Bone that grows to another by simple
and immediate Contiguity, through not with so
even a Surface, but with some kind of ingress of
one Bone into the Cavitie of the other, like that
Coarticulation wherewith the Bones form the
Joynts, but without any Motion.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epiplasma</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Cataplasma</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epiplocele</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Rupture when the Cavile falls
into the outward Skin of the Cods.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epiplocomist&aelig;</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="caul-bearer(n)">are fat big-bellied Men, who have
fat huge Cawls; which Writers say, has some&shy;
times hindred Conception in Women; and there&shy;
</page>

<page no="121">
fore they are named Cawl-bearers.</xpln><lemenote>"caul-bearer" not found in OED.</lemenote></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epiplomphalum</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="navel rupture(n)">is a Navel Rupture, when it juts
out by reason of a swoln Cawl that is fallen
down.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epiploon, Omentum, <term lang="en">or</term> Reticula</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="cawl(n)">the Cawl, is a
cover spread over the Intestines, arising from the
bottom of the Ventricle, and the back of the Gut
<term lang="la">Colon</term>; to wit, from the doubling of the <term lang="la">Periton&aelig;&shy;
um</term>; it is shaped like a Net, or a Fowlers Bag;
and abounds with several Sanguinary Vessels. Its 
use is to cherish the Stomach, and the Guts with
its fat.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Episarcidium</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Anasarca</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Episemasia</form> <xpln lang="en">is the very time that a Disease first
seizes a Person, and is properly called <term lang="la">Signifi&shy;
catio</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epision</form> <xpln lang="en">is the place of the Secret Parts, or
<term lang="la">Aqualiculus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Episph&aelig;ria</form> <xpln lang="en">are windings and turnings in the 
outer substance of the Brain, that the Sanguiferous
Vessels may pass more securely.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epispastica</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with  <term lang="la">Attrahentia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epistomia</form> <xpln lang="en">are the utmost gapings and meetings
of Vessels.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epistropheus, <term lang="en">or</term> Cardo</form>, <xpln lang="en">is the second Vertebre of
the Neck; so called from turning, because the
Head turns upon it.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epithema</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Medicine applyed outwardly to
the more Noble parts of the body, especially to
the Heart and Liver.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epneumatosis</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Expiratio</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epomis</form> <xpln lang="en">is the upper part of the Shoulder, called
also <term lang="la">Acronium</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epomphalum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Plaister, or any such thing ap&shy;
</page>

<page no="122">
Plyed to the Protuberances of the Navel.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epsema</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Decoction of new Wine till half be
boyled away.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epulis</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Excrescence in the Gums which
reaches the farthest Axel-Teeth; so that it hinders
the opening of the Mouth.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Epulotica</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Cicatrizantia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Erodentia</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines which gnaw and prey
upon the Flesh, with their Acute Particles.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Erpes</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Herpes</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Errhinum</form>, <xpln lang="en">barbarously called <term lang="la">Nasale</term>, is a Me&shy;
dicine which being made like a Pyramid, is put up
the Nostrils, and cleanses the Brain of Viscous
Humours, especially without sneezing: and it is
either <f type="i">Liquid</f>, <f type="i">Soft</f>, or <f type="i">Solid</f>. The <f type="i">Liquid</f> is made
of the juices of <f type="i">Cephalic</f> cleansing Herbs, Ex&shy;
tracted by Wine or other Liquor, to which Spi&shy;
rit of Wine is sometimes added. Or of a Decoction
of fit Simples, to which are added sometimes
Juices, Honey, Syrup, and Powders too. The
<f type="i">soft</f> is made of Powders, with Honey, Oyl, or
Juices, boiled to a kind of Ointment. The <f type="i">Solid</f>,
is given either in form of a Powder, and that
has place especially in Medicines which provoke
sneezing; or in form of a Pellet, and it is called
<term lang="la">Nasale</term>, and is prepared of fit Powders mixed with
Viscid Extractions from Seeds, Gums, Roots, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.
with Wax, or with Turpentine.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Erysipelas</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="wildfire(n)">Wild-fire, is a swelling in the Skin,
or any other Fleshie or membraneous part,
red, broad, not spreading high, nor beating, but
attended <emend err="wih">with</emend> a pricking sort of pain, arising
from a sharp, and frequently a Sulphureous Blood.
I take the cause of it not to be the Blood, but a
</page>

<page no="123">
serous sweating, which is sharp and sulphureous,
and flows from the Fibres themselves.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Erysipelatodes</form> <xpln lang="en">is a swelling like an <term lang="la">Erysipelas</term>, or 
a bastard <term lang="la">Erysipelas</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Erythremata</form> <xpln lang="en">are red spots like Flea-bites, com&shy;
mon in Pestilential Fevers.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Erythroides</form> <xpln lang="en">is a red Membrane of the Testicles,
the first of the proper Tunics.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Eschara</form> <xpln lang="en">is a crust or shell brought over an Ul&shy;
cer, or raised with a Seering Iron.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Escharoticum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Seering Iron, Fire, or the like,
which burns the Skin and Flesh into a crustie Sub&shy;
stance.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Essentia</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="essence(n)">Essence, in acurate speaking signifies
the <f type="i">Balsamic</f> part of any thing separated from the
thicker matter, so that when ever this is done by
means of Extraction, the <f type="i">Balsamic</f> part is called
Essence by way of Eminence; otherwise some&shy;
times, thickned juices are called Essences. But
'tis better to call these by their own Name, to
avoid Confusion. Some call Compounds of Oyl 
and Sugar, Essences: but it is an abuse of the 
word.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Essentia Quinta</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="quintessense(n)">Quintessence, is a Medicine 
made of the entire Energetical and Active Parti&shy;
cles of its Ingredients.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Essere, Sora, & Sare</form>, <xpln lang="en">they are little Pushes or
Wheals, something red and hard, which quickly
Infect the whole Body with a violent itching, as
if one were stung with Bees, or Wasps, or Flies,
or Nettles; yet they vanish after a little time,
and leave the Skin as smooth and well-coloured
as before. This Disease differs from an <term lang="la">Epinyctis</term>
in this, that an <term lang="la">Epinyctis</term> Sweats out Matter; but
an <term lang="la">Effere</term> does not.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="124">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Esthiomenos</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Winding Inflamation that con&shy;
sumes the parts: it proceeds from this, that the
little Pappie Substance of the Skin, keeps a cer&shy;
tain sharp Humour in it, which for want of Per&shy;
spiration, corrupts and gnaws not onely the Skin
with its Acrimonie, but the parts which are un&shy;
der it.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ethmoides</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Bone which resembles a Sieve,
placed above the inner part of the Nose, and full
of little holes to receive the Serous and Pituitous
Humours from the soft Pappie Processes of the
Brain.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Evacuatio</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="evacuation(n)">Evacuation, is either of the <f type="i">Blood</f>,
when it abounds too much, as in a <term lang="la">Plethora</term>, where
opening a vein is requisite. Or of ill Humours
in the Blood, and the <term lang="la">Prim&aelig; Vi&aelig;</term>, as they call
them, which is done by Purging or Vomi&shy;
ting.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Euchroa</form> <xpln lang="en">is a good colour and temper of the
Skin.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Euchymia</form> <xpln lang="en">is an excellent temper of the Blood.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Eucrasia</form> <xpln lang="en">is an excellent temper of the parts of
the Body.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Euectica</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Gymnastica</term>, or that part
of Physick which teaches how to acquire a good
Habit of Body.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Euelces</form>, <xpln lang="en">one that is troubled with Ulcers, easie
to be cured.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Euexia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a good sound Habit of Body.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Eugeos</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="womb(n)">is the Womb; so called from its Ana&shy;
logie to fruitful Ground; the <f type="i">Hymen</f> is also so 
called.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Euodes</form> <xpln lang="en">is a sweet smell of Excrements.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Euosma</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Euodes</term>.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="125">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Eupathia</form> <xpln lang="en">is an easiness in suffering.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Euphoria</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Eupnoea</form> <xpln lang="en">is a right natural Respiration.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Eurythmus</form> <xpln lang="en">is an excellent natural Pulse.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Eusarcus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="well-fleshed(a)">one that is well fleshed.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Eusema</form> <xpln lang="en">is a <f type="i">Crisis</f> excellently well judged.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Eustomachus</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="good stomach(n)" lexeme="meat(n)">is a good Stomach; as also Meat
convenient for it.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Euthanasia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a soft easie passage out of the
World.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Euthyporos</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="strait gate(n)">is a strait Gate.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Euthropia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a due Nourishment of the Body.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Exacerbatio</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Paroxysmus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Exaltatio <term lang="en">or</term> Sublimatio</form>, <xpln lang="en">is an Operation where&shy;
by a thing being changed in its natural qualifica&shy;
tions, is elevated to an higher degree of Vertue 
and Substance; or it is a Subtilizing of things by
gradually Dissolving them and Exalting them in&shy;
to a purer and higher degree of their own qua&shy;
lities: and it is done either by Circulation, or Ab&shy;
lution.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Exanastomosis</form> <xpln lang="en">is an opening of the Extremitie
of Vessels.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Exanthema</form> <xpln lang="en">is a certain <term lang="la">Efflorescen&aelig;</term> upon the
Skin of the Head, like those which appear in the
skin of the whole Body; it is described two ways 
by <f type="i">Senertus</f>; one is, that at least it changes the
colour of the Skin, as in continued Malignant
Fevers; wherein the skin is spotted as with Flea-&shy;
bites; the other is, when certain little swellings
break out in the Skin, which may be called <term lang="la">Pa&shy;
pill&aelig;</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Exarthrema</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Luxatio</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Exceptio</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Incorporation or Mixture of dry 
</page>

<page no="126">
Powders with some moisture or other; thus Electu&shy;
aries are made, Powders and Pulps are mixed
with Honey, or Syrup: and the powder of Pills
with Syrup, Honey, Wine, or Juice.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Excrementa</form>, <xpln lang="en">Excrements are whatsoever is sepa&shy;
rated from the Aliments after Concoction, and is
to be thrown out of the Body; as the moisture 
in the Mouth, Spittle, Snot, Milk, Bile, Sweat, the
Wax of the Ears, the Excrements of the Belly and
Bladder.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Exelcismus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a bringing of the Bones from the
surface downward.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Exercitatio</form> <xpln lang="en">is a vehement and voluntary Motion
of Humane Body, attended with an Alteration in
Breathing, undertook either for preserving, or ac&shy;
quiring Health.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Excercitium</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Motion whereby the Body is 
agitated in order to Health; and it is Threefold.
1. What proceeds onely from things Extrinsic; 
as in Riding, Navigation, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. 2. What proceeds 
partly from other things, partly from those who
are moved, as in Gladiators, and Wrestlers.
3. What comes from those onely who exercise, as 
in walking, and the Ball; and best of all in Hand-&shy;
ball: the end of Exercise is Threefold likewise;
either Heat, Sweat, or Breath, and this is suffici&shy;
ent.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Exomphalos</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Protuberance of the Navel, com&shy;
mon to Infants.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Exophthalmia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a protuberance of the Eye, out
of its natural Position.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Exostosis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Protuberance of the Bones out of
their Natural Place.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Expiratio</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Alternate Contraction of the
</page>

<page no="127">
Chest, whereby the Air, together with Fuliginous
Vapours is expelled by the Wind-pipe; the cause
of Expiration does not seem to consist in the con&shy;
traction of the Chest, but in the Relaxation of
the Tunic of the upper part of the Gullet, and
the Wind-pipe; for take that away, and you take
away the Motion of the Chest, and Abdomen.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Explosio</form> <xpln lang="en">is an action of the Spirits, whereby
the Nerves are suddenly Contracted; the reason
is, That some <f type="i">Heterogeneous Particles</f> are mixed
with the Animal Spirits or that they are driven
into a confusion, like Gun-power out of a
Gun.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Expulsio</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">vis Expultrix</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Expultrix vis</form>, <xpln lang="en">according to the Ancients, was
that facultie which expell'd the Excrements: but
we need not have recourse to those blind Facul&shy;
ties, since we know that this is performed by the
Animal Spirits, which cause the <f type="i">Peristaltic</f> Motion
of the Guts.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Exstasis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a depravation of the Judgment and
Imagination, familiar to Mad and Melancholy
Persons.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Extasis</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Exstasis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Extirpatio</form> <xpln lang="en">is the cutting of a part, by reason
of a Cancre, or Blasting; it is best to cut it off
Two, Three, or more Fingers breadths from the
Joynt, unless the Mortification have reached the 
upper parts of the Arms, or Thigh; for here we
are forced to chuse the Joynt it self: it is a su&shy;
rer way to make the Excision in a sound part,
though it be more painful.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Extractio</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Separating of the subtle parts 
of a mixed Body, from the more gross: for Ex&shy;
</page>

<page no="128">
ample, when the strength of any Medicine is Ex&shy;
tracted by Spirit of Wine, that which is left after
the Evaporation of the <term lang="la">Menstruum</term> is called the 
Extract.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Extractum</form> <xpln lang="en">is that pure, unmixed, and efficacious
Substance, which by the help of some Liquor is
separated from the duller and more unactive
parts.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Exulceratio</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="exulceration(n)">is a Solution of continued parts,
proceeding from some gnawing Matter, and in
soft parts of the Body, attended with a loss of
their quantity; it differs from an <term lang="la">Abscessus</term> in this, 
that an <term lang="la">Abscessus</term> is occasioned by a <f type="i">Crisis</f>. An Ex&shy;
ulceration is either great, little, broad, short, nar&shy;
row, strait, transverse, winding, equal, inequal,
deep, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>
</wordgroup1>

<wordgroup1 type="a" object="F">F.

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">FAcies Hyppocratica</form> <xpln lang="en">is when the Nostrils are
sharp, the Eyes hollow, the Temples low, the
Laps of the Ears contracted, and the Lobes In&shy;
versed, the Skin about the Forehead hard, and
dry; the Complexion pale, livid, of a leaden 
Colour, or Black.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Facultas</form> <xpln lang="en">is an action in Man, which is perfor&shy;
med, either by the Body alone, or by both Body
and Mind: Faculties are either <f type="i">Natural</f>, which
depends upon the <term lang="la">Cerebellum</term>: or <f type="i">Animal</f>, which
depend upon the Brain. The Ancients made
three Faculties, <f type="i">Natural</f>, <f type="i">Vital</f>, and <f type="i">Animal</f>: but
the <f type="i">Vital</f> belongs to the <f type="i">Natural</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">F&aelig;ces</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Excrementa</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Falx</form> <xpln lang="en">is a doubling of the <term lang="la">Dura Mater</term> like a
</page>

<page no="129">
Sickle, annexed below to the Third Cavitie where&shy;
by the Brain is divided into the right and left
<f type="i">Hemisphere</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fames</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="hunger(n)">Hunger, is either <f type="i">Natural</f>, which is a 
desire of Food, when an Animal from a Vellifi&shy;
cation of a Nerve of the <term lang="la">par vagum</term>, and the
Intercostal in the Stomach, which proceeds
from an Acid Humour, carried thither by the
<f type="i">C&aelig;liac Arteries</f>, or <f type="i">Glandulous Tunic</f>, is excited to
seek for Food as a Remedy to allay that Vellica&shy;
tion; or it is <f type="i">pr&aelig;ternatural</f>, which is either de&shy;
praved, as longing in Women with Child; or
it is a <f type="i">Canine Appetite</f>, want of Appetite, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fames Canina</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Cynodes Orexis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Farciminalis Tunica</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Allantoi&shy;
des</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fascia</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="swathe(n)">a Swathe, is a long Band, moderately
broad, which Chyrurgeons use: Swathes are
wound up; long, and all of a breadth; others are
cut, which are indeed of one piece of Linnen,
but that cut either at the ends, or middle: others
sewed together, which consists of Swathes and
Thongs of several ends, and like several Swathes.
Others are longer, some shorter; and others
broader, some narrower.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fasciatio</form> <xpln lang="en">is a binding of Swathes about a
Limb that is to be Cured.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fasciculus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Manipulus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fastidium Cibi</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Anorexia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fauces</form> <xpln lang="en">and <term lang="la">Frumen</term>, the same that <term lang="la">Pharynx</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Favus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see in <term lang="la">Achor</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Febris</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="fever(n)">a Fever, is an inordinate Motion, and
too <emend err="greata n">great an</emend> Effervescence of the Blood, attended
</page>

<page no="130">
with Cold first, and afterwards with Heat, Thirst,
and other Symptoms, wherewith the Animal
<term lang="la">Oeconomie</term> is variously disturbed. Fevers in ge&shy;
neral are divided into Intermittent, Continued, 
Continent, and Symptomatical. <f type="i">Scotus</f> in his
Magick assures us, <f type="i">That the Blood in a Fever has
Worms in it</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fecul&aelig;</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="dust(n)">are Dust that subsides in the squeezing
of certain Vegetables, as in <f type="i">Brionie, Ramp</f>, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fell</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Bullis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Femur, and Femen</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="thigh(n)">the Thigh, the part from
the Buttocks to the Knee; it is so called from bear&shy;
ing, because it holds up, and sustains an Animal;
it consists but of one Bone, but that the greatest
and longest in the whole Body, whose External
and fore part is gibbous or rising; but the Inter&shy;
nal hinder part flat and bending. <f type="i">Grammarians</f>
make <term lang="la">Femen</term> to be the hinder fleshy part; and
<term lang="la">Femur</term> the former outward part.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fermentatio</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Intestine Motion of Particles,
or of the Principles of any Body, tending to Per&shy;
fection, or a Change: and it is either <f type="i">Natural</f>,
which comes of its own accord, as in Natural
Actions; or <f type="i">Artificial</f>, which we make, as we see
in Beer, Wine, Bread, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ferul&aelig;</form> <xpln lang="en">are little light chips or planes, which are
made of different Matter, according to the nature
and necessities of the places to which they are
applyed, as of Barks of Trees, of the Bark of 
the Herb <f type="i">Sagapene</f>, in Latin <term lang="la">Ferula</term>; whence they
have their Name: they are made of Firr, Paper
glewed together, Leather, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. which are applyed
to Bones that have been loosened, or disjoynted
</page>

<page no="131">
after they are set again.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fibra Auris</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Lobus Auris</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fibr&aelig;</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="fibre(n)">Fibres, are little, round, oblong Vessels,
and are either <f type="i">Musculous</f> or <f type="i">Nervous</f>: the <f type="i">Ner&shy;
vous</f> are such as have no Valves, and by which
the Spirits flow conveniently from the Nerves to
the several parts: the <f type="i">Musculous</f> Fibres receive
the Blood from the Arteries, and discharge them&shy;
selves into the Veins, and have a great many Valves,
they are called long, round, or oblique from their
Scituation; some small threads interwoven with 
Trees and Leaves are called Fibres too: and so
are the small threads which stick to their Roots.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fibula</form>, <xpln lang="en">the Ancients mention them; for if there
be a Wound in the Flesh, says <f type="i">Celsus</f>, that gapes,
and cannot easily be closed, it is improper to
sew it, you must apply a <term lang="la">Fibula</term>; but because 
this way of closing the gaping of Wounds, by 
<term lang="la">Fibula</term>'s was so usual amongst the Ancients; they
have not been at all sollicitous in describing either
their Matter or Form. <f type="i">Guido</f> tells us, That they 
made these <term lang="la">Fibula</term>'s of Iron Circles as it were, or
Semi-circles crooked backward on both sides, the
hooks whereof being fastned on both sides to
the gaping Wound, answered exactly one ano&shy;
ther; but since this must be an unsupportable
pain to the poor Patient, it is hardly credible,
that they meant any such thing by their <term lang="la">Fibula</term>'s.
The Opinion of <f type="i">Fallopius</f> is more probable, who
tells us, That it was onely a sowing up the Wound
with a Needle and Thread, which is commonly 
used at this day. <f type="i">Sanctorius</f> writes thus, We
need not Discourse much of <term lang="la">Fibula</term>'s, since the
</page>

<page no="132">
use of them is almost out of dores; and though
the Ancients have not described them, yet they
forbear not to acquaint us how to use them; as
<f type="i">Argenterius</f> falsly imagines. For not onely Phy&shy;
sicians but some of the Ancients knew the form of 
them, since <f type="i">Corn.</f> <f type="i">Celsus</f> has informed us, That <term lang="la">Fi&shy;
bula's</term> as well as <f type="i">Sutures</f> were made of a Needle-full
of soft untwisted silk or thread, wherewith they
sowed the gaping Lips of the Wound together.
Some call <term lang="la">Acia</term>, or this needle-ful of Thred, <term lang="la">Vincu&shy;
lum</term>, <term lang="la">Ligatura</term>, <term lang="la">Colligatio</term>, <term lang="la">Obligatio</term>, <term lang="la">Ligamentum</term>;
all which signifie tying or binding. Whoever
would be farther informed in this particular, may
consult the Incomparable <f type="i">Rhodius</f> in his Discourse
about <term lang="la">Acia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fibula</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="lesser bone of the shank(n)">is the lesser Bone of the Shank, it seems 
to joyn the Muscles of the Leg like a Button, or
Clasp, in Latin <term lang="la">Fibula</term>; it is the hinder bone
betwixt the Knee and the Foot, smaller than the
other Bone, called <term lang="la">Tibia</term>, and fastned outwardly
to it; as the Bone called <term lang="la">Radius</term> in the Arm is to
the Cubit: its round head does not extend as far
as the Knee upward, but downward, it goes far&shy;
ther than the other Bone called <term lang="la">Tibia</term>, and there&shy;
fore is altogether as long a Bone as the <term lang="la">Tibia</term>. They
part in the middle, because the Muscles of the
Feet are placed there; in which interval, a slen&shy;
der broad Ligament joyns them together length&shy;
ways. It is joyned likewise to the <term lang="la">Tibia</term> with a 
common Ligament above and below; as it tends
acutely downwards it has an Appendix belong&shy;
ing to it, which growing thicker and thicker,
makes a Process, called <term lang="la">Malleolus Externas</term>.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="133">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ficus</form> <xpln lang="en">are Excrescencies about the Fundament
and other parts, like Figs; if they grow big, then 
they are called <term lang="la">Ficus</term>, or <term lang="la">Sycoses</term></xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Filtratio</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Percolating any Liquor through
a woollen Cloth, or course Paper.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">FIltram</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="woollen cloth(n)" lexeme="blotting paper(n)" lexeme="wine-sack(n)">is a woollen Cloth, or blotting Paper,
through which Liquors are strained to Clarifie:
as through a <term lang="la">Manca Hippocratis</term>, a Wine-sack
which draws Wine from the dregs.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fissura ossis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a fracture of a Bone length-&shy;
ways.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fistula</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="cavity(n)" lexeme="ulcer(n)">is a strait long Cavity, or a winding,
narrow and callous Ulcer, of difficult Cure; pro&shy;
ceeding for the most from an Aposteme. <term lang="la">Fistu&shy;
la's</term> differ from winding Ulcers in this, that <term lang="la">Fistu&shy;
la's</term> are callous and hard, but Ulcers are not.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fistula Lachrymalis</form> <xpln lang="en">is when the <term lang="la">Punctum Lachry&shy;
male</term>, the little hole in the bone of the Nose,
through which the Liquid Matter passes to the
Nostrils, is grown hard and callous, from an Ul&shy;
cer of a <term lang="la">Caruncula</term>, <f type="i">Glandules</f> placed at the grea&shy;
ter corners of the Eye, by which means there hap&shy;
pens a continual Defluxion of Tears.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fistula Pulmonis</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Aspera Arte&shy;
ria</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fistula Sacra</form>, <xpln lang="en">is that part of the Back-bone
which is Perforated.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fistula Urinaria</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Urethra</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Flatus</form> <xpln lang="en">are Effervescencies excited in the Body
from wind let in, or from Flatulent Meats, or from
the Bile and Pancreatic juice mixed together,
whence wind and noise.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Flores Chymici</form> <xpln lang="en">are the Subtiler parts of the Bo&shy;
</page>

<page no="134">
dy separated from the grosser by Sublimation, in
a dry Form.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fluor Albus</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Fluor Uterinus</term>, is a continual Eva&shy;
cuation of corrupt Humors from the Womb, or
the Pores in the <term lang="la">Vagina</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fluor Muliebris</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Fluor Albus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fluor Uterinus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fluxio</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Catarrhus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fluxus Chylosus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">C&aelig;liaca passio</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fluxus Hepaticus</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="dysentery(n)">is a kind of Dysentery, where&shy;
in black shining blood, and too long rosted as it
were, is driven out of the Guts by the Funda&shy;
ment: it is sometimes taken for a Dysentery
wherein serous sharp Blood is evacuated.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Focile Majus</form> <xpln lang="en">is the greater Bone of the Cubit
called <term lang="la">Ulna</term>; or the greater bone of the Leg
called <term lang="la">Tibia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Focile Minus</form> <xpln lang="en">is the lesser Bone of the Cubit cal&shy;
led <term lang="la">Radius</term>, or the lesser bone of the Leg, cal&shy;
led <term lang="la">Fibula</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Focus</form> <xpln lang="en">is some place in the Misenterie and other
parts, whence they formerly deduced the Origi&shy;
nal of Fevers.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fodina</form> <xpln lang="en">is the less Labyrinth in the bone of the
Ears.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">F&oelig;cula</form> <xpln lang="en">signifies a Powder which subsides to
the bottom in certain strainings of Vegetables; for
it is prepared of some green, washed, and pared
Roots beat together, with a little water, then
strained, that there may subside a white sort of
Powder which is to be dryed lightly.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">F&oelig;tor oris</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="stinking breath(n)">a stinking Breath, proceeds from
the filth about the Teeth, and Gums: sometimes
from the Lungs, and a Consumptive or Scorbu&shy;
tic Blood.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="135">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Folliculus Fellis</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="bladder(n)">is a little Bladder fastned to the
Concave-part of the Liver, which receives the Bile,
which in proper time empties it self into the Gut
<term lang="la">Duodenum</term>, by a Ductus, or Passage called <term lang="la">Chole&shy;
dochus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fomentum</form>, <xpln lang="en">that which applyed to the Body che&shy;
rishes and warms it; and it is Twofold, either
wet, or dry; the latter is a Decoction applyed to
several parts of the Body for to cherish it, by the 
help of a linnen, or wollen Cloth, a Spunge, Blad&shy;
der, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fontanell&aelig;</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="issue(n)">Issues, are little Ulcers which Chy&shy;
rurgions make in sound parts of the Body, to
Evacuate bad Humors, Cure Diseases, or prevent
them. Issues are made either with an Actual or
a Potential Seering-Iron, with a Lance, and a 
pair of Scissers: You must always observe to make
Issues betwixt two Muscles.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fonticuli</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Forceps</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Instrument wherewith dead and
corrupt parts, (also things besides, or against Na&shy;
ture) are seised, cut off, or pulled out; they are
of several shapes, as long, crooked, with Teeth, 
with Beeks, in fashion of an half Moon, such as
will open the Mouth, or the Womb; and by
which you may see into either of them: which
according to the difference of their shape, are of
different use.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Forfex</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Instrument to pull out Teeth
with.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Formula</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Physitians Prescription, which the
Apothecaries prepare accordingly.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fornix</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Callous Substance of the Brain;
</page>

<page no="136">
so called, because it seems to sustain the Cavities
of the Ventricles, and the bulk of the impending
Brain, like an Arch or Vault.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fotus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Fomentum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fovea Cordis</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Anticardium</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fractura Ossis</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="breaking of a bone(n)">the breaking of a Bone, is a So&shy;
lution of the <term lang="la">Continuum</term> in the hard parts of the
Body, which is done by a hard External Instru&shy;
ment, forcibly impell'd upon the part; the diffe&shy;
rences whereof are taken from the Form, the
Part, and the Accidents of it.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fr&aelig;nulum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Membraneous Ligament under
the Tongue; in new-born Children, it sometimes
spreads over the whole under-side of the Tongue,
that the Midwife sometimes is forced to pull it
asunder with the Nails (which yet ought not to
be allow'd of) or the Chyrurgion with his Pen&shy;
knife.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Froenulum</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Froenum penis</term>, is a Membrane
which tyes the fore-skin to the Nut of the Yard.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Frons</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="forehead(n)">the forehead is the upper part of the
Face.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Frontale</form> <xpln lang="en">is an External Medicine, frequently
applyed to the Forehead, for a pain or heat in
the Head: it is made for the most part of Herbs,
Flowers, Seeds, Meal, moistned with Vinegar of
Roses.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fumigatio Chymica</form> <xpln lang="en">is an erosion of Metal by
smoak, or Vapour.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Functio</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Actio</term></xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Funda Galeni</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="swathe(n)">is a Swathe divided into Four
parts; useful in Accidents that happen to the Jaw&shy;
bone.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="137">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fungus</form> <xpln lang="en">is soft spongie Flesh which grows upon
Wounds.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Funiculus</form>, <xpln lang="en"><term lang="la">Intestinum</term>, <term lang="la">Laqueus</term>, or <term lang="la">Ductus Um&shy;
bilicalis</term>, the Navel-string, is a Membraneous Chan&shy;
nel or Conduct in a <term lang="la">F&oelig;tus</term> which reaches from the
Navel to the <term lang="la">Placenta</term> in the Womb; it contains
Two Arteries, one Vein, and the Urinarie passage
in the <term lang="la">F&oelig;tus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Furcale os</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Furcula</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Furcula Superior</form> <xpln lang="en">is the upper bone of the <term lang="la">Ster&shy;
num</term>, or Breast-bone, others call it <term lang="la">Jugulum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Furcella</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Furcula</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Furfuratio</form> <xpln lang="en">is when Dandriff falls from the Head
in Combing; it comes for the most part from
that skin which is under the Hair; also from the
Beard, and Eye-brows.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Furnuss</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="furnace(n)">a Furnace, is a place where a Fire is
conveniently kept for Chymical uses: and it is
either open or covered.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Furor</form> <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Manea</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Furor Uterinus</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="distemper(n)" lexeme="fervor of the womb(n)" lexeme="fervor of the matrix(n)">is an unseemly Distemper, which
is wont to seize upon Maids; especially those of
riper Years, and sometimes Widows too. They
who are troubled with it, throw off the Veil of
common Modesty, and Decency, and Delight one&shy;
ly in lascivious, obscene Discourses: they covet a 
man greedily, and even furiously, and omit no
inviting Temptations that may induce them to 
satisfie their desires. The cause seems to be in the
Seminal juice, which being exalted to the highest 
degree of Maturity, drives the Maids into a kind
of Fury; which is conspicuous every year in some
Bruits; as in Cats, Bulls, Bucks, Does, Harts.
</page>

<page no="138">
There is another Distemper akin to  this, which
the Ancients called, the <f type="i">Fervour of the Womb, or
the Matrix</f>, when the whole substance and body of
the Womb is extream hot, accompanied with a
pain and heaviness of the Loyns, a roughness
by the growth of Hair, Loathing, and a suppressi&shy;
on of the Urine, and Excrements: and the Wo&shy;
man all the while covets to be laid with, but by
reason of pain is still afraid of it.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Furunculus</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="boil(n)">a Boyl, is an acute swelling, as big
as a Pigeons Egg, attended with an Inflamation,
and Pain, especially when it begins to Corrupt,
and Putrifie: when it is opened, and the Matter
let out, part of the Flesh underneath is turned
into Corruption, of a whitish, and reddish Colour,
which some call the Ventricle of the <term lang="la">Furunculus</term>:
there is no danger in it, though you apply no Re&shy;
medy to it; for it ripens of it self, and bursts; but
the pain makes it more Elegible to apply a Reme&shy;
die, because that frees the Patient sooner from his
trouble.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Fusio</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="melting with heat(n)"> is a melting with heat.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">GAllactophori</form>, <xpln lang="en">are <term lang="la">Ductus's</term> which carry Milk,
convey the Chyle (as some Modern Au&shy;
thors have fancied) a streight way from the Guts
to the Glandules of the Breasts: yet the Arteries
were more properly so called, because they car&shy;
ry the Chyle along with the Blood to the Breasts,
wherein Milk is reserved for the use of the <term lang="la">F&oelig;&shy;
tus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<emend err="Parating">parating</emend> of Milk. See in the Word <term lang="la">Lac</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Galenica Medicina</form>, <xpln lang="en">is that Physick which is built

are <f type="i">Galenists</f> who embrace the Foundation of
their Art, which are fetched from <f type="i">Galen</f> and the
Philosophers, proved by Reason, and confirmed
by Experience.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Galea</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="pain in the head(n)">is a pain in the Head, so called from
the likeness of the place, because it takes in the
whole Head, like an Helmet; in Latin <term lang="la">Galea</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Galea</form> <xpln lang="en">is likewise when the Head of the <term lang="la">F&oelig;tus</term>

neos</term>, as it comes into the World.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Galreda, <term lang="en">or</term> Gelatina</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="jelly(n)">Gellie, is a Thickned, Vis&shy;
cous, and Lucid Juicie Substance; it is commonly

as of Calves Feet, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ganglion</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Humour in the Tendinous and
Nervous parts, proceeding from a Fall, Stroke,
or otherwise; it resists if stirred, if pressed upon
its side is not diverted, nor can be turned round.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Gangr&aelig;na</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="gangrene(n)">a Gangrene, is a Cadaverous Cor&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Gargarisma</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="gargarism(n)">a Gargarisme, is a Liquid Medicine

by Gargling, without swallowing; and it is <f type="i">either</f>
a Decoction, wherein convenient Syrups are dis&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Gelatina</form> <xpln lang="en">is almost the same with <term lang="la">Galreda</term>, but

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Gena Mala</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="chin(n)" lexeme="jaw-bone(n)">is part of the Face from the Nose

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Generatio</form> <xpln lang="en">is a natural Action, whereby an Ani&shy;
mal begets another like it of the same <term lang="la">Species</term>, of
convenient Seed, in Generation; the first thing
we see is a red Speck, which is clothed with a lit&shy;
tle bladder, next a little Heart, whence Veins and
Arteries flow, at the Extremitie whereof you see
the Viscera, the Bowels <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. afterward the whole
<term lang="la">F&oelig;tus</term> is formed and cloathed with Membranes;
before Generation the Seed of the Male being cast
into the Womb, enters and prepares its Pores, af&shy;
terwards sweats out a Viscous Substance, like the
white of an Egg, which moves the Egg out of 
the Testicles and Tubes; for the Womans Eggs
are impregnated by the influence of the Seed, are
</page>

<page no="141">
emitted out of the Testicles, and received by the 
Fallopian Tubes.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Genioglossum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a pair of Muscles proceeding in&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Gercomia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a part of that part of Physick cal&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ginglymus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Conjunction of Bones, when the

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Glandula</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="glandule(n)">a Glandule, is a Substance of a pe&shy;

</page>

the separated Humour into the Veins, as the

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Glandula Guidonis</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="tumor(n)">is a Tumor like a <term lang="la">Glandul&aelig;</term>,

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">H&aelig;matosis</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="sanguification(n)">or Sanguification, depends prin&shy;
cipally upon the Fermentation, Dissolution, and

Air, which accends the Sulphureous Blood in the
Lungs. <f type="i">Sanguification</f> is performed in all the parts
of the Body, and not in any peculiar part, as
the Heart, Liver, or Spleen.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">H&aelig;modia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a great pain in the Teeth, which

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">H&aelig;mophobus</form> <xpln lang="en">is one who fears to be let Blood.</xpln></wordentry>

the little Bladers of the Lungs themselves.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">H&aelig;morrhagia</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="flux of blood(n)">is a Flux of Blood at the Nostrils,

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Haustus, <term lang="en">or</term> Potio</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Liquid Medicine taken in&shy;

ents, mixed with a suitable Liquor, by Decoction,

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hectica</form> <xpln lang="en">is a continued Fever arising from the

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hedisma</form> <xpln lang="en">is any thing that gives Medicines a

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hegemonic&aelig;</form> <xpln lang="en">are the principal Actions in Human

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Helcrydria</form> <xpln lang="en">are certain little Ulcers, thick and
