<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Helminthes</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Elminthes</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Helodes</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Elodes</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Helos, <term lang="en">or</term> Clavus</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a round, white, callous
swelling of the Foot, like the head of a Nail, and
</page>

<page no="147">
fixed in the Roots of the hard Skin of the Foot.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">H&aelig;losis</form>, <xpln lang="en">a reflexed inversion of the Eye&shy;
lid.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hemeralopia, <term lang="en">or</term> Acies Nocturna</form>, <xpln lang="en">is when one sees
better in the Night than in the Day.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hemicrania</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="headache(n)">is an Head-ach in either part of
the Brain.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hemina Italica</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Measure containing half an
<f type="i">Attic Sextarie</f>, and nine Ounces: So much is a 
<term lang="la">Cotyla Attica</term>, and a <term lang="la">Cotyla Italica</term> is Twelve 
Ounces.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hemipagia</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Hemicrania</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hemiplegia</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="palsy(n)">is a Palsie on one side below the
Head, proceeding from an Obstruction in one
part or other of the Spinal Marrow; or from a 
blow; whence it comes to pass, that the Animal
Spirits are Obstructed in their passage.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hemiplexia</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Hemiplegia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hepar</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="liver(n)">the Liver, is a <f type="i">Parenchymous</f> Substance
placed under the right side of the <term lang="la">Diaphragme</term>,
considerably thick and big in a Man; it is clothed
with a thin Membrane, which proceeds from the 
<term lang="la">Periton&aelig;um</term>; and is fastned to other parts with
three strong Ligaments. 1. To the Abdomen,
by the Navel-vein. 2. Upwards, to the Dia&shy;
phragme, by a broad thin Membranous Liga&shy;
ment, on the right side. 3. To the Diaphragme
likewise, by a round and exceeding strong Liga&shy;
ment, the Bladder of the Gall, and the <term lang="la">Ductus
Hepaticus</term> are in the low flat part; it is of a red&shy;
dish Colour: its substance seems to be compoun&shy;
ded of several Membranes and clusters, or Glan&shy;
dules joyned together like Concreted Blood, which
</page>

<page no="148">
I observed from frequently washing it. The
Blood of the Spleen which is carryed thither by
the <term lang="la">Vena Port&aelig;</term> does in some measure Ferment in 
the Liver, with the Arterious Blood, which the <f type="i">C&aelig;&shy;
liac Arterie</f> affords, (to wit, when after Nutriti&shy;
on it is discharged into the Veins again) and dis&shy;
solves the Contexture of the Blood; whereupon 
its Saline Sulphureous Particles, which constitute
the Gall, are Segregrated by the Glandulous
Clusters, and conveyed to the Gut <term lang="la">Duodenum</term> by
the Bladder of the Bile, and the Ductus in the
Liver called <term lang="la">Hepaticus</term>. There are no <term lang="la">Lobes</term> in a 
Man's Liver; but in Brutes it is divided into se&shy;
veral Portions, which they call <term lang="la">Lobes</term>, the <f type="i">Fibres</f>
of the Liver, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. The Ancients believed, That the
Chyle was elaborated and Sanguified in the Li&shy;
ver, whilest onely its bilious Recrements are se&shy;
parated there.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hepatica vena</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Basilica</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hepaticus Morbus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Dejection of a watery sharp 
Blood, like the washing of Flesh, when the Ner&shy;
vous Juice, or Watery Blood, being not rightly 
Concocted, but sharp, is discharged into the Guts. 
Also when black, shining, dryed Blood is driven 
into the Gut: the Disease is so called, because 
they attributed Sanguification to the Liver.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hepiala</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Epiala</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Herculeus Morbus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Epilepsia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hermophroditus</form> <xpln lang="en">is one of both Sexes: but they
onely use the Womans Instruments, they are sel&shy;
dom Men, this abuse in Nature happens, when 
the <term lang="la">Clitoris</term> hangs out too far.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hermetica Medicina</form>, <xpln lang="en">which the <f type="i">&AElig;gyptians</f> falsly 
</page>

<page no="149">
fetched from <f type="i">Mercury</f>, refers the Cause of Disea&shy;
ses to Salt, Sulphur and Mercury; and prepares 
most noble Medicines, not only of Vegetables 
and Animals, but of Minerals too.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hernia</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="falling of the intestines(n)">or <term lang="la">Ramex</term>, is properly the falling of the
Intestines, Cawl, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. by the Processes of the <term lang="la">Peri&shy;
ton&aelig;um</term> Dilated into the Groin: also a Protu&shy;
berance of the Navel. The falling down of the 
Womb is improperly so called; swelling in the
<term lang="la">Larynx</term>; winding Tumours of the Spermatic
Vessels; Distentions from Flatulent Matter; Wa&shy;
tery Humours, or Swellings.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Herpes</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="inflammation(n)">a spreading, and winding Inflamation,
is Twofold, either <term lang="la">Miliaris</term>, or <term lang="la">Pustularis</term>, like Mil&shy;
let Seed, which seizes the Skin onely, and itches;
or <term lang="la">Exedens</term>, Consuming, which not onely seizes
the Skin, but the Muscles underneath: The
cause of it is, That the Glandules of the Skin are
too much stuffed with salt Particles, which are
kept there by others that are Viscous, whence
proceed the little Ulcers like Millet Seed, that oc&shy;
casion an Itching in the Skin, which if the Pec&shy;
cant Matter abound, they grow into a Crust, and 
eat the parts they lye upon.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Heterocrania</form> <xpln lang="en">is a pain in one part or other of
the Head.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Heterogeneum</form> <xpln lang="en">is when any thing disproportio&shy;
nate is mixed with the Blood and Spirits, as in
Fevers, Swimmings in the Head, Explosive Mo&shy;
tions, and the Apoplexie.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Heterorythmus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Life unsuitable to the Years
of those who live it; as if a Young Man should 
live an Old Man's Life, and on the contrary:
</page>

<page no="150">
this Word is said of Pulses too, when in Diseases
the Pulse beats diversly.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hexis</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="habit(n)" lexeme="habitude(n)">is a Habit, or Habitude of Body.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hidroa</form> <xpln lang="en">are Pimples about the Secret parts,
proceeding from a sharp Humour.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hydrocritica</form>, <xpln lang="en">are Critical Judgings of Distem&shy;
pers, taken from Sweating.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hidronosus</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="fever(n)" lexeme="English sweat(n)">is a Fever, wherein the Patient sweats
Extreamly. The <f type="i">English</f> call it the <f type="i">English</f> Sweat.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hydros</form> <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Sudor</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hidrotica</form>, <xpln lang="en">things that provoke Sweating, are
those which by Fermenting, and Attenuating parts
penetrate the closest Pores of the Blood, cut into
 things, rarifie them, and turn them into a kind
of Vapour, whatsoever they meet carry along 
with them, and drive it to the Surface of the
Body; where being condensed into an insensible
Liquor, it makes its way out.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hiera Picra</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Electuary of Aloes, Lignum
Aloes, Spikenard, Saffron, Mastick, Honey, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hieroglyphic&aelig; Not&aelig;</form>, <xpln lang="en">are foldings and Wrinkles
in the hand, from which vain curiosity pretends
to predict strange things.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hippus</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Affection of the Eyes, wherein
they continually shake and tremble, and now and
then twinkle, as it happens in Riding.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hircu</form>, <xpln lang="en"><term lang="la">Hirci</term>, or <term lang="la">Hirqui</term>, the corners of the
Eyes.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hirquus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Canthus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Holipp&aelig;</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="little cake(n)" lexeme="wafer(n)">are little Cakes or Wafers made of a 
Medicinal Infusion, with Wheat-flower and Su&shy;
gar.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">H&aelig;meomeres</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Similares Partes</term>.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="151">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Homogene&aelig; Particul&aelig;</form> <xpln lang="en">are such Particles as are
Pure, Entire, Unmixed and altogether like one
another.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Homoplata</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="shoulder-blade(n)"><term lang="la">Scapula, Spatula</term>, <term lang="la">Scoptula aperta</term>, the 
Shoulder-blade, is a broad and Triangular Bone
which constitutes the breadth of the Shoulder,
thin, especially in the middle, but thick in its
Processes, on each side one, lying upon the up&shy;
per Ribs behind, like a Target; it has Three
Processes, <term lang="la">Acromium</term>, or the Shoulder point; <term lang="la">Ca&shy;
rocoides</term>, or <term lang="la">Anchoralis</term>; and <term lang="la">Cervix</term>: its use is to
strengthen the Ribs, to joynt the Shoulder and
Neck Bones, and to implant Muscles therein.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Homotona</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="fever(n)">is a continued Fever that acts al&shy;
ways alike.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hora</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="hour(n)">an Hour, signifies the determinate space
of a Year with <f type="i">Hippocrates</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hor&aelig;a</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="summer fruit(n)">are seasonable or Summer-Fruits, as

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hordeatum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Liquid Medicine taken inward&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hordeolum</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Crithe</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Horrifica Febris</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Phricodes</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Horror</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Vibration and Trembling of the

it.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Humectantia</form>, <xpln lang="en">moistning things, are such as can

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Humidum Primogenium</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="blood(n)">may be properly called
</page>

<page no="152">
the Blood, which is seen in Generation before
any thing else.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Humores Oculares</form>, <xpln lang="en">the humours of the Eye, are
Three: the <f type="i">Watery</f>, which is contained between
the <term lang="la">Tunica Cornea</term>, and <term lang="la">Urea</term>. 2. The <f type="i">Chrystaline</f>,
or <f type="i">Icie Humour</f>, which is contained in the <term lang="la">Tunica
Uvea</term>, and is thicker than the rest. 3. The <f type="i">Vitre&shy;
ous</f>, or Glassy humour, bigger than any of the rest,
fills the backward Cavitie of the Eye.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Humores</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="yellow choler(n)" lexeme="black choler(n)">the Ancients made Four Humours
in the Blood, the Bilious Pituitous, (Yellow, and
Black Choller) Melancholic, and the Blood, pro&shy;
perly so called; and that according to the Four
Peripatetic Elements: but this Opinion is Cashier&shy;
ed, since the invention of the Circulation of the
Blood. Yet they are found, when the blood pre&shy;
ternaturally departs from its due Temperature;
but they do not constitute an integral part of
the blood; for the blood is onely one humour;
if otherwise, Tartar in Wine, and Dregs in Beer
were constituent parts of Wine and Beer. In
Blood that is let, there appear onely Three diffe&shy;
rent species of bodies; for in the Surface you
see a kind of Fibrous Crust of Coagulated Blood, 
which spreads it self over all the whole Mass;
then you see certain Red Particles amongst the
Fibres, which grow black about the bottom, by
reason of their fewness; lastly, you see the <term lang="la">Se&shy;
rum</term> wherein it swims. But if any one will pro&shy;
ceed more acurately, Distill the Blood, and Dis&shy;
solve it Chymically, he shall find Five pure bo&shy;
dies in it: to wit, Spirit, Sulphur, or Oyl, Water,
Salt, and Earth. There are Three General Hu&shy;
</page>

<page no="153">
mours which wash the whole Body, Blood, Lym&shy;
pha, (a sort of pure Water) and the Nervous
Juice; but there are several particular Humors,
as Chyle, Bile, Spittle, Pancreatic, Juice, Seed, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Humores in Secundinis</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="urine(n)">Humours in the Three 
Membranes that cloathe the <term lang="la">F&oelig;tus</term> in the Womb,
are Three in those Animals which have Bladders:
at the beginning, when the Eggs fall down from
the Testicles into the Womb, the Humours which
are to this purpose in the bottom of the Womb;
first sink into the Membrane called <term lang="la">Chorion</term>, and
then into the <term lang="la">Amnium</term>: but in progress of time,
when the <term lang="la">F&oelig;tus</term> is Formed, and the Navel Vessels
are extended to the <term lang="la">Chorion</term>, and the <term lang="la">Amnium</term>, we
imagine that the Nutritious Humour being recei&shy;
ved by the opening of the Veins, is carried to
the <term lang="la">F&oelig;tus</term>, and thence by the Arteries some part
of it is carried into the <term lang="la">Amnium</term>, as into the
Childs Store-house; so that at the said time, the 
Liquor of the <f type="i">Membrane</f> <term lang="la">Amnium</term> may be encrea&shy;
sed upon this double account. At last, when the
time of delivery draws near, that way of Sweat&shy;
ting through seems to cease, and the other onely
to take place: unless (as <f type="i">Wharton</f> Writes) The
Nutritious Humour descend from the <term lang="la">Placenta</term> by
the Navel-string, and by the little soft Protube&shy;
rances thence pass into the Cavity of the <term lang="la">Amni&shy;
um</term>: The use of these Humours is to nourish the
<term lang="la">F&oelig;tus</term> at the Mouth. The Third Humour is
the Urine, which flows from the Bladder by the
Urinarie Passage, into the Urinarie Membrane.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hyaloides</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Vitrous Humour of the Eye,
contained betwixt the <term lang="la">Tunica Retina</term>, and the
<term lang="la">Avea</term>.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="154">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hybona</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Incurvation of all the <f type="i">Vertebres</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hydatides</form> <xpln lang="en">are little Watery Bladders in the
Liver, Spleen, or some other Viseus, common to
Hydropical Persons: also an increase of Fat about
the Eye-lids.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hydatoides</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Watery humour of the Eye,
contained betwixt the <term lang="la">Tunica Cornea</term>, and <term lang="la">Uvea</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hyderos</form> <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Hydrops</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hydragia</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Ven&aelig; Lymphatic&aelig;</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hydragoga</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines which by Fermen&shy;
tation and Precipitation purge out the Watery
Humours.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hydrel&aelig;um</form> <xpln lang="en">is a mixture of Water and Oyl.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hydrenterocele</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="falling of the intestines(n)">is a falling of the Intestines, to&shy;
gether with Water, into the outward Skin of the
Cods.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hydroa</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="pimple(n)">are certain little, broad, moist, itching
Pimples, like Millet-Seed; sometimes without
itching, which render the Skin Ulcerous and
rough: the occasion of them is, that Nature en&shy;
deavouring to expel the sweat by the skin, is hin&shy;
dred sometimes by its thickness; so that the Mat&shy;
ter being lodged there, and the Subtiler parts be&shy;
ing either carryed back, by the Lymphatic Ves&shy;
sels, or Evaporated, the Skin swells. This Distem&shy;
per is familiar and common to Boys, and Young
Men; especially of a hot Constitution, when they
use too much Exercise in Summer; it infects the
Neck, Shoulder-Blades, Breast, Arms, Thighs;
yet more frequently the Secret Parts, and the
Fundament.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hydrocele</form> <xpln lang="en">is a swelling of the outermost Skin
of the Cods, proceeding from a Watery Humour.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="155">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hydrocephalum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a swelling of the Head, by rea&shy;
son of a Watery Humour, whence the Sutures of
the Brain are forced asunder; it proceeds some&shy;
times from a Bursting of the Lymphatic Vessels.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hydromel</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="mead(n)">Mead, is a Decoction of Water, and
Honey.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hydromphalum</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="protuberance of the navel(n)">is a Protuberance of the Na&shy;
vel, proceeding from Watery Humours in the
<term lang="la">Abdomen</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hydrophobia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Distemper highly Convulsive,
accompanied with Fury, and shunning of all
things that are Liquid, and Splendid; sometimes
with a <term lang="la">Delirium</term>, a Fever, and other Symptoms, not
without great danger of Life, proceeding from 
a Bite of a Mad Dog, or a Contagion analogous 
to it.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hydropica</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines that expel the Watery
Humours in a Dropsie.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hydrops</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="dropsy(n)">is a Stagnation of a Watery Humour
in the habit of the Body, or some other Cavity;
and it is either <f type="i">general</f>, as an <term lang="la">Anasarca</term> and <term lang="la">Asci&shy;
tes</term>, to which some add a Tympany, but ill: Or
<f type="i">particular</f>, confined to one part, as a Dropsie in
the Head, Breast, Hand, Foot, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. of which in
their proper place severally.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hydrops ad Matulam</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Diabetes</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hydrosaccharum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Syrup boiled of Water,
and Sugar.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hygieia</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="health(n)">is health, which consists in a good tem&shy;
perature, and right confirmation of Parts. Health
is a disposition of the parts of humane body, fit
for the performance of the Actions of the Body.
Signs of Health are Three, due Actions, suitable
Qualities, and when things taken in, and let out,
are proportionable.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="156">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hygieina</form> <xpln lang="en">is that part of Physick, which teaches
the way of preserving Health: some divide it in&shy;
to Three parts, <f type="i">Prophylactic</f>, which takes notice
of future imminent Diseases; <f type="i">Synteretic</f>, which pre&shy;
serves present health: and <f type="i">Analeptic</f>, which re&shy;
covers the Sick.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hygrocyrsocele</form> <xpln lang="en">is a branch of a Winding Vein
swoln with ill Blood, accompanied with other
Moisture.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hymen</form> <xpln lang="en">is properly a Membrane; it is taken
also for the Private Membrane in a Virgin, which
arises from the wrinkling of the lower part of the
<term lang="la">Vagina</term>; and in Women with Child, when the 
Womb grows thicker, it disappears.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hyoides</form> <xpln lang="en">is a bone placed at the <f type="i">Basis</f> of the
Tongue.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hyothorides</form> <xpln lang="en">are Two Muscles of the <term lang="la">Larynx</term>,
proceeding from the Bone <term lang="la">Hyoides</term> into the Car&shy;
tilage called <term lang="la">Scutiformis</term>, like a Shield, and desti&shy;
ned to contract, or shut up the opening of the
Wind-pipe.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hypercatharsis</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="purge(n)">is a Purge that works too much.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hypercrisis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Critical Excresion aboe mea&shy;
sure.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hyperephidresis</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="sweating(n)">is a too great Sweating.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hyperoon</form> <xpln lang="en">are two holes in the upper part of
the Palate, which receives the Pituitous humours
from the Mammillary Processes; and after they
are separated, discharges them at the Mouth.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hypersarcosis</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Excrescence of Flesh in any 
part.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hipnotica</form> <xpln lang="en">are those things which by fixing the
Spirits, by straitning and shutting up the Pores
of the brain, cause Sleep.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="157">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hypochondriacha Affectio</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Hypochondriacus 
Affectus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hypochondriumor <term lang="en">or</term> Subcartilagineum</form>, <xpln lang="en">is the upper
part of the Abdomen, under the Cartilages of
the Chest.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hypocondriacus Affectus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a purely Flatulent
and Convulsive Passion, arising from the Flatulent and
Pungent humours in the Spleen, or Sweet-bread
which Afflict the Nervous and Membranous
parts.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hypochyma</form> <xpln lang="en">is a depraved sight, whereby Gnats,
Cob-webs, little Clouds, or such like, seem to
swim before the Eyes: the cause of it seems to
consist in turbid humours, or sometime in the
Optic Nerves, whose little Pores are obstructed
by the Matter that is thrust into them.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hypochysis</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Hypochyma</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hypocratis Manica</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Manica Hypocratis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hypogastrium</form> <xpln lang="en">is the outermost part of the Ab&shy;
domen, betwixt the <term lang="la">Hypocondres</term> and the Navel.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hypoglossis <term lang="en">or</term> Ranula</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Inflamation, or Ex&shy;
ulceration under the Tongue: also a Medicine
that takes away the Asperity of the <term lang="la">Larynx</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hypophaulum</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="vulgar diet(n)" lexeme="plain diet(n)" lexeme="exquisite diet(n)">is a vulgar Diet which observes a
mean betwixt a plain and an exquisite Diet.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hypophor&aelig;</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="ulcer(n)">are deep and Fistulous Ulcers which
gape like Ulcers, and cavities in the Flesh.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hypophysis</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Hypochyma</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hypophthalmia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a pain in the Eye under the
Horney Tunic.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hypopyon</form> <xpln lang="en">is a gathering of Matter under the 
Horney Tunic of the Eye.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hyposarca</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Anasarca</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hyposarcidium</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="158">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hyposphagma</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="blood-shot(n)">is a blood-shot, from a stroak upon
the Eye.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hypostasis Urin&aelig;</form> <xpln lang="en">is that thick Substance which
generally subsides at the bottom of Urine.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hypothenar</form> <xpln lang="en">is the space from the fore to the lit&shy;
tle Finger.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hypothesis</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="supposition(n)">is the supposition of a thing.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hypozoma</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Membrane that parts two Ca&shy;
vities, as the <term lang="la">Mediastinum</term> in the Thorax.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hyposiloides</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Hyoides</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hysteralgia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a pain in the Womb, proceeding
from an Inflamation, or otherwise.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hysterica Passio</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="fit of the mother(n)">Fits of the Mother, is a Con&shy;
vulsion of the Nerves of the <term lang="la">Par Vagum</term>, and
Intercostal in the Abdomen, proceeding from a
Pricking Irritation, or Explosion of Spirits: this
Distemper does not always depend upon the
Womb, as is commonly thought; we have seen it
more than once in Men, because the Spleen,
Pancreas, and other adjacent Bowels, are often
the cause of it.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hysterica</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines against the Diseases of
the Womb.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hysterotomotocia, <term lang="en">or</term> Sectio C&aelig;sarea</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a cutting
the Child out of the Womb, which is done thus;
You make a <f type="i">Semilunar Section</f> under the Navel,
along the White line, the cavity whereof looks to&shy;
wards the said Line; then according to the leading
of the Fibres, the <term lang="la">F&oelig;tus</term> being extracted after the
Section, the wound in the Womb contracts of it self
so that the Blood scarce flows more plentifully than
in a Natural Birth; but if the Mother be dead,
chuse the most convenient place you can.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Hysterotomia</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Anatomical Dissection of the
Womb.</xpln></wordentry>
</wordgroup1>
</section>
</page>

<page no="161">
<section type="Dictionary I-Z">

<wordgroup1 type="a" object="I">I.

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Janitor</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Pylorus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ichor</form> <xpln lang="en">is a sulphureous and watery Humour
which flows from Ulcers.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ichoroides</form> <xpln lang="en">is a moisture like Corruption.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Icterus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="jaundice(n)">the Jaundice, is a changing the Skin
into the yellow Colour from an obstruction of the
<term lang="la">ductus choledochus</term>, or the Glandules of the Liver,
through the weakness, obstruction, or Schirres
of the Liver, or because the Gall abounds more
than can be conveniently excerned, so that it
stays in the Blood. It takes its Name from
<term lang="gk">&#x1F30;&#x03BA;&#x03C4;&#x03B9;&#x03C2;</term>, a <f type="i">Ferret</f>, whose Eyes are tinged with the
like Colour. Or from a Bird called <term lang="la">Icterus</term> of
the same Colour, which the <f type="i">Latines</f> call <term lang="la">Galbu&shy;
lus</term>, which if one sick of the Jaundice sees, says
<f type="i">Pliny</f>, the Party is cured, and the Bird dies.
The <f type="i">Latines</f> call it <term lang="la">Regius Morbus</term>, the Kingly Dis&shy;
ease, because it is easily cured in Courts with the
Pastimes and Divertisements there which cheer
the Mind. It is also called a Suffusion of Gall.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Idea morbi</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Propriety and Essence of a
Disease.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Idiopathia</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="primary disease(n)">is a primary Disease, which neither
depends on, nor proceeds from any other.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Idiosyncrasia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Temperament peculiar to any 
Body.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Jecur</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Hepar</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Jecur uterinum</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Placenta uteri</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Jejunum intestinum</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Second of the small
Guts, so called, because it is frequently empty:
The little glandulous Nipples in it inbibe the
</page>

<page no="162">
Chyle, and convey it to the Milky Veins. <f type="i">Varro</f>
calls it <term lang="la">Hilla</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ignis actualis</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="actual fire(n)">actual Fire, is that which burns
at first touch, as Fire it self, and seering Irons.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ignis potentialis</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="potential fire(n)">potential Fire, is a Medicine
which after it has laid sometimes upon the part,
exerts it self.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ignis persicus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="carbuncle(n)">the same that <term lang="la">Gangr&aelig;na:</term> It is
taken also for a Carbuncle.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ignis sacer</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Erysipelas:</term> yet some
take it for an <term lang="la">Herpes</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ignis sylvestris</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Phlyct&aelig;na</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ignitio</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="calcination(n)">is Calcination made by Fire.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ile</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Cavity from the <term lang="la">Thorax</term> to the Bones
of the Thighs: <f type="i">Pliny</f> observes, that all the Inte&shy;
stines in all Animals, except a Man and a Sheep,
are called <term lang="la">Ile</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ilia</form> <xpln lang="en">are the lateral parts of the <term lang="la">Abdomen</term>, be&shy;
twixt the last Rib and the secret Parts.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ilingus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Scotomia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ilium</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Third of the small Guts: It begins
where the <term lang="la">Jejunum</term> ends, and ends it self at the
Gut called <term lang="la">C&aelig;cum</term>: It is one and twenty Hand&shy;
breadths in length.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ilium</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Disease, for the most part, of the 
Gut <term lang="la">Ilium</term>, and is called <term lang="la">Volvulus</term>, when the up&shy;
per part of any Intestine is involved in the under,
and on the contrary.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ilium os</form> <xpln lang="en">is part of the Bone <term lang="la">Innominatum</term>,
without any particular Name: It is so named 
because it contains the Gut <term lang="la">Ilium</term>. Its Circum&shy;
ference is circular, the upper broadest, it is con&shy;
nected to the <term lang="la">os Sacrum</term>: The upper part of it is
called <term lang="la">Spina</term>, the interior <term lang="la">Costa</term>, and the exteri&shy;
</page>

<page no="163">
or <term lang="la">Dorsum</term>: It is larger in Women than Men.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Iliaca passio</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Ilium Morbus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Illiaca vasa</form> <xpln lang="en">are those double forked Vessels of
the Truncs of the great Artery, and the great
Vein of the <term lang="la">Abdomen</term>, about the place where the
Bladder and the Womb are scituate.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Imaginatio</form> <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Phantasia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Imperfecta crisis</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <f type="i">Crisis</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Impetigo Celsi, <term lang="en">the same that</term> Lepra Gr&aelig;corum.
</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="lentel(n)"><term lang="la">Celsus</term> makes four sorts. The most harmless,
says he, is that which is like a Scab, for it is red
and harder, and exulcerated and gnawed: But
it differs from it, in that it is more exulcerated,
and is accompanied with speckled Pimples: and
there seem to be in it certain Bubbles, from
which after a certain time there fall, as it were,
little Scales, and it returns more certainly.
Another sort is worse, almost like a sort of 
Meezles, or hot Pimples in the Skin, but more
rugged, and redder, and of different Figures:
In this Distemper little Scales too fall from the
surface of the Skin, and it is called <term lang="la">Rubrica</term>. The
third sort is yet worse, for it is thicker and har&shy;
der, and swells more, and is cleft on the top of
the Skin, and gnaws more violently: It is scaly
too, but black, and spreads broad and slow: It
is called <term lang="la">Nigra</term>. The fourth sort is altogether
incurable, of a different colour from the red;
for it is something white, and like a fresh Scar,
and has pale Scales; some whitish, some like the
little Pulse calld <term lang="la">Lintell</term>, which being taken a&shy;
way, sometimes the Blood follows: Otherwise
the Humour that flows from it is white, the Skin
hard and cleft, and spreads farther. All these
</page>

<page no="164">
sorts arise especially in the Feet and Hands, and
infest the Nails likewise. <term lang="la">Impetigo</term> some reckon
the same with <term lang="la">Lichen</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Impetigo Plinii</form>, <xpln lang="en"><f type="i">Pliny</f>'s <term lang="la">Impetigo</term> is the same
with <term lang="la">Lichen Gr&aelig;corum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Inappetentia</form>, <xpln lang="en">is want of Stomach, for want of
Ferment in it.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Inceratio</form> <xpln lang="en">is a mixture of Moisture with some&shy;
thing that's dry, by a gentle soaking till the sub&shy;
stance be brought to the consistence of soft Wax.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Incidentia</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Attenuantia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Incineratio</form> <xpln lang="en">is the reducing the Bodies of Vege&shy;
tables and Animals into Ashes by a violent Fire.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Incisores dentes</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Primores</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Incisorii</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same <term lang="la">Primores</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Incorporatio</form> <xpln lang="en">is a mixture whereby moist things
are contemperated with dry into one Body, as
into a Mass, therefore here is no lingring Nu&shy;
trition, but as much moisture is added as is re&shy;
quisite to the consistence of the mixed Body, so
that it becomes like a Pudding as it were; whence
it may be called also <term lang="la">Impastatio</term>, and in some
things <term lang="la">Subactio</term>, a Kneading. Things thus incor&shy;
porated must be left in a digestive Heat, that by
mutual Action and Suffering they may get one
temperature common to them both.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Incrassantia</form>, <xpln lang="en">thickning things, are those which
being endued with thick ropie parts, and mixed
with thin liquid Juices, bring them to a thicker
consistence by joining and knitting their parts.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Incubus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Epialtes</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Incus</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="oval window(n)">is one of the Bones in the inner part of
the Ear: It is like a Grinder, and lies under the
Bone called <term lang="la">Malleus</term>. It has two Processes below;
</page>

<page no="165">
one shorter, which leans upon the scaly Bone;
another longer, which sustains the top of the
<term lang="la">Stapes</term> or triangular Bone, that bears upon the
Cavity of the inner part of the Ear, whilst it
immerges it self into the place called the Oval
Window with a pretty broad <f type="i">Basis</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Indicans</form> <xpln lang="en">is nothing else than something ob&shy;
served in the Body, upon whose account some&shy;
thing is said to be done that ought to contribute
thereunto.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Indicantes dies</form> <xpln lang="en">are those days which signify
that a Crisis will happen on such a day, which 
are therefore called indicant and contemplable:
Such are 4, 11, 17, 24.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Indicatio</form> <xpln lang="en">is that which demonstrates what is to
be done in Diseases, and it is threefold, <f type="i">pr&aelig;ser&shy;
vatorie</f>, which preserves Health; <f type="i">Curative</f>, which
expels a Disease that has already seized upon a 
Person; and <f type="i">Vital</f>, which respects the Strength
and way of living.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Indicatum</form> <xpln lang="en">is that which is signified to be done
in order to the recovery of Health.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Indices dies</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Critici dies</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Indurantia</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Sclerotica</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Indusium</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Amnios</term>.</xpln></wordentry> 

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Inedia</form> <xpln lang="en">is abstaining from Meat, when one eats
less than formerly.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Infimus venter</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Abdomen</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Inflammatio</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Phlegmone</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Inflatio</form> <xpln lang="en">is the distention of a part from flatulent
matter.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Infundibulum cerebri</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Choana</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Infundibulum renum</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Pelvis or Basin
through which the Urine passes to the Ureters
</page>

<page no="166">
and the Bladder.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Infusio</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Extraction of the Virtue of Medi&shy;
cines with a convenient Liquor, which if it be
purgative, it may be taken at once; and to this
the Name properly agrees.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Inguen</form>, <xpln lang="en">is the place from the bending of the
Thigh to the secret parts.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Injectio intestinalis</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <f type="i">Clyster</f>.</xpln></wordentry> 

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Inium</form> <xpln lang="en">is the beginning of the oblongated
Marrow, which is the common Sensory, because
the Species which are received from the exter&shy;
nal Organs are conveyed thither by the Nerves.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Innominata tunica oculi</form>, <xpln lang="en">the Tunic of the Eye 
that wants a Name, is a certain subtile Expansion
of the Tendons from the Muscles which move the
Eye to the circumference of the <term lang="la">Iris</term> or horney
Membrane.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Innominatum os</form>, <xpln lang="en">others call it <term lang="la">os Cox&aelig;</term>, or <term lang="la">Ili&shy;
um</term>, is placed at the side of the <term lang="la">os Sacrum</term>, con&shy;
sisting of three Bones, <term lang="la">Ilium</term>, <term lang="la">Os Pubis</term>, and <term lang="la">Ischi&shy;
um</term>, joined by Cartilages, and appear distinct by
three Lines till seven years old, but grow all
into one Bone at riper years. They are called al&shy;
so <term lang="la">Cuneiformia</term>, and <term lang="la">Ossa Innominata</term>, nameless
Bones.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Innominatus humor, <term lang="en">or</term> Infitus</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a secondary
Humour, as the Ancients call it, wherewith they
thought the Body was nourished: For those nu&shy;
tritious Humours they talked of are four; <term lang="la">Inno&shy;
minatus</term>, <term lang="la">Ros</term>, <term lang="la">Gluten</term>, <term lang="la">Cambium</term>.</xpln></wordentry> 

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Insania, <term lang="en">or</term> Amentia</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="madness(n)">Madness, is an Aboli&shy;
tion or Depravation of Imagination and Judg&shy;
ment.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="167">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Insessus</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="bath for the belly(n)">is a Bath for the Belly, proper for the
lower Parts, wherein the Patient sits down to
the Navel. They are for several uses, as for ea&shy;
sing of Pain, softning of Parts, dispelling flatu&shy;
lent matter; and frequently for exciting the
Courses.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Inspiratio</form> <xpln lang="en">is an alternate Dilatation of the
Chest, whereby the nitrous Air is communicated
to the Blood to accend it by the Wind-Pipe, and
its <f type="i">Vesicular</f> parts. The cause of Respiration does
not seem to consist only in the Dilatation of the
Thorax, as is commonly thought, but in the
Contraction of the Tunic which covers the up&shy;
per part of the <term lang="la">&oelig;sophagus</term>, and the most close Re&shy;
cesses of the Wind-Pipe.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Intellectus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="cogitation(n)">is Cogitation, whereby a Man ap&shy;
prehends an Object: It seems to be transacted in
the <term lang="la">Corpus Callosum</term>, from the expansion of Spi&shy;
rits there.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Intemperies</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Disease which consists in in&shy;
convenient qualities of the Body, and these are
either manifest or occult: The Manifest are either
simple or compound; the Simple is when one
Quality is peccant; as an hot, thin, hard, acid, 
salt Disposition, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. the Compound is when
more Qualities than one are peccant; as an hot
and salt, a cold and acid Disposition, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. An Oc&shy;
cult ill Disposition or Distemper is such as pro&shy;
ceeds from some poysonous Qualities, as from
the Air from poysonous Animals, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. It comes
from the Air, when the Nitre in it becomes
contagious by reason of standing stinking Wa&shy;
ters, daily Droughts, Earth-quakes, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term> whence
malignant pestilent Feavers, and Plagues them&shy;
</page>

<page no="168">
selves arise: For the Vapours being taken away,
that which remains of the Air (by reason of the 
Sulphur and Salt in it) contracts an ill Savour,
whereupon the Air and its Nitre degenerate from
their due Temperature and Crasis. And I be&shy;
lieve the same happens from very dry Grounds,
for sulphureous and saline Particles intermix with
the watery ones above, which render the Nitre
of the Air sharp and pointed, like <f type="i">Arsenic</f>, sub&shy;
limated <f type="i">Mercury</f>, or <term lang="la">Aqua stygia</term>, which being
sucked into the Lungs do coagulate, and cor&shy;
rode the Mass of the Blood and make its Spirits
vanish; whence proceed Quinzies, Plurisies,
Pestilential Swellings, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Intercalares dies, <term lang="en">or</term> intercidentes, <term lang="en">which others
call</term> Provocatorii</form>, <xpln lang="en">are those Days wherein Na&shy;
ture, either by reason of the vehemency of the
Fit, or some external cause, is excited to expel
her Load unseasonably: Such are the 3<f type="i">d</f>, 5, 9,
13, 19.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Intercidentes dies</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Intercalares</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Intercus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Anasarca</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Interforamineum</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Perin&aelig;um</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Intermittens morbus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Disease which comes at

mittent Feavers, or Agues, proceed not from
any fictitious <f type="i">Focus</f>, but only from a wrong

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Interscapularia</form> <xpln lang="en">are the Cavities betwixt the

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Intertrigo</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Attritus</term>, is an Excoriation of

</page>

<page no="169">
Thighs; or a Fleaing of the Skin proceeding 
from a violent Motion, especially Riding: It
happens frequently to Children, that the <term lang="la">Cuti&shy;
cula</term> in their Thighs and Hips is separated, and
as it were shaven off from the true Skin, which
pains them so that it makes them restless.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Intestina</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Entera</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Involucrum cordis</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Pericardium</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Jonthus</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">varus</term>, is a little, hard, callous

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Iris</form> <xpln lang="en">is that fibrous Circle next to the <f type="i">Pupil</f> of

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Isatodes</form> <xpln lang="en">is a blew Bile, like the Herb <f type="i">Woad</f>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Isch&aelig;ma</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines that stop the Blood, which

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ischias</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="gout in the hip(n)">is the Gout in the Hip.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ischophonus</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="small voice(n)">is a small Voice.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ischuretica</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines which thicken the

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ischuria</form> <xpln lang="en">is such a Supression of Urine in the

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Isthmus</form> <xpln lang="en">is that part which lies betwixt the

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Jugale os</form> <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Zygoma</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Julepus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Liquid Medicine taken inwardly,
of a grateful taste and clear, made of a conveni&shy;
ent Liquor with Syrup or Sugar without any 
boyling, and of the quantity of three or four
Doses, to alter or refrigerate. A <f type="i">Julep</f> consists
commonly of one pound and an half of Barley-&shy;
Water, or of distilled Waters, rarely of Wine,
of the cooling Syrup of red Goose-berries, Ber&shy;
beries, Violets, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. to which they commonly
add some drops of Sulphur, Vitriol, Salt, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.
to give it a good taste. <f type="i">Juleb</f>, whence the word
<term lang="pe">Julepus</term> comes, is a <f type="i">Persian</f> word, and signifies a
sweet Potion.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">LAbia leporina</form> <xpln lang="en">are such Lips as by reason of

some call <term lang="la">rostra leporina</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Labyrinthus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Body full of windings and
turnings, as may be seen in the inner part of
the Ear, and in the outer surface of the Brain.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Lac</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="milk(n)">Milk, is made by separating of Chyle
from the arterious Blood by the <f type="i">Glandules</f> of the
</page>

<page no="171">
Breast. Milk begins to be made for the most part
after the going with Young, or a little before
the Birth; but it ceases in old Creatures, in
those with Young, and in menstruous Persons.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Lacertus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Brachium</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Lachrymale punctum</form> <xpln lang="en">is an hole made in the
Bone of the Nose, by which the matter that
makes Tears passes to the Nostrils; if the hole
grow hard and brawny from an Ulcer in one of
the Glandules at the Corners of the Eyes, thence
arises a <term lang="la">Fistula Lacrymalis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Lachrym&aelig;</form> <xpln lang="en">are a moisture which is separated
by the Glandules of the Eye to moisten the Eyes,
which if it be too much so that it cannot be re&shy;
ceived by the <term lang="la">Punctum Lachrimale</term>, they fall from
the Eyes and are called Tears.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Laconicum, Caldarium, <term lang="en">and</term> Assa, <term lang="en">or</term> Balneum
aereum</form>, <xpln lang="en">was formerly a Cellar without any Wa&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Lacun&aelig;</form> <xpln lang="en">are little Pores or Passages in the <term lang="la">Va&shy;

<page no="172">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Lagochilus</form> <xpln lang="en">one who has cloven Lips, see <term lang="la">Labia

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Lanceta</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Chyrurgions little Knife, streight,

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Laqueus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Band so tied, that if it be attra&shy;
cted, or pressed with weight it shuts up close: Its
use is to extend broken or disjointed Bones, to
keep them in their places when they are set, to
bind the parts close together; the differences of 
these <term lang="la">Laquei</term>, or Bands, are several, having
their names either from the Inventors, or from
their Use, or from their likeness to or shape of
any thing, or from the manner of lying, or their 
Effect, which unless they were here delineated,
can scarce be understood by a bare Description.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Laryngotomia</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Bronchotomia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Larynx</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="Adam's apple(n)"><term lang="la">Guttur</term>, according to <f type="i">Galen</f> <term lang="la">Larynx</term> is
properly the head or top of the Wind-Pipe,
which consists of five <term lang="la">Cartilages</term>. The first pair
is called <term lang="la">Scutiforme</term>, like a Shield, which consti&shy;
tutes the protuberance in the Neck called <f type="i">Adam</f>'s
Apple: The second pair is called <term lang="la">Annular</term>, be&shy;
cause it is round like a Ring: The third and
fourth Cartilage some reckon but one, but if the
Membrane be took off, it appears to be two, and
it is called <term lang="la">Guttalis</term> and <term lang="la">Glottis:</term> The fifth is called
<term lang="la">Epiglottis</term>, which covers the opening of the Wind-&shy;
Pipe at the top. Its use is in the Voice and Respi&shy;
ration.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="173">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Lassitudo</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Copos</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Laudanum</form> <xpln lang="en">is meant only of a Medicine made

num</term>, from its excellent Qualities. Authors give

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Laxantia</form>, <xpln lang="en">loosening Medicines, are those which

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Lenientia</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Laxantia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Leno</form> <xpln lang="en">and <term lang="la">Linon</term> is that part of the Brain called

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Lentigines</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="freckle(n)">Freckles, are little Spots especi&shy;
ally in Women, and chiefly in their Faces, but
sometimes in their Hands, Arms, and the upper
part of the Chest which is exposed to the Air;
the Skin is sometimes spotted thicker sometimes
thinner with them, like as with so many drops,
but without any Trouble or Pain; in some they
appear only in Summer, and disappear in Win&shy;
ter, in others they continue the Year round.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Lepidoides</form> <xpln lang="en">is the scaly Suture of the Scull, see
<term lang="la">Mendosa</term></xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Lepra</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="leprosy(n)"><f type="i">a Leprosie</f>, is a dry Scab, whereby the
Skin becomes scaly like Fish: It differs from
<term lang="la">Leuce</term> and <term lang="la">Alphus</term>, in that a Leprosy is rough to
the touch, and causes an Itching; for the Skin
is the only part affected, and therefore that be&shy;
ing flea'd off, the Flesh underneath appears sound
and well.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="174">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Lepra Arabum</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Elephantiasis 
Gr&aelig;corum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Lepra Gr&aelig;corum, <term lang="en">or</term> Impetigo Celsi</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="scabbedness(n)" lexeme="elephantiasis(n)" lexeme="leprosy(n)">is the high&shy;
est degree of Scabbedness; but it must be obser&shy;
ved, lest any should be gravell'd in the reading
of Authors, that we here speak of the <f type="i">Leprosy of
the Greeks</f>, not the <f type="i">Arabians</f>. That which the <f type="i">Ara&shy;
bians</f> call a Leprosy is the <f type="i">Elephantiasis of the
Greeks</f>, which is nothing else than an Universal
Canker of the whole Body. A Leprosy is a Dis&shy;
ease proceeding from the black Bile diffused through
the whole Body, whence the Temperature, the
Form and Figure, and at last the very Continu&shy;
ity of the Body is corrupted, and it is a Canker
common to the whole Body. The <f type="i">Arabians</f> call
the Leprosy of the Greeks <term lang="la">Albaras nigra</term>, which
is the same with a kind of Ring-worm or Tetter
which fleas the Flesh, and it is a rough violent
Scab in the Skin, accompanied with Scales like
Fish and itching. There is a greater Corrupti&shy;
on of Humours in a Leprosy than in a <f type="i">Scabbedness</f>,
and from the latter there only fall little flakes
like Dendriff from the Head, but from the for&shy;
mer as it were Scales of Fish; so that one passes
from Itching to a Leprosy by the Scab. For
<term lang="la">Pruritus</term>, or Itching, is a certain small Asperity
of the Skin, wherein, unless you scratch very
hard, nothing falls from the Skin: When it is
grown to a scab the Humour is more apparent,
and certain little Particles like Dendriff fall off,
where it be scratched or no. For in a Scab
the matter is thinner, and at least preys upon
the Surface of the Skin: But then in a Leprosy
the matter is thicker, and not only feeds upon 
</page>

<page no="175">
the Surface but the inner parts of the Skin.
<term lang="la">Celsus</term> doubtless meant this Leprosy of the
<f type="i">Greeks</f> by the Word <term lang="la">Impetigo</term>, but not the
<term lang="la">Lichen</term> of the <f type="i">Greeks</f>, which some call <term lang="la">Impeti&shy;
go</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Leptuntica</form> <xpln lang="en">are attenuating cutting Medicines, 
which part the crass and viscous Humours with
their acute Particles.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Lethargus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="lethargy(n)" lexeme="drousiness(n)">a Lethargy, is a Drowziness like
another Disease causing an heavy sleep called
<term lang="la">Coma</term>, accompanied with a Feaver and a <term lang="la">Deli&shy;
rium</term>; and it is nothing else but an heap of too
much or incongruous moist Matter within the
Pores of the barky substance of the Brain. This
Distemper does not seem to come of it self, but
rather from the demigration of Feavers.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Leuce</form> <xpln lang="en">is when the Hairs, Skin, and sometimes
the Flesh underneath turns white; the Flesh be&shy;
ing pricked with a Needle is not sensible, nor
emits Blood but a Milky Humour. It differs
from <term lang="la">Alphus</term> in that it penetrates deeper and
changes the Skin so that the Hairs are changed
too.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Leucoma</form> <xpln lang="en">is a white Scar in the horney Tunic
of the Eye.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Leucophagum</form> <xpln lang="en">is made of Almonds macerated
in Rose-Water, and of Capon or Partridg boi&shy;
led, bruised and strained through a Sieve made
of Bristles: It is used in a Consumption.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Leucophlegmatia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a pituitous Dropsy, or a
Dropsy that has seized the whole Body.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Lichen</form> <xpln lang="en">barbarously called <term lang="la">Serpigo</term> or <term lang="la">Zerna</term>,
<f type="i">Halliabbas</f> calls it <term lang="la">Petigo</term> and <term lang="la">Sarpedo</term>; the vulgar
<term lang="la">Voliatica</term>. <term lang="la">Lichenes</term> are certain Asperities of the
</page>

<page no="176">
Skin, and as it were Tumors, which itch much
and send forth Matter: The <f type="i">Greeks</f> and <f type="i">Arabi&shy;
ians</f> have made two sorts of <term lang="la">Lichens</term>, the one mild 
and gentle, the other fierce and cruel. And ac&shy;
cording to <f type="i">Avicen</f>, some are moist, which being
rubbed send forth a kind of Dew, others are
dry; and the moist are more safe, but the dry is
made of salt pituitous Matter turned into Melan&shy;
cholly Blood. And again he writes, that one
Manginess (<term lang="la">Impetigo</term>) brings off the Skin by rea&shy;
son of its great Dryness, and another does not;
and that one in ambulatory and malignant, ano&shy;
ther fixed and standing; as also one is old, ano&shy;
ther fresh. Hence it appears, that the <f type="i">Scabies</f> of
<f type="i">Corn</f>. <f type="i">Celsus</f> was nothing but these <term lang="la">Lichenes</term> of the
<f type="i">Greeks</f>, and the <term lang="la">Impetigo</term> of the <f type="i">Arabians</f>. It
comes in any part of the Body, but especially in
the Face and Chin, as <f type="i">Galen</f> has it; for a <term lang="la">Lichen</term>,
says he, is a most ungrateful Distemper in the
Chin, because it makes it itch exceedingly, and
stretches out the parts affected: It is not a little
dangerous, it spreads over the whole Face, and
sometimes reaches the Eyes, and at last makes
the Person affected extream filthy and loathsom.
<f type="i"><term lang="la">Lichen</term> of the Greeks</f> is <f type="i">Pliny</f>'s <term lang="la">Impetigo</term>, or an In&shy;
equality of the Skin, extending it self to the
neighbouring parts, and accompanied with an
extraordinary Itching and dry Pimples. <term lang="la">Lichen</term>
is also the callous part in an Horses Foot; like&shy;
wise a sort of green Moss.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Libra medica</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="physician's pound(n)">a Physicians Pound, is twelve
Ounces; for as often as they prescribe a Pound
they mean so many Ounces.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Lien</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Splen</term>.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="177">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Lienteria</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Looseness when the Meat is sent
out before it be altered.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ligamentum</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="ligament(n)">a Ligament, is a solid and very
fibrous part, proceeding almost from Matter like 
a Cartilage, different in size, number, and sci&shy;
tuation, broad or round, cold, as it comes near
the constitution of a Membrane or a Cartilage,
dryer or moister, harder or softer, more or less
tough and flexible, and designed by Nature for
the connecting of Parts, especially Bones, that
they may better perform their Motions.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ligula</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Clavicula</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Linea alba</form> <xpln lang="en">is a concourse of the Tendons of
the Muscles of the <term lang="la">Abdomen</term>, excepting the Ten&shy;
dons of the streight ones. For the Tendons of
the Oblique Muscles unite, and meet so on both
sides, that they make a kind of Tunic that co&shy;
vers the <term lang="la">Abdomen</term>, as if they were all but one
Tendon. It is white and not fleshy, proceeding
from the pointed Cartilage to the <term lang="la">os Pubis</term>; and
is narrower below the Navel than above.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Lingua</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="tongue(n)">the Tongue, is an oblong, broad,
thick Member, and thicker at the Roots and
thinner and sharper at the end; of a moderate
bigness, that it may move more quickly. In 
the Exterior and upper parts of the Tongue there
are a great many little Bodies which break out
from the Surface of the Tongue, and crooking
moderately incline backwards towards the Root,
so that they look like a Comb that cards Wooll.
These Cartilaginous Bodies in an Ox especially
seem to resemble the Figure of a Boare's Tooth;
in the lower part they have a certain Cavity:
They are made of a thick tenacious fibrous Mat&shy;
</page>

<page no="178">
ter, which seems like a heap of little Rods:
About the sides of the Tongue they grow smal&shy;
ler and smaller, so that they almost disappear,
and certain membranous Bodies are placed at
their Basis, which look like a Conical, and then
by and by a more obtuse pappy Substance: All
the little Protuberances are clothed with the
Membrane of the Tongue; they are firmly im&shy;
planted in a certain tenacious Tunic of the
Tongue, there being under them a crass viscous,
or nervous Substance, especially in those places,
where there are remarkable Pits in the Tongue
disposed in like order and manner, so that in
the inner part of the Tongue there are a great
many of them, which are firmly implanted in a 
certain viscous sort of Body. When the Mem&shy;
brane that covers the whole Tongue is taken off
there appears a certain glutinous Substance;
then a nervous pappy Body something yellow,
which spreads like the Membrane, and discovers
remarkable nervous Protuberances disposed of
in a wonderful order. The next thing that ap&shy;
pears are little Nipples in greater abundance
than those spoke of and of another order; for
as many little Protuberances as cover the outside
of the Tongue, so many nervous Nipples of this
sort are found within; these proceed from the
common pappy Substance, grow tolerably high,
and shoot out farther into nervous Sprouts from
the top of them, about which you discover innu&shy;
merable little Protuberances proceeding from 
the same Stock, and of an equal height, only
slenderer, like a Cone, and which go within
their proper Cavities ready made in the crass
</page>

<page no="179">
viscous Substance before mentioned, and at last
end towards the outermost Membrane. Fur&shy;
thermore the Substance of the Tongue is Muscu&shy;
lous. The Centre of the Tongue consists of se&shy;
veral sorts of Fibres, long, transverse, and ob&shy;
lique, which being mutually interwoven with
one another look like a Coverlet or Blanket: It
owes its Motion to peculiar Muscles of its own,
wherewith it is contracted and abbreviated.
The pair of Muscles are the <term lang="la">Styloglossum</term>, <term lang="la">Basio&shy;
glossum</term>, <term lang="la">Genioglossum</term>, <term lang="la">Ceratoglossum</term>, and <term lang="la">Mylo&shy;
glossum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">* Lithontriptica</form>, <xpln lang="en">are Medicines which break
the Stone.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Lithotomia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a cutting the Stone out of the
Bladder, and is thus performed. The Opera&shy;
tor lays the sick Person upon a soft Pillow in the
Bosom of some strong Man, after he has lept
three or four times from on high, then he ties
the Hands on each side fast to the sole of the
Foot, and two People standing on each side hold
the Knees as open as possible: After this the O&shy;
perator moistening one Finger of his left Hand,
or if necessity require, the two foremost, with
Oil of white Roses, thrusts them up into the
Fundament, and with his right Hand presses the
upper parts of the Secrets lightly, that by this
means the Stone may be brought to the <term lang="la">Perin&aelig;um</term>,
which when he has forced thither with his Fin&shy;
gers, he cuts with a two edged Knife proporti&shy;
onably to the bigness of the Stone, in the left
side betwixt the Testicles and the Fundament,
near to the Suture of the <term lang="la">Perin&aelig;um</term>, bringing the
Stone towards the Knife: And if the Stone
</page>

<page no="180">
come not out either of its own accord, or by the
thrusting of the Fingers, he draws it out with
Pincers, or some such Instrument of Art. The
Stone being drawn out, and all the Bands being
loosed, he closes the Wound duly, applys Reme&shy;
dies to stop the Blood, and takes care that the
Wound be closed up, least the Urine should con&shy;
tinually drop through. This way is called <term lang="la">Ap&shy;
paratus minor</term>, and is used especially in Boys, tho
it be frequently practised too in adult Persons in
these Countries. But in the <term lang="la">Apparatus major</term>,
or the greater Operation, the Patient bound as
before is set upon a Table and held there, then
the Chyrurgion thrusts in his Instrument called
<term lang="la">Itinerarium</term> by the Urinary Passage into the Blad&shy;
der as far as the very Stone, and cutting an hole
as before, He puts another Instrument called
<term lang="la">Conductor</term> into the hollow part of the <term lang="la">Itinerarium</term>
through the Wound, then the <term lang="la">Itinerarium</term> being
taken out of the Urinary Passage, he puts in his
Instrument called <term lang="la">Forceps</term> (a sort of Pincers) or
any other fit to pull out the Stone, through the
Wound he made, that he may lay hold of the
Stone and bring it out. This being done, the
Wound is bound up and consolidated as 'tis in
Children, only if it be large, it is saved, and an
Instrument of Silver applyed to it for two or
three days, which is useful to let out concreted
Blood, Flegm, and gravelly Urine. There is
yet another way of taking out the Stone, to wit,
by making an hole in the <term lang="la">Abdomen</term> by which the 
Stone is taken out of the bottom of the Bladder,
and in this way no dribling of Urine need to
be feared.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Lithotomus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Chyrurgion who is skilful in

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Lotio</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="bath(n)">is in a manner a particular Bath, where&shy;

tural Parts are washed, and that with physical

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Lumbaga</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Pain in the Muscles of the Loins

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Lumbrici</form> <xpln lang="en">are little Worms or Animals pro&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Lycanthropia, rabies Hydrophobica</form>, <xpln lang="en">a Madness

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Lygmos</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="hickets(n)">the Hickets, is a convulsive Motion
of the Nerves which spread up and down the
Gullet, returning after short Intermissions: It
proceeds from some <emend err="truoblesome">troublesome</emend> Matter that
vellicates the <term lang="la">&AElig;sophagus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Lympha</form> <xpln lang="en">is a clear limpide Humour, consisting
of the nervous Juice and of Blood, which being
continually separated by the Glandules, is at last
</page>

<page no="183">
discharged into the Blood again by Vessels pe&shy;
culiar to it. The <term lang="la">Lympha</term> comes not immedi&shy;
ately from the Blood or nervous Juice, as some
think, but it is the Superfluity of each, which
was more than enough for the Nourishment of a
part, like the Marrow in Bones: It is taken
sometimes for that Water which flows from the
Pricking of Nerves and other Wounds, and
which does not really flow from the Nerves 
themselves, but from the Lymphatick Vessels
which are cut and wounded.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Lymphatica vasa</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Ven&aelig; Lymphatic&aelig;</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Lyteria</form> <xpln lang="en">is a sign of the loosening of a great

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">MAcrocosmus</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="universe(n)">is the whole Universe.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Macula epatica</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Spot of a brown, or of
a sad yellow Colour, about an hand's breadth
broad, chiefly seizing upon the Groins, the
Breast and back; nay sometimes it covers the
whole Body, is attended with a certain sleight
Asperity of the Skin, which lets fall Scales, or a 
sort of Dendriff from it, which yet do not stick
altogether, but are disseminated here and there,
and sometimes disappear, sometimes break out
again.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Macula Matricalis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a spot with which a 
Child is born, of brownish Colour.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Macula volatica</form> <xpln lang="en">is a red or purple Spot here
and there in the Skin, which if it touch any
Orifice in the Body, as the Mouth, Nostrils,
</page>

<page no="184">
Eyes, Ears, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. and pierce so far, it becomes
mortal; fatal to Children.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Madarosis</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="baldness(n)">is a Baldness of the Head.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Magdateones</form> <xpln lang="en">are pieces of Plaister made up in

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Magisterium</form> <xpln lang="en">properly signifies a Powder pre&shy;
pared by Solution and Precipitation, impro&shy;
perly a resinous Matter made the same way,
which is more truly called an Extract. <term lang="la">Magi&shy;
steria</term> as they are various, so are they variously 
prepared; a solvent Liquor is always poured 
upon a dry Matter, reduced to durst, if it can
be had, or (if necessary) calcined, which is diffe&shy;
rent according to the Diversity of the <term lang="la">Magisteri&shy;
um</term>, plain or distilled Vinegar, both by it self,
and sharpened with Spirit of Nitre, Vitriol,
Salt, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. These are only in Minerals and Ani&shy;
mals; a <term lang="la">Lixivium</term> prepared of Salt of Tartar
and Water in Vegetables, Spirit of Wine in
things sulphureous, that is, endued with an
oily part; Yet these things belong rather to
Extracts. There is a precipitating Liquor
poured upon dissolved Bodies, commonly 
Oil of Tartar <term lang="la">per deliquium</term>, Urine, salt Water,
Spirit of Vitriol, Nitre, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. in Minerals and
Animals common Water, or Allum-water in
Vegetables; and there will subside at the bot&shy;
tom of the Glass a coagulated Substance which
must be dried, and if necessity require, first
sweetened and then burned.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Magistralia medicamenta</form> <xpln lang="en">are those Medicines

alia</term>, usual, because they ought to be used fre&shy;
</page>

quently once a Week, twice a Month, or the
like.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Malum mortuum</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="dead disease(n)">the dead Disease, is a sort of
