<page no="186">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mamma</form>, <xpln lang="en"><term lang="la">Mammilla</term>, <term lang="la">Uber</term>, the Breast, Dugs, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.
the <f type="i">Grammarians</f> call the inner part <term lang="la">Vbera</term>, and
the outward Protuberances <term lang="la">Mamm&aelig;</term>. A Breast
or Dug is a globous, white, and soft Body, lay&shy;
ing upon the pectoral Muscle on both sides, made
up of conglomerated Glandules in the in-side,
by the mediation whereof the Milk is separated
from the arterious Blood, and is conveyed out
by very little Pipes, which pass through the
Nipples.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mammiformes processus</form> <xpln lang="en">are two Apophyses of
the Bone of the back part of the Scull.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mammilla</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Mamma</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mandibula, Maxilla</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="jaw(n)">the Jaw, is either upper or
lower. The <f type="i">upper</f> is made of twelve Bones, on
each side six. The first is at the external corner
of the Eye, which joyned with the fore-pro&shy;
cess of the Bone of the Temples produces the
jugal Bone. The second constitutes the inner
corner of the Eye, has a large Passage in it, by
which the superabundant Moisture of the Eye
descends to the Nostrils. The third is within
the circle of the Eye, interposed betwixt the
other two. The fourth, the greatest of all, makes
the greatest part of the Cheeks and the Palate,
and is elaborately carved for the Reception of
the Teeth. The fifth helps to make the Nose.
The sixth with another Bone along with it ter&shy;
minates the extremity of the Palate: And all
these are joined rather by a plain Line than by
Sutures. The <f type="i">lower</f> Jaw at riper Years grows
into one continued Bone, extream hard, and
thick, and consequently very strong: It has
two Processes, one acute, called <term lang="la">Corone</term>, the
</page>

<page no="187">
other in the form of a little Head, called <term lang="la">Con&shy;
dylus</term>. It has two Holes within, and as many
without which make way for the Nerves; the 
under Teeth are implanted in it, and it is joyn&shy;
ted with the inner side of the Bone of the Temp&shy;
ples called <term lang="la">Os petrosum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mania</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="madness(n)">a sort of Madness, is a deprivation
of Imagination and Judgment, with great Rage
and Anger, but without a Feaver and Fear: It
proceeds from <term lang="la">sulphureo-saline</term> Animal Spirits,
like <term lang="la">Aqua stygia</term>, which cause strange furious
Impulses in the Body, not by consent of Parts,
but by their own Strength.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Manica Hypocratis</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a woollen Sack, in form
of a <term lang="la">Piramide</term>, wherewith <f type="i">Aromatick</f> Wines,
Medicines, and other Liquors are streined.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Maniodes</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="frenzy(n)">is a Phrensy, like the Madness which
is meant by <term lang="la">Mania</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Manipulus</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="handful(n)" lexeme="armful(n)">is a dry Measure, usual with Physi&shy;
cians in their Prescriptions; for it is a determi&shy;
nate quantity, to wit, as much as can be held
in one hand; meant for the most part of Herbs.
<term lang="la">Fasciculus</term> is a different quantity from <term lang="la">Mani&shy;
pulus</term>, an handful, for it properly signifies an
arm-full.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Manus Christi</form> <xpln lang="en">is a sort of Sugar, so called be&shy;
cause it is put into Cordials for very weak
People.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Marasmodes</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Feaver which at last ends in a
Consumption.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Marisca</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Ficus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Marmaryg&aelig;</form> <xpln lang="en">are the Glistenings and Corrusca&shy;
tions of the Eyes.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="188">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Marmelata</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="marmalade(n)">Marmelate, is the Juice of Quin&shy;
ces condensated into a Gelly with Sugar; and 
is either plain or spiced, for the use of Families.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Marmorata aurium</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="ear-wax(n)">Ear-wax, is a certain Ex&shy;
crement of the Ears, laid there in the auditory 
Passage from the openings of the Arteries, or 
sweat out from the Cartilages.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Masseteres</form> <xpln lang="en">are Muscles of the lower Jaw, pro&shy;
duced from the upper and the jugal Bone, they 
are connected to the lower Jaw, and can move 
it right-side, left-side, and forward, by reason of 
the various Disposition of <f type="i">Fibres</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Masticatio</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="chawing(n)">chawing, is an Action whereby we 
mince the Meat, and mix it with the Spittle
cated Juice in the Mouth.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Masticatorium</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Medicine which is masti&shy;
<emend err="">cated</emend> to provoke spitting.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mastoidei</form> <xpln lang="en">are Processes like Breasts or Dugs,
which from a broad Basis end in an obtuse top,
and are shaped like Tears in a Cows Udder: Also
Muscles which bend the Head, proceeding from
the Neck-bone and the Breast- bone, termina&shy;
ting in the Process <term lang="la">Mammiformis</term>, i.e. like a Dug
or Pap.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mastos</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Mamma</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mater dura</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="little brain(n)">is a Membrane which sticks close
to the Scull within in some places, and mediate&shy;
ly covers both the Brain and <term lang="la">Cerebellum</term>, or little
Brain; it has four Cavities which supply the
place of Veins, and come together betwixt the
Brain and <term lang="la">Cerebellum</term>, which Conjunction <f type="i">Hero&shy;
philus</f> calls <term lang="la">torcular</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Matter tenuis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Membrane which immediate&shy;
ly clothes the Brain and <term lang="la">Cerebellum</term>, extreamly
</page>

<page no="189">
full of sanguinary Vessels, made to keep in the
Spirits generated in the Brain and <term lang="la">Cerebellum</term>,
that they fly not away.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Matracium</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="little sack(n)">is nothing but a little Sack, where&shy;
in is calcinated <f type="i">Tartar</f> or the like, pricked here
and there for the emission of Liquor.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Matrix</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Uterus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Maxilla superior</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="upper jaw-bone(n)">the upper Jaw-bone, has
eleven Bones belonging to it, five on each side,
and one without a fellow. 1. In the lesser Cor&shy;
ner of the Eye. 2. In the greater Corner of 
the Eye. 3. Which is the greatest of all, con&shy;
stitutes the whole Palate, and contains the up&shy;
per Teeth. 4. With its Partner constitutes the
ridge of the Nose. 5. Is placed at the extre&shy;
mity of the Palate, where the Holes of the No&shy;
strils tend towards the upper part of the Gul&shy;
let: See <term lang="la">Mandibula</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Maxilla inferior</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="lower jaw-bone(n)">the lower Jaw-<emend err="borne">bone</emend> is that
which contains the under-Teeth; it has a Pro&shy;
cess on each side, the foremost, called <term lang="la">Corone</term>,
the hinder <term lang="la">Condylus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Meatus auditorius</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="drum of the ear(n)">the auditory Passage begins
from the Cavity of the inner part of the Ear,
and is clothed with a thin Skin as far as the brim
of the <term lang="la">Tympanum</term>, or drum of the Ear: It's use
is to receive the Air and audible Species, and to
contain the Ear-wax.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Meatus urinarius</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Urethra</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Meconium</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="opiate(n)">Opiate, or the condensed Juice of
Poppies. Also the Excrements of a <term lang="la">F&oelig;tus</term>,
which stick to the Intestines after the Birth,
so called from the Blackness of Poppy-Juice.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Meconologia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Description of <term lang="la">opium</term>.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="190">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mediana Vena</form> <xpln lang="en">is the middle Vein in the bend&shy;
ing of the Cubit betwixt the Cephalick and Ba&shy;
silick: It is safely opened, because there's nei&shy;
ther Nerve nor Artery under it.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mediastinum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a doubling of the Membrane of
the sides, which divides the Lungs and other
<term lang="la">Viscera</term> of the Breast into two parts. It pro&shy;
ceeds from the Vertebres of the Back, and go&shy;
ing on forward reaches the Breast-bone, and
makes this Partition.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Medicamentum</form>, <xpln lang="en">a <f type="i">Medicine</f>, is a convenient
help, whereby Diseases are repelled for the re&shy;
covery of Health; and it is either <f type="i">actual</f>, which 
affects the Body at first touch with that Quali&shy;
ty it is endowed with, as hot Iron, cold Water:
Or <f type="i">potential</f>, whose Efficacy is not perceived till
it be stirred up from some stay in the Body, as
Pepper, Raddish, sharp Salts, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. Again, a Me&shy;
dicine is endowed with first, or second, or 
third Qualities, all which depend upon the Temp&shy;
perament and the various Motion of Particles
in our Bodies. Medicine is threefold, Chy&shy;
rurgery, Physick, strictly so called, and Diet.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Medicina</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="physic(n)">Physick, is an Art assistant to Na&shy;
ture, and preserving Health in Human Bodies as
much as is possible by convenient Remedies.
<f type="i">Senertus</f> and others rightly divide it into five
parts: 1. <term lang="la">Physiologia</term>, which treates of Human
Constitution, as it is sound and well, to which
belongs <f type="i">Anatomy</f> too. 2. <term lang="la">Pathalogia</term>, which
treats of the preternatural Constitution of our
Bodies. 3. <term lang="la">Semiotica</term>, which treats of the signs
of Health and Diseases. 4. <term lang="la">Hygieina</term>, which
delivers Rules of the Regimen to be observed in
</page>

<page no="191">
the Preservation of Health. 5. <term lang="la">Therapeutica</term>,
which teaches <f type="i">Diet</f>, <f type="i">Chyrurgery</f>, and <f type="i">Medicine</f>.
The general division of Physick is only into 
two parts: the <f type="i">Theory</f>and the <f type="i">Practice</f>; the
Subject of Physick is human Body, as curable;
and its end and design <f type="i">Health</f>. <f type="i">Hippocrates</f> calls 
it a long Art, and <f type="i">Paracelsus</f> a short one; and 
certain <f type="i">Arabians</f> a little one, but in reality it is
a long, a great, and noble art.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Medicinalis dies</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Critici dies</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Medicus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="physician(n)">a Physician, is a Man highly skilful
in the art of Physick, modest, sober, and cour&shy;
teous. <f type="i">Scaliger</f> describes a Physician thus, That
he ought to be a learned, honest, mild, dili&shy;
gent, a fortunate Man, and of ripe Years, one
that relies upon God, not arrogant with his
Knowledg, Labour or Success, nor covetous.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Medius Venter</form>; <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Thorax</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Medulla</form> <xpln lang="en">in <term lang="la">Mineralogia</term> in the Description of
Minerals, is that softish par, which is found in
some Stones in <term lang="la">Phytologia</term>, or Description of
Plants, it signifies the middle, softer and more
excellent part, which they call also <term lang="la">Cor</term> and
<term lang="la">Matrix</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Medulla cerebri</form> <xpln lang="en">is a white soft Substance, cove&shy;
red on the out-sdie with the barky Substance,
which is more of an ashy Colour; it makes that
which is called the <term lang="la">Corpus callosum</term>, or callous Bo&shy;
dy, within: Imagination and the Distribution of
Animal Spirits are performed there. <f type="i">Mal&shy;
pighius</f> asserts that it consists of innumerable
Threds or Filaments.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Medulla oblongata</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="common sensory(n)">is the beginning of the Spi&shy;
nal Marrow, whence arise the Nerves within
</page>

<page no="192">
the Scul, it descends to the <term lang="la">Os sacrum</term>, through
the Hole of the hinder part of the Head and the
Vertebres. It sends out ten pair of Nerves to
the Chest, the Abdomen, and the Limbs. It is
called also the common Sensory, because that
where the Original of the Nerves is, there is the 
common place of the Reception of Species from
the external Senses.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Medulla Ossium</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="marrow(n)">Marrow in the Bones, is a
fat Substance laid up in the Cavities, or Poro&shy;
sities of the Bones by the Arteries; it is kept in 
a Membrance, and is quite destitute of all Sense;
it is red in the greater Cavities, white in the
less, soft and succulent in spungy Bones. We
may imagine likewise, that it is but a sweating of
the Bones, in that they receive more sulphure&shy;
ous fat Matter than they can convert into Nou&shy;
rishment, which afterwards flows to the inner
part of the Bones by <term lang="la">Ductus</term>'s and little Ca&shy;
vities for that purpose, after that is received by
the Veins, and communicated to the Blood.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Medulla spinalis</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="spinal marrow(n)" lexeme="tail of the brain(n)">the spinal Marrow, or the
tail of the Brain, is that part which goes down
the middle of the Back by the Vertebres, and is
terminated at the <term lang="la">Os Sacrum</term>; it is also of the same
nature and use with the Brain; it is a Coagmen&shy;
tation of Nerves, and has the use of them;
upwards it is forked; hence if either party be
obstructed there arises a Palsy of one side. It
sends out thirty pair of Nerves on each side to 
the Limbs, great Cavities, and other parts of the
Body. If it be washed with a convenient Li&shy;
quor, it twill sever into a great many little
Fibres.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="193">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Megalosphlanchnus</form> <xpln lang="en">is one who has great swell&shy;
ing Bowels.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mela</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="tent(n)">is a Chyrurgeons Instrument, called <term lang="la">Spe&shy;
cillum</term>, the vulgar call it <term lang="la">Tenta</term>, a Tent, from
trying. It is made for the most part of Silver, or
Ivory, and that to probe Ulcers, or to draw
the Stone out of the Yard, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. It is of different
Shapes according as it is differently used.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Melanagoga</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines that expel black
Choler.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Melancholia</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="sadness(n)">is a Sadness without any evident
Cause, whereby People fancy terrible and some&shy;
times ridiculous things to themselves: It pro&shy;
ceeds from the Degeneracy of the Animal Spirits
from their own spirituous saline Nature into 
an Acide, like the Spirit of Vitriol, Box-tree,
Oak, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. Also it is called black Choler, or
black Blood, Adust, and <f type="i">Salino-Sulphureous</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Melas</form>, <xpln lang="en">see in <term lang="la">Alphus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Meliceri</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="tumor(n)">is a Tumour shut up within a Tu&shy;
nick, proceeding from matter like Honey, with&shy;
out Pain, round, yielding if pressed, but quickly
returning again. It seems to proceed from
Lymphatick Particles which do not circulate
right, and which when the Moisture is evapo&shy;
rated, leave a honyish-kind of Substance.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Melicratum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Drink made of one part Ho&shy;
ney, and eight parts Rain-water.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Membrana</form> <xpln lang="en">is a nervous, fibrous, broad, plain,
white, and dilatable Substance, which covers 
the Bowels, the great Cavities of the Body, the
Muscles, <term lang="la">&amp;c.</term> and is endowed with an exqui&shy;
site Sense.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="194">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Membrana carnosa</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Panniculus
carnosus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Membrana Urinaria</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Allantois</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Membrum</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="member(n)">a Member, is an organical Body,
made up of several similar parts, designed for
the performance of voluntary Actions.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Memoria</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="memory(n)">Memory, is the retention of Marks or 
Footsteps impressed in several places in the
barky Substance, or folding Fibres of the Brain
by the motion of Objects. Memory resides in
the substance of the Brain, called <term lang="la">Corticalis</term>, like
Bark.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mendosa Sutura</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Squammea</term>, is a scaly Con&shy;
nexion of Bones, as may be seen in the Bone of
the Temples, and the Bone of the fore part of
the Head.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Meningophylax</form> <xpln lang="en">is that which preserves the Me&shy;
ninx or Membrane of the Head, as thin Gold or
Silver Plates, which are applied when the Skull
is opened.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Meninx</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Mater dura</term> <f type="i">&</f> <term lang="la">tenuis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mensa</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="grinder(n)">is the broader part of the Teeth called,
Grinders, which chaws and minces the Meat.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Menses</form>, <xpln lang="en">the Courses, are Excretions of Blood
every Month from the Womb, and not from its
Neck or Passage called <term lang="la">Vagina</term>. The cause thereof 
consists in a fermentative Matter, generated in the
Substance of the Womb; or a seminal Matter,
infused into the Blood from the Testicles, or
<term lang="la">Ovaria</term> in a Woman, which being mixed with
the mass of the Blood, ferments it into such  a 
motion, that it is forced to discharge it self
every Month. They begin usually when young
Maids grow ripe, at twelve or fourteen, but
</page>

<page no="195">
cease naturally in Women with Child, past
Children, and those that give suck.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Menstrua alba</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Fluor albus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Menstruum Mulierum</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Menses</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Menstruum</form> <xpln lang="en">is that which is to be distilled, or
a Liquor which corrodes Metals, and dissolves
Stones, as Vinegar, <term lang="la">Aqua fortis</term>, Spirit of
Wine, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term> It may be taken also for the <term lang="la">Caput
mortuum</term>, which is left after Distillation.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mentagra</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="wild tetter(n)" lexeme="ringworm(n)">is a sort of wild Tetter or Ring&shy;
worm, which was not known in <f type="i">Claudius</f>'s days.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mesar&aelig;um</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Mesenterium</term>; whence
its Vessels are called as well Mesaraick, as Me&shy;
senterick.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mesaraica vasa</form>, <xpln lang="en">see in <term lang="la">Mesar&aelig;um</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mesenteria vasa</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Masar&aelig;on</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mesenterium</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Membrane of the <term lang="la">Periton&aelig;&shy;
um</term> doubled, enriched with Glandules, Nerves, 
Arteries, Veins, Chyliferous and Lymphatick
Vessels; it is in the middle of the Abdomen, and
contains the Intestines in a wonderful manner.
It has a great Glandule in the middle called <term lang="la">Pan&shy;
creas Asellis</term>; about which are several other less
Glandules, to which the milky Vessels of the
first rank tend from the Intestines, and Lympha&shy;
tick Vessels from the Liver and other Parts;
from these Glandules again the milky Vessels of
the second rank ascend to the Vessel that carries 
the mass of Chyle, and discharge themselves
into it.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Meser&aelig;um</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Mesar&aelig;um</term> and <term lang="la">Mesenterium</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mesocolon</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="mesentery(n)">is that part of the Mesentery which
is continued to the great Guts.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mesonuctium</form> <xpln lang="en">is the middle of the Night.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="196">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mesopleurii</form> <xpln lang="en">are the intercostal Muscles, twenty
two on each side, eleven external, and as many
internal.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Metabole</form> <xpln lang="en">is a change of Time, Air, or Diseases.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Metacarpus <term lang="en">and</term> Metacarpium</form> <xpln lang="en">is the back of the
Hand, made of four oblong little Bones, which
expand the Palm of the Hand, and they are
called <term lang="la">Post-Brachialia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Metacondyli</form> <xpln lang="en">are the utmost Bones of the
Fingers.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Metalepticus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Metaleptick Motion of the
Muscles.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Metallum</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="metal(n)">Mettal, is a solid, rigid Substance,
found in Mountains and subterraneous Cavities.
The several sorts of them are comprehended
in this Verse.
<f type="i">Sol, Mars, Luna, Venus, Saturnus, Jupiter, Hermes</f>.
Gold is the most solid Metal, the Tincture 
whereof is highly extolled by the Chymists.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Metallurgus, <term lang="en">or</term> Metallicus</form>, <xpln lang="en">is one who searches
after Metalls, as the Chymists.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Metapedium</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same in the Foot, that <term lang="la">Meta&shy;
carpus</term> is in the Hand.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Metaphrenum</form> <xpln lang="en">is that part of the Back which
comes after the <term lang="la">Diaphragme</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Metaptosis</form> <xpln lang="en">is the degenerating of one Disease
into another, as of a Quartane Ague into a 
Tertian; and on the contrary, of an Apoplexy 
into a Palsy, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Metastasis</form> <xpln lang="en">is when a Disease goes from one
part to another; which happens to Apoplectick
People, when the Matter which affects the
</page>

<page no="197">
Brain is translated to the Nerves.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Metasyncrisis</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Operation of a Medicine
externally applied, which fetches out the Hu&shy;
mours from their closest Recesses.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Metatarsus</form> <xpln lang="en">are the five little Bones of the
Foot, connected to the Bones of the first part
of the Foot, which immediately succeeds the
Leg.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Methodica Medicina</form> <xpln lang="en">is that which was inven&shy;
ted by <f type="i">Themison Laodiceus</f>, and improved by
<f type="i">Thessalus Trallianus</f>, who said that the Art might
be learned in six Months time.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Methodus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a part of Physick whereby Reme&shy;
dies are found out by Indications for the Re&shy;
stauration of Health.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Metopum</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="forehead(n)">is the Fore-head.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Metrenchyta</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Instrument wherewith Li&shy;
quors are injected into the Womb.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Miasma</form> <xpln lang="en">is a contagious Infection in the Blood
and Spirits, as in the Plague and Scurvy.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Microcosmus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="little world(n)">Man is called the little World
as a Compendium of the greater.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Microphthalmus</form> <xpln lang="en">is one who has little Eyes from
his Birth.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Miliaris herpes</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Herpes</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Miserere mei</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Chordapsus</term>, is a most vehe&shy;
ment Pain in the Guts, proceeding from an In&shy;
flammation of them, or Involution and the pe&shy;
ristaltick Motion inversed; whence the Excre&shy;
ments are discharged by the Mouth. It is called
also <term lang="la">Volvulus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mitella</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="swathe(n)">is a Swathe that holds up the Arm
when it is hurt or wounded.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="198">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Miva</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="quince(n)">is the Flesh or Pulp of a Quince boiled
up with Sugar into a thick Consistence.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mixtura</form> <xpln lang="en">is a <f type="i">solid</f> or <f type="i">liquid</f> Substance mixed
together of several Medicines. Mixtures are
very different according to the scope of the
Physician; they are taken especially in Drops
or Spoonfuls, and sometimes in Draughts. They
are made either of Liquors only, such as are di&shy;
stilled Waters, Spirits, and Oils, any way mix&shy;
ed together, as Waters with Waters, Oil with
Oil, Waters with Spirits, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. or of Liquors
with convenient Syrups, Pouders, Confections,
Opiates, all of them together, or only some.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mna, <term lang="en">or</term> Mina</form>, <xpln lang="en">an <term lang="la">Attick Mna</term> contains an
hundred Drams, or twelve Ounces and an
half; the <f type="i">Roman</f>, ninety six Drams, or twelve 
Ounces; the <f type="i">Alexandrian</f>, an hundred and sixty
Drams, or twenty Ounces.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Modiolus, Trepanum, <term lang="en">or</term> Anabaptiston</form>, <xpln lang="en">is an In&shy;
strument which they use in profound Corrupti&shy;
os, Contusions, Cuts and Fractures of Bones,
not easily, tho to be, applied; unless, 1. The 
Chips and Prominences of the Bones prick.
2. When the upper Table is entire, but de&shy;
pressed, and the lower broken. 3. When the
extravasated Blood would choak a Man with
Corruption. The manner of perforating is thus:
When the Hairs are shaven off, the Skin is to be
cut to the <term lang="la">Pericranium</term>, avoiding as prudently
as may be the Muscles of the Temples and the
Sutures, and for this time the Wound is to be 
bound up, unless there be so little Blood spilt,
that the Membrane, called <term lang="la">Pericranium</term>, may at
the same time be pulled off from the Scull:
</page>

<page no="199">
Then after a few Hours you may stop the Ears
of the Patient, and take one of these Instruments
called a <term lang="la">Masculine Modiolus</term>, whose point is to
be fixed in the Skull, but so far off the Fracture,
that it touch it not, much less the Suture, with
its Teeth; tho some never avoid the Sutures,
and assure us that they have perforated them as
successfully as any other part: Then hold the In&shy;
strument fast with the left-hand, and turn it
round with the right, till you have cut out a
pretty deep Circle: After this take a <term lang="la">Feminine
Modiolus</term> (which has no point in the middle)
and turn it round as before: In the mean time
take away the Dust that proceeds from the Per&shy;
foration, and moisten the Instrument in Oil and
Water to make it cool and slippery: The
Blood that appears will shew that you are now
gone as deep as the second Table, <term lang="la">i.e.</term> beyond
the Scull to the Meninx, and then you must press
very gently, lest the Membrane of the Brain be
unadvisedly hurt; when the Bone begins to 
wag, put something in betwixt the sides of the 
Wound, loosen it, and take it out with a pair
of Chirurgeons Pincers.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mola, Patella, <term lang="en">or</term> Rotula</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a round and
broad Bone, at the joynting of the Thigh and
Leg, where the Knee, excepting this Bone, is 
begirt with a Membranous Ligament.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mola carnea</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a fleshy, and sometimes a spun&shy;
gy Substance without Bones or Bowels; it is
often black like concreted Blood; and some&shy;
times extream hard, preternaturally brought
into the World instead of a <term lang="la">F&oelig;tus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Molares, <term lang="en">or</term> Maxillares Dentes</form>; <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Dentes</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<page no="200">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mollientia</form>; <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Emollientia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la"><emend err="Melopes">Molopes</emend></form>, <xpln lang="en"><term lang="la">Vibices</term>, <term lang="la">Enchymoma</term>, <term lang="la">Sugillationes</term>, all

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Molynsis</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Miasma</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Monocolum</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Gut <term lang="la">C&aelig;eum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Monohemera</form> <xpln lang="en">are Diseases that are cured in

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Monopagia</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Monopegia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Menopegia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a sharp Pain in the Head, afflict&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mons Veneris</form> <xpln lang="en">is the upper part of a Woman's

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Morbilli</form>, <xpln lang="en">the Meazles, are red Spots which
proceed from an aerial Contagion in the Blood,
they neither swell nor are suppurated, and
differ only in degree from the Small-ox.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Morbus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="disease(n)">a Disease, is such a Constitution of
Body as renders us inapt for the due perfor&shy;
mance of our Actions: Or, it is an ill Constitu&shy;
tion in a Man which hurts any of our Faculties,
according to <f type="i">Sylvius de la Boc</f>. Diseases are two&shy;
fold, either from an <f type="i">ill Conformation</f>, or an <f type="i">In&shy;
disposition</f>: An ill Conformation is six-fold, for it
consists in Number, Magnitude, Figure, Cavity,
Surface and Situation: Indisposition is either
occult or manifest; the Occult is poysoned, con&shy;
tagious, and pestilent; the Manifest is either
simple, as hot, cold, moist, dry, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. or com&shy;
pound, when more Qualities than one are
peccant at once, as cold and moist, hot and
moist, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. There's a Disease by <term lang="la">Idiipothia</term>,
peculiar to ones self, by <term lang="la">Protopathia</term>, when one
</page>

<page no="2010">
has it first, by <term lang="la">Deuteropathia</term>, at second hand,
and by Sympathy. Also Diseases are simple or 
compound, gentle or malignant, short, long,
acute, continued, intermittent, hereditary, na&shy;
tive, Pituitous, bilious, melancholy, Summer,
Winter, Autumnal, Epidemick, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Morbus Regius</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Icterus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Moretum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a sort of Drink which our Wo&shy;
men use much when they think they have con&shy;
ceived, for they are perswaded that it spoils a
false Conception and strengthens a true one: 
It is so called from the Mulberries they put
in it.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Moria</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="dullness(n)" lexeme="folly(n)" lexeme="stupidity(n)">Dulness or Folly, or Stupidity, is a de&shy;
fect of Judgment and Understanding; it pro&shy;
ceeds chiefly from lack of Imagination and Me&shy;
memory.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Morosis</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Moria</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Morsuli</form>, <xpln lang="en"><term lang="la">Tabell&aelig;</term>, they are Medicines of a square

upon a wooden, stone, or brazen Table, to be

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Motus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a peice of Linnen teezed like Wool,

Blood.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Motus Peristalticus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Peristalticus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Muccus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Mucus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<page no="202">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mucago</form> <xpln lang="en">is a viscous Extraction, made of Seeds,
Gums, Roots, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. with Water.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mucilago</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Mucago</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mucro cordis</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Apex</term>, is the lower pointed

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mucronatum os</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Ensiformis Cartilago</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mucus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="snot(n)">we call it Snot, is a liquid, thick, and
viscous Excrement, which flows from the <term lang="la">Pro&shy;
cessus Papillares</term> by the <term lang="la">Os Cribfriforme</term> to the No&shy;
strils and Palate.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Muliebria</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Cunnus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Musc&aelig; caput</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Myocephalum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Musculus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="muscle(n)">a Muscle, is an organical part fur&shy;
nished with two Tendons, and a fibrous or fleshy
Belly or middle part: Its Office is to move the
Members that are contiguous to it. This Mo&shy;
tion or Contraction is performed by the flowing
of the Animal Spirits from the Brain to the Ten&shy;
dons by the Nerves, and thence to the middle of
the Muscles, where they contract them, and
when that is done, recede to the Muscles again.
The Antients divided the Body of a Muscle into
the Head, Belly, and Tail; in which division
they called the Extremity of the Muscle, con&shy;
nected to that part towards which the Contracti&shy;
on was made, the Head; the end or part of the
Muscle, inserted into that part which was to be
moved, the Tail; and lastly the intermediate
part of the Muscle, which is more swell'd with
Flesh, they called the Belly; and then in the per&shy;
formance of Motion they supposed the Muscle
was swell'd about the Head and Belly, and con&shy;
sequently shortned in its length, so that it drew
the Member, to which it was fastned, near to it.
</page>

<page no="203">
But how this was done they say  not. Muscles
are destined either to the use of Cavities, or
Limbs, and are diversly denominated from their
Shapes, Places where they are, and Actions they
perform.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mycteres</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="nostrils(n)">are the Nostrils, or the Receptacles
of pituitous Humors, which distil out of the Brain
by the <term lang="la">Processus Papillares</term>, the Extremities of the
<f type="i">Olfactory</f> Nerves.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mydesis</form> <xpln lang="en">is Corruption or Rottenness from too
much moisture.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mydriasis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a too great Dilatation of the <f type="i">Pupil</f> 
of the Eye which makes the Sight dim.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Myelos</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="marrow(n)">the Marrow of the Bones, or of the
Brain, or Spinal Marrow.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Myle</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Molagenu</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Myloglossum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a pair of Muscles which arise a&shy;
bout the back side of the grinding Teeth, and 
are inserted into the Ligament of the Tongue, 
and are said to turn the Tongue upwards.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mylph&aelig;</form> <xpln lang="en">signify the falling off of the Hairs of
the Eye-lids: Also Medicines against the falling
off of Hair.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Myocephalum</form> <xpln lang="en">is the falling of the <term lang="la">Tunica uvea</term>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Myodes platysma</form> <xpln lang="en">is a broad musculous Expansi&shy;
on in the Neck, proceeding there from a sort of
a fat Membrane.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Myologia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Description of Muscles.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Myopia</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="purblindness(n)">is a certain Dimness of sight in distant
Objects, and yet a Perspicacity in things near at

</page>

<page no="204">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Myopiasis</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Myopia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Myops</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="purblind(a)">is one that is Purblind; which is occa&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Myrach</form>, <xpln lang="en">is an <f type="i">Arabian</f> Word, and signifies the

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Myracopum</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Ointment that takes away

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Myrmecia</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="wart(n)">is a sort of Wart; they are harder
and lower than those fleshy Tumors called <term lang="la">Thymi</term>,
take deeper Root, and occasion greater Pain, 
broad below, small at top, and emit less Blood.
They are scarce ever bigger than a sort of Pulse
called <term lang="la">Lupines</term>. They breed in the Palms of the
Hand, or the sole of the Foot.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Myrinx</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Tympanum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Myropola</form>, <xpln lang="en">is one that sells Ointments.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Myrtum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a little piece of Flesh in a Womans

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Mystax</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="upper lip(n)">is the upper Lip and the Hairs upon it.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Myurus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a mutilated Pulse, increasing or de&shy;
creasing gradually.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Myxa</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="snot(n)">is Snot, a pituitous Humour, which de&shy;
scends from the Extremity of the <f type="i">olfactory</f> Nerves
to the Nostrils.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">N&AElig;vi</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="mole(n)">Moles, are certain native Spots, and
are two-fold, either plain, or protuberant,
different in shape and colour. They happen to 
Child-bearing Women from a false Imagination,
Drunkenness, Extasy, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Narcosis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a privation of Sense, as in a Palsy,
or in taking of <term lang="la">Opium</term>, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Narcotica</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines that stupify, and allay
Pain.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nasalia</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Errhina</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nascalia</form>, <xpln lang="en">are little globular Bodies which are
put into the Neck of the Matrix, made of the 
same substance as <term lang="la">Pessaria</term>: see <term lang="la">Pessaria</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nata</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Natta</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nates cerebri</form> <xpln lang="en">are two round Prominences, 
behind the Beds of the <f type="i">Optick</f> Nerves, which grow
to the upper part of the Marrowy Substance,
they are small in Men, and larger in Brutes.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Natta</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="tumor(n)">is a great soft Tumor, without Pain
and Colour, which grows especially in the Back,
yet sometimes in the Shoulders; its Root is slen&shy;
der, yet it encreases so prodigiously that it will
grow as big as a Melon, or a Gourd; it is made
of fat Matter; and therefore ought to be
reckoned amongst the <term lang="la">Steatomata</term>. See <term lang="la">Steato&shy;
mata</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Natura</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Cunnus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Naturalis facultas</form>, <xpln lang="en">a natural Faculty, is an
Action depending chiefly upon the <term lang="la">Cerebellum</term>,
whereby the Body, without our notice, is nou&shy;
rished, encreased, and preserved by the Blood
</page>

<page no="206">
and Animal Spirits; upon which likewise all Ex&shy;
cretions, Digestions, and Generations depend.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Naviculare os</form>, <xpln lang="en">called also <term lang="la">Cymbiforme</term>, is the
third Bone in each Foot, in that part of it which
immediately succeeds the Leg.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Necrosis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a black and blew Mark in any part.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nectar</form> <xpln lang="en">is the drink of the Gods, as <term lang="la">Ambrosia</term>
is their drink. But with Physicians it signifies
rather a Medicinal Drink, but with a most de&shy;
licious colour, taste and smell.</xpln></wordentry> 

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nemomena</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Nomas</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nepenthes</form>, <xpln lang="en"><term lang="la">Opiate Laudunum</term>, a Medicine wor&shy;
thy indeed of Praise. It signifies as much as with&shy;
out Pain and Trouble, and by reason of the in&shy;
comparably admired Effects it produces, highly
deserves the name of <term lang="la">Laudunum</term> (a Word im&shy;
porting Praise.) <term lang="la">Nepenthes</term> they say was <f type="i">Helen</f>'s
Remedy, wherewith she expelled all Sorrow from
her Heart, and waxed merry and cheerful.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nephel&aelig;</form> <xpln lang="en">are small white Spots upon the Eyes.
Also little Clouds as it were that swim in the
middle of Urine; likewise little white Spots in 
the surface of the Nails like little Clouds.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nephritica</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines against the Diseases
of the Reins.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nephriticus</form> <xpln lang="en">is one who is troubled with a Dis&shy;
ease in the Reins.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nephritis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Pain in the Reins, proceeding
either from an ill Disposition, or an Inflamma&shy;
tion, or from the Stone and Gravel, accompa&shy;
nied with Vomiting and Stretching of the Thigh.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nephros</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="kidney(n)">is a Kidney, on each side of the <term lang="la">Abdo&shy;
men</term> one, placed about the Loins under the Li&shy;
ver and Spleen; it is shaped like a Kidney Bean:
</page>

<page no="207">
Its Substance is made up of a great company of
little Conduits. On both sides it receives the
<term lang="la">Serum</term> from the Glandules which border upon
the Arteries, and carries it to the little Bodies
in the Reins called <term lang="la">Caruncul&aelig; Papillares</term> (which
see) that so it may be discharged by the <term lang="la">Pelvis</term>, 
the Basin, the Ureters, the Bladder, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nervus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="nerve(n)">a Nerve, is a fibrous, round, long, 
white, porous Substance like an <f type="i">Indian</f>  Cane,
which conveys the Animal Spirits to make the
parts of the Body moveable and sensible. Ten
pair of Nerves proceed from the oblongated
Marrow within the Scull: As the Odoratory,
and Opthalmick Nerve, that which moves the
Eyes; the Pathetick, the Gustatory, or that
which perceives Tastes; the Nerve called <term lang="la">Timi&shy;
dus</term> or fearful, that which serves the Organ of
Hearing; the <term lang="la">Parvagum</term>, that which moves the
Tongue, and the Muscles of the Neck. The
Ancients only acknowledg Seven pair within the 
Scull. Below the Scull they reckon Thirty pair;
seven from the Spinal Marrow in the Neck;
twelve from the same in the Back; five from the
Loins, and six from the <term lang="la">Os Sacrum</term>: All the
Nerves below the Scull proceed from the Spinal
Marrow, which pass through the holes in the
sides of the Vertebres, and are designed for the
use of the Limbs and great Cavities. A Nerve,
a Tendon, and a Ligament are impertinently
taken for one and the same thing by Chirurge&shy;
ons.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Neurodes</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="fever(n)">is a sort of lingring Fever, so called
by the most Learned <f type="i">Willis</f>; because that the ner&shy;
vous Juice, departing from its own right natural
</page>

<page no="208">
Crasis, becomes the occasion of an <term lang="la">Atroph&aelig;</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Neurologia</form> <xpln lang="en">is an elegant Description of the
Nerves, which <f type="i">Willis</f> has performed beyond any
Man whatsoever.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Neuron</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Nervus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Neurotica</form> <xpln lang="en">are Remedies against the Diseases
of the Nerves.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Neurotomia</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Anatomical Section of
Nerves; also a pricking of Nerves.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Neurotomus</form> <xpln lang="en">is one who is troubled with a 
pricking of the Nerves. Or one who dissects
them Anatomically.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Neuritica</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Neurotica</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nidrosa Dyspepsia</form>; <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Dyspepsia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nidus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Focus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Noctambulo</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Noctambulus</term>, is one who walks
in his Sleep, opens Doors and Windows, and
goes over the highest and most dangerous Places
without perceiving it: The Cause of it is hardly
to be given, unless Sleep be divided into Total
and Partial; the Total is common ordinary
Sleep, but the Partial takes place in this case,
because that Objects are seen indeed, and are of&shy;
fered to the common Sensory, but penetrate not
to the place of Imagination, so that they may be
perceived.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nodulus</form>, <xpln lang="en"><term lang="la">Nodus</term>, is a Bag of suitable Ingredi&shy;
ents as the Disease requires, put into Beer or
Wine, the Tincture whereof the Patient is to
drink.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nodus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Ganglion</term> and <term lang="la">Nodulus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Noli me tangere</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="canker(n)">is a sort of Canker in the Face,
especially above the Chin. There arises a Tu&shy;
mour or Ulcer about the Mouth and Nose, like
</page>

<page no="207">
an exulcerated Canker, which grows slowly at
the beginning, like a little Pimple; it remains a
whole Year, otherwise is less troublesome than
a Canker, which gnaws and eats more in one
Day than a <term lang="la">Noli me tangere</term> doth in a Month.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nomas</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="ulcer(n)">is a putrid Ulcer that feeds upon the
parts.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nosocomium</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="hospital(n)">is an Hospital for poor sick Peop&shy;
ple, where they are attended, and cured, if pos&shy;
sible.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nosologia</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Pathalogia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nosos</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Morbus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Not&aelig; matern&aelig;</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">N&aelig;vus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Noth&aelig; cost&aelig;</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="bastard ribs(n)">are the five lowest Ribs on each
Side, called Bastard Ribs, so called because they do
do not join with the Breast-Bone as other Ribs,
nor are as the others Boney but Cartilaginous.
Diseases are likewise called <term lang="la">Nothi</term>, or Bastard,
which exceed the ordinary and common Rule;
as tertian, quartane, or quotidian Bastard Agues;
a Bastard Plurisy <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nothus</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="back(n)">is the Back, the back part of the
Chest.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Novacula</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="surgeon's knife(n)">is a Chirurgeons Knife, the shape
whereof differs according to the difference of
Operations: And therefore can hardly be de&shy;
scribed.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nubecul&aelig;</form> <xpln lang="en">are little light Particles which mu&shy;
tually, but loosely, close with one another, and
swim upon the Urine.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nucha</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="nap(n)">is the hinder part, or nap of the Neck,

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nuciositas</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Myopia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="208">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Numero</form>, <xpln lang="en">not only Fruits and Seeds are mea&shy;
sured by  Number, but likewise the parts of Ani&shy;
mals, as Yolks of Eggs. It is commonly noted
thus, <f type="i">No</f> or <f type="i">Num</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nutrimentum</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Alimentum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nutritio</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="increase(n)">is a natural Increase, whereby that
which continually decays of any corporeal Sub&shy;
stance, is repaired by convenient Nourishment.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nux</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="pain in the head(n)">is a sort of Pain in the Head, which afflicts
a place about as big as a Nut; as an <term lang="la">Ovum</term>, a 
<term lang="la">Clavus</term>, and other sorts.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nychthemerum</form> <xpln lang="en">is four and twenty hours space.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nyctalopia</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="dimness of sight(n)">is two-fold: the first is a Dimness
of Sight in the Night, or in dark Places, with&shy;
out any Impediment in the Light: The other is
a Dimness in the Light, and clear Sight in the
Night, or in Shades.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nymph&aelig;</form> <xpln lang="en">are little pieces of Flesh in a Woman's
Secrets. So called because they stand near the
Water that comes out of the Bladder. Also the 
hollowness or void space in the nether Lip.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nymphomania</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Furor Uterinus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Nymphotomia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a cutting off of the <term lang="la">Nymph&aelig;</term>, the
too great Protuberance whereof in marriageable
Virgins sometimes hinders the Enjoyment, or
at least renders it difficult. The <f type="i">Egyptians</f> cut 
them frequently.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">OBel&aelig;a</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="suture(n)">is the <term lang="la">Sagittalis</term> Suture in the Scull
(see <term lang="la">Sagittalis</term>) which touches the <term lang="la">Corona&shy;
lis</term> Suture forward, and the <term lang="la">Lamdoides</term> back&shy;
ward; for it is made of the mutual Conjunction
of the Bones of the Forehead.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Oblat&aelig; Laxative & Purgantes</form> <xpln lang="en">are made of Meal

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Oblivio</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="forgetfulness(n)">Forgetfulness, is a loss of the ideas
of Things once perceived out of the Brain.
Which happens when things make but a light
Impression upon the Brain; as a light Motion is
scarce perceived, so a light Impression easily
decays.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Obolus</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="half a scruple(n)">is half a Scruple; it weighs ten Grains.
Physitians mark it thus <term lang="gk">&infin;</term>, but now the <f type="i">Hollan&shy;
ders</f> do not use this Character.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Obstructio</form> <xpln lang="en">is a shutting up of the Passages of
the Body either by Contraction, or by some for&shy;
reign Body that has entered within them.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Occiput</form> <xpln lang="en">is the hinder part of the Scull.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ochema</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Liquor or Vehicle wherewith Me&shy;
dicines are mixed.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ochthodes</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="ulcer(n)">are Ulcers whose sides are callous, or

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Oculares dentes</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="eye-teeth(n)">the Eye-Teeth: The same
that <term lang="la">Cynodontes</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Oculus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="eye(n)">the Eye, is the external Organ of
Sight; it is compounded of six Muscles, to wit
of two Direct, and as many Transverse, to
which a seventh is added in Brutes. It has seven
Tunics, the <term lang="la">Adnata</term>, <term lang="la">Innominata</term>, <term lang="la">Cornea</term>, <term lang="la">Uvea</term>,
</page>

<page no="210">
<term lang="la">Retiformis</term>, <term lang="la">Chrystallina</term>, and <term lang="la">Vitrea</term>. It has also
the <f type="i">Optick</f> Nerve, the <term lang="la">Iris</term>, and the <term lang="la">Pupilla</term>. See
them singly in their proper places.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Oculi</form> <xpln lang="en">are the forerunners of Flowers, which
are likewise called <term lang="la">Gemm&aelig;</term>, Buds.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Odaxismus</form> <xpln lang="en">is the itching of the Gums, when
Children breed Teeth.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Odontagra</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Forfex</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Odonthalgia</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="toothache(n)">is the Teeth-ach; which is caused
by black rotten Teeth, or an Effervescence of
fixed and acid Salt; and therefore it is called
the Gout in the Teeth. Cold also will cause 
it.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Odontiasis</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Dentitio</term>, and <term lang="la">Odon&shy;
tophyia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Odontica</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines against Pains in the

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Odontoides</form>, <xpln lang="en">that which is like a Tooth; as the
Tooth of the second Vertebre, and of other
Bones.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Odontophyja</form>, <xpln lang="en">breeding of Teeth.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Odoramentum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Medicine applyed for its
Smell. It is compounded of <term lang="la">Laudunum, Storax,
Benzoin</term><f type="i">, Must, Civet</f>, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Odoratus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="smell(n)">the Smell, is a Sence whereby odo&shy;
riferous Effluviums are offered and represented
to the common Sensory, from the Motion and Ir&shy;
ritation of Nerves, implanted in the Membranes
of the Nose.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Oeconomia</form> <xpln lang="en">is the management of Family-Con&shy;
cerns.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Oedema</form> <xpln lang="en">is sometimes taken in a large Sence by 
<f type="i">Hippocrates</f>, for any Tumor, but strictly for a
white, soft, insensible Tumor proceeding from
</page>

<page no="211">
pituitous Matter heaped up together. It has no
Pulse, and yields easily to the Fingers. It may
proceed likewise in some measure from the <term lang="la">Lym&shy;
pha</term> or nutritious Juice extravasated and turned
into a Gelly.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Oenoides</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="diluted wine(n)">is diluted Wine, or a Liquor Analo&shy;
gous to Wine.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Oenomel</form> <xpln lang="en">is Wine and Honey.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Oesophag&aelig;us</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="sphincter(n)">is a Muscle that closes the Gullet,
called Sphincter.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Oesophagus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="gullet(n)">the Gullet, is a membranaceous
Pipe reaching from the Palate to the Stomach,
whereby the Meat, chawed in the Mouth and
mixed with the Juice there, passes to the Ventri&shy;
cle: It has three Tunics; the <f type="i">outermost</f> or <f type="i">mem&shy;
branaceous</f> Tunic, which comes from the <term lang="la">Periton&aelig;
um</term>, or inner rine of the Belly, and clothes the
Ventricle. The innermost is <f type="i">Musculous</f>; the 
whole <f type="i">Oesophagus</f> seems to consist of two Muscles, 
which with their opposite Fibres crossing one
another make four <f type="i">Parallelograms</f>. The Third
is altogether <f type="i">Nervous</f>, which is covered on the
inside with an hairy sort of Coat, and which may
pass for a fourth Tunic.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Oesypus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the Filth and Greasiness of Sheep,
proceeding of Sweat, and cleaving fast to their
Wooll. Therefore they are mistaken who take
it to signify the little Clods of Dung that stick
to their Wooll.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Olecranum, <term lang="en">or</term> Ancon</form>, <xpln lang="en">is the greater Process of
the first Bone of the Cubit called <term lang="la">Ulna</term>. Also the
upper part of the Shoulder.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Olecranus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Ancon&aelig;us</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Olfactus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Odoratus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<page no="212">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Oligophoros</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="small wine(n)">is a small Wine, with few Spi&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Oligotrophia</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="decrease in nutrition(n)">is a Decrease of Nutrition.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Oligotrophus</form> <xpln lang="en">is Meat that nourishes little, to

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Omentum, Reticulum</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="caul(n)">the Cawle, is a double
Membrane spread upon the Intestines, interwo&shy;

riched also with two or three Glandules, annex&shy;
ed to the Stomach, the Gut <term lang="la">Colon</term>, and the <term lang="la">Pan&shy;
creas</term>, and useful to cherish the Intestines with its
warmth: It hath some milky and Lymphatic
Vessels, as also a great many <term lang="la">Ductus</term>'s and little
Bags of Fat, concerning which see our <f type="i">Reformed
Anatomy</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Omoplata, <term lang="en">and</term> Homoplata</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Sca&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Omphalocele</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Rupture about the Navel, to

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Omphalos</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Umbilicus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ophiasis</form> <xpln lang="en">is when the Hairs grow thin and fall
off here and there, so that they leave the Head
spotted like a Serpent.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Opthalmia</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Inflammation of the Tunics of
the Eyes, proceeding from arterious Blood col&shy;
lected and extravasated there, because it cannot
return by the Veins.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Opiatea, <term lang="en">or</term> Electuarium</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Medicine taken
inwardly, of a consistence like to those Opiates
</page>

<page no="213">
in the Shops, (Triacle or Mithridate) and is
made up into several Doses of several Ingredi&shy;
ents mixed with Honey or Syrup.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Opiatum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Medicine in form of an Electuary

date, Dias-Cordium, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Opiologia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Description of <term lang="la">Opium</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Opisthotonus, <term lang="en">or</term> Tetanus</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a kind of Cramp,
or stretching of the Muscle of the Neck back&shy;
wards; which proceeds sometimes from a Palsy
of the Muscles in the Neck, whereupon the An&shy;
tagonists or opposite Muscles move the interme&shy;
diate parts too much; or from a sharp and se&shy;
rous Matter in the Tendons; or from the Ani&shy;
mal Spirits which enter the Fleshy Pipes more 
than is useful and will not easily recede, so that
the parts are swelled and wrinkled up.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Opium</form> <xpln lang="en">is the condensed Juice of Poppies; the 
purest <term lang="la">Opium</term> is made of white Drops.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Opticus Nervus, <term lang="en">or</term> Visorius</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="optic nerve(n)">the Optic Nerve
is that which carries the visible Species from the
Eye to the common Sensory. The Nerves of
both Eyes proceed from the <term lang="la">Thalami</term> of the Op&shy;
tic Nerves, afterwards these Nerves come toge&shy;
ther, and as they enter the Scull separate again.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Optica</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines against Distempers of the
Eyes.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Orchis</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="testicle(n)">is a Testicle, whose Substance in Men
is nothing else but a Contexture of very little
Vessels which make the Seed: But it is quite
otherwise in Women; where they are made of
several Membranes and little Fibres loosely uni&shy;
ted to one another, betwixt which several
white Bodies are found, which are there either
</page>

<page no="214">
naturally or preternaturally: The Testicles of
Women breed Eggs, and therefore they are 
rightly called <term lang="la">Ovaria</term>. They are also called <term lang="la">Tes&shy;
tes</term>, <term lang="la">Colei</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Orchotomus</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="gelder(n)">is a Gelder: One who gelds Ani&shy;
mals that they cannot copulate.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Orexis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Natural Appetite of Meat, which 
proceeds from an acid Ferment in the Ventricles
that comes from the <term lang="la">C&aelig;liac</term> Arteries, with which
the nervous Tunic of the Stomach and its Nerves
are extraordinarily moved to covert Nourish&shy;
ment.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Organum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a part which requires a right and
determinate and sensible Conformation to its
constitution and the performance of its Actions;
as an Arm, Muscle, Heart, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Orgasmus</form> <xpln lang="en">is an <term lang="la">Impetus</term> and quick Motion of
Blood or Spirits; as when the Animal Spirits rush
violently upon the Nerves.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Oroboides</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="vetch(n)">is a subsiding in Urine, like to a kind
of Pulse called <f type="i">Vetches</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Orthocolon</form> <xpln lang="en">is a preternatural Rectitude of a
Joint.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Orthopn&aelig;a</form> <xpln lang="en">is an ill Respiration, when the Per&shy;
son affected cannot breathe but with his Neck 
erect.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Os</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="bone(n)">a Bone, is an hard, dry, and cold Sub&shy;
stance, consisting especially of earthy and saline
Particles, designed for the upholding of the Bo&shy;
dy, to render its Motion easy, and for a Fence 
for several parts. Some make their Number
249, others commonly 304, and others as ma&shy;
ny as the Days of the Year. Yet the number
of them is uncertain, because the Bones of Infants
</page>

<page no="215">
differ from those of Adult Persons. Also be&shy;
cause the Bones called <term lang="la">Sesamoidea</term> (see them in
their proper place) and the Teeth are not de&shy;
termined to a certain number in old Men and 
Adult Persons. They are of different Shapes,
some are round, others plain, acute, obtuse,
hollow, spungy, solid, oblong, triangular, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.
A Nut-Shell is also called <term lang="la">Ossiculum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Oscitatio</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="yawning(n)">Yawning, is a certain light convul&shy;
sive Motion of Muscles which open the lower
Jaw of the Face. Some look upon it as a light
Motion whereby Excrementitious and Halituous 
Matter, which irritates the neighbouring parts,
is expelled.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Oscula</form> <xpln lang="en">are the openings of Vessels at the end.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Osculum uteri</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Cavity where Conception
is made and the Mans Yard enters; it is so small
in Maids that it can only receive the bigness of
a small Pen we use for Writing Tables, and 
you cannot thrust your least Finger into it by
any means; the Courses flow out of it. It sticks
out in the Vagina, and it is like the Mouth of a 
Tench, or, as <f type="i">Galen</f> will have it, like the
Nut of a Man's Yard; it has a transverse cleft; 
in Virgins 'tis very small, but grows bigger in 
Women who have had many Children; if it be
too much stretched, or exulcerated, covered
over with a Scarr, or too moist, Barrenness fol&shy;
lows thereupon.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Osteologia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Description of Bones.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Osteon</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Os</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ostocopi</form>, <xpln lang="en">are Pains in the Bones, or rather in
the Membranes and Nerves about the Bones: For
Bones as such are insensible.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="216">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Otalgia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Pain in the Ears, whencesoever it

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Otenchyta</form> <xpln lang="en">an auricular Clyster. <f type="i">Celsus</f> calls it,

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Otica</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines against Distempers in the

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ovarium</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="woman's testicle(n)">is a Womans Testicle.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Oviductus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Tuba Fallopiana</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ovum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a sort of pain in the Head affecting a

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Oxel&aelig;um</form> <xpln lang="en">is a mixture of Vinegar with Oyl.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Oxycratum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a mixture of Vinegar with Wa&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Oxygala</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="sour milk(n)">is sowre Milk.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Oxyregmia</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="belch(n)">is an acid sowre Belch from the

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Oxyrhodinum</form> <xpln lang="en">is Vinegar of Roses, mixed with

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="gk">&#x039F;&#x039E;&#x03A5;' &#x039D;&#x039F;'&#x03A3;&#x0397;&#x039C;&#x0391;</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Morbus

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">PAchuntica</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines of a thickning na&shy;
ture, but withal cold, and full of thick and
boughy parts, which if they are mix'd with a 
thin Juice, by joyning and stifning the Parts one
with another, make a more Dense and firm Com&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">P&aelig;dotropica</form> <xpln lang="en">is a part of <term lang="la">Hygrena</term> that concerns

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Palatum</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="palate(n)" lexeme="roof of the mouth(n)">the Palate is the upper part of the

the upper part of an House, is thence called the

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Palliatio</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Cura Palativa</term>, is a Medicine which

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Palindrome</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Disease into which one re&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Palma</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="palm(n)">is the inside of a Man's Hand, which

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Palmus</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="shivering of the heart(n)" lexeme="palpitation of the heart(n)">is a Shivering, or palpitation of the

the Nerves; the cause whereof consists in the

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Palpebr&aelig;</form> <xpln lang="en">are the Coverings of the Eyes, made

nick, and another little Skin called <term lang="la">Tarsus</term>, with
