</page>

<page no="218">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Palpitatio cordis naturalis</form>, <xpln lang="en">the natural Palpi&shy;
tation of the Heart, is in the Systole thereof,
whilst the Cone and the Sides are press'd toge&shy;
ther, the Basis and the Roots of the Vessels, being
blown up with the Blood that gathers there,
grows big and swoln. It oft proceeds from an
extraordinary Contraction of the Heart, or a
thick and irritating Matter which sticks in the 
Heart.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Panac&aelig;a</form> <xpln lang="en">is a general sort of Physick for all
Diseases indifferently; but I question if there be
any such thing. Many People brag much of
Tobacco, Tincture of the Sun, the Philosophers&shy;
stone, vitriolated Tartar, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Panaritium</form>, <xpln lang="en">vid. <term lang="la">Paronychia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Panc&aelig;nus</form>, <xpln lang="en">vid. <term lang="la">Pandemius</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Panchymagoga</form> <xpln lang="en">are purgative Medicines that
expel all corrupt Humours.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="pancreas(n)" lexeme="sweetbread(n)" lexeme="pancration(n)">Pancreas, the Sweet-bread, Pancration, <term lang="la">Pancre&shy;
on, Callicreas, Callicreon, & Lactes</term></form>, <xpln lang="en">are all syno&shy;
nimous. It is a conglomerated Glandule in the
Abdomen, placed behind the Ventricle, and
fastened to the Gut <term lang="la">Duodenum</term>, and reaches as
far as the Liver and the Spleen; the Use and
Office thereof is to convey a volatile, Insipid,
and Lymphatick Juice, or as others will have 
it (for 'tis a disputable Point) a something
acid Juice, by its own <term lang="la">Ductus</term> to the Gut <term lang="la">Duo&shy;
denum</term>, in order to a farther Fermentation and
Volatilisation of the Chyle, and to attemperate
and allay the Qualities of the Gall: It is the
biggest Glandule in the whole Body, but bigger
in a Dog than a Man.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="219">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pandalea</form>, <xpln lang="en">as the modern Physicians call it, is
the same with a solid Electuary, but that it re&shy;
mains <f type="i">intire</f>, for the Sugar being rightly boiled
is let grow hard; the Patient takes a piece of it
like a Lambative; it only in the shape differs
from Rolls and Morsels.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pandemius</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Disease which is rife in some
places or another.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pandiculatio</form> <xpln lang="en">is a certain Dilatation and con&shy;
vulsive Distension of the Muscles, by which the
Vapours that annoy them are cast off.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Panicus</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="sudden fear(n)" lexeme="consternation(n)">is a sudden Fear or Consternation.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Panniculus Carnosus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a fat sort of Membrane,
in some parts thick and musculous; in other
parts thin, with many <term lang="la">Ductus</term>'s of Fat in it; it
covers the whole Body.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Panus</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="botch(n)" lexeme="sore(n)">is a sort of Botch or Sore under the

the Glandulous Parts. It is also taken for <term lang="la">Phy&shy;
gethus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Papill&aelig; Intestinorum</form> <xpln lang="en">are little Glandules where&shy;
with the in-most Tunick of the Entrails is full,
they soak in the percolated Chyle, and dispense
it to the lacteal Veins.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Papilla</form> <xpln lang="en">is a red Excrescency in the middle of 
the Breast, in the Pores whereof are received all
the milky Tubes or Pipes, proceeding from the
Glandules of the Breasts.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Papillarum processus</form> <xpln lang="en">are the Extremities of the
Olfactory Nerves, which convey the slimy,
viscous Humours by the Fibres, which perforate
the <term lang="la">Os cribriforme</term> to the Nostrils and Palate.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Papul&aelig;</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="small-pox(n)">vid. <term lang="la">Pustul&aelig;</term>, also a kind of small Pox.
See <term lang="la">Exanthemata</term>.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="220">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Paracelsistica</form> <xpln lang="en">Med. <term lang="la">vid Hermetica</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Paracentesis, <term lang="en">or</term>Punctio</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Perforation of
the Chest and Abdomen through a cuspidate
Channel: It hapens in the Breast when it is
stuff'd with putrified Matter, or Water, and
then there's a pricking in the side between the
fifth and sixth Vertebre. It happens in the <term lang="la">Ab&shy;
domen</term>, when it is swell'd by a Dropsy near the
white Seam in the <term lang="la">Abdomen</term>, in the Muscles that
either ascend right or oblique. If a Man be
strong and has taken a Purge, and also his Lungs,
and the rest of his Entrails be uncorrupted, when 
the Navel doth protuberate, don't look ano&shy;
ther way, for there you must make the Incision;
don't let Purulency and Water come out both
together, for that were to kill the Patient, but
one after the other, as in seven days a pound,
or a pound and an half as the Patient can en&shy;
dure it: After the Operation is finished, draw
the Wound up with an astringent Plaister: If
the inward Vessels and Passages be broke through
this pricking, it's to no purpose to endeavour 
the Cure.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Paracheteusis</form>, <xpln lang="en">vid. <term lang="la">Derivatio</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Paracmastica</form> <xpln lang="en">is a daily declining Feaver, also
declining Age.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Paracme</form>, <xpln lang="en">vid <f type="i">in</f> <term lang="la">Acme</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Parachynanche</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Inflammation with a con&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Paralysis</form> <xpln lang="en">is an <emend err="Aboition">Abolition</emend> of voluntary Motion,
or Sense, or both, either in all the Body, or only 
some part. It comes by either an Obstruction,
Obscission, Contusion, or pressing of the Nerves,
</page>

<page no="221">
or by an Indisposition, or ill Conformity of the
Muscles.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">P&aelig;raphrenitis</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="madness(n)">is a Madness accompanied with
a continual Feaver through the Inflammation of
the Midriff, with difficulty of breathing as the
Ancients dream'd. But Dr. <f type="i">Willis</f> has confuted
this Opinion of it, and says the matter of it
lies in the <term lang="la">Cerebellum</term>, whereby the Animal Spi&shy;
<emend err="Spirits">rits</emend> cannot flow, and thence the Midriff and 
Lungs are troubled.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Paraphrosyne</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="doting(n)">is a slight sort of Doting in the

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Paraphlegia</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="palsy(n)">is a Palsy which seizeth all the

an Obstruction of the spinal Marrow.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Paraplexia</form>, <xpln lang="la">idem quod Paraplegia.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Parasananche</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Inflammation of the Muscles

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Paremptosis</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="falling(n)">is a falling, as when Blood slides

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Parencephalos</form>, <xpln lang="en"><term lang="la">idem quod</term> <term lang="la">Cerebellum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Perenchymata</form> <xpln lang="en">are Entrails by which the Blood
passes for better Fermentation and Perfection,
as the Lungs, Liver, Heart, and Spleen, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.
Sometimes <term lang="la">Parenchyma</term> is taken in a large
Sence for all the Entrails.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="222">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Paristhmia</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Amygdal&aelig;</term>, are two Glandules
tied together by a broad slender Production,
they have one common Cavity large and oval,
opening into the Mouth; the Use they serve
for is, to transmit a certain slimy or pituitous
Matter into the Jaws and Mouth: They are
also called <term lang="la">Tonsill&aelig;</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Paronychia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a preternatural Swelling in the
Fingers end very troublesome; it rises from a
sharp, malign Humour, which can gnaw the
Tendons Nerves, the Membrane about the
Bone, and the very Bone it self.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Parotides</form> <xpln lang="en">are Glandules behind the Ears, also
a preternatural Swelling of those Glandules.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Paroxysmus</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="fit(n)">a Fit, is part of the Period of
Diseases, whereby they encrease and grow
worse. It is either Ordinate, which returns at
certain times, as in a Tertian Ague; or Inordi&shy;
nate, that has no certain time, but comes some&shy;
times one day, sometims another, as the Erra&shy;
tick Ague.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pars</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="part(n)">a part, is a Piece of the whole serving each
for their proper Uses. The Parts are either
sensible or insensible, spermatick or bloody, si&shy;
milar, or the contrary; organical or inorgani&shy;
cal, principal or inservient.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Partus</form> <xpln lang="en">is the bringing forth of a Mature <term lang="la">F&oelig;&shy;
tus</term>, or Young, in natural Births. The <term lang="la">F&oelig;tus</term>
having broken the Membranes, turns his Head
forward, and inclining it towards the neck of
the Womb, strives to get forth; the usual man&shy;
ner is after nine Months; yet I have known
some at <f type="i">Amsterdam</f> born at seven Months, who
have lived to fifty or sixty.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="223">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Partus C&aelig;sareus</form> <xpln lang="en">is when Children are forc'd
for want of Passage to be cut out.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Partus difficilis</form>, <xpln lang="en"><term lang="la">idem quod</term> <term lang="la">Dystocia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Parylis</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Inflammation, Rottenness, or 
Excrescency besides the Gums.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Passio</form>, <xpln lang="en">vid. <term lang="la">Pathema</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pastillum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a sweet Ball compos'd of sweet
Dust, Wax, the Gum-Storax, and <f type="i">India</f>-Balsam
with a little Goats-flower and Turpentine; it
serves for Swelling.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Patella</form>, <xpln lang="en">vid. <term lang="la">Mola Genu</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pathema</form> <xpln lang="en">is all preternatural Conturbation
wherewith our Body is molested.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Patheticus</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Nerve of the fourth pair
within the Scull, as Dr. <f type="i">Willis</f> saith, tho <f type="i">Fallopi&shy;
us</f> reckons it one of the eighth pair.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pathognomonicum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a proper separable Sign,
which agrees only to such a thing, and to all of
that kind, and tells the Essence of its Subject, and
also lasts from the beginning to the end; as in a
true Plurisy, there's always a continual Fever,
hard Breathing, and Stitches, and a Cough.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pathologia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a part of Physick that teacheth us
the preternatural Constitution of a Man's Body.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pepasmus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Concoction, or rather a Fer&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pepasticum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Medicine that allays and di&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pepsis</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Concoction or Fermentation of

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pericardium</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Membrane which surrounds

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pericholus</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="choleric(a)">very Cholerick.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Perin&aelig;um</form> <xpln lang="en">is the ligamentous Seam betwixt

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Periodus Morborum</form> <xpln lang="en">is the space betwixt the

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Periodus Sanguinis</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="circulation of the blood(n)">is a continued Circulation
of the Blood through the Body, which is thus.
The Blood is carried out of the Arteries by Fi&shy;
bres, either of the Flesh or of the Entrails, or the
membranous parts to the Mouths of the greater 
Veins. Now we say that those Fibres are ter&shy;
minated at the Mouths of the Veins, and im&shy;
planted in them, as we see many other little
Channels in the Veins; so the Blood, passing
through these out of the Arteries, is presently
sent to the Veins, that it may be carried back
again to the right Ventricle of the Heart; and
thence by an arterious Vein to the Lungs,
in which after the Blood has been accended by
some nitrous Particles, breathed in thither by 
the Air, it goes into the veinous Artery, thence
into the left Ventricle of the Heart; which
again empties it self into the <term lang="la">Aorta</term> or great
Artery; so that the Body may be nourished and
enliven'd, it goes into every part of it.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Periosteum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a thin Membrane that incloses 
immediately the Bones, except a few.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Peripheria</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Circumference of the Body,
or any Entrail thereof.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Perisistole</form> <xpln lang="en">is the time of Rest between the Con&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Peristalticus Motus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Crawling as it were of

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Peristromata</form> <xpln lang="en">are the sick Mans Bed-clothes;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Periton&aelig;um</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Membrane which cloaths the

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Perittoma</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Excrement in the Body, left

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pernio</form> <xpln lang="en">is a preternatural Swelling caus'd by

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Perona</form> <xpln lang="en">is also called <term lang="la">Fibula</term>, because it joyns

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pestis</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="plague(n)">the Plague, is an epidemick conta&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Phrenetis</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="dotage(n)">is a Dotage with a continual Fever,

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pili</form>, <xpln lang="en">the Hairs, are round, oblong, slender Bo&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Placenta Uterina</form> <xpln lang="en">is a red Substance, like the
Liver, full of Glandulous Kernals: It has an Ar&shy;
tery and a Vein from the Navel-string, and per&shy;
haps lymphatick Vessels from the neighbouring
parts; outwardly sticks to the Womb, to either
side indifferently, yet more commonly to the
middle; within it is covered with the <term lang="la">Chorrium</term>.
It has its nourishing Moisture from the Porosities
of the Womb, (as it happens with the <term lang="la">Papill&aelig;</term> of
the Guts which drink in the Chyle and commu&shy;
nicate it to the milky Vessels) which through
the Navel-vein feeds the Young. The superflu&shy;
</page>

<page no="232">
ous part whereof the Arteries lodg in the <term lang="la">Am&shy;
mion</term>, that the Young may be nourished by its
Mouth. The <term lang="la">Placenta</term> together the Mem&shy;
branes is expelled after the Birth, and are called
<term lang="la">Secundin&aelig;</term>, <term lang="la">Secundines</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pladarosis</form> <xpln lang="en">are little soft Tumors which grow
under the Eye-lids.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Plagula</form>, <xpln lang="en">vid. <term lang="la">Splenia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Planta Noctis</form>, <xpln lang="en">vid. <term lang="la">Sudamin&aelig; & Hydroa</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Plastica Virtus</form> <xpln lang="en">is that which can form or fa&shy;
shion any thing; it's an old saying and a sure
Refuge of Ignorance, for what the Ancients
could not explain they called a plastick Virtue.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Platisma</form> <xpln lang="en">is a broad Linnen-cloth put upon

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Platysma Myodes</form>, <xpln lang="en">vid. <term lang="la">Myodes</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Plectrum</form>, <xpln lang="en">vid. <term lang="la">Cion</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Plenitudo</form> <xpln lang="en">is when a Man has too much Blood:
The same that <term lang="la">Plethora</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Plerotica</form> <xpln lang="en">are Medicines that breed Flesh and
fill up Wounds.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Plethora</form>, <xpln lang="en">when there's more good Blood than's
requisite. It happens either to the Vessels, when
they are stretcht out and cannot hold all; or to
the Strength, for sometimes tho the Vessels be
not over full, the Strength is over loaded.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Plethoricus</form>, <xpln lang="en">a Man troubled with a <term lang="la">Plethora</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pleura</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Membrane that incloses the Breasts
and its Entrails.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pleuritis</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="pleurisy(n)">a Pleurisy, is an Inflammation of the
Membrane <term lang="la">Pleura</term>, and the intercostal Muscles,
attended with a continual Fever and Stitches in
the Side, difficulty of Breathing, and sometimes
spitting Blood, and it's either a true Pleurisy,
</page>

<page no="233">
this which we have described, or a bastard
Pleurisy.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pleuritis Notha</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="bastard pleurisy(n)">a bastard Pleurisy, that differs
in some thing from the other.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Plexus choroides</form> <xpln lang="en">seems to hang over the pineal
Glandule, as it were over a Button. It is an 
admirable Contexture of small Arteries in the
Brain like a Net.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Plexus nervosus</form> <xpln lang="en">is when two or three Nerves

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Plexus reticularis</form>, <xpln lang="en">vid. <term lang="la">Choroides</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Plica</form> <xpln lang="en">is an epidemical Disease in <term lang="la">Polonia</term>, when
their Hairs grow together like a Cow's Tail;
besides, they are crook'd-back'd, have loose
Joynts, it wrenches their Limbs and loosens
them, breeds Lice, with other Symptoms.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pleumaceola</form>, <xpln lang="en">vid. <term lang="la">Splenia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pneumatocele</form> <xpln lang="en">is a windy Rupture, when the

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pneumatodes</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="short breathing(n)">is a short Breathing.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pneumatosis</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Generation of Animal Spi&shy;
rits, which is performed in the barky Substance
of the Brain; the little Arteries there are emp&shy;
tied, and the Spirits distil, which after they are
come as far as the middle of the Brain, they
actuate and Invigorate all the Nerves.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pneumatomphalus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a swelling in the Navel,

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pneumon</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="lungs(n)">the Lungs</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pnigalium</form>, <xpln lang="en">vid. <term lang="la">Epialtes</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<page no="234">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Polychronius</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Disease that holds a Man

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Polygophora</form> <xpln lang="en">are Drinks or Wines full of ex&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Polypus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Swelling in the hollow of the No&shy;
strils, and is twofold; either like a Tent, and
goes by the general name of <term lang="la">Sarcoma</term>; or such a
one that has a great many distinct Branches or
Feet, which extend either to the outside of the
Nose or the inside of the Mouth: Their Colour
is white, oftentimes reddish, and sometimes black
and livid. Excrescencies of this nature happen
not only in the Nostrils, but sometimes in the
Heart and in the Cavities of the thicker Mem&shy;
brane of the Brain.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Polytarcia</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="corpulency(n)">Corpulency.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pompholigodes</form>, <xpln lang="en">Urine with many Bubbles upon

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pomum Adami</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Protuberance is the fore&shy;
side of the Throat; so called, because 'tis com&shy;
monly thought a piece of the Apple stuck in his

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pondo</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="pound-weight(n)">a Pound-weight. <f type="i">Joh. Rhodius</f> writes,

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Poplitea Vena</form>, <xpln lang="en">a Vein that consists of a double

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pori</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="pore(n)">Pores, are little unperceptible Holes in

<page no="237">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Procidentia uteri</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a relaxing of the inner Tu&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Procondyli</form> <xpln lang="en">are the Bones of the Fingers next

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Prodromus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Disease that comes before a

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Productio</form>, <xpln lang="en">vid <term lang="la">Apophysis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pr&oelig;gumena</form> <xpln lang="en">is an antecedent internal Cause of a

causing the Disease, that if it be taken away, the
Disease may still continue; as a <term lang="la">Plethora</term>, or ill
Juice in the Blood, produced by an ill way of
Diet, whence proceeds an Obstruction of Ves&shy;
sels and Passages, and a Constipation of the

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Prolepticus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Disease always anticipating;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Prophasis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Fore-knowledg in Diseases; also

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Prostar&aelig;, Adstantes, <term lang="en">or</term> Corpora glandulosa</form>, <xpln lang="en">are

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Prostethis</form> <xpln lang="en">is the fore-side of the Breast; also

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Psydracia</form>, <xpln lang="en">according to <f type="i">Paulus</f> and <f type="i">Alexander</f>,

</page>

<page no="240">
says, they are an hard sort of Pustle something

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ptarmica</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Sternuta loria</term>, are those things

extreamly irritate and shrivel up the Membranes

mour at the Nostrils in an extraordinary Mea&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pterystaphylini</form> <xpln lang="en">are Muscles of the peice of Flesh
in the Roof of the Mouth called <term lang="la">Gargareon</term>,
which proceed from the Wing-like Processes, and
are terminated in the sides of the <term lang="la">Uvula</term>, or
<term lang="la">Gargareon</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ptylosis</form> <xpln lang="en">is when the Brims of the Eye-lids be&shy;
ing grown thick the Hairs of the Eye-Brows
fall off.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ptisana</form>, <xpln lang="en">Ptisan, is a Decoction of Barley
</page>

<page no="241">
husked, Liquorish, Raisins.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ptyalismus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a too great Spitting.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ptyalon</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="spit(n)" lexeme="spittle(n)">is Spit, or that Matter which is 
brought up from the Lungs by Coughing; for
<term lang="la">Saliva</term> (which we English Spittle too) properly
signifies the Moisture which is excerned by the
<term lang="la">Ductus Salivales</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ptysma</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Ptyalon</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pugillus</form> <xpln lang="en">is an handful of any Herbs. Others
interpret it as much as may be taken up with
three Fingers.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pulmones</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="lungs(n)">the Lungs, are Organs of Respira&shy;
tion. The Famous <f type="i">Malpighius</f> makes the Sub&shy;
stance of the Lungs (excepting the Nerves, a few
Vessels, and the Branches of the Wind-Pipe) to
be nothing but an Heap of little Bladders, the
contexture whereof is so ordered, that there's a 
Passage into them from the Wind-Pipe, and into
one another; till they all open into the Mem&shy;
brane which clothes the Lungs. The use of the
Lungs is to breathe withal, and to mix and ac&shy;
cend the Blood with the Nitre they suck in.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pulpa</form> <xpln lang="en">is the fleshy part of Fruits, Roots, or
other Bodies, which is extracted by Infusion or
Boyling, and passing through a Sive: As the
Pulp of <f type="i">Tamarinds, Cassia</f>, <term lang="la">Alth&aelig;a</term>, <f type="i">Dates</f>, &amp;c.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pulsus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="pulse(n)">the Pulse, is the immediate Index of
the Heart, by the mediation whereof the Blood
is diffused through the whole Body, and is diffe&shy;
rently affected thereby according to the different
Influx of the Animal Spirits; the Motion where&shy;
of is chiefly to be attributed to the circular and
direct Fibres. Others affirm it to be the Dila&shy;
tation and Contraction of the Heart and Blood.
</page>

<page no="242">
A Pulse is either natural or preternatural; of
the former we have spoken already; the latter is
such as is different according to the different
Circumstances of the Fibres and Animal Spirits.
to wit, <f type="i">strong, weak, swift, slow, equal, unequal, 
intermittent</f>, &amp;c.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pulvilli</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Splenia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pulvis</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Species</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Punctum lachrymale</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Lachrymale punctum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Puntum saliens</form>, <xpln lang="en">in the growth of an Egg you
see a little Speck, or Cloud as it were, in the in&shy;
nermost Tunic of it, called <term lang="la">Amnios</term>, which grow&shy;
ing gradually thicker, acquires a kind of slimy
Matter, in the middle whereof you see first this
<term lang="la">Punctum saliens</term> (a little Speck that seems to leap;)
afterward the rude Body of an <term lang="la">Embrio</term>, just like
a shapeless kind of Maggot; which tends every
Day more and more to Perfection.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pupilla</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Pupula</term>, is the opening of the Tu&shy;
nic of the Eye, called <term lang="la">Uvea</term> or <term lang="la">Choroides</term>; it is
round in Man, and is wont to be contracted or
dilated like a Muscle, according to the different
Influx of the Animal Spirits.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pupula</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Pupilla</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Purgantia</form>, <xpln lang="en">Purging Medicines are those, which
by reason of a peculiar disposition of their parts
irritate the fleshy Fibres of the Ventricle, which
become swoln and consequently contracted at
the right end, so that the whole Substance of
the Stomach is drawn up together and inclined
towards the <term lang="la">Pylorus</term>, whence follows an Excre&shy;
tion downwards.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Purgatio</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="purging(n)">Purging, is an Excretory Motion
quick and frequent, proceeding from a quick and
</page>

<page no="243">
orderly Contraction of the carneous Fibres of the
Stomach and Intestines; whereby the Chyle,
and Excrements, and corrupted Humors, either
bred or sent there from other parts, are pro&shy;
truded from part to part, till they be quite exclu&shy;
ded the Body.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Pyon</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pustul&aelig;</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="pimple(n)">Pimples, are the Recrements of ill
Blood that shoot forth in the Skin, and for want
of Perspiration, or too viscous a Matter, stick
there and cause an unequal Surface.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Putrefactio Chymica</form>, <xpln lang="en">is the Dissolution of a con&shy;
crete Body, by natural Rottenness, in a moist
Heat which corrupts the very Substance of it,
and penetrates its most intimate parts.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pyon, <term lang="en">or</term> Pus</form>, <xpln lang="en">is putrified Blood concocted in&shy;
to white Matter.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pycnosis</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Pycnotica</term></xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pycnotica</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Incrassantia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pyelos</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Choana</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pylorus</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Janitor</term>, is the right Orifice of
the Ventricle, which sends the Meat out of the
Stomach.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pyosis</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Collection of <term lang="la">Pus</term> in any part of the
Body.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pyramidales Musculi</form> <xpln lang="en">are placed in the <term lang="la">Abdo&shy;
men</term>, and lye upon the lowest Tendons of the
right Muscles. They are not parts of the right
Muscles, as <f type="i">Vesalius</f> and <f type="i">Columbus</f> are of opinion,
but distinct, as <f type="i">Falopius</f> proves, tho with some
pertinent some impertinent Arguments. The
peculiar Membrane wherewith they are clothed,
and the order of their Fibres, shew them to be
different from the right Muscles. They proceed
</page>

<page no="244">
from the external <term lang="la">Os Pubis</term>, and the higher they
climb the narrower they grow, and end about
the Navel in the white Seam; sometimes they are
wanting, or the left is less than the right, or the
right than the left.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pyramidalia</form> <xpln lang="en">are Vessels which prepare the Seed,
of which in their proper place. Also Muscles of
the Nostrils and of the <term lang="la">Abdomen</term> called <term lang="la">Pyrami&shy;
dales</term>, or of a Pyramidical Figure. Also two
Strings of Marrow about the Basis of the ob&shy;
longated Marrow.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pyretologia</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Description of Fevers: Of
which Dr. <f type="i">Willis</f> has writ most accurately.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pyrotechnia</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Chymia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pyrotica</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Urentia</term>, are Medicines virtually
hot, which being applied to Human Bodies, grow
extreamly hot; because that having Particles and
Pores so ordered, that Vapors and Humors in&shy;
sinuating into them, the subtile Matter finds such
Passages, that it being moved extream violently,
forces certain earthy, hard, and acute Particles,
which flote in the Passages, upon the neighbour&shy;
ing parts with great Impetuosity, and so excites
an Heat which corrupts, or changes differently,
according to the diversity of its Motion, and the 
Particles which are moved. Such are things
that cause Redness, that blister, that ripen or
rot, that close up and bring Wounds to a Crust,
and that pulls Hairs out of the Body.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pyulcus</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Instrument wherewith <term lang="la">Pus</term>, or
corrupted Matter, is evacuated.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Pyxis</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Cavity of the Hip-Bone, which is
called <term lang="la">Acetabulum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>
</wordgroup1>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">QUadrans</form>, <xpln lang="en">Physitians reckon a Weight of three
Ounces, that is the fourth part of a <f type="i">Roman</f>
Pound.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Qualitas</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Disposition or Contexture of lit&shy;
tle Particles, whence our Bodies may be any way
denominated of such a Quality. Quality is ma&shy;
nifest, hidden, poysonous, contagious, Pesti&shy;
lent, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Quartana febris intermittens</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="quartan ague(n)">a Quartan Ague,
which the Ancients called <f type="i">Saturn</f>'s Daughter.
It is at this Day a Scandal to Physicians, because
it is so hard to be cured by those who follow the
old way. It is a preternatural Effervescence of
the Blood, which attaques a Man every fourth 
Day, and then leaves him. It is caused by an acid
austere Blood, and nutritious Juice hindred in
its Assimilation.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Quartarium</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Quadrans</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Quid pro Quo</form> <xpln lang="en">is when a Medicine of one Na&shy;
ture and Quality is substituted for another,
which is not to be done without the consent of
Physicians.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Quinta Essentia</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Essentia quinta</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Quotidiana febris intermittent</form>, <xpln lang="en">an intermitting
Quotidian Ague, is that which returns every
Day, and proceeds from crude Blood and an ill
Assimilation of Chyle.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordgroup1 type="a" object="R">R.

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">RAbdoides</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Sutura Sagittalis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Rabies Hydrophobica</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Hydrophobia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Rachit&aelig;</form> <xpln lang="en">and <term lang="la">Rachi&aelig;i</term> are Muscles belonging to
the Back.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Rachitis</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Rhachitis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Radius</form> <xpln lang="en">is the less Bone of the Cubit, called <term lang="la">Fo&shy;
cile minus</term>; it is more oblique than the great Bone
called <term lang="la">Ulna</term>, and is more distant a little from it in the
middle, where there occurs a small Ligament:
Above the <term lang="la">Ulna</term> receives the <term lang="la">Radius</term>, and below
the <term lang="la">Radius</term> receives it. The upper part of the
<term lang="la">Radius</term> is jointed with the outward Process of
the Arm by <term lang="la">Diarthrosis</term> (which see); the lower
by way of Appendix with the wrist Bone at the
middle Finger. Its upper end is small, and the
lower thick. It is also the greater Bone of the
Leg.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ramex</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Hernia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ranula</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Hypoglossum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Raphe</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Sutura</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Rarefacientia</form>, <xpln lang="en">rarifying Remedies, are such as
by dissipating a little the Vapours and Humors
make the Pores of Bodies larger.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Rasetta</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Carpus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Raspatorium</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Scalprum Rasorium</term>, is a Chi&shy;
rurgeons Instrument to scrape or shave filthy and
scaly Bones with.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Raucedo</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Branchus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="247">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Recidivus morbus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="relapse(n)">a Relapse, is when the mor&shy;
bifick Matter, that was left in the first Distemper,
begins to work and ferment again.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Rectificatio</form> <xpln lang="en">is a repeated distillation of Liquors,
to exalt and purify them the more.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Reduvia</form> <xpln lang="en">is a certain light Cleft or Chap in the
Skin at the Roots of the Nails.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Refrigeratorium</form> <xpln lang="en">is a wooden Vessel, full of Wa&shy;
ter with a streight or spiral Pipe in it of Tin or
Lead, which distilled Water is to flow through
to cool it.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Regius morbus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Icterus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Relaxantia</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Chalastica</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Relaxatio</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Dilatation of Parts or Vessels.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Reminiscentia</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="remembrance(n)">Remembrance, is a Perception
whereby the Ideas of things before perceived,
and impressed upon the Mind by Sensation or o&shy;
ther Perception, are again offered and represen&shy;
ted to the Soul, by the Mediation of Animal Spi&shy;
rits, in the common Sensory; either by their
former Footsteps and Images impressed upon the
Brain, or by some Words or other Signs which
awakened and stirred them up. Or Reminiscence 
is an arbitrary drawing out of things, which were
before impressed upon the Brain, for its own
use.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Remissio Febrium</form>, <xpln lang="en">a remitting of Fevers, is a 
boyling down of hot and over-boyling Blood,
which is Absolute in intermittent Fevers, and but
Partial in continued ones.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Renes</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="reins(n)" lexeme="kidney(n)">the Reins or Kidneys; there are two of
them in the <term lang="la">Abdomen</term>, placed under the Liver
and Spleen; the right Kidney is lower in a Man
than the left: They are chiefly made up of lit&shy;
</page>

<page no="248">
tle Channels, or Conduits, which arise from the
Glandules that lye about the Extremities of the
Arteries, whence they receive the <term lang="la">Serum</term>, which
passes on to the <term lang="la">Caruncul&aelig; Papillares</term>, or little
pieces of pappy Flesh, to the <term lang="la">Pelvis</term>, (or Basin)
to the Ureters, the Bladder, and so out of
Doors.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Renes succenturiati</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Capsul&aelig; atrabilari&aelig;</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Repellentia</form> <xpln lang="en">are such things as by stopping the
Heat and Afflux of Humors, and by shutting up
the Pores with their cold or binding Qualities,
decrease the swelling of a part, and drive the
Humors another way.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Res naturales</form>, <xpln lang="en">Natural things are three: Health,
the Causes of Health, and its Effects. Others
reckon seven, as the Elements, Temperaments,
Humors, Spirits, Parts, Faculties, Actions; but
Elements and Temperaments belong to natural
Philosophy; Humors, Spirits and Parts are
reckoned amongst the Causes of Health, which
consist of a good Temperature and a due Con&shy;
formation; Faculties and Actions are compre&shy;
hended under the Effects of Health.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Res non naturales</form>, <xpln lang="en">Things that are not Natural
are Six: Air, Meat and Drink, Motion and
Rest, Sleep and Waking, the Affections of the
Mind, Things that are let out of, and Things re&shy;
tained in the Body. They are so called, because
that if they exceed their due Bounds, they often
occasion Diseases.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Res preter Naturam</form>, <xpln lang="en">things beside Nature are
Diseases, their Causes, their Symptoms and
Effects.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="249">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Resolventia</form>, <xpln lang="en">dissolving Remedies are such as
are apt to dissipate or scatter Particles, that are
driven into the Body or any part of it, with
their own spirituous and sulphureous Parti&shy;
cles.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Respiratio</form>, <xpln lang="en">Breathing, is an alternate Dilata&shy;
tion and Contraction of the Chest, whereby the
nitrous Air is taken in by the Wind-Pipe for
the accension of the Blood, and by and by is
driven out again with other vaporous Effluvi&shy;
ums. The Cause of Respiration does not seem
to consist in the Dilatation and Contraction of 
the <term lang="la">Thorax</term>, as is commonly thought, but in the
Contraction of the Tunic which covers the upper
part of the <term lang="la">Oesophagus</term> and the Wind-Pipe as far
as its Closest Recesses.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Rete mirabile</form>, <xpln lang="en">the wonderful Net, in the Brain,
is so called by reason of its admirable Structure;
it consists of several small Arteries; it is under
the Basis of the Brain, and comprehends the 
pituitary Glandule, by the sides of the Bone
<term lang="la">Ophenoides</term>: The Use of it is, that the Blood may
cast off its serous parts into the putuitary Glan&shy;
dule, that it may afford finer and purer Spirits:
Secondly, lest the Blood by rushing too sudden&shy;
ly upon the Brain, should in some measure
suppress it; it is not so found in a Man and an
Horse, which perform noble things.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Reticularis plexus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Choroides</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Reticulum</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Omentum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Retiformis plexus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Plexus retiformis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Retiformis tunica</form> <xpln lang="en">is a certain Expansion of the 
inner Substance of the Optic Nerve in the Eye,
which is to the Eye like a whited Wall in a dark
</page>

<page no="250">
Chamber, which receives and represents the vi&shy;
sible Species that are let in by a hole in a darken&shy;
ed Room.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Retina tunica</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Retiformis</term> and <term lang="la">Amphible&shy;
stroides</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Retorta</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="retort(n)">a Retort, is a Chymical Vessel, made
of Glass, Stone, or Iron; of a round Figure,
to the side whereof there is fastened a bended,
retorted, and hollow Beak or Nose, where&shy;
by the things that are to be distilled are put in
and out.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Reverberatio chymica</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="burning(n)">is a Burning, whereby
Bodies are calcined by an actual Fire in a Furnace
called <term lang="la">Reverberium</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Reverberium</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="chemical over(n)" lexeme="furnace(n)">is a Chymical Oven or Furnace,
wherein Bodies that are to be burned or distil&shy;
led are calcined.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Revulsoria</form>, <xpln lang="en">V.S. is whereby the Blood that
gushes upon one part is diverted a contrary way,
by the opening of a Vein in a remote and con&shy;
venient place.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Rhachitis</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="spinal marrow(n)">is the Spinal Marrow, which see in
its proper place: Also a Disease common a&shy;
mongst the <f type="i">English</f>, which is an unequal Nourish&shy;
ing of parts accompanied with Looseness of
parts, Softness, Weakness, Faintness, Drow&shy;
zyness, a great swelling Head, with Leanness
below the Head, with Protuberances about the
Joints, Crookedness of Bones, Straitness of the 
Breast, Swelling of the <term lang="la">Abdomen</term>, Stretching of
the <term lang="la">Hypochondres</term>, a Cough, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. The <f type="i">English</f>
call it the <f type="i">Rickets</f>: But because the occasion of it
often lyes in the Spinal Marrow, the Famous
<f type="i">Glisson</f> calls it appositely enough <term lang="la">Rhachitis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="251">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Rhagades</form>, <xpln lang="en">the <f type="i">Latines</f> say <term lang="la">Scissur&aelig;, Fissur&aelig;,
Rim&aelig;</term>, Chinks, Clefts, which as they happen in
other parts of the Body, Hands, Feet, Lips,
the entrance of the Womb; so they may hap&shy;
pen in the Fundament, in the Extremity of the
Gut <term lang="la">Rectum</term>, and in the Sphincter or Muscle
which closes the Fundament. <term lang="la">Rhagades</term> in the
Fundament are certain oblong little Ulcers,
without Swelling, like those which are some&shy;
times occasioned in the Hands by great Cold.
Some are superficial, others deep: Some are
not hard nor callous, others are: Some are
moist and send forth Matter, others dry and
cancrous.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Rhegma</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Breaking or Bursting of any part,
as of a Bone, the inner Rine of the Belly, the
Eye, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Rheuma</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="rheum(n)">Rheum, is a Defluxion of Humor
from the Head upon the parts beneath, as upon
the Eyes, or Nose.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Rheumatismus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a wandring Pain in the Body,
often accompanied with a small Fever, Swelling,
Inflammation, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Rhexis</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Rhegma</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Rhinenchytes</form> <xpln lang="en">is a little Syringe to inject Medi&shy;
cines into the Nostrils.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Rhodinum</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="rose vinegar(n)">is Rose-Vinegar, or any thing made
of Roses.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Rhomboides</form> <xpln lang="en">is a pair of Muscles proceeding
from the three lowermost Vertebres of the
Neck, and as many upper Spinal Processes
of the Vertebres of the Back: By and by
they descend, and being fleshy at the begin&shy;
ning and end, go as far as the Basis of the Shoul&shy;
</page>

<page no="252">
der-blade, which they move backward and ob&shy;
liquely upward.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Rhyptica</form> <xpln lang="en">are scouring Medicines which cleanse
away Filth.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Rhythmus</form> <xpln lang="en">is a certain proportion of Pulses,
Time, Life, Age, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Rhythidosis</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="wrinkling(n)">is a Wrinkling of any part.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Rigor</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Vibration and Concussion of the
Skin and Muscles of the whole Body, accompa&shy;
nied with Chilness.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Rima pudendi</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Fissura magna</term>, is so called,
because it reaches from the lower part of the
<term lang="la">Os Pubis</term> almost as far as the Fundament, so that
the space betwixt the one and the other, which
is called <term lang="la">Perin&aelig;um</term>, or <term lang="la">Interforamineum</term>, is scarce
a Fingers breadth. By frequent Coition it grows
larger. The use of it is for Generation, Excre&shy;
tion of Urine and other Excrements, and for the
bearing of Young.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Risus Sardonius</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Contraction of each
Jaw.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Rob</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Apochylisma</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Robub</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Roriferus ductus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Ductus chyli&shy;
ferus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ros</form>, <xpln lang="en">in the account of the Ancients, was the
first Moisture that falls from the Extremities of
Vessels, and is dispersed upon the Substance of
the Members. <term lang="la">Ros</term>, says <f type="i">Galen</f>, is a third sort 
of Moisture whereby the parts of our Body are
nourished, and is contained in all the parts of
an Animal, like a certain Dew sprinkled upon
them: This is the Opinion of Ancients.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="253">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Rosa</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Erysipelas</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Rostriformis processus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Coracoides</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Rotator major & minor</form>, <xpln lang="en">are two <term lang="la">Apophyses</term> in
the upper part of the Thigh-Bone, called <term lang="la">Tri&shy;
chanteres</term>, in which the Tendons of many Muscles
are terminated.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Rotula</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Mola genu</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Rotul&aelig;</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Tabell&aelig;</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Rubrica</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Impetigo</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ructatio</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="belching(n)">Belching, is a depraved Motion of
the Stomach, occasioned by an Effervescence
there, whereby Vapours and flatulent Matter
are sent out at the Mouth. And it is either acid,
or stinking, or savours like something burnt or 
roasted.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ructus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Bombus</term> and <term lang="la">Ructatio</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Rugitus</form> <xpln lang="en">is an Effervescence of Chyle and
Excrements in the Blood, whereby Wind and
several other Motions are excited in the Guts,
and rowl up and down the Excrements, when
there's no easy Vent nor upwards nor down&shy;
wards.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ruptio</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Rhegma</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ryas</form> <xpln lang="en">is a too plentiful and preternatural fal&shy;
ling of Tears.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">SAccus</form> <xpln lang="en">is the Gut called <term lang="la">Rectum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sacculus Chyliferus</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Roriferus</term>, is the lower
part of the Passage of the Chyle, into which are
inserted all the Lacteal Veins of the second
sort, and a great number of the Lymphatic Ves&shy;
sels.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sacculus Cordis</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Pericardium</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sacculi Medicinales</form>, <xpln lang="en">are when several Sim&shy;
ples, according to the Nature of the Disease,
are compounded and beaten together, and tied
up in a little Bag, to be applyed to the part affe&shy;
cted. The Bag is to be sewed or quilted down
in several places, that the Ingredients run not al&shy;
together in a Lump.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sacer Ignis</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Herpes Exedens</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sacer Morbus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Epilepsia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sacrum Os</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="holy bone(n)">the Holy Bone, consists of the six
lower <term lang="la">Vertebres</term>, to which are joyned the <term lang="la">Ossa
Coccygis</term>, or Hip-Bones; in the hinder part of the
<term lang="la">Abdomen</term> it makes that Cavity which is called
<term lang="la">Pelvis</term> or the Bason.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sagittalis Sutura</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Veruculata</term>, is that Suture
of the Scull, which begins at the Coronal or
Crown Suture, and ends in the Lambdoidal Su&shy;
ture.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Saliva</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="spittle(n)"><term lang="la">& Salivum</term>, Spittle, is an inspid Li&shy;
quor, which being separated in the <term lang="la">Maxillar</term>
Glandules or Glandules of the Jaws, and by
proper Passages flowing into the Mouth, serves
to moisten its Mouth and Gullet, and assists to
the chewing of Meat, and in some measure to
</page>

<page no="255">
the Digestion and Fermentation of it in the Sto&shy;
mach.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Salivatio</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="salivation(n)">Salivation, is an Evacuation of Spit&shy;
tle by Salivating Medicines, of which sort prin&shy;
cipally are Mercurial Preparations. Salivation
is sometimes taken for a preternatural Increase
of Spittle.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Salvatella</form>, <xpln lang="en">is that Vein which from the Veins
of the Arm is terminated in the little Finger.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sanguificatio</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">H&aelig;matosis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sanguis</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="blood(n)">Blood, is a red florid Liquor con&shy;
tained in the Veins and Arteries, and consists of
all those parts of the Chyle which pass through
the <term lang="la">Papill&aelig;</term>, the little soft risings of the Intestines.
This is that which gives Nourishment, Life and
Strength to all the parts of the Body.  The
Microscope discovers that the parts of the Blood
are round or globular naturally, but that in Fe&shy;
vers 'tis full of Worms.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sanies</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a thick and bloody <term lang="la">Pus</term>, or Matter.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sanitas</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Hygieia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Saphatum</form> <xpln lang="en">is a dry Scurf in the Head, see <term lang="la">Achor</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Saponea</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="lambitive(n)">is a Lambitive made of Almonds.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sarcocele</form> <xpln lang="en">is a Rupture, which consists in a fleshy

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sarcoma</form> <xpln lang="en">is a fleshy Excrescence.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sarcotica</form> <xpln lang="en">are those Medicines which fill up
</page>

<page no="256">
Wounds with Flesh, such as by their moderate
Heat and cleansing qualities keep Wounds and 
Ulcers free from Filth and preserve the natural
temper of the Parts, so that the Aliment easily
supplies the Solution of the Parts.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sare</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Essere</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Satyriasis</form>, <xpln lang="en"><term lang="la">sive Priapismus</term>, is an immoderate
desire of Venery, which upon Coition vanishes.
'Tis taken sometimes for the Leprosy, because
in that Disease the Skin acquires the Roughness
of a Satyr: 'Tis likewise used for the Swelling of
the Glandules behind the Ears.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Satyriasmus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Satyriasis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Scabies</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="itch(n)" lexeme="dry itch(n)">the Itch: 'Tis of two sorts, moist and
dry; the moist is an inequality or roughness of
the Skin with moist and purulent Pustles, accom&shy;
panied with a constant Itching; the Dry Itch is
fourfold <term lang="la">Pruritus, Impetigo, Psora</term>, and <term lang="la">Lepra</term>,
which see.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Scalenum</form>, <xpln lang="en">is that pair of Muscles which extend

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Scalpellum Umbilicarium</form>, <xpln lang="en">is the Knife with

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Scamnum Hypocratis</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="Hypocrates' bench(n)"><f type="i">Hypocrates</f>'s Bench, is

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Scarificatio</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="scarification(n)">Scarification, 'tis an Incision of

without Cupping-Glasses if there by any Morti&shy;
fication or Gangrene, because the Separation is

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Scelotyrbe</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a wandring Pain in the Legs, pro&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Schetica febris</form>, <xpln lang="en">is opposed to the Hectic Fever,

ry Habit of the Body, and not to be removed 
without great difficulty.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Schisma</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="cut(n)">a Cut in any part either hard or soft.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sclerotica</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Cornea</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sclerotica</form>, <xpln lang="en">or hardning Medicines, are such as
unite the parts more firmly amongst themselves,
and that either by dissipating the thin and soft
parts, or else sometimes by retaining them; the
first by hardning the Matter into a <term lang="la">Schirrus</term> by
too hot Medicines, the latter is done when the
part affected acquires a Hardness by cooling and
astringent Medicines, such are <f type="i">Sengreen, Night&shy;
shade, Porcelan</f>, and <f type="i">Water-Lintels</f>. Therefore
these <f type="i">Sclerotic</f> Medicines are either healing, or
else cooling and astringent.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Scleruntica</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Sclerotica</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Scoliasis</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Distortion of the Back-Bone to
one or t'other side.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Scolopomach&aelig;rion</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Chirurgions Knife, with
which Wounds of the <term lang="la">Thorax</term> are widened; 'tis
used also in opening larger Swellings; as also
in opening the <term lang="la">Abdomen</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Scorbutus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="scurvy(n)">the Scurvy, is a Disease that is Epi&shy;
demial to the <f type="i">Hollanders</f>. The Symptoms of it
are generally, livid Spots on the Hands and Feet,
weakness of the Legs, stinking Breath, looseness
of the Teeth, bleeding of the Gums, Convul&shy;
ions, Pains, running Gout, Cholick, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. This
is of two kinds, either <f type="i">Salino-Sulphureus</f>, when
the Sulphur is predominant to Salt; or <f type="i">Sulphureo-&shy;
Salinus</f>, when the Salt is predominant to the Sul&shy;
phur; this is likewise either in the Blood or ner&shy;
vous Juice.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Scriptulus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Scrupulus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Scotomia,</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="dizziness(n)" lexeme="swimming of the head(n)">Dizziness or Swimming of the Head,

</page>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Scroptula</form>, <xpln lang="en">are preternatural hard Glandules,

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Scrotum</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="cod(n)">the Cod, is a Bag which contains
the Testicles of the Male, it consists of a Skin
fleshy Panniculus, the two Tunics <term lang="la">Erythrois</term>
and <term lang="la">Elythrois</term>. In the middle of it is a Line ex&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Secundin&aelig;</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="secundine(n)" lexeme="afterbirth(n)">the Secundine, or After-Birth, are

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sedimentum Urin&aelig;</form>, <xpln lang="en">the Sediment of Urine,
are parts of the nutritious Juice, which being 
separated from the Blood, with the <term lang="la">Serum</term>, be&shy;
cause of their gravity, sink to the bottom of the 
Urine.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="260">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sella Equina</form>, <xpln lang="en"><term lang="la">feu Turcica</term>, it is compounded of
four Processes of the Bone <term lang="la">Sphenoeides</term>, or Wedg&shy;
like Bone; it contained the <f type="i">Pituitarian</f> Glandule,
and in Brutes the <term lang="la">Rete Mirabile</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sella Sphenoeidis</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Sella Equina</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sella Turcica</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Semeiosis</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Diagnosis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Semeiotica</form>, <xpln lang="en">is that part of Physick which treats
of the Signs of Health and Sickness.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Semen</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="seed(n)">Seed, is a white, hot, spirituous, 
thick, clammy, saltish Humor, which is made
out of the thinnest parts of the Blood in the Te&shy;
sticles and <term lang="la">Epididymides</term>, and by proper Passages
is ejected into the Womb of the Female. There
is also in the Female a Matter which is called 
Seed, which proceeds from the <term lang="la">Prostates</term>, and
frequently in their Lechery is emitted forth:
The use of this is to raise Titillation, and render
the Coition more pleasant.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Semicupium</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Bath in which the Patient is
only up to the Navel in Water.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sensorium Commune</form>, <xpln lang="en">or the Seat of common
Sense, is that part of the Brain in which the
Nerves from the Organs of all the Senses are
terminated, which is in the beginning of the
<term lang="la">Medulla Oblongata</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sensus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="sense(n)">Sense, is when the Motion impressed
by the outward Objects upon the Fibres of the 
Nerves is convey'd, by the help of the Animal
Spirits in the Nerves, to the common Sensory
or <term lang="la">Medulla Oblongata</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sephyros</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a hard Inflammation of the Womb.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Septa</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same with <term lang="la">Septica</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Septica</form>, <xpln lang="en"><term lang="la">five Putrefacientia</term>, are those things
</page>

<page no="261">
which by a malignant Heat and sharpness rot
and corrupt the Flesh.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Septum Lucidum</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="partition(n)">is a Partition, upon the ac&shy;
count of its thinness Diaphanous, which distin&shy;
guishes the Ventricles of the Brain.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Septum Transversum</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Diaphragma</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Serpigo</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Lichen</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Serapium</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Syrupus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Serra</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="saw(n)">a Saw.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Serum</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a watery, thin, yellowish, and saltish
Humor, which consists chiefly of Water, with
a moderate quantity of Salt and a little Sulphur:
The Use of it is to be a Vehicle to the Blood.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sesamoeidea Ossa</form>, <xpln lang="en">are 16, 19, 20, and some&shy;
times more little Bones, so called from the like&shy;
ness they have to <f type="i">Sesamum</f> Seeds, which are
found in the Joynts of the Hands and Feet.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Setaceum</form>, <xpln lang="en">is when the Skin of the Neck is ta&shy;
ken up and run through with a Needle; and the
Wound afterward kept open by Bristles, a Skean
of Silk, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. that so the ill Humors may vent
themselves.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sextans</form>, <xpln lang="en">is the sixth part of a Pound, contain&shy;
ing two Ounces.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sialismus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Ptyalismus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sialochus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Ptyalismus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sialon</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Sielos</term> & <term lang="la">Saliva</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sideratio</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Spacelos</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sief Album</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Collyrium</term>.</xpln></wordentry> 

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sigmoides</form>, <xpln lang="en">are the <term lang="la">Apophyses</term> of the Bones,
representing the Letter C of the ancient <f type="i">Greeks</f>.
Also the three <f type="i">Valves</f> of the Great Artery that
hinder the Blood from returning back to the
Heart.</xpln></wordentry>

<page no="262">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Signum Morbi</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="symptom(n)">the Symptome of a Disease.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Siliqua</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="lupin(n)">is half a Lupin, of which six weigh a 
Scruple. This is to be understood of the Seed
contained in it.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Similares partes</form>, <xpln lang="en">Similar Parts, are such as are
throughout of the same Nature and Texture.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Simplicia</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="simple(n)">Simples, are Medicines unmixt and
uncompounded.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sinapismus</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Medicine applyed to the Head,
and is prepared of Mustard, wild Radish, Salt,
and Leven.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sinciput</form>, <xpln lang="en">the sides of the Head.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Singultus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Lygmus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sinus Meningis</form>, <xpln lang="en">are those Cavities which <f type="i">Galen</f>
calls the Ventricles of the Thick Membrane. The
first and second, or the lateral <term lang="la">Sinus</term>'s, are seated
between the Brain and the <term lang="la">Cerebellum</term>, and end
in the Vertebral <term lang="la">Sinus</term>'s. The third begins from
the <term lang="la">Os Cribiforme</term>, and ends in the middle of the
former <term lang="la">Sinus</term>'s. The Insertion of these <term lang="la">Sinus</term>'s is
called <term lang="la">Torcular Herophili</term>. The <term lang="la">Sinus</term>'s after they
have passed through the Skull, are partly con&shy;
tinued with the Jugular Veins, and partly de&shy;
scend through the whole length of the Spinal
Marrow down to the <term lang="la">Os Sacrum</term>. The Use of
them is to supply the place of Veins, for they
convey the Blood from the Brain and <term lang="la">Cerebellum</term>,
partly into the Jugular Veins, and partly into
the Vertebral <term lang="la">Sinus</term>'s.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sinus Ossium</form>, <xpln lang="en">are those Cavities of the Bones
which receive the Heads of other Bones.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="263">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sircasis</form>, <xpln lang="en">is an Inflammation or rather great
Heat of the Brain and its Membranes, occasion'd
by the heat of the Sun: This is frequent in Chil&shy;
dren, because of the thinness of their Skulls.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sirones</form>, <xpln lang="en">are a sort of Pustles which arise in the
Palms of the Hands and Soles of the Feet, and 
contain in them a very little sort of Worms or
Lice.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sitis</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="thirst(n)">Thirst, is a Defect of the Salival Juice
which occasions the fancy and desire of Drink.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Solutio chymica</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a resolving any Body into its
Chymical Principles; which are, Spirit, Salt, 
Sulphur, Water and Earth.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Solutio continui</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Dissolution of the Unity and
Continuity of the Parts: As in Wounds, Ulcers,
Fractures, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Somnambulo</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Noctambulo</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Somnifera</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="sleeping medicine(n)">or Sleeping Medicines, are such
which consisting of f&aelig;tid Sulphureous parts, dis&shy;
sipate and extinguish the Animal Spirits, and
hinder their increase, whence follows Sleep.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Somnus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="sleep(n)">Sleep, is a streightning of the Pores
of the Brain, caused by the Rest of the Animal 
Spirits, by which means the outward Senses rest
from their Operations.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Somnolentia continua</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="drousiness(n)">is a constant Drouziness
and Inclination to Sleep; this comes to pass
when the Pores of the outward or Cortical Sub&shy;
stance of the Brain are quite closed up by some
viscous Matter, so that the Animal Spirits can&shy;
not freely pass.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Spagyrica Medecina</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Hermetica</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sparadrapum</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a piece of Linnen ting'd of
both sides, either with a thick Ointment, or
</page>

<page no="264">
Plaister, and is made this way; after you have
melted your Ointment, or Plaister, dip your
Linnen in it, extend it and keep it for use.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sora</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Essere</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sparganum</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Fascia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sparganosis</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Distention of the Breasts, oc&shy;
casioned by too much Milk.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Spasma</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="spasm(n)">see <f type="i">Spasms</f>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Spasmodica</form>, <xpln lang="en">are Medicines against Convulsi&shy;
ons.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Spasmologia</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Treatise of Convulsions.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Spasmus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="convulsive motion(n)">is any Convulsive Motion. <f type="i">Cardan</f>
makes two sorts of Convulsive Affections, <term lang="la">viz</term>.
<term lang="la">Tetanus</term> and <term lang="la">Spasmus</term>; by the former he under&shy;
stands a constant Contraction, whereby the
Member becomes rigid and inflexible; by the
latter he understands sudden Concussions and
Motions, which cease and return alternately.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Spatha</form>, <xpln lang="en">is an oblong Instrument, broad at the
lower end: Its Use is to take up Conserves and
Electuaries without fouling the Hands.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Spathomela</form>, <xpln lang="en">is an oblong Instrument, made of
Silver or Iron, which Chirurgions and Apothe&shy;
caries use.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Species</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="powder(n)">or Pouders, are those Simples which
are designed to make Compounds with. So <term lang="la">Spe&shy;
cies</term> of Treacle are those Ingredients of which
Treacle is compounded: By the same Name
are called the <term lang="la">Species</term> of ordinary Decoctions.
This Name is chiefly given to some Aromatick
and Purging Pouders: Perhaps because here&shy;
tofore they were made up into Electuaries,
Bolus's, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="265">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Specifica Medicamenta</form>, <xpln lang="en">are those Medicines

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Specillum</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="probe(n)">a Probe.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Speculum Oris</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Dilatatorium</term></xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Spermatic&aelig; Partes</form>, <xpln lang="en">are those Arteries and Veins
which bring the Blood to and convey it from the

the Seed passes: Likewise all whitish parts of
the Body, which because of their whiteness were

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Spermatocele</form>, <xpln lang="en">a Rupture caused by the Con&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sphacelodes</form>, <xpln lang="en">like to the Apoplexy.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sphacelus</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a sudden Extinction of Life and

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sphagitides</form>, <xpln lang="en">are the Jugular Veins in the Neck.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sphenois</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Os Cuneiforme</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sphenopharyng&aelig;us</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a pair of Muscles arising
