neiforme</term>, or Wedg-like Bone, and going oblique&shy;
ly downward, is extended into the sides of the
Gullet; it dilates the Gullet.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sphincter</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Muscle that contracts the Gullet,

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sphygmica</form>, <xpln lang="en">is that part of Physick which treats

<page no="266">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sphygmus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="pulse(n)">the Pulse.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Spina Dorsi</form> <xpln lang="en">are the hinder Prominences of the
<term lang="la">Vertebr&aelig;</term>'s.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Spina Ventosa</form>, <xpln lang="en">is an Ulceration in which the
Bones are eaten by a malignant Humor without
any pain of the <term lang="la">Periostium</term>, or Membrane that co&shy;
vers the Bone, after that a Swelling being risen
without any Pain, the part affected is quite eaten
out with the Ulcer, from whence frequently fol&shy;
lows a necessity of Amputation.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Spinalis medulla</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Medulla spinalis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Spiritus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="spirits(n)">Spirits, are reckon'd of three sorts,
the Animal Spirits in the Brain, the Vital in the
Heart, the Natural in the Liver; but late Au&shy;
thors distinguish 'em only into two kinds, the
Animal in the Brain, the Vital and Natural
(which are accounted the same) in the Mass of 
Blood. The Animal Spirits are a very thin
Liquor, which distilling from the Blood in the
outward or Cortical Substance of the Brain, are
by the proper Ferment of the Brain exalted into
Spirits, and thence through the Medullar Sub&shy;
stance of the Brain, the <term lang="la">Corpus Callosum</term>, and
<term lang="la">Medulla Oblongata</term>, are derived into the Nerves
and Spinal Marrow, and in them perform all the
Actions of Sense and Motion. The Vital or Na&shy;
tural Spirits, are the subtilest parts of the Blood
which actuate and ferment it, and make it fit for
Nourishment.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Splanchnica</form>, <xpln lang="en">are Medicines proper against Dis&shy;
eases of the Intestines.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Splanchnon</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Intestina</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Splen</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="spleen(n)"><term lang="la">sive</term> <term lang="la">Lien</term>, the Spleen, is a Receptacle for
the Salt and earthy Excrements of the Blood,
</page>

<page no="267">
that there, by the assistance of the Animal Spi&shy;
rits, it may be volatiliz'd, and returning again
into the Blood may concur to its farther Fer&shy;
mentation. The Spleen consists of a great num&shy;
ber of little Bladders, between which the Glan&shy;
dules are scatter'd up and down and supply the
place of Veins: The Spleen has likewise an Ar&shy;
tery, Nerves, and Lymphatick Vessels, first dis&shy;
covered by <term lang="la">Fr. Ruisch</term>. It's very like the Sole of
the Foot, and in Cows is exactly like a Beeves
Tongue.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Splenia</form>, <xpln lang="en">are Bolsters made of Linnen, three,
four, or five times doubled, even to the thick&shy;
ness of the Spleen, they are used upon Wounds
Ulcers, and Fractures. The Figure is three&shy;
fold according to the manner of Application, <term lang="la">viz</term>.
at length, obliquely, or transversely: They are
called also <term lang="la">Plumaceoli</term> and <term lang="la">Plagul&aelig;</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Splenica</form>, <xpln lang="en">Splenical Medicines, are such as by at&shy;
tenuating and volatilizing the grosser parts, re&shy;
move the Distempers and Obstructions of the 
Spleen.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Splenii Musculi</form>, <xpln lang="en">arise partly from the five low&shy;
er <term lang="la">Vertebr&aelig;</term>'s of the Neck, and partly from the
points of five of the upper <term lang="la">Vertebr&aelig;</term>'s of the Tho&shy;
rax; the Fibres of these Muscles tend obliquely,
and are fastned to the hinder part of the Head:
The Use of 'em is to draw the Head backward.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Spongoeidea Ossa</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Cribroformia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sporadici morbi</form>, <xpln lang="en">are those Diseases which (<f type="i">dif&shy;
ferent in Nature</f>) seize several People at the same
time, and in the same Countrey.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sputum</form>, <xpln lang="en">a Liquor thicker than ordinary Spittle.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Squammosa Sutura</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Lepidoides</term>.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="268">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Stagma</form>, <xpln lang="en">are Juices of Plants mixt together in 
order to Distillation.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Stalagma</form>, <xpln lang="en">is that which is distilled from the
<term lang="la">Stagma</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Staltica</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Sarcotica</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Stapes</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Incus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Staphyle</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Cion</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Staphyloma</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Disease of the Eye, in which
the two Tunics of the Eye <term lang="la">Cornea</term> and <term lang="la">Uvea</term>, be&shy;
ing broken, fall outward in the shape of a Grape.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Status Morbi</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Acme</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Steatocele</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Rupture or Tumor in the <term lang="la">Scro&shy;
tum</term> of a Fatty or Suet-like Consistence.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Steatoma</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a preternatural Swelling, which
consists of a Matter almost like Suet, of the same
Colour throughout, soft, and tho not easily
yielding to the touch, yet suddenly returns, the 
Fingers removed, to its proper shape and bigness.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Stegnosis</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Constriction and stopping up of

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Stegnotica</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Astringentia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Stercus</form>, <xpln lang="en">is that Excrement which is voided by
Stool; it consists of those parts of the Aliment
and Bile which is unfit for Nourishment.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sterilitas</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Agonia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sternum Os</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="breast-bone(n)">the Breast-Bone, is joyn'd to the
Ribs in the foremost part of the Breast; it consists
of 3 or 4 Bones, and frequently in those that are
come to ripeness of Age grows into one Bone; to
this is joyned in the lower part of it the <term lang="la">Cartila&shy;
go Ensiformis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sternohyoides</form>, <xpln lang="en">is that pair of Muscles which

<page no="269">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sternothuroeides</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a pair of Muscles of the <term lang="la">Car&shy;
tilago Scutiformis</term> which draw it downward; this 
arises from the uppermost and inward part of the
Breast-Bone, and is inserted into the lower side

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sternutatio</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="sneezing(n)">Sneezing, is a forcible driving
out of the Head some sharp Matter which velli&shy;
cates and disturbs the Nerves and Fibres: 'Tis
defin'd likewise an involuntary Motion of the
Brain, which also contracts the Muscles of the
Thorax and <term lang="la">Abdomen</term>, to the intent that the
Matter which vellicates the Nostrils and Brain
may be driven out.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Stigma</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="scar(n)">a Scar.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Stoma</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="mouth(n)">the Mouth, as also the Mouths of any

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Stomachus</form>, <xpln lang="en">is properly the left Orifice of the

ceived into it. To this part descend Nerves

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Strabilismus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Strabismus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Strabismus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="squinting(n)">Squinting, is occasioned by the Re&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Strabositas</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Strabismus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Stranguria</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="strangury(n)">the Strangury, is a difficulty of U&shy;
rine, when the Urine comes away by Drops

<page no="270">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Stratificatio</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a corroding of Metals by cor&shy;
rosive Pouders. The Operation is performed in
this manner: Put first in the bottom of the Cru&shy;
cible some of the corroding Pouder; then some
of the Metal you are to corrode beaten into thin
Plates; then some of the Pouders, and upon
them some more Plates of your Metal, and so on
till the Crucible be full; then make <term lang="la">Ignemrot&aelig;</term>,
or a Fire round your Crucible to the top, or else
place it in a Reverbatory, according as the Ope&shy;
ration shall require.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Struma</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Scrophula</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Stupea</form>, <xpln lang="en"><term lang="la">seu Stupa</term>, is a piece of Linnen dipt in

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Styloglossum</form>, <xpln lang="en">is that pair of Muscles which lift

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Styloeides</form>, <xpln lang="en">are Processes of Bone fashioned

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Stylopharyng&aelig;us</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a pair of Muscles that di&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sudamina</form>, <xpln lang="en">are little Pimples in the Skin, like

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sutura Ossium</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="suture(n)">a Suture is the Juncture of

meeting together.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sutura</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Connexion of the Sides or Lips of
a Wound: This is of two sorts, Actual, which is
done with a Needle of a triangular point, a Pipe,
or Cane, and waxed Thread, first in the middle
of the Wound you must sew it together with a
double Thread, and having made a knot, cut it
off; the rest of the Wound must be sewed up
with a single Thread; care must be taken that
the Stitches are not set too wide, nor too close,
especially not too close, that there may be room
for any corrupt Matter bred in the Wound to
work out: The other sort of Suture is much like
</page>

<page no="273">
the way that Skinners use to sew Skins together:
this is proper in Wounds of the Intestines, and
in Cuts of the Veins and Arteries.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sycosis</form>, <xpln lang="en">is an Excrescence of the Flesh about
the Fundament. 'Tis also an Ulcer so called
from the resemblance of a Fig; this is of two
kinds, one hard and round; the other soft and
flat: Out of the hard issues a very small quanti&shy;
ty of glutinous Matter; out of the Moist pro&shy;
ceeds a greater quantity, and of an ill Smell:
These Ulcers grow in those patts only which are
covered with Hair; the hard and round chiefly 
in the Beard, the moist for the most part in the
Scalp.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Syderatio</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Apoplexia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Symbebecota</form>, <xpln lang="en">are Accidents which happen to

toms which happen in Diseases.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Symmetria</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="good temper(n)">is a good Temper.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sympasma</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Ph&aelig;nigmus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Sympepsis</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Coction of those Humors which
are growing into an Imposthume.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Symphysis</form>, <xpln lang="en">is the Joining of two Bones of which
neither has a proper distinct Motion: This is
either without any Medium, or else with it, as
with a Cartilage or Grisle, a Ligament or Flesh.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Symptoma</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a preternatural Disposition of
the Body occasioned by some Disease: This is
either a Disease caused by another Disease; or
else the Cause of a Disease proceeding from ano&shy;
ther Disease; or else simply a Symptome: This
last is either some Action of the Body hindred or
disturb'd, some fault of the Excrement, or change
of the natural Temper.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Synedreuonta</form>, <xpln lang="en">are common Symptoms which

ing signify the Greatness, Continuance, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. of

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Synocha</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a continued intermitting Fever;

sometimes Putrefaction of the Blood: It is either
quotidian, tertian, or quartan.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Synochos</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a continued Fever without any In&shy;

continues for many days: This is either Simple,

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">TAbella</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a solid Medicine taken inwardly,
made of Powder, and three or four times
as much Sugar, dissolved in a convenient Li&shy;
quor, boiled to the Consistence of a Syrup, and
made into little round Cakes upon a Marble-&shy;
Stone.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Tabes</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Atrophia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Tabes dorsalis</form>, <xpln lang="en">a Consumption in the spinal
Marrow, most incident to Lechers, and fresh
Bride-grooms; they are without a Fever, eat
well, and melt or consume away: If you ask
one in this Disease an account of himself, he
will tell you, that there seem so many Pismires
to fall from his Head down upon his spinal
Marrow; when he eases Nature either by U&shy;
rine or Stool, there flows thin liquid Seed
plentifully; nor can he generate, but when he
sleeps, whether it be with his Wife or no; he
has lascivious Dreams. When he goes or runs any
way, but especially up a steep place, he grows
weak and short breathed, his Head is heavy, and
his Ears tingle: So in progress of Time being
taken with violent Fevers; he dies of a Fever
called <term lang="la">Lipyria</term>, wherein the external Parts are
cold, and the internal burn at the same time.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Tabula</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Tabella & Morsuli</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Tabum</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a thin sort of Matter that comes
from an ill Ulcer.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Tactus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="touch(n)">the Touch, is a Sense whereby the
tactile Qualities of Bodies are offered to the
common Sensory (and there perceived) by
</page>

<page no="277">
the different motion of Nerves diffused through
the whole Body, the Skin being intermediate:
Or Touch is the Sense of a thing touched,
offered to the common Sensory by the Nerves,
the Skin being intermediate, and there per&shy;
ceived.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Talpa</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Tumor, so called, because that
as a Mole (in Latine <term lang="la">Talpa</term>) creeps under
ground; so this feeds upon the Scull under the
Skin: It may be referred to the Species of <term lang="la">A&shy;
theromas</term>; which see.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Talparia</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Talpa</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Talus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Astragalus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Taraxis</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Perturbation of the Humours

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Tarsus</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a cartilaginous Extremity of the
Eye-lids, whence the Hairs spring, called <term lang="la">Cili&shy;
um</term>. Also eight backward Bones of the Foot,
ordered like Grates.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Tecmarsis</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Conjecture at Diseases.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Telephium</form>, <xpln lang="en">is the same Ulcer with <term lang="la">Chironia</term>,
which see; it is so called from <term lang="la">Telephus</term>, who
was a long time troubled with this Disease.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Temperamentum</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="temperament(n)">Temperament, is a Quality
that results from the Union and Mixture of Ele&shy;
ments: See <term lang="la">Crasis</term>.</xpln></wordentry> 

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Temperies</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Crasis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Tempus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="temple(n)">the Temple, is a lateral part of the
Scull in the middle betwixt the Ears and Eyes,
where Cephalick Plaisters are applied for the
Tooth-ach, and Head-ach.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Tendo</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="tendon(n)">a Tendon, is a similar nervous part
annexed to Muscles and Bones, whereby the
voluntary Motion of the Members is chiefly
</page>

<page no="278">
performed: The generality of Chirurgeons
scarce ever distinguish betwixt a Tendon and a
Nerve.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Tenesmus</form>, <xpln lang="en"><term lang="la">Tenasmus</term>, is a continual Desire of
going to Stool, yet attended with an Inability
of doing any thing, but bloody slimy Matter.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Tentigo</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Priapismus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Teredum</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Caries</term></xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Tergum</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Dorsum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Terminthus</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a swelling in the Thighs with a
black Pimple at the top, as big as the Fruit of
the Turpentine-tree.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Terra mortua</form>, <xpln lang="en">is the earthy part that remains
after Elixivation, destitute of all active efficaci&shy;
ous Qualities.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Tertiana Febris intermittens</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="tertian ague(n)">a Tertian Ague,
is an Effervescence of the Blood every third day,
which with its various Symptoms, comes exactly
at a set time. The Cause of it is Nitro-sulphu&shy;
reous Blood; and it is either a true Tertian or
a spurious.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Testes Muliebres</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Orchis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Testes viriles</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="testicle(n)">Mens Testicles, consist of seve&shy;
ral small Vessels wherein the Seed is generated:
It is covered on the out-side with several Tu&shy;
nicks.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Testes Cerebri</form>, <xpln lang="en">are two backward Prominences
of the Brain, called <term lang="la">Testes</term>, from the likeness they
have to Testicles: They are bigger in Men than
in Brutes.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Testudo Cerebri</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Fornix</term>.</xpln></wordentry> 
</page>

<page no="279">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Testudo</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a soft, large Swelling, or not very
hard, in the Head, broad, in form of an Arch
or Tortoise, from which Resemblance it takes
its Name. At the beginning it grows like a
Chest-nut, afterwards like an Egg, wherein is
contained a soft Matter clothed with a certain
Tunick (whence some refer this sort of Tu&shy;
mour to <term lang="la">Meliceres</term>, which see) which sticks so
close to the Scull, that many times it infects and
corrupts it.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Tetanus</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a constant Contraction, whereby a 
Limb grows rigid and inflexible. The Cause of
it is, sometimes a Relaxation or Palsy in some
other Muscles, which when they are relaxed,
the opposite Muscles act too strongly, so that
they draw the part wholly to themselves, which
ought to consist as it were in an <term lang="la">&AElig;quilibrium</term>
betwixt both: Yet sometimes such a permanent
Contraction may proceed, from the Tendons be&shy;
ing loaded and obstructed with serous Matter,
which thereupon grow rigid and stiff: This
Distemper is frequent in the Scurvies, that the
Patient can extend neither Joint nor Limb: The
Tendons in the Back are sometimes contracted
into a round globular Form, which by reason of
such an Afflux of Humours upon them, draw the
Bones out of their due place, and cause an hun&shy;
ched Back, or a stooping and bending of it: It
is usually distinguished into <f type="i">Universal</f>, or which
there are three sorts, <term lang="la">Emprosthotonos, Opisthotonos</term>,
and <term lang="la">Tetanos</term>, properly so called; and <f type="i">Particular</f>,
which respects a certain Member, or a particular
Joint.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="280">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Tetrapharmacum</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Medicine consisting of
four Ingredients, as <term lang="la">Unguentum Basilicum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Theorema</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Theoria</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Theoria</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="speculation(n)">is the speculative part of Physick;
whence <term lang="la">Theorema</term>, a Speculation, and <term lang="la">Theoretica</term>,
those things which belong to the speculative
part of Physick.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Therapeutica</form>, <xpln lang="en">is that part of Physick which
delivers the Method of Healing.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Theriaca</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="triacle(n)">Triacle, is a Medicine that expels

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Therioma</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a wild cruel Ulcer, like <term lang="la">Carcino&shy;
ma</term>, which see.</xpln></wordentry> 

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Therm&aelig;</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="natural bath(n)">are natural Baths.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Thermantica</form>, <xpln lang="en">are healing Medicines.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Therminthus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Terminthus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Thermomethron</form>, <xpln lang="en">is natural Heat, which is per&shy;
ceived by the Pulses.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Thlipsis</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Compression of Vessels.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Thorax</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="chest(n)">or <term lang="la">medius Venter</term>, the Chest, is all that
Cavity which is circumscribed above by the
Neck-bones, below by the <term lang="la">Diaphragme</term>, before
by the Breast-bone, behind by the Back-bones,
on the sides by the Ribs; it is of an Oval Figure,
contains the Heart and Lungs, and is covered
on the inside with a Membrane called <term lang="la">Pleura</term>.
<f type="i">Hippocrates</f> and <f type="i">Aristotle</f> took all that space
from the Neck-bone to the very Secrets, both
the middle and lowermost Cavity, for the
Thorax.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Thorexis</form>, <xpln lang="en">is the drinking of a generous Wine,
which warms the Breast.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="281">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Thrombus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="coagulation(n)">is the Coagulation of Blood or
Milk into Clots or Clusters.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Thymiama</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Suffitus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Thymus</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Glandule in the Throat, which
separates the watery Humour, called <term lang="la">Lympha</term> 
from the Blood, and empties it by the Lympha&shy;
tick Vessels. It is also a fleshy Tumour that
hangs upon the Body like a Wart, of a Colour
like the Flower of Time, whence it has its
Name.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Thyroaryt&aelig;noides</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a pair of Muscles that pro&shy;
ceed from the Cartilage called <term lang="la">Scutiformis</term>, and
extending themselves forward to the Sides of the
<term lang="la">Aryt&aelig;noides</term> (the fourth and fifth part of the 
<term lang="la">Larynx</term>) serve to contract and close the opening
of the <term lang="la">Larynx</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Thyroid&aelig;&aelig; Glandul&aelig;</form>, <xpln lang="en">are two, of a viscous, solid,
bloody Substance, wonderfully adorned with
Vessels of all sorts, and hard Membranes, almost
of the bigness and shape of an Hen's Egg, situ&shy;
ate about the lower seat of the <term lang="la">Larynx</term>, at the 
sides of the Cartilages of the <term lang="la">Thorax, Cricoides</term>,
and some first rings of the Wind-Pipe, upon
which Parts they immediately lye; yet so as
they may be easily separated, unless where they
stick something obstinately, about the beginning
and the end; Nature has placed them in those
parts, that they may warm them when cold,
receive superfluous Moisture, and contribute to
the Ornament of the Neck.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Thyroides</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="cartilage(n)">is the Cartilage, called <term lang="la">Scutiformis</term>,
of the <term lang="la">Larynx</term>: Also the Hole of the <term lang="la">Os pubis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Tibia</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="leg(n)">the Leg, is the part betwixt the Knee
and the Ancle. It consists of two Bones: One
</page>

<page no="282">
outward, called <term lang="la">Focile minus</term>; another Inward
and larger, which has usurped the Name of the
whole, and is called <term lang="la">Tibia</term>, <term lang="la">Focile majus</term> others
call it, <term lang="la">& Canna major</term>. The upper end has a
Process which is received by a Cavity in the
Thigh, and two oblong Cavities to admit the
Heads of the Thigh-bone, the Depth of which
Cavities is encreased by a Cartilage that is an&shy;
nexed thereunto by Ligaments: This Cartilage
is movable, soft, slippery, moistened with an
unctuous Humour, thick in its Circumference,
and smaller towards the Center, whence it is
called <term lang="la">Lunata</term>, made like an Half-moon; there
are rugged sharp Ligaments before, which En&shy;
crease the Lunary Cartilages. The fore part,
which is acute and long, is called <term lang="la">Spina</term>: There
is below a prominent and gibbous Process in
the inner side, nigh the Foot, and is called
<term lang="la">Malleolus externus</term>; one of the Ankle-bones.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Tinctura</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="tincture(n)">a Tincture, or <term lang="la">Elixir</term>, is the Ex&shy;
traction of the Colour, Quality, and Strength of
any thing.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Tinea</form>, <xpln lang="en"><emend err="if">is</emend> running Sores in the Head full of
little Holes, called <term lang="la">Achores</term>, continue long, or
be too slowly or ill cured, they grow into <term lang="la">Tine&shy;
as</term>, crusty stinking Ulcers of the Head, which
gnaw and consume its Skin; therefore it is de&shy;
servedly reckoned amongst the Diseases of Chil&shy;
dren, but when they are a little grown; for
tho Adult Persons are sometimes troubled with
this Disease, yet they contracted the Rudiments
and Seeds of it in their Infancy. It is called
<term lang="la">Tinea</term>, which signifies a Moth, from those little
Worms which eat and consume Clothes: be&shy;
</page>

<page no="283">
cause those Ulcers prey upon the Skin of the
Head, as those Animals upon Clothes. What
the <f type="i">Greeks</f> called this Distemper is not so obvi&shy;
ous.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Tinnitus Aurium</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="buzzing in the ears(n)">is a certain Buzzing or ting&shy;
ling in the Ears, proceeding from Obstruction, 
or something that irritates the Ear, whereby
the Air that is shut up is continually moved by
the beating of the Arteries, and the Drum of
the Ear is lightly verberated, whence arises a
Buzzing and Noise.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Tometica</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Attenuantia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Trachea</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">aspera Arteria</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Trachoma</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Scab, or Asperity of the inner

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Trage&aelig;</form>, <xpln lang="en">differ not from Powders, but that
the Ingredients whereof they are prepared, are
</page>

<page no="284">
not beat so small: And they are applied exter&shy;
nally to the Body, either put to or resolved into
Smoak, or they are put into a Linnen Bag, and
then into Wine or other Liquor, that they may
communicate their Strength and Qualities to it.
Yet sometimes they are compounded of some sort
of Antidotes, or Counter-poisons, and other
odoriferous things, and of simple Medicines re&shy;
duced into a Powder, with an Addition of Sugar.
In the making these, they commonly take one
Ounce of Sugar to every Dram of Ingredient,
especially those which are bitter and unpleasant.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Tragema</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Trag&aelig;a</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Traulus</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="stammering(n)">and <term lang="la">Traulotes</term>, is a Stammering, or

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Traumatica</form>, <xpln lang="en">are those things, which be&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Trombosis</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="coagulation(n)">is a Coagulation of Milk or Blood

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Tromos</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="trembling(n)">is a Trembling, or a Depravation of

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Tub&aelig; Fallopian&aelig;</form>, <xpln lang="en">are two slender Passages, pro&shy;

a little removed from it, grow gradually wider;
</page>

<page no="286">
they have large Holes or Orifices, which almost
lye shut, the extream Edges falling flat; yet if
they be diligently opened and dilated, they re&shy;
present the extream Orifice of a brazen Pipe.
Their Use is to receive the Eggs from the Te&shy;
sticles and carry them into the Womb, according
to the excellent <f type="i">R. de Graaf</f>. the Truth where&shy;
of is evident from the Inspection of Rabits
dissected.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Tubercula</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Phymata</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Tunica</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Membrana</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Tussis</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="cough(n)">a Cough, is a vehement Efflation of

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Tympanias</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Tympanites</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Tympanities</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="tympany(n)"><term lang="la">Tympanias</term>, <term lang="la">Aqua intercus sicca</term>, a
Tympany, is a fixed, constant equable, hard,
resisting Tumour of the <term lang="la">Abdomen</term>, which, being
beat, sounds: It proceeds from a stretching In&shy;
fl<emend err="aa">a</emend>tion of the parts, and of the membrana&shy;
ceous Bowels, whose Fibres are too much swoln
with Animal Spirits, and hindred from receed&shy;
ing by the nervous Juice which obstructs the
</page>

<page no="287">
Passage; to which Distemper there is conse&shy;
quently added, as the Complement of all, an a&shy;
bundance of flatulent Matter in the places that

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Tympanum</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="ear-drum(n)">the Drum of the Ear, is a small,
thin, orbicular, transparent Membrane, stretched

Ear, called <term lang="la">Concha</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Typhodes</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="fever(n)">is a symptomatical, continued, burn&shy;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Typhomania</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a <term lang="la">Delirium</term> with a Phrensy,

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Typhonia</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Typus</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Periodus</term> and <term lang="la">Circuitus</term>, is an Order
of Fevers, consisting of Intension and Remiss&shy;
on, or encreasing and decreasing.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Tyria</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Ophiasis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Tyroides</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Thyroides</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Tyrosis</form>, <xpln lang="en">is when Milk which is eaten curdles
into a Substance like Cheese.</xpln></wordentry>
</wordgroup1>
</page>

<page no="288">
<wordgroup1 type="a" object="V">V.

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">VAacuatio</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Evacuatio</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vacui dies</form>, <xpln lang="en">are those Days wherein an im&shy;
perfect and ill <term lang="la">Crisis</term> frequently happens; and
those are 6, 8, 10, 12, 16, 18. to which some
add, 22, 23, 25, 29, 30, 32, 33, 35, 38, 39.
these are called medicinal Days, because Medi&shy;
cines may be given on them.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vagina uteri</form>, <xpln lang="en">it is called also <term lang="la">Matrix</term>, <term lang="la">Uteri Osti&shy;
um, Uteri Cervix</term>, is that Passage into which a
Man's Yard is sheathed as it were in Coition;
it is placed in the <term lang="la">Hypogastrium</term>, and is of an ob&shy;
long Figure, and of different Magnitude accor&shy;
ding to the Age of the Woman, and her Use of
Men; its upper part is as thick as the breadth of
a Straw, but the lower twice or thrice as thick
again: It is about as broad as the Gut <term lang="la">Rectum</term>,
nervous and wrinkled within: It is perforated
with a great many little Pores, especially in
the lower part, about the end of the urinary 
Passage.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vaginalis tunica</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Elythroides</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Valetudo</form>, <xpln lang="en">is either a good or ill Disposition of
the Parts of the Body.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Valvul&aelig;</form>, <xpln lang="en">are little thin Membranes in Vessels
or Fibres, like Folding-doors as it were; they
have received different Names, according to the
Diversity of their Figuration, as <term lang="la">Sigmoides</term>, like
the Letter <term lang="la">Sigma</term>, <term lang="la">Semilunares</term>, like an Half&shy;
moon, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. They are found in Veins, Arteries,
Lymphatick and Lacteal Vessels, and in muscu&shy;
lous Fibres, which were first discovered by our
</page>

<page no="289">
Curiosity, and of which we have discoursed in
a particular Tract: The Use of them is to hin&shy;
der the Blood and other Liquors, from return&shy;
ing the same way they came.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Valvul&aelig;</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="valve(n)" lexeme="fold(n)">Valves, are also found in the Inte&shy;
stines, in the small and great Guts, especially in
the <term lang="la">Jejunum</term>, and about the beginning of the
<term lang="la">Ileum</term>, which are called Semi-circular from their
Figure. These Valves or Folds grow more and 
more oblique by little and little the nearer you
come to the <term lang="la">Ileum</term>, and at the beginning of the
<term lang="la">Ileum</term> they are less oblique than farther on. In 
like manner near the end of the <term lang="la">Jejunum</term>, they
are gradually more and more distant from one
another; and so in the <term lang="la">Ileum</term> too. At the be&shy;
ginning and in the middle of the <term lang="la">Jejunum</term>, they
are scarce distant half a Thumbs breadth; in
the <term lang="la">Ileum</term> a whole Thumbs breadth and more.
They yield a little if thrust with your Finger,
and move here and there: At the beginning of
the <term lang="la">Colon</term> there is a fleshy and circular Valve,
besides several others in that Gut. The Use of
them is to stop the Meat a little, that it may be 
the better fermented, the Chyle distributed, 
the adjacent Parts be cherished with Heat, and
lastly, that it ascends not again.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vaporarium</form>, <xpln lang="en">is when the Patient does not sit in
Liquor, but receives Vapours through an Hole,
under which there is placed a Pot full of appo&shy;
site and boyling hot Ingredients, which cooling,
fresh Matter is added.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Varicosum corpus</form>, <xpln lang="en">is that Contexture of Sper&shy;
matick Vessels which enters the Testicles.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="290">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Variol&aelig;</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="smallpox(n)">the small Pox, consists in a contagi&shy;
ous Disorder of the Blood, contracted from the
Air, or otherwise; accompanied with a conti&shy;
nued wandring Fever, which sometimes in&shy;
creases, sometimes decreases, with a Pain in the
Head and Loins, <emend err="Anixety">Anxiety</emend> and Inquietude, and
with a breaking forth of Pimples or Wheals,
which swell and suppurate. The famous <f type="i">Willis</f>
attributes the Cause of this Distemper to some
filthy and fermentative Matter, which is com&shy;
municated to the <term lang="la">F&oelig;tus</term>, together with the
Nourishment, from the Womb; but how this
can hold in Adult Persons, whose Blood has
undergone so many Alterations, I could never
yet understand from his Writings. It seems ra&shy;
ther to consist in a depraved Temperature of
Air, with a peculiar Disposition of the Blood
and the nervous Juice towards this Distemper.
This poysonous Quality of the Air first infects
the nervous Juice (whence proceeds the Pain
of the Head and Loins) wherewith the Blood
boils and ferments, and parts into little Pieces
or Clots, which in the Course of Circulation
stick to the outward Parts, and to the inner <term lang="la">Vis&shy;
cera</term> too; after a while they grow ripe and sup&shy;

purate.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Varix</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Cirsos</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Varus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Jonthus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vas breve</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Breve vas</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vasa</form>, <xpln lang="en">the Vessels, are Cavities through which
the Liquors of the Body pass, as a Vein, an Ar&shy;
tery, lymphatick Vessels, the <term lang="la">Ductus</term> that con&shy;
veys the Chyle, and those of the Spittle.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="291">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vasa lactea</form>, <xpln lang="en">the Milky Vessels, in the Mesen&shy;
tery, they which reach from the Guts, especi&shy;
ally the small Guts, to the Glandules in the Me&shy;
sentery, are said to be of the First sort; and they
which reach from those Glandules to the Bag
that carries the Chyle, are of the Second sort.
Their Use is to convey the Chyle from the Guts
to the little Bag that holds the Chyle, and thence
to the <term lang="la">Ductus</term>, which conveys it along the <term lang="la">Tho&shy;
rax</term>. <f type="i">Asellius</f> was the first who discovered them,
and the dextrous <f type="i">F. Ruischius</f> afterwards disco&shy;
vered Valves in them.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vasa Lymphatica</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Ven&aelig; Lymphatic&aelig;</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vena</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="vein(n)">a Vein, the Species of them are the <term lang="la">Ve&shy;
na cava</term>, the <term lang="la">Vena port&aelig;</term>, the lymphatick and
milky Veins. Arteries are sometimes taken for
Veins. They consist of four Tunicks, a nervous, 
a glandulous, a muscular, and a membranaceous
one. The Branches of the <term lang="la">Vena cava</term> above the
Heart, are called <f type="i">Jugular</f> Veins, which go to&shy;
wards the Head; they which go towards the
Arms, are called <f type="i">Axillary</f>; that about the Heart
<f type="i">Coronary</f>; in the Lungs <f type="i">Pulmonary</f>; in the Liver
<f type="i">Hepatick</f>, or Liver-Vein; in the <term lang="la">Diaphragme</term>
<term lang="la">Phrenica</term>; in the Thighs <f type="i"><term lang="la">Crural</term>; in the Reins <f type="i">E&shy;
mulgent</f>; and so from its various Ramificati&shy;
on, it is variously denominated.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vena port&aelig;</form>, <xpln lang="en">is only in the <term lang="la">Abdomen</term>, and extends
its Roots to the Liver, Spleen, Ventricle, Me&shy;
sentery, Intestines, Pancreas, Cawl, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. The
Office of the <term lang="la">Vena cava</term> and <term lang="la">port&aelig;</term>, is, to convey
the Blood that is more than what serves for
Nourishment, to the Liver, or Heart, or Lungs.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="292">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ven&aelig; Lymphatic&aelig;</form>, <xpln lang="en">the Lymphatick Veins, re&shy;
reive the <term lang="la">Lympha</term> from the conglobated Glan&shy;
dules, and discharge themselves either into the
Sanguinary Veins, or into the Receptacle of the
Chyle.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ven&aelig; lacte&aelig;</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Vasa lactea</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ven&aelig; sectio</form>, <xpln lang="en">is the Opening of a Vein, which
is either for Evacuation, or to derive the Blood
to another part, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>. In Bleeding respect must
always be had to the Strength of the Person.
There never ought to be taken away above a
Pound; but the better way is, to take away first
six or eight Ounces, and if Occasion require, to 
repeat the Operation. A Vein is to be cut ac&shy;
cording to the length of the Fibres, and not A&shy;
cross or Traverse.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Veneris OEstrum</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Clitoris</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Venter infimus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Hypogastrium</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ventosa</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Cucurbitula</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ventres</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Cavitates</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ventriculus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="stomach(n)">the Stomach, is a membranous
Bowel in the <term lang="la">Abdomen</term>, under the Diaphragme,
betwixt the Liver and the Spleen, consisting of
four Tunicks; a nervous, fibrous, glandulous,
and membranous one: It has two Orifices, one
on the Right-hand, called <term lang="la">Pylorus</term> or <term lang="la">Janitor</term>,
whereat the Meat is sent out into the Guts;
another on the Left-hand, at which the Meat
enters: Its Office is to concoct or ferment the
Meat; it is called also <term lang="la">Stomachus</term> and <term lang="la">Aqua&shy;
liculus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ventriculi cerebri</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="ventricle of the brain(n)">the Ventricles of the Brain,
are four; the Use of them is to receive the se&shy;
rous Humours, and to bring them by the <term lang="la">Pelvis</term>
</page>

<page no="293">
to the Pituitary Glandule; or into the <term lang="la">Processus
mammillares</term> by the <term lang="la">Os cribrifrome</term> to the No&shy;
strils. They are nothing but Complications
of the Brain, which happened there as 'twere
by accident.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ventriculi cordis</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="ventricle of the heart(n)">the Ventricles of the Heart,
are two; the first or Right Ventricle receives
the Blood from the <term lang="la">Vena cava</term>, and sends it to
the Lungs; the Left receives the Blood from the
Lungs, and sends it through the whole Body
by the <term lang="la">Arteria Aorta</term>; In the Systole or Con&shy;
traction of the Ventricles the Blood is sent out:
In the Diastole or Dilatation it is let into the
Heart: Yet others explain it on the contrary,
because they understand not Greek.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vermes</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Lumbrici</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vermiformis processus</form>, <xpln lang="en">is the Prominence of the
<term lang="la">Cerebellum</term>, so called from its shape.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vertebra</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Spondylus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vertigo</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Scotomia</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Verruc&aelig;</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="wart(n)">Warts, are a sort of <term lang="la">Tubercula</term>; they
are called also <term lang="la">Porri</term>, because if you look into
the tops of them, they seem to resemble the
Capillaments, or little Threds of Onyons:
They are an hard, high, callous, little <term lang="la">Tubercu&shy;
lum</term>, or Swelling, which break out of the Skin,
and breed in any part of the Body.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vertex</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="crown of the head(n)">the Crown of the Head, is the gib&shy;
bous middle part of the fore and back part of
the Head.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vesica</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="bladder(n)">the Bladder, is an hollow membra&shy;
naceous Part, wherein any Liquor that is to be
excerned, is contained; as the Bladder that
contains the Urine, the Gall, the Seed.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="294">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vesica</form>, <xpln lang="en"><term lang="la">destillatoria</term>, is a Brazen or Copper
Vessel, which contains any thing that is to be
destilled.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vesicatoria</form>, <xpln lang="en">are Medicines which act upon and
rarify the Spirits and serous Particles, gather
them betwixt the Skin and <term lang="la">Cuticula</term>, the thin
fine Skin, and consequently separate them, and
raise little Bladers full of serous Matter.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vesicula fellis</form>, <xpln lang="en">see  <term lang="la">Folliculus fellis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vespertilionum al&aelig;</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="bats' wings(n)">Bats Wings, are two broad
membranous Ligaments, on each side one, where&shy;
with the bottom of the Womb is loosely tied 
to the Bones of the Flank. <term lang="la">Aret&aelig;us</term> likens them
to Bats-wings.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Veternus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Lethargus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vibex</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Enchymoma</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Victus ratio</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a way Living, whereby Health
is preserved, and Diseases repelled by things
convenient: It consists in the Use of things
called <term lang="la">non Naturales</term>, not natural (which see in
their place;) and it is in Diseases threefold,
thick, moderate, thin; the thin is again ei&shy;
ther simply thin, more thin, or the thinnest
of all.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vigilia</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="waking(n)">Waking, is an Agitation and Expan&shy;
sion of animal Spirits in the Pores of the Brain,
whereby the Motions of Objects are easily re&shy;
presented to the common Sensory by the ex&shy;
ternal Organs; which Spirits if they be too
much expanded and agitated, they cause an
obstinate long Wakening.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vigor Morbi</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Acme</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vinum Cos</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Wine of good Colour, Smell,
and Taste.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="295">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vinum Hypocraticum</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Wine wherein Sugar
and Spices have been infused, and is afterwards
strained through a Bag, which they call <term lang="la">Manica
Hypocratis</term>, which see.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vinum Medicatum</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Wine wherein Medi&shy;
cines have been infused for the use of sick
People.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Virga</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Penis</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Virginale claustrum</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Hymen</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Viscera</form>, <xpln lang="en">are Organs contained in the three
great Cavities of the Body: They are called al&shy;
so <term lang="la">Exta</term> and <term lang="la">Interranea</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Visus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="sight(n)">Sight, is a Sence whereby Light and
Colours, are perceived from the Motion of
subtile Matter upon the <term lang="la">Tunica retina</term> of the
Eye.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vitalis facultas</form>, <xpln lang="en">the Vital Faculty, is an Action
whereby a Man lives, which is performed, whe&shy;
ther we design it or no; such are the Moti&shy;
ons of the Heart, Respiration, Nutrition, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.
It depends chiefly upon the <term lang="la">Cerebellum</term>. It is the
same with Natural Faculty, tho the Ancients di&shy;
stinguished them, placing the Natural in the
Liver, and the vital in the Heart.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vitalis Indicatio</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a way whereby Strength
and Vigor are continually renewed and pre&shy;
served.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vitiligo</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="leprosy(n)">a sort of Leprosy; there are Three
kinds of them. <term lang="la">Alphus</term> where the Colour is white,
something rough, and not continued, like so
many Drops here and there; but sometimes it
spreads broader, and with some Intermissions.
<term lang="la">Melas</term> differs in Colour, because it is black, and
like a Shade; in the rest they agree. <term lang="la">Leuce</term> has
</page>

<page no="296">
something like <term lang="la">Alphus</term>, but it is whiter, and
descends deeper, and in it the Hairs are white, 
and like Down: All these spread, but in some
quicker, in others slower.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vitreus Humor</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Humores Oculi</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ulceratio</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Exulceratio</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ulcus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="ulcer(n)">an Ulcer, is a Solution of the <term lang="la">Continu&shy;
um</term>, proceeding from a consuming Matter, in the
soft parts of the Body, and attended with a Di&shy;
minution of Magnitude.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ulna</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Focile majus</term>, is the greater Bone be&shy;
twixt the Arm and the Wrist, which is jointed
upward with the Shoulder by <term lang="la">Ginglimus</term> (which
see,) and therefore it has there both Processes
and Cavities: Two oblong Processes, and as it
were triangular, and rugged, that the Liga&shy;
ments may knit it strongly. The fore-most
and upper-most is less, and goes into the Cavity 
of the Shoulder: The backward Process is
thicker and larger, ends in an obtuse Angle,
and enters the hinder Cavity of the Shoulder;
the Latines call it <term lang="la">Gibberus</term>: In the middle of
these there's a great Cavity like a Semicircle.
It has yet another external lateral Cavity for
the Head of the <term lang="la">Radius</term>, or lesser Bone of the
Cubit; it is joynted at the lower end with
the Wrist, both by a Cartilage in the middle,
and by an acute Process, and therefore called
<term lang="la">Styloides</term> (or like a sharp-pointed Pen used in
Writing-Tables) whence there arises a Liga&shy;
ment, which fastens the Cubit and the Joynt
of the Wrist together.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ulomelia</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Soundness of the whole Body.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="297">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Umbilicus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="navel(n)">the Navel, is a Boss in the middle
of the <term lang="la">Abdomen</term>, to which the Navel-string in
a <term lang="la">F&oelig;tus</term> is joined, which is cut off after Deli&shy;
very.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Uncia</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="ounce(n)">an Ounce, is the Twelfth part of a
Physicians Pound, containing eight Drams.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Undimia</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Oedema</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Unguentum</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="ointment(n)">an Ointment, is a Medicine out&shy;
wardly applied, of a Consistence something
thicker than a <term lang="la">Linimentum</term>: It is called also
<term lang="la">Unguen</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Unguis</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="nail(n)">a Nail, is a similar, flexible, white,
and hard part, which defends the Fingers from
external Injuries, and in some measure adorns
them. The root of it is joined to a certain Liga&shy;
ment, and by reason of the neighbouring Ten&shy;
dons it becomes sensible: They seem to be 
made of a Collection of very little Pipes, which
adhere extreamly thick to one another, and
shoot out into length. Where they begin, there
you find certain nervous Fibres like so many
small Nipples lengthened, the lengthened parts
whereof are seen as far as the Nail: If they be
forcibly torn off, they leave divers Holes, so
that the Horney Substance of the Nails looks
like a Net. Under the Nails there is a pappy
sort of Body, which has its Vessels of Excretion.
The <term lang="la">Apices</term>, or tops of the Nails, are they which
grow beyond the Flesh; the Parts which are
cut, are called the <term lang="la">Segmina</term>, the parings of the
Nails, the parts under the Nails, are the <term lang="gk">&#x03BD;&#x03C1;&#x03C5;&#x03C0;&#x03C4;&#x03B1;</term>,
the hidden parts; the White semilunar part
next the Root, is the Rise of the Nail; the very 
beginnings that grow into the Skin, are called
</page>

<page no="298">
the Roots of the Nails; the Sides, the Clefts;
the white Spots, <term lang="la">Nubecula</term>, little Clouds, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ungula</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a sort of hooked Instrument to
draw a dead <term lang="la">F&oelig;tus</term> out of the Womb.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ungula Oculi</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Pterygium</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vola</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="palm of the hand(n)">is the Palm of the Hand; also the Cavi&shy;
ty of the Foot.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Volatica</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Lichen</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Volsella, <term lang="en">or</term> Vulsella</form>, <xpln lang="en">is an Instrument to pull
up Hairs with by the Root, Tweezers: Or a
Chyrurgions little Tongs, which are of dif&shy;
ferent shape according to the Diversity of their
Use.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Volvulus</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Ileon</term> and <term lang="la">Chordapsus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vomica</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a fault in the Lungs, from Heteroge&shy;
neous Blood, which being lodged perhaps in
one of the little Bladdery Cells there, occasi&shy;
ons neither a Fever nor a Cough; but after&shy;
ward when it is encreased, it oppresses the
neighbouring Sanguiferous Vessels, and impreg&shy;
nates the Blood as it passes along with its <term lang="la">Efflu&shy;
viums</term>; whereupon there succeeds a small Fever,
accompanied with Inquietude and Leanness;
at last when it is full grown and concocted
into Matter, it makes a Nest as it were and
lodges there.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vomitorium</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Medicine taken inwardly,
made of <f type="i">Emeticks</f>, or things that provoke Vo&shy;
miting, infused, dissolved, or decocted.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vomitus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="vomiting(n)">a Vomiting, is a violent and inverse
Motion of the Ventricle, wherein its fleshy Fi&shy;
bres being irritated, and contractedg towards
the left Orifice, send out at the Mouth whatso&shy;
ever is contained in the Stomach.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="299">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Urachus</form> <xpln lang="en">is the urinary Passage in <term lang="la">F&oelig;tus</term>'s,
reaching from the Bladder to the Membrane
called <term lang="la">Allanitodes</term>; which after the <term lang="la">F&oelig;tus</term> is
born becomes like a Ligament, and is that
which suspends the Bladder; it is joyned with
the Navel and the bottom of the Bladder.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Uranismus</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Palatum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Urentia</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Pyrotica</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Ureter</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a fistulous membranaceous Vessel,
which proceeds from both Reins, and opens be&shy;
tween the Membranes of the Bladder, by which 
the Urine passes from the Reins to the Bladder:
<f type="i">Celsus</f> calls it the White Vein.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Urethra</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Fistula</term>, is the urinary Passage
whereby the Urine is discharged at the Yard in
Man, and in like manner in Women: It serves
also for the Ejection of Seed. The seminal
little Bladders, empty themselves into it by two
Holes at the beginning of it, when there is oc&shy;
casion; which Bladders or Vessels are surround&shy;
ed with glandulous Prostates, perforated with
several Holes; to which there is a little peice of
Flesh affixed.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Urinaria Fistula</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Urethra</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Uretica</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Diuretica</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Urina</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Uron</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Urocrisis</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Urocritica</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Urocriterium</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Judgment upon Urine.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Urocritica</form>, <xpln lang="en">are Signs which are observed from
Urines.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Uromantia</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Urocriterium</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Uromantis</form>, <xpln lang="en">is one who can divine something
from Urines.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="300">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Uron</form>, <xpln lang="en"><term lang="la">Urina, Lotium</term>, is a serous Excrement
conveyed from the Blood, that passes the Reins
by the Ureters to the Bladder, and so is excern&shy;
ed when occasion requires it: It consists of much
Salt, a little Sulphur, of Earth and Spirit.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Uroscopia</form>, <xpln lang="en">is the Inspection of Urine.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Uteri osculum</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Osculum uteri</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Uteri Procidentia</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Procidentia uteri</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Usnea</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="moss(n)">is the Moss which grows upon Bones or
Trees.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Uterus</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="womb(n)">the Womb, is an organical part pla&shy;
ced in a Woman's <term lang="la">Abdomen</term>, which is divided
into the Bottom, the Neck, and the Sheath: It
has two broad Ligaments, and two round: It
is of a nervous and fibrous Substance; and is of
different Thickness according to the difference
of Age, and time of going with Child. At
the bottom within, there is a Cavity whence the
Courses flow, wherein likewise Generation and
Conception flow, wherein likewise Generation and
Conception are made: Before it is the Bladder;
behind it is the Gut <term lang="la">Rectum</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vulneraria</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Traumatica</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vulnas</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="wound(n)" lexeme="cutting(n)" lexeme="incision(n)" lexeme="pricking(n)">a Wound, is a Solution of the <term lang="la">Conti&shy;
nuum<emend err="n"></emend></term> with some external Instrument. It is
different, as well according to the place or part
whence it is inflicted, as upon a Nerve, or
the Flesh, as according to the Instrument which
inflicts it, so that if it be done by a sharp keen
Instrument, it is called <term lang="la">Sectio & Incisio</term>, cutting
or Incision; if by pricking, 'tis called <term lang="la">Punctura</term> or
<term lang="la">Punctio</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vulsella</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Volsella</term>.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="301">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Vulva</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Woman's secret Parts: See <term lang="la">Cun&shy;
nus</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Uvula</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Cion</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Uvea Membrana</form>, <xpln lang="en">or <term lang="la">Choroides</term>, is almost all&shy;
together Continuous on the inside to the <term lang="la">Tunica
Scelerotis</term>; it is perforated in the fore part, and 
leaves a space for the Apple of the Eye, which
may be contracted or dilated.</xpln></wordentry>
</wordgroup1>

<wordgroup1 type="a" object="X">X.

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">XErophthalmia</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a dry Bleardness or Blood&shy;
shot of the Eyes.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Xerotes</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a dry Disposition of Body.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Xiphoides</form>, <xpln lang="en">is the pointed Cartilage of the
Breast.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Xyster</form>, <xpln lang="en">is an Instrument to shave and scrape
Bones with.</xpln></wordentry>
</wordgroup1>

<wordgroup1 type="a" object="Z">Z.

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">ZErna</form>, <xpln lang="en">the same that <term lang="la">Lichen</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Zirbus</form> <xpln lang="en" lexeme="caul(n)">with the <f type="i">Arabians</f>, is the same that
<term lang="la">Omentum</term> the Cawl.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Zone</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="holy fire(n)">is that part of the Body where we
are begirt; also a sort of Herpes called Holy&shy;
fire.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Zoogonia</form>, <xpln lang="en">is a Generation of perfect Animals
born alive.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Zootomia</form>, <xpln lang="en">is an artificial Dissection of Ani&shy;
mals.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>

<page no="302">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Zotica</form>, <xpln lang="en">is the vital Faculty.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Zygoma</form>, <xpln lang="en">is the jugal Bone about the Temp&shy;
ples.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Zymoma</form>, <xpln lang="en" lexeme="ferment(n)">is a Ferment, as the nitrous Air,
the Watery Juice in the Mouth, the acide
Liquor in the Stomach, the Blood in the
the Spleen, <term lang="la">&amp;c</term>.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="la">Zymosis</form>, <xpln lang="en">see <term lang="la">Fermentatio</term>.</xpln></wordentry>
